<h2><a id="user-content-register-8" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#register-8"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Register 8</h2>
<p><a name="user-content-figure28"></a><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/83120345edb72a53eb0e7965c865b0aff90ac884/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830334632382e737667"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/83120345edb72a53eb0e7965c865b0aff90ac884/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830334632382e737667" alt="" data-canonical-src="https://rawgit.com/oraculo666/the-msx-red-book/master/images/CH03F28.svg" style="max-width:100%;"></a></p>
<p><strong>Figure 28</strong></p>
<p>The four Amplitude bits determine the amplitude of Channel A from a minimum of 0 to a maximum of 15. The Mode bit selects either fixed or modulated amplitude: 0=Fixed, 1=Modulated. When modulated amplitude is selected the fixed amplitude value is ignored and the channel is modulated by the output from the Envelope Generator.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-register_9"></a></p>
<h2><a id="user-content-register-9" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#register-9"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Register 9</h2>
<p>This register controls the amplitude of Channel B as for Channel A.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-register_10"></a></p>
<h2><a id="user-content-register-10" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#register-10"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Register 10</h2>
<p>This register controls the amplitude of Channel C as for Channel A.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-registers_11_and_12"></a></p>
<h2><a id="user-content-registers-11-and-12" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#registers-11-and-12"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Registers 11 and 12</h2>
<p><a name="user-content-figure29"></a><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/23100cd486df24b1a4070c2bb15bfc24ce74a53b/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830334632392e737667"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/23100cd486df24b1a4070c2bb15bfc24ce74a53b/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830334632392e737667" alt="" data-canonical-src="https://rawgit.com/oraculo666/the-msx-red-book/master/images/CH03F29.svg" style="max-width:100%;"></a></p>
<p><strong>Figure 29</strong></p>
<p>These two registers control the frequency of the single Envelope Generator used for amplitude modulation. As for the Tone Generators this frequency is determined by placing a divider count in the registers. The divider value may range from 1 to 65535 with Register 11 holding the least significant eight bits and Register 12 the most significant. The master frequency for the Envelope Generator is 6991 Hz so the envelope frequency may range from 6991 Hz (divide by 1) to 0.11 Hz (divide by 65535).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-register_13"></a></p>
<h2><a id="user-content-register-13" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#register-13"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Register 13</h2>
<p><a name="user-content-figure30"></a><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/faf529aed3d51efd006fa8307b243696fded6829/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830334633302e737667"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/faf529aed3d51efd006fa8307b243696fded6829/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830334633302e737667" alt="" data-canonical-src="https://rawgit.com/oraculo666/the-msx-red-book/master/images/CH03F30.svg" style="max-width:100%;"></a></p>
<p><strong>Figure 30</strong></p>
<p>The four Envelope Shape bits determine the shape of the amplitude modulation envelope produced by the Envelope Generator:</p>
<p><a name="user-content-figure31"></a><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/cf972a3afa28710ce8632859beddb76efab8a08a/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830334633312e737667"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/cf972a3afa28710ce8632859beddb76efab8a08a/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830334633312e737667" alt="" data-canonical-src="https://rawgit.com/oraculo666/the-msx-red-book/master/images/CH03F31.svg" style="max-width:100%;"></a></p>
<p><strong>Figure 31</strong></p>
<p><a name="user-content-register_14"></a></p>
<h2><a id="user-content-register-14" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#register-14"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Register 14</h2>
<p><a name="user-content-figure32"></a><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/b0cf81bf958ee5ccf2e06b60a5e042e406babec7/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830334633322e737667"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/b0cf81bf958ee5ccf2e06b60a5e042e406babec7/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830334633322e737667" alt="" data-canonical-src="https://rawgit.com/oraculo666/the-msx-red-book/master/images/CH03F32.svg" style="max-width:100%;"></a></p>
<p><strong>Figure 32</strong></p>
<p>This register is used to read in PSG Port A. The six joystick bits reflect the state of the four direction switches and two trigger buttons on a joystick: 0=Pressed, 1=Not pressed. Alternatively up to six Paddles may be connected instead of one joystick. Although most MSX machines have two 9 pin joystick connectors only one can be read at a time. The one to be selected for reading is determined by the Joystick Select bit in <a href="#register_15">PSG Register 15</a>.</p>
<p>The Keyboard Mode bit is unused on UK machines. On Japanese machines it is tied to a jumper link to determine the keyboard's character set.</p>
<p>The Cassette Input is used to read the signal from the cassette EAR output. This is passed through a comparator to clean the edges and to convert to digital levels but is otherwise unprocessed.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-register_15"></a></p>
<h2><a id="user-content-register-15" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#register-15"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Register 15</h2>
<p><a name="user-content-figure33"></a><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/4d8807ec34ffee2d6796d43febb6e65897409dae/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830334633332e737667"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/4d8807ec34ffee2d6796d43febb6e65897409dae/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830334633332e737667" alt="" data-canonical-src="https://rawgit.com/oraculo666/the-msx-red-book/master/images/CH03F33.svg" style="max-width:100%;"></a></p>
<p><strong>Figure 33</strong></p>
<p>This register is used to output to PSG Port B. The four least significant bits are connected via TTL open-collector buffers to pins 6 and 7 of each joystick connector. They are normally set to a 1, when a paddle or joystick is connected, so that the pins can function as inputs. When a touchpad is connected they are used as handshaking outputs.</p>
<p>The two Pulse bits are used to generate a short positive- going pulse to any paddles attached to joystick connectors 1 or 2. Each paddle contains a monostable timer with a variable resistor controlling its pulse length. Once the timer is triggered the position of the variable resistor can be determined by counting until the monostable times out.</p>
<p>The Joystick Select bit determines which joystick connector is connected to PSG Port A for input: 0=Connector 1, 1=Connector 2.</p>
<p>The Kana LED output is unused on UK machines. On Japanese machines it is used to drive a keyboard mode indicator.</p>
<p><br><br><br></p>
<p><a name="user-content-chapter_4"></a></p>
<h1><a id="user-content-4-rom-bios" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#4-rom-bios"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>4. ROM BIOS</h1>
<p>The design of the MSX ROM is of importance if machine code programs are to be developed efficiently and Operate reliably. Almost every program, including the BASIC Interpreter itself, will require a certain set of primitive functions to operate. These include screen and printer drivers, a keyboard decoder and other hardware related functions. By separating these routines from the BASIC Interpreter they can be made available to any application program. The section of ROM from 0000H to 268BH is largely devoted to such routines and is called the ROM BIOS (Basic Input Output System).</p>
<p>This chapter gives a functional description of every recognizably separate routine in the ROM BIOS. Special attention is given to the "standard" routines. These are documented by Microsoft and guaranteed to remain consistent through possible hardware and software changes. The first few hundred bytes of the ROM consists of Z80 JP instructions which provide fixed position entry points to these routines. For maximum compatibility with future software an application program should restrict its dependence on the ROM to these locations only. The description of the ROM begins with this list of entry points to the standard routines. A brief comment is placed with each entry point, the full description is given with the routine itself.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-data_areas"></a></p>
<h2><a id="user-content-data-areas" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#data-areas"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Data Areas</h2>
<p>It is expected that most users will wish to disassemble the ROM to some extent (the full listing runs to nearly four hundred pages). In order to ease this process the data areas, which do not contain executable Z80 code, are shown below:</p>
<pre><code>0004H-0007H     185DH-1863H     4B3AH-4B4CH     73E4H-73E4H
002BH-002FH     1B97H-1BAAH     4C2FH-4C3FH     752EH-7585H
0508H-050DH     1BBFH-23BEH     555AH-5569H     7754H-7757H
092FH-097FH     2439H-2459H     5D83H-5DB0H     7BA3H-7BCAH
0DA5H-0EC4H     2CF1H-2E70H     6F76H-6F8EH     7ED8H-7F26H
1033H-105AH     3030H-3039H     70FFH-710CH     7F41H-7FB6H
1061H-10C1H     3710H-3719H     7182H-7195H     7FBEH-7FFFH
1233H-1252H     392EH-3FE1H     71A2H-71B5H
13A9H-1448H     43B5H-43C3H     71C7H-71DAH
160BH-1612H     46E6H-46E7H     72A6H-72B9H
</code></pre>
<p>Note that these data areas are for the UK ROM, there are slight differences in the Japanese ROM relating to the keyboard decoder and the video character set. Disparities between the ROMs are restricted to these regions with the bulk of the code being identical in both cases.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-terminology"></a></p>
<h2><a id="user-content-terminology" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#terminology"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Terminology</h2>
<p>Reference is frequently made in this chapter to the standard routines and to Workspace Area variables. Whenever this is done the Microsoft-recommended name is used in upper case letters, for example "the <a href="#filvrm">FILVRM</a> standard routine" and "<a href="#scrmod">SCRMOD</a> is set". Subroutines which are not named are referred to by a parenthesized address, "the screen is cleared (<a href="#0777h">0777H</a>)" for example. When reference is made to the Z80 status flags assembly language conventions are used, for example "Flag C" would mean that the carry flag is set while "Flag NZ" means that the zero flag is reset. The terms "EI" and "DI" mean enabled interrupts and disabled interrupts respectively.</p>

<p><a name="user-content-01b6h"></a><a name="user-content-rdslt"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 01B6H
Name...... RDSLT
Entry..... A=Slot ID, HL=Address
Exit...... A=Byte read
Modifies.. AF, BC, DE, DI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to read a single byte from memory in any slot. The Slot Identifier is composed of a Primary Slot number a Secondary Slot number and a flag:</p>
<p><a name="user-content-figure34"></a><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/522aad79a749521eb47c17ec5db80410112bb370/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830344633342e737667"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/522aad79a749521eb47c17ec5db80410112bb370/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830344633342e737667" alt="" data-canonical-src="https://rawgit.com/oraculo666/the-msx-red-book/master/images/CH04F34.svg" style="max-width:100%;"></a></p>
<p><strong>Figure 34:</strong> Slot ID</p>
<p>The flag is normally 0 but must be 1 if a Secondary Slot number is included in the Slot ID. The memory address and Slot ID are first processed (<a href="#027eh">027EH</a>) to yield a set of bit masks to apply to the relevant slot register. If a Secondary Slot number is specified then the Secondary Slot Register is first modified to select the relevant page from that Secondary Slot (<a href="#02a3h">02A3H</a>). The Primary Slot is then switched in to the Z80 address space, the byte read and the Primary Slot restored to its original setting via the <a href="#rdprim">RDPRIM</a> routine in the Workspace Area. Finally, if a Secondary Slot number is included in the Slot ID, the original Secondary Slot Register setting is restored (01ECH).</p>
<p>Note that, unless it is the slot containing the Workspace Area, any attempt to access page 3 (C000H to FFFFH) will cause the system to crash as <a href="#rdprim">RDPRIM</a> will switch itself out. Note also that interrupts are left disabled by all the memory switching routines.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-01d1h"></a><a name="user-content-wrslt"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 01D1H
Name...... WRSLT
Entry..... A=Slot ID, HL=Address, E=Byte to write
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, BC, D, DI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to write a single byte to memory in any slot. Its operation is fundamentally the same as that of the <a href="#rdslt">RDSLT</a> standard routine except that the Workspace Area routine <a href="#wrprim">WRPRIM</a> is used rather than <a href="#rdprim">RDPRIM</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-01ffh"></a><a name="user-content-calbas"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 01FFH
Name...... CALBAS
Entry..... IX=Address
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF', BC', DE', HL', IY, DI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to call an address in the BASIC Interpreter from any slot. Usually this will be from a machine code program running in an extension ROM in page 1 (4000H to 7FFFH). The high byte of register pair IY is loaded with the MSX ROM Slot ID (00H) and control transfers to the <a href="#calslt">CALSLT</a> standard routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0205h"></a><a name="user-content-callf"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0205H
Name...... CALLF
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF', BC', DE', HL', IX, IY, DI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to call an address in any slot. The Slot ID and address are supplied as inline parameters rather than in registers to fit inside a hook (<a href="/gseidler/The-MSX-Red-Book/blob/master/chapter_6">Chapter 6</a>), for example:</p>
<pre><code>RST 30H
DEFB Slot ID
DEFW Address
RET
</code></pre>
<p>The Slot ID is first collected and placed in the high byte of register pair IY. The address is then placed in register pair IX and control drops into the <a href="#calslt">CALSLT</a> standard routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0217h"></a><a name="user-content-calslt"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0217H
Name...... CALSLT
Entry..... IY(High byte)=Slot ID, IX=Address
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF', BC', DE', HL', DI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to call an address in any slot. Its operation is fundamentally the same as that of the <a href="#rdslt">RDSLT</a> standard routine except that the Workspace Area routine <a href="#clprim">CLPRIM</a> is used rather than <a href="#rdprim">RDPRIM</a>. Note that <a href="#calbas">CALBAS</a> and <a href="#callf">CALLF</a> are just specialized entry points to this standard routine which offer a reduction in the amount of code required.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-025eh"></a><a name="user-content-enaslt"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 025EH
Name...... ENASLT
Entry..... A=Slot ID, HL=Address
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, BC, DE, DI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to switch in a page permanently from any slot. Unlike the <a href="#rdslt">RDSLT</a>, <a href="#wrslt">WRSLT</a> and <a href="#calslt">CALSLT</a> standard routines the Primary Slot switching is performed directly and not by a Workspace Area routine. Consequently addresses in page 0 (0000H to 3FFFH) will cause an immediate system crash.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-027eh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 027EH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the memory switching standard routines to turn an address, in register pair HL, and a Slot ID, in register A, into a set of bit masks. As an example a Slot ID of FxxxSSPP and an address in Page 1 (4000H to 7FFFH) would return the following:</p>
<pre><code>Register B=00 00 PP 00 (OR mask)
Register C=11 11 00 11 (AND mask)
Register D=PP PP PP PP (Replicated)
Register E=00 00 11 00 (Page mask)
</code></pre>
<p>Registers B and C are derived from the Primary Slot number and the page mask. They are later used to mix the new Primary Slot number into the existing contents of the Primary Slot Register. Register D contains the Primary Slot number replicated four times and register E the page mask. This is produced by examining the two most significant bits of the address, to determine the page number, and then shifting the mask along to the relevant position. These registers are later used during Secondary Slot switching.</p>
<p>As the routine terminates bit 7 of the Slot ID is tested, to determine whether a Secondary Slot has been specified, and Flag M returned if this is so.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-02a3h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 02A3H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the memory switching standard routines to modify a Secondary Slot Register. The Slot ID is supplied in register A while registers D and E contain the bit masks shown in the previous routine.</p>
<p>Bits 6 and 7 of register D are first copied into the Primary Slot register. This switches in page 3 from the Primary Slot specified by the Slot ID and makes the required Secondary Slot Register available. This is then read from memory location FFFFH and the page mask, inverted, used to clear the required two bits. The Secondary Slot number is shifted to the relevant position and mixed in. Finally the new setting is placed in the Secondary Slot Register and the Primary Slot Register restored to its original setting.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-02d7h"></a><a name="user-content-chkram"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 02D7H
Name...... CHKRAM
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, BC, DE, HL, SP
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to perform memory initialization at power- up. It non-destructively tests for RAM in pages 2 and 3 in all sixteen possible slots then sets the Primary and Secondary Slot registers to switch in the largest area found. The entire Workspace Area (F380H to FFC9H) is zeroed and <a href="#exptbl">EXPTBL</a> and <a href="#slttbl">SLTTBL</a> filled in to map any expansion interfaces in existence Interrupt Mode 1 is set and control transfers to the remainder of the power-up initialization routine (<a href="#7c76h">7C76H</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-03fbh"></a><a name="user-content-iscntc"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 03FBH
Name...... ISCNTC
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to check whether the CTRL-STOP or STOP keys have been pressed. It is used by the BASIC Interpreter at the end of each statement to check for program termination. <a href="#basrom">BASROM</a> is first examined to see if it contains a non-zero value, if so the routine terminates immediately. This is to prevent users breaking into any extension ROM containing a BASIC program.</p>
<p><a href="#intflg">INTFLG</a> is then checked to determine whether the interrupt handler has placed the CTRL-STOP or STOP key codes (03H or 04H) there. If STOP has been detected then the cursor is turned on (<a href="#09dah">09DAH</a>) and <a href="#intflg">INTFLG</a> continually checked until one of the two key codes reappears. The cursor is then turned off (<a href="#0a27h">0A27H</a>) and, if the key is STOP, the routine terminates.</p>
<p>If CTRL-STOP has been detected then the keyboard buffer is first cleared via the <a href="#kilbuf">KILBUF</a> standard routine and <a href="#trptbl">TRPTBL</a> is checked to see whether an "<code>ON STOP GOSUB</code>" statement is active. If so the relevant entry in <a href="#trptbl">TRPTBL</a> is updated (<a href="#0ef1h">0EF1H</a>) and the routine terminates as the event will be handled by the Interpreter Runloop. Otherwise the <a href="#enaslt">ENASLT</a> standard routine is used to switch in page 1 from the MSX ROM, in case an extension ROM is using the routine, and control transfers to the "<code>STOP</code>" statement handler (63E6H).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0468h"></a><a name="user-content-kilbuf"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0468H
Name...... KILBUF
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. HL
</code></pre>
<p>Standard Routine to clear the forty character type-ahead keyboard buffer <a href="#keybuf">KEYBUF</a>. There are two pointers into this buffer, <a href="#putpnt">PUTPNT</a> where the interrupt handler places characters, and <a href="#getpnt">GETPNT</a> where application programs fetch them from. As the number of characters in the buffer is indicated by the difference between these two pointers <a href="#keybuf">KEYBUF</a> is emptied simply by making them both equal.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-046fh"></a><a name="user-content-breakx"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 046FH
Name...... BREAKX
Entry..... None
Exit...... Flag C if CTRL-STOP key pressed
Modifies.. AF
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine which directly tests rows 6 and 7 of the keyboard to determine whether the CTRL and STOP keys are both pressed. If they are then <a href="#keybuf">KEYBUF</a> is cleared and row 7 of <a href="#oldkey">OLDKEY</a> modified to prevent the interrupt handler picking the keys up as well. This routine may often be more suitable for use by an application program, in preference to <a href="#iscntc">ISCNTC</a>, as it will work when interrupts are disabled, during cassette I/O for example, and does not exit to the Interpreter.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-049dh"></a><a name="user-content-initio"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 049DH
Name...... INITIO
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, E, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to initialize the PSG and the Centronics Status Port. <a href="#register_7">PSG Register 7</a> is first set to 80H making PSG Port B=Output and PSG Port A=Input. <a href="#register_15">PSG Register 15</a> is set to CFH to initialize the Joystick connector control hardware. <a href="#register_14">PSG Register 14</a> is then read and the Keyboard Mode bit placed in <a href="#kanamd">KANAMD</a>, this has no relevance for UK machines.</p>
<p>Finally a value of FFH is output to the Centronics Status Port (I/O port 90H) to set the <a href="#strobe">STROBE</a> signal high. Control then drops into the <a href="#gicini">GICINI</a> standard routine to complete initialization.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-04bdh"></a><a name="user-content-gicini"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 04BDH
Name...... GICINI
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to initialize the PSG and the Workspace Area variables associated with the "<code>PLAY</code>" statement. <a href="#quetab">QUETAB</a>, <a href="#vcba">VCBA</a>, <a href="#vcbb">VCBB</a> and <a href="#vcbc">VCBC</a> are first initialized with the values shown in Chapter 6. PSG Registers <a href="#register_8">8</a>, <a href="#register_9">9</a> and <a href="#register_10">10</a> are then set to zero amplitude and <a href="#register_7">PSG Register 7</a> to B8H. This enables the Tone Generator and disables the Noise Generator on each channel.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0508h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0508H
</code></pre>
<p>This six byte table contains the "<code>PLAY</code>" statement parameters initially placed in <a href="#vcba">VCBA</a>, <a href="#vcbb">VCBB</a> and <a href="#vcbc">VCBC</a> by the <a href="#gicini">GICINI</a> standard routine: Octave=4, Length=4, Tempo=120, Volume=88H, Envelope=00FFH.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-050eh"></a><a name="user-content-initxt"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 050EH
Name...... INITXT
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, BC, DE, HL, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to initialize the VDP to <a href="#40x24_text_mode">40x24 Text Mode</a>. The screen is temporarily disabled via the <a href="#disscr">DISSCR</a> standard routine and <a href="#scrmod">SCRMOD</a> and <a href="#oldscr">OLDSCR</a> set to 00H. The parameters required by the <a href="#chput">CHPUT</a> standard routine are set up by copying <a href="#linl40">LINL40</a> to <a href="#linlen">LINLEN</a>, <a href="#txtnam">TXTNAM</a> to <a href="#nambas">NAMBAS</a> and <a href="#txtcgp">TXTCGP</a> to <a href="#cgpbas">CGPBAS</a>. The VDP colours are then set by the <a href="#chgclr">CHGCLR</a> standard routine and the screen is cleared (077EH). The current character set is copied into the VRAM Character Pattern Table (<a href="#071eh">071EH</a>). Finally the VDP mode and base addresses are set via the <a href="#settxt">SETTXT</a> standard routine and the screen is enabled.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0538h"></a><a name="user-content-init32"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0538H
Name...... INIT32
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, BC, DE, HL, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to initialize the VDP to <a href="#32x24_text_mode">32x24 Text Mode</a>. The screen is temporarily disabled via the <a href="#disscr">DISSCR</a> standard routine and <a href="#scrmod">SCRMOD</a> and <a href="#oldscr">OLDSCR</a> set to 01H. The parameters required by the <a href="#chput">CHPUT</a> standard routine are set up by copying <a href="#linl32">LINL32</a> to <a href="#linlen">LINLEN</a>, <a href="#t32nam">T32NAM</a> to <a href="#nambas">NAMBAS</a>, <a href="#t32cgp">T32CGP</a> to <a href="#cgpbas">CGPBAS</a>, <a href="#t32pat">T32PAT</a> to <a href="#patbas">PATBAS</a> and <a href="#t32atr">T32ATR</a> to <a href="#atrbas">ATRBAS</a>. The VDP colours are then set via the <a href="#chgclr">CHGCLR</a> standard routine and the screen is cleared (077EH). The current character set is copied into the VRAM Character Pattern Table (<a href="#071eh">071EH</a>) and all sprites cleared (06BBH). Finally the VDP mode and base addresses are set via the <a href="#sett32">SETT32</a> standard routine and the screen is enabled.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0570h"></a><a name="user-content-enascr"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0570H
Name...... ENASCR
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, BC, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to enable the screen. This simply involves setting bit 6 of VDP <a href="#mode_register_1">Mode Register 1</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0577h"></a><a name="user-content-disscr"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0577H
Name...... DISSCR
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, BC, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to disable the screen. This simply involves resetting bit 6 of VDP <a href="#mode_register_1">Mode Register 1</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-057fh"></a><a name="user-content-wrtvdp"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 057FH
Name...... WRTVDP
Entry..... B=Data byte, C=VDP Mode Register number
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, B, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to write a data byte to any VDP <a href="#vdp_mode_registers">Mode Register</a>. The register selection byte is first written to the VDP <a href="#commandpport">Command Port</a>, followed by the data byte. This is then copied to the relevant register image, <a href="#rg0sav">RG0SAV</a> to <a href="#rg7sav">RG7SAV</a>, in the Workspace Area</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0594h"></a><a name="user-content-settxt"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0594H
Name...... SETTXT
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, BC, DE, HL, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to partially set the VDP to <a href="#40x24_text_mode">40x24 Text Mode</a>. The mode bits M1, M2 and M3 are first set in VDP Mode Registers <a href="#mode_register_0">0</a> and <a href="#mode_register_1">1</a>. The five VRAM table base addresses, beginning with <a href="#txtnam">TXTNAM</a>, are then copied from the Workspace Area into VDP Mode Registers <a href="#mode_register_2">2</a>, <a href="#mode_register_3">3</a>, <a href="#mode_register_4">4</a>, <a href="#mode_register_5">5</a> and <a href="#mode_register_6">6</a> (<a href="#0677h">0677H</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-05b4h"></a><a name="user-content-sett32"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 05B4H
Name...... SETT32
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, BC, DE, HL, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to partially set the VDP to <a href="#32x24_text_mode">32x24 Text Mode</a>. The mode bits M1, M2 and M3 are first set in VDP Mode Registers <a href="#mode_register_0">0</a> and <a href="#mode_register_1">1</a>. The five VRAM table base addresses, beginning with <a href="#t32nam">T32NAM</a>, are then copied from the Workspace Area into VDP Mode Registers <a href="#mode_register_2">2</a>, <a href="#mode_register_3">3</a>, <a href="#mode_register_4">4</a>, <a href="#mode_register_5">5</a> and <a href="#mode_register_6">6</a> (<a href="#0677h">0677H</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-05d2h"></a><a name="user-content-inigrp"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 05D2H
Name...... INIGRP
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, BC, DE, HL, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to initialize the VDP to <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a>. The screen is temporarily disabled via the <a href="#disscr">DISSCR</a> standard routine and <a href="#scrmod">SCRMOD</a> set to 02H. The parameters required by the <a href="#grpprt">GRPPRT</a> standard routine are set up by copying <a href="#grppat">GRPPAT</a> to <a href="#patbas">PATBAS</a> and <a href="#grpatr">GRPATR</a> to <a href="#atrbas">ATRBAS</a>. The character code driver pattern is then copied into the VDP Name Table, the screen cleared (07A1H) and all sprites cleared (06BBH). Finally the VDP mode and base addresses are set via the <a href="#setgrp">SETGRP</a> standard routine and the screen is enabled.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0602h"></a><a name="user-content-setgrp"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0602H
Name...... SETGRP
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, BC, DE, HL, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to partially set the VDP to <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a>. The mode bits M1, M2 and M3 are first set in VDP Mode Registers <a href="#mode_register_0">0</a> and <a href="#mode_register_1">1</a>. The five VRAM table base addresses, beginning with <a href="#grpnam">GRPNAM</a>, are then copied from the Workspace Area into VDP Mode Registers <a href="#mode_register_2">2</a>, <a href="#mode_register_3">3</a>, <a href="#mode_register_4">4</a>, <a href="#mode_register_5">5</a> and <a href="#mode_register_6">6</a> (<a href="#0677h">0677H</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-061fh"></a><a name="user-content-inimlt"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 061FH
Name...... INIMLT
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, BC, DE, HL, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to initialize the VDP to <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a>. The screen is temporarily disabled via the <a href="#disscr">DISSCR</a> standard routine and <a href="#scrmod">SCRMOD</a> set to 03H. The parameters required by the <a href="#grpprt">GRPPRT</a> standard routine are set up by copying <a href="#mltpat">MLTPAT</a> to <a href="#patbas">PATBAS</a> and <a href="#mltatr">MLTATR</a> to <a href="#atrbas">ATRBAS</a>. The character code driver pattern is then copied into the VDP Name Table, the screen cleared (07B9H) and all sprites cleared (06BBH). Finally the VDP mode and base addresses are set via the <a href="#setmlt">SETMLT</a> standard routine and the screen is enabled.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0659h"></a><a name="user-content-setmlt"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0659H
Name...... SETMLT
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, BC, DE, HL, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to partially set the VDP to <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a>. The mode bits M1, M2 and M3 are first set in VDP Mode Registers <a href="#mode_register_0">0</a> and <a href="#mode_register_1">1</a>. The five VRAM table base addresses, beginning with <a href="#mltnam">MLTNAM</a>, are then copied from the Workspace Area to VDP Mode Registers <a href="#mode_register_2">2</a>, <a href="#mode_register_3">3</a>, <a href="#mode_register_4">4</a>, <a href="#mode_register_5">5</a> and <a href="#mode_register_6">6</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0677h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0677H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the <a href="#settxt">SETTXT</a>, <a href="#sett32">SETT32</a>, <a href="#setgrp">SETGRP</a> and <a href="#setmlt">SETMLT</a> standard routines to copy a block of five table base addresses from the Workspace Area into VDP Mode Registers <a href="#mode_register_2">2</a>, <a href="#mode_register_3">3</a>, <a href="#mode_register_4">4</a>, <a href="#mode_register_5">5</a> and <a href="#mode_register_6">6</a>. On entry register pair HL points to the relevant group of addresses. Each base address is collected in turn shifted the required number of places and then written to the relevant Mode Register via the <a href="#wrtvdp">WRTVDP</a> standard routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-06a8h"></a><a name="user-content-clrspr"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 06A8H
Name...... CLRSPR
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, BC, DE, HL, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to clear all sprites. The entire 2 KB Sprite Pattern Table is first filled with zeros via the <a href="#filvrm">FILVRM</a> standard routine. The vertical coordinate of each of the thirty-two sprite attribute blocks is then set to -47 (D1H) to place the sprite above the top of the screen, the horizontal coordinate is left unchanged.</p>
<p>The pattern numbers in the Sprite Attribute Table are initialized with the series 0, 1, 2, 3, 4,... 31 for 8x8 sprites or the series 0, 4, 8, 12, 16,... 124 for 16x16 sprites. The series to be generated is determined by the Size bit in VDP <a href="#mode_register_1">Mode Register 1</a>. Finally the colour byte of each sprite attribute block is filled in with the colour code contained in <a href="#forclr">FORCLR</a>, this is initially white.</p>
<p>Note that the Size and Mag bits in VDP <a href="#mode_register_1">Mode Register 1</a> are not affected by this routine. Note also that the <a href="#init32">INIT32</a>, <a href="#inigrp">INIGRP</a> and <a href="#inimlt">INIMLT</a> standard routines use this routine with an entry point at 06BBH, leaving the Sprite Pattern Table undisturbed.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-06e4h"></a><a name="user-content-calpat"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 06E4H
Name...... CALPAT
Entry..... A=Sprite pattern number
Exit...... HL=Sprite pattern address
Modifies.. AF, DE, HL
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to calculate the address of a sprite pattern. The pattern number is first multiplied by eight then, if 16x16 sprites are selected, multiplied by a further factor of four. This is then added to the Sprite Pattern Table base address, taken from <a href="#patbas">PATBAS</a>, to produce the final address.</p>
<p>This numbering system is in line with the BASIC Interpreter's usage of pattern numbers rather than the VDP's when 16x16 sprites are selected. As an example while the Interpreter calls the second pattern number one, it is actually VDP pattern number four. This usage means that the maximum pattern number this routine should allow, when 16x16 sprites are selected, is sixty-three. There is no actual check on this limit so large pattern numbers will produce addresses greater than 3FFFH. Such addresses, when passed to the other VDP routines, will wrap around past zero and corrupt the Character Pattern Table in VRAM.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-06f9h"></a><a name="user-content-calatr"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 06F9H
Name...... CALATR
Entry..... A=Sprite number
Exit...... HL=Sprite attribute address
Modifies.. AF, DE, HL
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to calculate the address of a sprite attribute block. The sprite number, from zero to thirty-one, is multiplied by four and added to the Sprite Attribute Table base address taken from <a href="#atrbas">ATRBAS</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0704h"></a><a name="user-content-gspsiz"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0704H
Name...... GSPSIZ
Entry..... None
Exit...... A=Bytes in sprite pattern (8 or 32)
Modifies.. AF
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to return the number of bytes occupied by each sprite pattern in the Sprite Pattern Table. The result is determined simply by examining the Size bit in VDP <a href="#mode_register_1">Mode Register 1</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-070fh"></a><a name="user-content-ldirmv"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 070FH
Name...... LDIRMV
Entry..... BC=Length, DE=RAM address, HL=VRAM address
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, BC, DE, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to copy a block into main memory from the VDP VRAM. The VRAM starting address is set via the <a href="#setrd">SETRD</a> standard routine and then sequential bytes read from the VDP <a href="#data_port">Data Port</a> and placed in main memory.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-071eh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 071EH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used to copy a 2 KB character set into the VDP Character Pattern Table in any mode. The base address of the Character Pattern Table in VRAM is taken from <a href="#cgpbas">CGPBAS</a>. The starting address of the character set is taken from <a href="#cgpnt">CGPNT</a>. The <a href="#rdslt">RDSLT</a> standard routine is used to read the character data so this may be situated in an extension ROM.</p>
<p>At power-up <a href="#cgpnt">CGPNT</a> is initialized with the address contained at ROM location 0004H, which is <a href="#1bbfh">1BBFH</a>. <a href="#cgpnt">CGPNT</a> is easily altered to produce some interesting results, <code>POKE &amp;HF920,&amp;HC7:SCREEN 0</code> provides a thoroughly confusing example.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0744h"></a><a name="user-content-ldirvm"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0744H
Name...... LDIRVM
Entry..... BC=Length, DE=VRAM address, HL=RAM address
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, BC, DE, HL, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to copy a block to VRAM from main memory. The VRAM starting address is set via the <a href="#setwrt">SETWRT</a> standard routine and then sequential bytes taken from main memory and written to the VDP <a href="#data_port">Data Port</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0777h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0777H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine will clear the screen in any VDP mode. In <a href="#40x24_text_mode">40x24 Text Mode</a> and <a href="#32x24_text_mode">32x24 Text Mode</a> the Name Table, whose base address is taken from <a href="#nambas">NAMBAS</a>, is first filled with ASCII spaces. The cursor is then set to the home position (<a href="#0a7fh">0A7FH</a>) and <a href="#linttb">LINTTB</a>, the line termination table, re-initialized. Finally the function key display is restored, if it is enabled, via the <a href="#fnksb">FNKSB</a> standard routine.</p>
<p>In <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> the border colour is first set via VDP <a href="#mode_register_7">Mode Register 7</a> (0832H). The Colour Table is then filled with the background colour code, taken from <a href="#bakclr">BAKCLR</a>, for both 0 and 1 pixels. Finally the Character Pattern Table is filled with zeroes.</p>
<p>In <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a> the border colour is first set via VDP <a href="#mode_register_7">Mode Register 7</a> (0832H). The Character Pattern Table is then filled with the background colour taken from <a href="#bakclr">BAKCLR</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-07cdh"></a><a name="user-content-wrtvrm"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 07CDH
Name...... WRTVRM
Entry..... A=Data byte, HL=VRAM address
Exit...... None
Modifies.. EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to write a single byte to the VDP VRAM. The VRAM address is first set up via the <a href="#setwrt">SETWRT</a> standard routine and then the data byte written to the VDP <a href="#data_port">Data Port</a>. Note that the two seemingly spurious <code>EX(SP),HL</code> instructions in this routine, and several others, are required to meet the VDP's timing constraints.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-07d7h"></a><a name="user-content-rdvrm"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 07D7H
Name...... RDVRM
Entry..... HL=VRAM address
Exit...... A=Byte read
Modifies.. AF, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to read a single byte from the VDP VRAM. The VRAM address is first set up via the <a href="#setrd">SETRD</a> standard routine and then the byte read from the VDP <a href="#data_port">Data Port</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-07dfh"></a><a name="user-content-setwrt"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 07DFH
Name...... SETWRT
Entry..... HL=VRAM address
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to set up the VDP for subsequent writes to VRAM via the <a href="#data_port">Data Port</a>. The address contained in register pair HL is written to the VDP <a href="#command_port">Command Port</a> LSB first, MSB second as shown in <a href="#figure7">Figure 7</a>. Addresses greater than 3FFFH will wrap around past zero as the two most significant bits of the address are ignored.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-07ech"></a><a name="user-content-setrd"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 07ECH
Name...... SETRD
Entry..... HL=VRAM address
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to set up the VDP for subsequent reads from VRAM via the <a href="#data_port">Data Port</a>. The address contained in register pair HL is written to the VDP <a href="#command_port">Command Port</a> LSB first, MSB second as shown in <a href="#figure7">Figure 7</a>. Addresses greater than 3FFFH will wrap around past zero as the two most significant bits of the address are ignored.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-07f7h"></a><a name="user-content-chgclr"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 07F7H
Name...... CHGCLR
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, BC, HL, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to set the VDP colours. <a href="#scrmod">SCRMOD</a> is first examined to determine the appropriate course of action. In <a href="#40x24_text_mode">40x24 Text Mode</a> the contents of <a href="#bakclr">BAKCLR</a> and <a href="#forclr">FORCLR</a> are written to VDP <a href="#mode_register_7">Mode Register 7</a> to set the colour of the 0 and 1 pixels, these are initially blue and white. Note that in this mode there is no way of specifying the border colour, this will be the same as the 0 pixel colour. In <a href="#32x24_text_mode">32x24 Text Mode</a>, <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> or <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a> the contents of <a href="#bdrclr">BDRCLR</a> are written to VDP <a href="#mode_register_7">Mode Register 7</a> to set the colour of the border, this is initially blue. Also in <a href="#32x24_text_mode">32x24 Text Mode</a> the contents of <a href="#bakclr">BAKCLR</a> and <a href="#forclr">FORCLR</a> are copied to the whole of the Colour Table to determine the 0 and 1 pixel colours.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0815h"></a><a name="user-content-filvrm"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0815H
Name...... FILVRM
Entry..... A=Data byte, BC=Length, HL=VRAM address
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, BC, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to fill a block of the VDP VRAM with a single data byte. The VRAM starting address, contained in register pair HL, is first set up via the <a href="#setwrt">SETWRT</a> standard routine. The data byte is then repeatedly written to the VDP <a href="#data_port">Data Port</a> to fill successive VRAM locations.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-083bh"></a><a name="user-content-totext"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 083BH
Name...... TOTEXT
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, BC, DE, HL, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to return the VDP to either <a href="#40x24_text_mode">40x24 Text Mode</a> or <a href="#32x24_text_mode">32x24 Text Mode</a> if it is currently in <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> or <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a>. It is used by the BASIC Interpreter Mainloop and by the "<a href="#input">INPUT</a>" statement handler. Whenever the <a href="#initxt">INITXT</a> or <a href="#init32">INIT32</a> standard routines are used the mode byte, 00H or 01H, is copied into <a href="#oldscr">OLDSCR</a>. If the mode is subsequently changed to <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> or <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a>, and then has to be returned to one of the two text modes for keyboard input, this routine ensures that it returns to the same one.</p>
<p><a href="#scrmod">SCRMOD</a> is first examined and, if the screen is already in either text mode, the routine simply terminates with no action. Otherwise the previous text mode is taken from <a href="#oldscr">OLDSCR</a> and passed to the <a href="#chgmod">CHGMOD</a> standard routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0848h"></a><a name="user-content-cls"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0848H
Name...... CLS
Entry..... Flag Z
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, BC, DE, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to clear the screen in any mode, it does nothing but call the routine at 0777H. This is actually the "<code>CLS</code>" statement handler and, because this indicates that there is illegal text after the statement, it will simply return if entered with Flag NZ.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-084fh"></a><a name="user-content-chgmod"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 084FH
Name...... CHGMOD
Entry..... A=Screen mode required (0, 1, 2, 3)
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, BC, DE, HL, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to set a new screen mode. Register A, containing the required screen mode, is tested and control transferred to <a href="#initxt">INITXT</a>, <a href="#init32">INIT32</a>, <a href="#inigrp">INIGRP</a> or <a href="#inimlt">INIMLT</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-085dh"></a><a name="user-content-lptout"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 085DH
Name...... LPTOUT
Entry..... A=Character to print
Exit...... Flag C if CTRL-STOP termination
Modifies.. AF
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to output a character to the line printer via the Centronics Port. The printer status is continually tested, via the <a href="#lptstt">LPTSTT</a> standard routine, until the printer becomes free. The character is then written to the Centronics Data Port (I/O port 91H) and the <a href="#strobe">STROBE</a> signal of the Centronics Status Port (I/O port 90H) briefly pulsed low. Note that the <a href="#breakx">BREAKX</a> standard routine is used to test for the CTRL-STOP key if the printer is busy. If CTRL-STOP is detected a CR code is written to the Centronics Data Port, to flush the printer's line buffer, and the routine terminates with Flag C.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0884h"></a><a name="user-content-lptstt"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0884H
Name...... LPTSTT
Entry..... None
Exit...... A=0 and Flag Z if printer busy
Modifies.. AF
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to test the Centronics Status Port BUSY signal. This just involves reading I/O port 90H and examining the state of bit 1: 0=Ready, 1=Busy.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-088eh"></a><a name="user-content-posit"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 088EH
Name...... POSIT
Entry..... H=Column, L=Row
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to set the cursor coordinates. The row and column coordinates are sent to the <a href="#outdo">OUTDO</a> standard routine as the parameters in an ESC,"Y",Row+1FH, Column+1FH sequence. Note that the BIOS home position has coordinates of 1,1 rather than the 0,0 used by the BASIC Interpreter.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-089dh"></a><a name="user-content-cnvchr"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 089DH
Name...... CNVCHR
Entry..... A=Character
Exit...... Flag Z,NC=Header; Flag NZ,C=Graphic; Flag Z,C=Normal
Modifies.. AF
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to test for, and convert if necessary, characters with graphic headers. Characters less than 20H are normally interpreted by the output device drivers as control characters. A character code in this range can be treated as a displayable character by preceding it with a graphic header control code (01H) and adding 40H to its value. For example to directly display character code 0DH, rather than have it interpreted as a carriage return, it is necessary to output the two bytes 01H,4DH. This routine is used by the output device drivers, such as the <a href="#chput">CHPUT</a> standard routine, to check for such sequences.</p>
<p>If the character is a graphic header <a href="#grphed">GRPHED</a> is set to 01H and the routine terminates, otherwise <a href="#grphed">GRPHED</a> is zeroed. If the character is outside the range 40H to 5FH it is left unchanged. If it is inside this range, and <a href="#grphed">GRPHED</a> contains 01H indicating a previous graphic header, it is converted by subtracting 40H.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-08bch"></a><a name="user-content-chput"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 08BCH
Name...... CHPUT
Entry..... A=Character
Exit...... None
Modifies.. EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to output a character to the screen in <a href="#40x24_text_mode">40x24 Text Mode</a> or <a href="#32x24_text_mode">32x24 Text Mode</a>. <a href="#scrmod">SCRMOD</a> is first checked and, if the VDP is in either <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> or <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a>, the routine terminates with no action. Otherwise the cursor is removed (<a href="#0a2eh">0A2EH</a>), the character decoded (<a href="#08dfh">08DFH</a>) and then the cursor replaced (<a href="#09e1h">09E1H</a>). Finally the cursor column position is placed in <a href="#ttypos">TTYPOS</a>, for use by the "<code>PRINT</code>" statement, and the routine terminates.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-08dfh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 08DFH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the <a href="#chput">CHPUT</a> standard routine to decode a character and take the appropriate action. The <a href="#cnvchr">CNVCHR</a> standard routine is first used to check for a graphic character, if the character is a header code (01H) then the routine terminates with no action. If the character is a converted graphic one then the control code decoding section is skipped. Otherwise <a href="#esccnt">ESCCNT</a> is checked to see if a previous ESC character (1BH) has been received, if so control transfers to the ESC sequence processor (<a href="#098fh">098FH</a>). Otherwise the character is checked to see if it is smaller than 20H, if so control transfers to the control code processor (<a href="#0914h">0914H</a>). The character is then checked to see if it is DEL (7FH), if so control transfers to the delete routine (0AE3H).</p>
<p>Assuming the character is displayable the cursor coordinates are taken from <a href="#csry">CSRY</a> and <a href="#csrx">CSRX</a> and placed in register pair HL, H=Column, L=Row. These are then converted to a physical address in the VDP Name Table and the character placed there (<a href="#0be6h">0BE6H</a>). The cursor column position is then incremented (<a href="#0a44h">0A44H</a>) and, assuming the rightmost column has not been exceeded, the routine terminates. Otherwise the row's entry in <a href="#linttb">LINTTB</a>, the line termination table, is zeroed to indicate an extended logical line, the column number is set to 01H and a LF is performed.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0908h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0908H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine performs the LF operation for the <a href="#chput">CHPUT</a> standard routine control code processor. The cursor row is incremented (<a href="#0a61h">0A61H</a>) and, assuming the lowest row has not been exceeded, the routine terminates. Otherwise the screen is scrolled upwards and the lowest row erased (0A88H).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0914h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0914H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the control code processor for the <a href="#chput">CHPUT</a> standard routine. The table at <a href="#092fh">092FH</a> is searched for a match with the code and control transferred to the associated address.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-092fh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 092FH
</code></pre>

<p><a name="user-content-0980h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0980H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine performs the ESC,"x" operation for the <a href="#chput">CHPUT</a> standard routine control code processor. <a href="#esccnt">ESCCNT</a> is set to 01H to indicate that the next character received is a parameter.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0983h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0983H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine performs the ESC,"y" operation for the <a href="#chput">CHPUT</a> standard routine control code decoder. <a href="#esccnt">ESCCNT</a> is set to 02H to indicate that the next character received is a parameter.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0986h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0986H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine performs the ESC",Y" operation for the <a href="#chput">CHPUT</a> standard routine control code processor. <a href="#esccnt">ESCCNT</a> is set to 04H to indicate that the next character received is a parameter.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0989h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0989H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine performs the ESC operation for the <a href="#chput">CHPUT</a> standard routine control code processor. <a href="#esccnt">ESCCNT</a> is set to FFH to indicate that the next character received is the second control character.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-098fh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 098FH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the <a href="#chput">CHPUT</a> standard routine ESC sequence processor. If <a href="#esccnt">ESCCNT</a> contains FFH then the character is the second control character and control transfers to the control code processor (0919H) to search the ESC code table at <a href="#0953h">0953H</a>.</p>
<p>If <a href="#esccnt">ESCCNT</a> contains 01H then the character is the single parameter of the ESC,"x" sequence. If the parameter is "4" (34H) then <a href="#cstyle">CSTYLE</a> is set to 00H resulting in a block cursor. If the parameter is "5" (35H) then <a href="#csrsw">CSRSW</a> is set to 00H making the cursor normally disabled.</p>
<p>If <a href="#esccnt">ESCCNT</a> contains 02H then the character is the single parameter in the ESC,"y" sequence. If the parameter is "4" (34H) then <a href="#cstyle">CSTYLE</a> is set to 01H resulting in an underline cursor. If the parameter is "5" (35H) then <a href="#csrsw">CSRSW</a> is set to 01H making the cursor normally enabled.</p>
<p>If <a href="#esccnt">ESCCNT</a> contains 04H then the character is the first parameter of the ESC,"Y" sequence and is the row coordinate. The parameter has 1FH subtracted and is placed in <a href="#csry">CSRY</a>, <a href="#esccnt">ESCCNT</a> is then decremented to 03H.</p>
<p>If <a href="#esccnt">ESCCNT</a> contains 03H then the character is the second parameter of the ESC,"Y" sequence and is the column coordinate. The parameter has 1FH subtracted and is placed in <a href="#csrx">CSRX</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-09dah"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 09DAH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used, by the <a href="#chget">CHGET</a> standard routine for example, to display the cursor character when it is normally disabled. If <a href="#csrsw">CSRSW</a> is non-zero the routine simply terminates with no action, otherwise the cursor is displayed (09E6H).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-09e1h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 09E1H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used, by the <a href="#chput">CHPUT</a> standard routine for example, to display the cursor character when it is normally enabled. If <a href="#csrsw">CSRSW</a> is zero the routine simply terminates with no action. <a href="#scrmod">SCRMOD</a> is checked and, if the screen is in <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> or <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a>, the routine terminates with no action. Otherwise the cursor coordinates are converted to a physical address in the VDP Name Table and the character read from that location (<a href="#0bd8h">0BD8H</a>) and saved in <a href="#cursav">CURSAV</a>.</p>
<p>The character's eight byte pixel pattern is read from the VDP Character Pattern Table into the <a href="#linwrk">LINWRK</a> buffer (<a href="#0ba5h">0BA5H</a>). The pixel pattern is then inverted, all eight bytes if <a href="#cstyle">CSTYLE</a> indicates a block cursor, only the bottom three if <a href="#cstyle">CSTYLE</a> indicates an underline cursor. The pixel pattern is copied back to the position for character code 255 in the VDP Character Pattern Table (<a href="#0bbeh">0BBEH</a>). The character code 255 is then placed at the current cursor location in the VDP Name Table (<a href="#0be6h">0BE6H</a>) and the routine terminates.</p>
<p>This method of generating the cursor character, by using character code 255, can produce curious effects under certain conditions. These can be demonstrated by executing the BASIC statement <code>FOR N=1 TO 100: PRINT CHR$(255);:NEXT</code> and then pressing the cursor up key.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0a27h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0A27H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used, by the <a href="#chget">CHGET</a> standard routine for example, to remove the cursor character when it is normally disabled. If <a href="#csrsw">CSRSW</a> is non-zero the routine simply terminates with no action, otherwise the cursor is removed (0A33H).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0a2eh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0A2EH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used, by the <a href="#chput">CHPUT</a> standard routine for example, .to remove the cursor character when it is normally enabled. If <a href="#csrsw">CSRSW</a> is zero the routine simply terminates with no action. <a href="#scrmod">SCRMOD</a> is checked and, if the screen is in <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> or <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a>, the routine terminates with no action. Otherwise the cursor coordinates are converted to a physical address in the VDP Name Table and the character held in <a href="#cursav">CURSAV</a> written to that location (<a href="#0be6h">0BE6H</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0a44h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0A44H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine performs the ESC,"C" operation for the <a href="#chput">CHPUT</a> standard routine control code processor. If the cursor column coordinate is already at the rightmost column, determined by <a href="#linlen">LINLEN</a>, then the routine terminates with no action. Otherwise the column coordinate is incremented and <a href="#csrx">CSRX</a> updated.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0a4ch"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0A4CH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine performs the BS/LEFT operation for the <a href="#chput">CHPUT</a> standard routine control code processor. The cursor column coordinate is decremented and <a href="#csrx">CSRX</a> updated. If the column coordinate has moved beyond the leftmost position it is set to the rightmost position, from <a href="#linlen">LINLEN</a>, and an UP operation performed.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0a55h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0A55H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine performs the ESC,"D" operation for the <a href="#chput">CHPUT</a> standard routine control code processor. If the cursor column coordinate is already at the leftmost position then the routine terminates with no action. Otherwise the column coordinate is decremented and <a href="#csrx">CSRX</a> updated.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0a57h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0A57H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine performs the ESC,"A" (UP) operation for the <a href="#chput">CHPUT</a> standard routine control code processor. If the cursor row coordinate is already at the topmost position the routine terminates with no action. Otherwise the row coordinate is decremented and <a href="#csry">CSRY</a> updated.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0a5bh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0A5BH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine performs the RIGHT operation for the <a href="#chput">CHPUT</a> standard routine control code processor. The cursor column coordinate is incremented and <a href="#csrx">CSRX</a> updated. If the column coordinate has moved beyond the rightmost position, determined by <a href="#linlen">LINLEN</a>, it is set to the leftmost position (01H) and a DOWN operation performed.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0a61h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0A61H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine performs the ESC,"B" (DOWN) operation for the <a href="#chput">CHPUT</a> standard routine control code processor. If the cursor row coordinate is already at the lowest position, determined by <a href="#crtcnt">CRTCNT</a> and <a href="#cnsdfg">CNSDFG</a> (<a href="#0c32h">0C32H</a>), then the routine terminates with no action. Otherwise the row coordinate is incremented and <a href="#csry">CSRY</a> updated.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0a71h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0A71H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine performs the TAB operation for the <a href="#chput">CHPUT</a> standard routine control code processor. ASCII spaces are output (<a href="#08dfh">08DFH</a>) until <a href="#csrx">CSRX</a> is a multiple of eight plus one (BIOS columns 1, 9, 17, 25, 33).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0a7fh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0A7FH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine performs the ESC,"H" (HOME) operation for the <a href="#chput">CHPUT</a> standard routine control code processor, <a href="#csrx">CSRX</a> and <a href="#csry">CSRY</a> are simply set to 1,1. The ROM BIOS cursor coordinate system, while functionally identical to that used by the BASIC Interpreter, numbers the screen rows from 1 to 24 and the columns from 1 to 32/40.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0a81h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0A81H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine performs the CR operation for the <a href="#chput">CHPUT</a> standard routine control code processor, <a href="#csrx">CSRX</a> is simply set to 01H .</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0a85h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0A85H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine performs the ESC,"M" function for the <a href="#chput">CHPUT</a> standard routine control code processor. A CR operation is first performed to set the cursor column coordinate to the leftmost position. The number of rows from the current row to the bottom of the screen is then determined, if this is zero the current row is simply erased (<a href="#0aech">0AECH</a>). The row count is first used to scroll up the relevant section of <a href="#linttb">LINTTB</a>, the line termination table, by one byte. It is then used to scroll up the relevant section of the screen a row at a time. Starting at the row below the current row, each line is copied from the VDP Name Table into the <a href="#linwrk">LINWRK</a> buffer (<a href="#0baah">0BAAH</a>) then copied back to the Name Table one row higher (<a href="#0bc3h">0BC3H</a>). Finally the lowest row on the screen is erased (<a href="#0aech">0AECH</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0ab4h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0AB4H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine performs the ESC,"L" operation for the <a href="#chput">CHPUT</a> standard routine control code processor. A CR operation is first performed to set the cursor column coordinate to the leftmost position. The number of rows from the current row to the bottom of the screen is then determined, if this is zero the current row is simply erased (<a href="#0aech">0AECH</a>). The row count is first used to scroll down the relevant section of <a href="#linttb">LINTTB</a>, the line termination table, by one byte. It is then used to scroll down the relevant section of the screen a row at a time. Starting at the next to last row of the screen, each line is copied from the VDP Name Table into the <a href="#linwrk">LINWRK</a> buffer (<a href="#0baah">0BAAH</a>), then copied back to the Name Table one row lower (<a href="#0bc3h">0BC3H</a>). Finally the current row is erased (<a href="#0aech">0AECH</a>).</p>
<pre><code>Address... 0AE3H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used to perform the DEL operation for the <a href="#chput">CHPUT</a> standard routine control code processor. A LEFT operation is first performed. If this cannot be completed, because the cursor is already at the home position, then the routine terminates with no action. Otherwise a space is written to the VDP Name Table at the cursor's physical location (<a href="#0be6h">0BE6H</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0aech"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0AECH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine performs the ESC,"l" operation for the <a href="#chput">CHPUT</a> standard routine control code processor. The cursor column coordinate is set to 01H and control drops into the ESC,"K" routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0aeeh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0AEEH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine performs the ESC,"K" operation for the <a href="#chput">CHPUT</a> standard routine control code processor. The row's entry in <a href="#linttb">LINTTB</a>, the line termination table, is first made non-zero to indicate that the logical line is not extended (<a href="#0c29h">0C29H</a>). The cursor coordinates are converted to a physical address (0BF2H) in the VDP Name Table and the VDP set up for writes via the <a href="#setwrt">SETWRT</a> standard routine. Spaces are then written directly to the VDP <a href="#data_port">Data Port</a> until the rightmost column, determined by <a href="#linlen">LINLEN</a>, is reached.</p>
<pre><code>Address... 0B05H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine performs the ESC,"J" operation for the <a href="#chput">CHPUT</a> standard routine control code processor. An ESC,"K" operation is performed on successive rows, starting with the current one, until the bottom of the screen is reached.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0b15h"></a><a name="user-content-erafnk"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0B15H
Name...... ERAFNK
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, DE, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to turn the function key display off. <a href="#cnsdfg">CNSDFG</a> is first zeroed and, if the VDP is in <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> or <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a>, the routine terminates with no further action. If the VDP is in <a href="#40x24_text_mode">40x24 Text Mode</a> or <a href="#32x24_text_mode">32x24 Text Mode</a> the last row on the screen is then erased (<a href="#0aech">0AECH</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0b26h"></a><a name="user-content-fnksb"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0B26H
Name...... FNKSB
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, BC, DE, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to show the function key display if it is enabled. If <a href="#cnsdfg">CNSDFG</a> is zero the routine terminates with no action, otherwise control drops into the <a href="#dspfnk">DSPFNK</a> standard routine..</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0b2bh"></a><a name="user-content-dspfnk"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0B2BH
Name...... DSPFNK
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, BC, DE, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to turn the function key display on. <a href="#cnsdfg">CNSDFG</a> is set to FFH and, if the VDP is in <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> or <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a>, the routine terminates with no further action. Otherwise the cursor row coordinate is checked and, if the cursor is on the last row of the screen, a LF code (0AH) issued to the <a href="#outdo">OUTDO</a> standard routine to scroll the screen up.</p>
<p>Register pair HL is then set to point to either the unshifted or shifted function strings in the Workspace Area depending upon whether the SHIFT key is pressed. <a href="#linlen">LINLEN</a> has four subtracted, to allow a minimum of one space between fields, and is divided by five to determine the field size for each string. Successive characters are then taken from each function string, checked for graphic headers via the <a href="#cnvchr">CNVCHR</a> standard routine and placed in the <a href="#linwrk">LINWRK</a> buffer until the string is exhausted or the zone is filled. When all five strings are completed the <a href="#linwrk">LINWRK</a> buffer is written to the last row in the VDP Name Table (<a href="#0bc3h">0BC3H</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0b9ch"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0B9CH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the function key display related standard routines. The contents of register A are placed in <a href="#cnsdfg">CNSDFG</a> then <a href="#scrmod">SCRMOD</a> tested and Flag NC returned if the screen is in <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> or <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0ba5h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0BA5H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine copies eight bytes from the VDP VRAM into the <a href="#linwrk">LINWRK</a> buffer, the VRAM physical address is supplied in register pair HL.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0baah"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0BAAH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine copies a complete row of characters, with the length determined by <a href="#linlen">LINLEN</a>, from the VDP VRAM into the <a href="#linwrk">LINWRK</a> buffer. The cursor row coordinate is supplied in register L.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0bbeh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0BBEH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine copies eight bytes from the <a href="#linwrk">LINWRK</a> buffer into the VDP VRAM, the VRAM physical address is supplied in register pair HL.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0bc3h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0BC3H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine copies a complete row of characters, with the length determined by <a href="#linlen">LINLEN</a>, from the <a href="#linwrk">LINWRK</a> buffer into the VDP VRAM. The cursor row coordinate is supplied in register L.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0bd8h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0BD8H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine reads a single byte from the VDP VRAM into register C. The column coordinate is supplied in register H, the row coordinate in register L.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0be6h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0BE6H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine converts a pair of screen coordinates, the column in register H and the row in register L, into a physical address in the VDP Name Table. This address is returned in register pair HL.</p>
<p>The row coordinate is first multiplied by thirty-two or forty, depending upon the screen mode, and added to the column coordinate. This is then added to the Name Table base address, taken from <a href="#nambas">NAMBAS</a>, to produce an initial address.</p>
<p>Because of the variable screen width, as contained in <a href="#linlen">LINLEN</a>, an additional offset has to be added to the initial address to keep the active region roughly centered within the screen. The difference between the "true" number of characters per row, thirty-two or forty, and the current width is halved and then rounded up to produce the left hand offset. For a UK machine, with a thirty-seven character width in <a href="#40x24_text_mode">40x24 Text Mode</a>, this will result in two unused characters on the left hand side and one on the right. The statement <code>PRINT (41-WID)\2</code>, where <code>WID</code> is any screen width, will display the left hand column offset in <a href="#40x24_text_mode">40x24 Text Mode</a>.</p>
<p>A complete BASIC program which emulates this routine is given below:</p>
<pre><code>10 CPR=40:NAM=BASE(0):WID=PEEK(&amp;HF3AE)
20 SCRMD=PEEK(&amp;HFCAF):IF SCRMD=0 THEN 40
30 CPR=32:NAM=BASE(5):WID=PEEK(&amp;HF3AF)
40 LH=(CPR+1-WID)\2
50 ADDR=NAM+(ROW-1)*CPR+(COL-1)+LH
</code></pre>
<p>This program is designed for the <code>ROW</code> and <code>COL</code> coordinate system used by the ROM BIOS where home is 1,1. Line 50 may be simplified, by removing the "-1" factors, if the BASIC Interpreter's coordinate system is to be used.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0c1dh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0C1DH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine calculates the address of a row's entry in <a href="#linttb">LINTTB</a>, the line termination table. The row coordinate is supplied in register L and the address returned in register pair DE.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0c29h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0C29H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine makes a row's entry in <a href="#linttb">LINTTB</a> non-zero when entered at <a href="#0c29h">0C29H</a> and zero when entered at 0C2AH. The row coordinate is supplied in register L.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0c32h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0C32H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine returns the number of rows on the screen in register A. It will normally return twenty-four if the function key display is disabled and twenty-three if it is enabled. Note that the screen size is determined by <a href="#crtcnt">CRTCNT</a> and may be modified with a BASIC statement, <code>POKE &amp;HF3B1H,14:SCREEN 0</code> for example.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0c3ch"></a><a name="user-content-keyint"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0C3CH
Name...... KEYINT
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to process Z80 interrupts, these are generated by the VDP once every 20 ms on a UK machine. The <a href="#vdp_status_register">VDP Status Register</a> is first read and bit 7 checked to ensure that this is a frame rate interrupt, if not the routine terminates with no action. The contents of the <a href="#vdp_status_register">Status Register</a> are saved in <a href="#statfl">STATFL</a> and bit 5 checked for sprite coincidence. If the Coincidence Flag is active then the relevant entry in <a href="#trptbl">TRPTBL</a> is updated (<a href="#0ef1h">0EF1H</a>).</p>
