<p><a href="#intcnt">INTCNT</a>, the "<code>INTERVAL</code>" counter, is then decremented. If this has reached zero the relevant entry in <a href="#trptbl">TRPTBL</a> is updated (<a href="#0ef1h">0EF1H</a>) and the counter reset with the contents of <a href="#intval">INTVAL</a>.</p>
<p><a href="#jiffy">JIFFY</a>, the "<code>TIME</code>" counter, is then incremented. This counter just wraps around to zero when it overflows.</p>
<p><a href="#musicf">MUSICF</a> is examined to determine whether any of the three music queues generated by the "<code>PLAY</code>" statement are active. For each active queue the dequeueing routine (<a href="#113bh">113BH</a>) is called to fetch the next music packet and write it to the PSG.</p>
<p><a href="#scncnt">SCNCNT</a> is then decremented to determine if a joystick and keyboard scan is required, if not the interrupt handler terminates with no further action. This counter is used to increase throughput and to minimize keybounce problems by ensuring that a scan is only carried out every three interrupts. Assuming a scan is required joystick connector 1 is selected and the two Trigger bits read (<a href="#120ch">120CH</a>), followed by the two Trigger bits from joystick connector 2 (<a href="#120ch">120CH</a>) and the SPACE key from row 8 of the keyboard (<a href="#1226h">1226H</a>). These five inputs, which are all related to the "<code>STRIG</code>" statement, are combined into a single byte where 0=Pressed, 1=Not pressed:</p>
<p><a name="user-content-figure35"></a><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/27e75aaf7559c0cb3cb9e4f15585d8e4ff2b796d/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830344633352e737667"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/27e75aaf7559c0cb3cb9e4f15585d8e4ff2b796d/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830344633352e737667" alt="" data-canonical-src="https://rawgit.com/oraculo666/the-msx-red-book/master/images/CH04F35.svg" style="max-width:100%;"></a></p>
<p><strong>Figure 35:</strong> "<code>STRIG</code>" Inputs</p>
<p>This reading is compared with the previous one, held in <a href="#trgflg">TRGFLG</a>, to produce an active transition byte and <a href="#trgflg">TRGFLG</a> is updated with the new reading. The active transition byte is normally zero but contains a 1 in each position where a transition from unpressed to pressed has occurred. This active transition byte is shifted out bit by bit and the relevant entry in <a href="#trptbl">TRPTBL</a> updated (<a href="#0ef1h">0EF1H</a>) for each active device.</p>
<p>A complete scan of the keyboard matrix is then performed to identify new key depressions, any found are translated into key codes and placed in <a href="#keybuf">KEYBUF</a> (<a href="#0d12h">0D12H</a>). If <a href="#keybuf">KEYBUF</a> is found to be empty at the end of this process <a href="#repcnt">REPCNT</a> is decremented to see whether the auto-repeat delay has expired, if not the routine terminates. If the delay period has expired <a href="#repcnt">REPCNT</a> is reset with the fast repeat value (60 ms), the <a href="#oldkey">OLDKEY</a> keyboard map is reinitialized and the keyboard scanned again (0D4EH). Any keys which are continuously pressed will show up as new transitions during this scan. Note that keys will only auto-repeat while an application program keeps <a href="#keybuf">KEYBUF</a> empty by reading characters. The interrupt handler then terminates.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0d12h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0D12H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine performs a complete scan of all eleven rows of the keyboard matrix for the interrupt handler. Each of the eleven rows is read in via the PPI and placed in ascending order in <a href="#newkey">NEWKEY</a>. <a href="#enstop">ENSTOP</a> is then checked to see if warm starts are enabled. If its contents are non-zero and the keys CODE, GRAPH, CTRL and SHIFT are pressed control transfers to the BASIC Interpreter (409BH) via the <a href="#calbas">CALBAS</a> standard routine. This facility is useful as even a machine code program can be terminated as long as the interrupt handler is running. The contents of <a href="#newkey">NEWKEY</a> are compared with the previous scan contained in <a href="#oldkey">OLDKEY</a>. If any change at all has occurred <a href="#repcnt">REPCNT</a> is loaded with the initial auto-repeat delay (780 ms). Each row 1, reading from <a href="#newkey">NEWKEY</a> is then compared with the previous one, held in <a href="#oldkey">OLDKEY</a>, to produce an active transition byte and <a href="#oldkey">OLDKEY</a> is updated with the new reading. The active transition byte is normally zero but contains a 1 in each position where a transition from unpressed to pressed has occurred. If the row contains any transitions these are decoded and placed in <a href="#keybuf">KEYBUF</a> as key codes (<a href="#0d89h">0D89H</a>). When all eleven rows have been completed the routine checks whether there are any characters in <a href="#keybuf">KEYBUF</a>, by subtracting <a href="#getpnt">GETPNT</a> from <a href="#putpnt">PUTPNT</a>, and terminates.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0d6ah"></a><a name="user-content-chsns"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0D6AH
Name...... CHSNS
Entry..... None
Exit...... Flag NZ if characters in KEYBUF
Modifies.. AF, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to check if any keyboard characters are ready. If the screen is in <a href="#graphincsmode">Graphics Mode</a> or <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a> then <a href="#getpnt">GETPNT</a> is subtracted from <a href="#putpnt">PUTPNT</a> (0D62H) and the routine terminates. If the screen is in <a href="#40x24_text_mode">40x24 Text Mode</a> or <a href="#32x24_text_mode">32x24 Text Mode</a> the state of the SHIFT key is also examined and the function key display updated, via the <a href="#dspfnk">DSPFNK</a> standard routine, if it has changed.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0d89h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0D89H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine converts each active bit in a keyboard row transition byte into a key code. A bit is first converted into a key number determined by its position in the keyboard matrix:</p>
<p><a name="user-content-figure36"></a><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/7c4815efee516d629036ab938e4fe6c21985a284/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830344633362e737667"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/7c4815efee516d629036ab938e4fe6c21985a284/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830344633362e737667" alt="" data-canonical-src="https://rawgit.com/oraculo666/the-msx-red-book/master/images/CH04F36.svg" style="max-width:100%;"></a></p>
<p><strong>Figure 36:</strong> Key Numbers</p>
<p>The key number is then converted into a key code and placed in <a href="#keybuf">KEYBUF</a> (<a href="#1021h">1021H</a>). When all eight possible bits have been processed the routine terminates.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0da5h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0DA5H
</code></pre>
<p>This table contains the key codes of key numbers 00H to 2FH for various combinations of the control keys. A zero entry in the table means that no key code will be produced when that key is pressed:</p>
<pre><code>       37H  36H  35H  34H  33H  32H  31H  30H   Row  0
       3BH  5DH  5BH  5CH  3DH  2DH  39H  38H   Row  1
NORMAL 62H  61H  9CH  2FH  2EH  2CH  60H  27H   Row  2
       6AH  69H  68H  67H  66H  65H  64H  63H   Row  3
       72H  71H  70H  6FH  6EH  6DH  6CH  6BH   Row  4
       7AH  79H  78H  77H  76H  75H  74H  73H   Row  5

       26H  5EH  25H  24H  23H  40H  21H  29H   Row  0
       3AH  7DH  7BH  7CH  2BH  5FH  28H  2AH   Row  1
SHIFT  42H  41H  9CH  3FH  3EH  3CH  7EH  22H   Row  2
       4AH  49H  48H  47H  46H  45H  44H  43H   Row  3
       52H  51H  50H  4FH  4EH  4DH  4CH  4BH   Row  4
       5AH  59H  58H  57H  56H  55H  54H  53H   Row  5

       FBH  F4H  BDH  EFH  BAH  ABH  ACH  09H   Row  0
       06H  0DH  01H  1EH  F1H  17H  07H  ECH   Row  1
GRAPH  11H  C4H  9CH  1DH  F2H  F3H  BBH  05H   Row  2
       C6H  DCH  13H  15H  14H  CDH  C7H  BCH   Row  3
       18H  CCH  DBH  C2H  1BH  0BH  C8H  DDH   Row  4
       0FH  19H  1CH  CFH  1AH  C0H  12H  D2H   Row  5

       00H  F5H  00H  00H  FCH  FDH  00H  0AH   Row  0
       04H  0EH  02H  16H  F0H  1FH  08H  00H   Row  1
SHIFT  00H  FEH  9CH  F6H  AFH  AEH  F7H  03H   Row  2
GRAPH  CAH  DFH  D6H  10H  D4H  CEH  C1H  FAH   Row  3
       A9H  CBH  D7H  C3H  D3H  0CH  C9H  DEH   Row  4
       F8H  AAH  F9H  D0H  D5H  C5H  00H  D1H   Row  5

       E1H  E0H  98H  9BH  BFH  D9H  9FH  EBH   Row  0
       B7H  DAH  EDH  9CH  E9H  EEH  87H  E7H   Row  1
CODE   97H  84H  9CH  A7H  A6H  86H  E5H  B9H   Row  2
       91H  A1H  B1H  81H  94H  8CH  8BH  8DH   Row  3
       93H  83H  A3H  A2H  A4H  E6H  B5H  B3H   Row  4
       85H  A0H  8AH  88H  95H  82H  96H  89H   Row  5

       00H  00H  9DH  9CH  BEH  9EH  ADH  D8H   Row  0
       B6H  EAH  E8H  00H  00H  00H  80H  E2H   Row  1
SHIFT  00H  8EH  9CH  A8H  00H  8FH  E4H  B8H   Row  2
CODE   92H  00H  B0H  9AH  99H  00H  00H  00H   Row  3
       00H  00H  E3H  00H  A5H  00H  B4H  B2H   Row  4
       00H  00H  00H  00H  00H  90H  00H  00H   Row  5

        7    6    5    4    3    2    1    0    Column
</code></pre>

<p><a name="user-content-0ec5h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0EC5H
</code></pre>
<p>Control transfers to this routine, from <a href="#0fc3h">0FC3H</a>, to complete decoding of the five function keys. The relevant entry in <a href="#fnkflg">FNKFLG</a> is first checked to determine whether the key is associated with an "<code>ON KEY GOSUB</code>" statement. If so, and provided that <a href="#curlin">CURLIN</a> shows the BASIC Interpreter to be in program mode, the relevant entry in <a href="#trptbl">TRPTBL</a> is updated (<a href="#0ef1h">0EF1H</a>) and the routine terminates. If the key is not tied to an "<code>ON KEY GOSUB</code>" statement, or if the Interpreter is in direct mode, the string of characters associated with the function key is returned instead. The key number is multiplied by sixteen, as each string is sixteen characters long, and added to the starting address of the function key strings in the Workspace Area. Sequential characters are then taken from the string and placed in <a href="#keybuf">KEYBUF</a> (<a href="#0f55h">0F55H</a>) until the zero byte terminator is reached.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0ef1h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0EF1H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used to update a device's entry in <a href="#trptbl">TRPTBL</a> when it has produced a BASIC program interrupt. On entry register pair HL points to the device's status byte in the table. Bit 0 of the status byte is checked first, if the device is not "<code>ON</code>" then the routine terminates with no action. Bit 2, the event flag, is then checked. If this is already set then the routine terminates, otherwise it is set to indicate that an event has occurred. Bit 1, the "<code>STOP</code>" flag, is then checked. If the device is stopped then the routine terminates with no further action. Otherwise <a href="#ongsbf">ONGSBF</a> is incremented to signal to the Interpreter Runloop that the event should now be processed.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0f06h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0F06H
</code></pre>
<p>This section of the key decoder processes the HOME key only. The state of the SHIFT key is determined via row 6 of <a href="#newkey">NEWKEY</a> and the key code for HOME (0BH) or CLS (0CH) placed in <a href="#keybuf">KEYBUF</a> (<a href="#0f55h">0F55H</a>) accordingly.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0f10h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0F10H
</code></pre>
<p>This section of the keyboard decoder processes key numbers 30H to 57H apart from the CAP, F1 to F5, STOP and HOME keys. The key number is simply used to look up the key code in the table at <a href="#1033h">1033H</a> and this is then placed in <a href="#keybuf">KEYBUF</a> (<a href="#0f55h">0F55H</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0f1fh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0F1FH
</code></pre>
<p>This section of the keyboard decoder processes the DEAD key found on European MSX machines. On UK machines the key in row 2, column 5 always generates the pound key code (9CH) shown in the table at 0DA5H. On European machines this table will have the key code FFH in the same locations. This key code only serves as a flag to indicate that the next key pressed, if it is a vowel, should be modified to produce an accented graphics character.</p>
<p>The state of the SHIFT and CODE keys is determined via row 6 of <a href="#newkey">NEWKEY</a> and one of the following placed in <a href="#kanast">KANAST</a>: 01H=DEAD, 02H=DEAD+SHIFT, 03H=DEAD+CODE, 04H=DEAD+SHIFT+CODE.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0f36h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0F36H
</code></pre>
<p>This section of the keyboard decoder processes the CAP key. The current state of <a href="#capst">CAPST</a> is inverted and control drops into the <a href="#chgcap">CHGCAP</a> standard routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0f3dh"></a><a name="user-content-chgcap"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0F3DH
Name...... CHGCAP
Entry..... A=ON/OFF Switch
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to turn the Caps Lock LED on or off as determined by the contents of register A: 00H=On, NZ=Off. The LED is modified using the bit set/reset facility of the PPI Mode Port. As <a href="#capst">CAPST</a> is not changed this routine does not affect the characters produced by the keyboard.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0f46h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0F46H
</code></pre>
<p>This section of the keyboard decoder processes the STOP key. The state of the CTRL key is determined via row 6 of <a href="#newkey">NEWKEY</a> and the key code for STOP (04H) or CTRL/STOP (03H) produced as appropriate. If the CTRL/STOP code is produced it is copied to <a href="#intflg">INTFLG</a>, for use by the <a href="#iscntc">ISCNTC</a> standard routine, and then placed in <a href="#keybuf">KEYBUF</a> (<a href="#0f55h">0F55H</a>). If the STOP code is produced it is also copied to <a href="#intflg">INTFLG</a> but is not placed in <a href="#keybuf">KEYBUF</a>, instead only a click is generated (0F64H). This means that an application program cannot read the STOP key code via the ROM BIOS standard routines.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0f55h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0F55H
</code></pre>
<p>This section of the keyboard decoder places a key code in <a href="#keybuf">KEYBUF</a> and generates an audible click. The correct address in the keyboard buffer is first taken from <a href="#putpnt">PUTPNT</a> and the code placed there. The address is then incremented (<a href="#105bh">105BH</a>). If it has wrapped round and caught up with <a href="#getpnt">GETPNT</a> then the routine terminates with no further action as the keyboard buffer is full. Otherwise <a href="#putpnt">PUTPNT</a> is updated with the new address.</p>
<p><a href="#cliksw">CLIKSW</a> and <a href="#clikfl">CLIKFL</a> are then both checked to determine whether a click is required. <a href="#cliksw">CLIKSW</a> is a general enable/disable switch while <a href="#clikfl">CLIKFL</a> is used to prevent multiple clicks when the function keys are pressed. Assuming a click is required the Key Click output is set via the <a href="#ppi_mode_port">PPI Mode Port</a> and, after a delay of 50 µs, control drops into the <a href="#chgsnd">CHGSND</a> standard routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0f7ah"></a><a name="user-content-chgsnd"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0F7AH
Name...... CHGSND
Entry..... A=ON/OFF Switch
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to set or reset the Key Click output via the <a href="#ppi_mode_port">PPI Mode Port</a>: 00H=Reset, NZ=Set. This audio output is AC coupled so absolute polarities should not be taken too seriously.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0f83h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0F83H
</code></pre>
<p>This section of the keyboard decoder processes key numbers 00H to 2FH. The state of the SHIFT, GRAPH and CODE keys is determined via row 6 of <a href="#newkey">NEWKEY</a> and combined with the key number to form a look-up address into the table at <a href="#0da5h">0DA5H</a>. The key code is then taken from the table. If it is zero the routine terminates with no further action, if it is FFH control transfers to the DEAD key processor (<a href="#0f1fh">0F1FH</a>). If the code is in the range 40H to 5FH or 60H to 7FH and the CTRL key is pressed then the corresponding control code is placed in <a href="#keybuf">KEYBUF</a> (<a href="#0f55h">0F55H</a>). If the code is in the range 01H to 1FH then a graphic header code (01H) is first placed in <a href="#keybuf">KEYBUF</a> (<a href="#0f55h">0F55H</a>) followed by the code with 40H added. If the code is in the range 61H to 7BH and <a href="#capst">CAPST</a> indicates that caps lock is on then it is converted to upper case by subtracting 20H. Assuming that <a href="#kanast">KANAST</a> contains zero, as it always will on UK machines, then the key code is placed in <a href="#keybuf">KEYBUF</a> (<a href="#0f55h">0F55H</a>) and the routine terminates. On European MSX machines, with a DEAD key instead of a pound key, then the key codes corresponding to the vowels a, e, i, o, u may be further modified into graphics codes.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-0fc3h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 0FC3H
</code></pre>
<p>This section of the keyboard decoder processes the five function keys. The state of the SHIFT key is examined via row 6 of <a href="#newkey">NEWKEY</a> and five added to the key number if it is pressed. Control then transfers to <a href="#0ec5h">0EC5H</a> to complete processing.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-1021h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 1021H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine searches the table at <a href="#1b97h">1B97H</a> to determine which group of keys the key number supplied in register C belongs to. The associated address is then taken from the table and control transferred to that section of the keyboard decoder. Note that the table itself is actually patched into the middle of the <a href="#outdo">OUTDO</a> standard routine as a result of the modifications made to the Japanese ROM.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-1033h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 1033H
</code></pre>
<p>This table contains the key codes of key numbers 30H to 57H other than the special keys CAP, F1 to F5, STOP and HOME. A zero entry in the table means that no key code will be produced when that key is pressed:</p>
<pre><code>00H 00H 00H 00H 00H 00H 00H 00H Row 6
0DH 18H 08H 00H 09H 1BH 00H 00H Row 7
1CH 1FH 1EH 1DH 7FH 12H 0CH 20H Row 8
34H 33H 32H 31H 30H 00H 00H 00H Row 9
2EH 2CH 2DH 39H 38H 37H 36H 35H Row 10

 7   6   5   4   3   2   1   0  Column
</code></pre>

<p><a name="user-content-105bh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 105BH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine simply zeroes <a href="#kanast">KANAST</a> and then transfers control to <a href="#10c2h">10C2H</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-1061h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 1061H
</code></pre>
<p>This table contains the graphics characters which replace the vowels a, e, i, o, u on European machines.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-10c2h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 10C2H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine increments the keyboard buffer pointer, either <a href="#putpnt">PUTPNT</a> or <a href="#getpnt">GETPNT</a>, supplied in register pair HL. If the pointer then exceeds the end of the keyboard buffer it is wrapped back to the beginning.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-10cbh"></a><a name="user-content-chget"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 10CBH
Name...... CHGET
Entry..... None
Exit...... A=Character from keyboard
Modifies.. AF, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to fetch a character from the keyboard buffer. The buffer is first checked to see if already contains a character (<a href="#0d6ah">0D6AH</a>). If not the cursor is turned on (<a href="#09dah">09DAH</a>), the buffer checked repeatedly until a character appears (<a href="#0d6ah">0D6AH</a>) and then the cursor turned off (<a href="#0a27h">0A27H</a>). The character is taken from the buffer using <a href="#getpnt">GETPNT</a> which is then incremented (<a href="#10c2h">10C2H</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-10f9h"></a><a name="user-content-ckcntc"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 10F9H
Name...... CKCNTC
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to check whether the CTRL-STOP or STOP keys have been pressed. It is used by the BASIC Interpreter inside processor-intensive statements, such as "<code>WAIT</code>" and "<code>CIRCLE</code>", to check for program termination. Register pair HL is first zeroed and then control transferred to the <a href="#iscntc">ISCNTC</a> standard routine. When the Interpreter is running register pair HL normally contains the address of the current character in the BASIC program text. If <a href="#iscntc">ISCNTC</a> is CTRL-STOP terminated this address will be placed in <a href="#oldtxt">OLDTXT</a> by the "<code>STOP</code>" statement handler (63E6H) for use by a later "<code>CONT</code>" statement. Zeroing register pair HL beforehand signals to the "<code>CONT</code>" handler that termination occurred inside a statement and it will issue a "<code>Can't CONTINUE</code>" error if continuation is attempted.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-1102h"></a><a name="user-content-wrtpsg"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 1102H
Name...... WRTPSG
Entry..... A=Register number, E=Data byte
Exit...... None
Modifies.. EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to write a data byte to any of the sixteen <a href="#registers_0_and_1">PSG registers</a>. The register selection number is written to the PSG <a href="#address_port">Address Port</a> and the data byte written to the PSG <a href="#data_write_port">Data Write Port</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-110eh"></a><a name="user-content-rdpsg"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 110EH
Name...... RDPSG
Entry..... A=Register number
Exit...... A=Data byte read from PSG
Modifies.. A
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to read a data byte from any of the sixteen <a href="#registers_0_and_1">PSG registers</a>. The register selection number is written to the PSG <a href="#address_port">Address Port</a> and the data byte read from the PSG <a href="#data_read_port">Data Read Port</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-1113h"></a><a name="user-content-beep"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 1113H
Name...... BEEP
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, BC, E, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to produce a beep via the PSG. Channel A is set to produce a tone of 1316Hz then enabled with an amplitude of seven. After a delay of 40 ms control transfers to the <a href="#gicini">GICINI</a> standard routine to reinitialize the PSG.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-113bh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 113BH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the interrupt handler to service a music queue. As there are three of these, each feeding a PSG channel, the queue to be serviced is specified by supplying its number in register A: 0=<a href="#voicaq">VOICAQ</a>, 1=<a href="#voicbq">VOICBQ</a> and 2=<a href="#voiccq">VOICCQ</a>.</p>
<p>Each string in a "<code>PLAY</code>" statement is translated into a series of data packets by the BASIC Interpreter. These are placed in the appropriate queue followed by an end of data byte (FFH). The task of dequeueing the packets, decoding them and setting the PSG is left to the interrupt handler. The Interpreter is thus free to proceed immediately to the next statement without having to wait for notes to finish.</p>
<p>The first two bytes of any packet specify its byte count and duration. The three most significant bits of the first byte specify the number of bytes following the header in the packet. The remainder of the header specifies the event duration in 20 ms units. This duration count determines how long it will be before the next packet is read from the queue.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-figure37"></a><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/6e39bd6768ba4e6f2bb3e2d1bb38df4925663ad7/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830344633372e737667"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/6e39bd6768ba4e6f2bb3e2d1bb38df4925663ad7/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830344633372e737667" alt="" data-canonical-src="https://rawgit.com/oraculo666/the-msx-red-book/master/images/CH04F37.svg" style="max-width:100%;"></a></p>
<p><strong>Figure 37:</strong> Packet Header</p>
<p>The packet header may be followed by zero or more blocks, in any order, containing frequency or amplitude information:</p>
<p><a name="user-content-figure38"></a><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/a5d6b08e7c8f3107d65973c4e4d518c844ac33ef/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830344633382e737667"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/a5d6b08e7c8f3107d65973c4e4d518c844ac33ef/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830344633382e737667" alt="" data-canonical-src="https://rawgit.com/oraculo666/the-msx-red-book/master/images/CH04F38.svg" style="max-width:100%;"></a></p>
<p><strong>Figure 38:</strong> Packet Block Types</p>
<p>The routine first locates the current duration counter in the relevant voice buffer (<a href="#vcba">VCBA</a>, <a href="#vcbb">VCBB</a> or <a href="#vcbc">VCBC</a>) via the <a href="#getvcp">GETVCP</a> standard routine and decrements it. If the counter has reached zero then the next packet must be read from the queue, otherwise the routine terminates.</p>
<p>The queue number is placed in <a href="#queuen">QUEUEN</a> and a byte read from the queue (<a href="#11e2h">11E2H</a>). This is then checked to see if it is the end of data mark (FFH), if so the queue terminates (<a href="#11b0h">11B0H</a>). Otherwise the byte count is placed in register C and the duration MSB in the relevant voice buffer. The second byte is read (<a href="#11e2h">11E2H</a>) and the duration LSB placed in the relevant voice buffer. The byte count is then examined, if there are no bytes to follow the packet header the routine terminates. Otherwise successive bytes are read from the queue, and the appropriate action taken, until the byte count is exhausted.</p>
<p>If a frequency block is found then a second byte is read and both bytes written to PSG Registers <a href="#registers_0_and_1">0</a> and <a href="#registers_0_and_1">1</a>, <a href="#registers_2_and_3">2</a> and <a href="#registers_2_and_3">3</a> or <a href="#registers_4_and_5">4</a> and <a href="#registers_4_and_5">5</a> depending on the queue number.</p>
<p>If an amplitude block is found the Amplitude and Mode bits are written to PSG Registers <a href="#register_8">8</a>, <a href="#register_9">9</a> or <a href="#register_10">10</a> depending on the queue number. If the Mode bit is 1, selecting modulated rather than fixed amplitude, then the byte is also written to PSG <a href="#register_13">Register 13</a> to set the envelope shape.</p>
<p>If an envelope block is found, or if bit 6 of an amplitude block is set, then a further two bytes are read from the queue and written to PSG Registers <a href="#registers_11_and_12">11</a> and <a href="#registers_11_and_12">12</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-11b0h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 11B0H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used when an end of data mark (FFH) is found in one of the three music queues. An amplitude value of zero is written to PSG Register <a href="#register_8">8</a> <a href="#register_9">9</a> or <a href="#register_10">10</a>, depending on the queue number, to shut the channel down. The channel's bit in <a href="#musicf">MUSICF</a> is then reset and control drops into the <a href="#strtms">STRTMS</a> standard routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-11c4h"></a><a name="user-content-strtms"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 11C4H
Name...... STRTMS
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, HL
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine used by the "<code>PLAY</code>" statement handler to initiate music dequeueing by the interrupt handler. <a href="#musicf">MUSICF</a> is first examined, if any channels are already running the routine terminates with no action. <a href="#plycnt">PLYCNT</a> is then decremented, if there are no more "<code>PLAY</code>" strings queued up the routine terminates. Otherwise the three duration counters, in <a href="#vcba">VCBA</a>, <a href="#vcbb">VCBB</a> and <a href="#vcbc">VCBC</a>, are set to 0001H, so that the first packet of the new group will be dequeued at the next interrupt, and <a href="#musicf">MUSICF</a> is set to 07H to enable all three channels.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-11e2h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 11E2H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine loads register A with the current queue number, from <a href="#queuen">QUEUEN</a>, and then reads a byte from that queue (<a href="#14adh">14ADH</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-11eeh"></a><a name="user-content-gtstck"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 11EEH
Name...... GTSTCK
Entry..... A=Joystick ID (0, 1 or 2)
Exit...... A=Joystick position code
Modifies.. AF, B, DE, HL, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to read the position of a joystick or the four cursor keys. If the supplied ID is zero the state of the cursor keys is read via <a href="/gseidler/The-MSX-Red-Book/blob/master/ppi_port_b">PPI Port B</a> (<a href="#1226h">1226H</a>) and converted to a position code using the look-up table at 1243H. Otherwise joystick connector 1 or 2 is read (<a href="#120ch">120CH</a>) and the four direction bits converted to a position code using the look-up table at 1233H. The returned position codes are:</p>
<p><a name="user-content-figure39a"></a><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/1477369f5671b74a3923b34aaffe7a1412fc1d42/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f43483034463339612e737667"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/1477369f5671b74a3923b34aaffe7a1412fc1d42/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f43483034463339612e737667" alt="" data-canonical-src="https://rawgit.com/oraculo666/the-msx-red-book/master/images/CH04F39a.svg" style="max-width:100%;"></a></p>
<p><a name="user-content-120ch"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 120CH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine reads the joystick connector specified by the contents of register A: 0=Connector 1, 1=Connector 2. The current contents of PSG <a href="#register_15">Register 15</a> are read in then written back with the Joystick Select bit appropriately set. PSG <a href="#register_14">Register 14</a> is then read into register A (110CH) and the routine terminates.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-1226h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 1226H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine reads row 8 of the keyboard matrix. The current contents of <a href="/gseidler/The-MSX-Red-Book/blob/master/ppi_port_c">PPI Port C</a> are read in then written back with the four Keyboard Row Select bits set for row 8. The column inputs are then read into register A from <a href="/gseidler/The-MSX-Red-Book/blob/master/ppi_port_b">PPI Port B</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-1253h"></a><a name="user-content-gttrig"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 1253H
Name...... GTTRIG
Entry..... A=Trigger ID (0, 1, 2, 3 or 4)
Exit...... A=Status code
Modifies.. AF, BC, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to check the joystick trigger or space key status. If the supplied ID is zero row 8 of the keyboard matrix is read (<a href="#1226h">1226H</a>) and converted to a status code. Otherwise joystick connector 1 or 2 is read (<a href="#120ch">120CH</a>) and converted to a status code. The selection IDs are:</p>
<pre><code>0=SPACE KEY
1=JOY 1, TRIGGER A
2=JOY 2, TRIGGER A
3=JOY 1, TRIGGER B
4=JOY 2, TRIGGER B
</code></pre>
<p>The value returned is FFH if the relevant trigger is pressed and zero otherwise.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-1273h"></a><a name="user-content-gtpdl"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 1273H
Name...... GTPDL
Entry..... A=Paddle ID (1 to 12)
Exit...... A=Paddle value (0 to 255)
Modifies.. AF, BC, DE, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to read the value of any paddle attached to a joystick connector. Each of the six input lines (four direction plus two triggers) per connector can support a paddle so twelve are possible altogether. The paddles attached to joystick connector 1 have entry identifiers 1, 3, 5, 7, 9 and 11. Those attached to joystick connector 2 have entry identifiers 2, 4, 6, 8, 10 and 12. Each paddle is basically a one-shot pulse generator, the length of the pulse being controlled by a variable resistor. A start pulse is issued to the specified joystick connector via PSG <a href="#register_15">Register 15</a>. A count is then kept of how many times PSG <a href="#register_14">Register 14</a> has to be read until the relevant input times out. Each unit increment represents an approximate period of 12 µs on an MSX machine with one wait state.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-12ach"></a><a name="user-content-gtpad"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 12ACH
Name...... GTPAD
Entry..... A=Function code (0 to 7)
Exit...... A=Status or value
Modifies.. AF, BC, DE, HL, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to access a touchpad attached to either of the joystick connectors. Available functions codes for joystick connector 1 are:</p>
<pre><code>0=Return Activity Status
1=Return "X" coordinate
2=Return "Y" coordinate
3=Return Switch Status
</code></pre>
<p>Function codes 4 to 7 have the same effect with respect to joystick connector 2. The Activity Status function returns FFH if the Touchpad is being touched and zero otherwise. The Switch Status function returns FFH if the switch is being pressed and zero otherwise. The two coordinate request functions return the coordinates of the last location touched. These coordinates are actually stored in the Workspace Area variables <a href="#padx">PADX</a> and <a href="#pady">PADY</a> when a call with function code 0 or 4 detects activity. Note that these variables are shared by both joystick connectors.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-1384h"></a><a name="user-content-stmotr"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 1384H
Name...... STMOTR
Entry..... A=Motor ON/OFF code
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to turn the cassette motor relay on or off via <a href="/gseidler/The-MSX-Red-Book/blob/master/ppi_port_c">PPI Port C</a>: 00H=Off, 01H=On, FFH=Reverse current state.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-1398h"></a><a name="user-content-nmi"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 1398H
Name...... NMI
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. None
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to process a Z80 Non Maskable Interrupt, simply returns on a standard MSX machine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-139dh"></a><a name="user-content-inifnk"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 139DH
Name...... INIFNK
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. BC, DE, HL
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to initialize the ten function key strings to their power-up values. The one hundred and sixty bytes of data commencing at <a href="#13a9h">13A9H</a> are copied to the <a href="#fnkstr">FNKSTR</a> buffer in the Workspace Area.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-13a9h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 13A9H
</code></pre>
<p>This area contains the power-up strings for the ten function keys. Each string is sixteen characters long, unused positions contain zeroes:</p>
<pre><code>F1 to F5  F6 to F10
color     color 15,4,4 CR
auto      cload"
goto      cont CR
list      list. CR UP UP
run CR    run CLS CR
</code></pre>
<p><a name="user-content-1449h"></a><a name="user-content-rdvdp"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 1449H
Name...... RDVDP
Entry..... None
Exit...... A=VDP Status Register contents
Modifies.. A
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to input the contents of the <a href="#vdp_status_register">VDP Status Register</a> by reading the <a href="#command_port">Command Port</a>. Note that reading the <a href="#vdp_status_register">VDP Status Register</a> will clear the associated flags and may affect the interrupt handler.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-144ch"></a><a name="user-content-rslreg"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 144CH
Name...... RSLREG
Entry..... None
Exit...... A=Primary Slot Register contents
Modifies.. A
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to input the contents of the Primary slot Register by reading <a href="/gseidler/The-MSX-Red-Book/blob/master/ppi_port_a">PPI Port A</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-144fh"></a><a name="user-content-wslreg"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 144FH
Name...... WSLREG
Entry..... A=Value to write
Exit...... None
Modifies.. None
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to set the Primary Slot Register by writing to <a href="/gseidler/The-MSX-Red-Book/blob/master/ppi_port_a">PPI Port A</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-1452h"></a><a name="user-content-snsmat"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 1452H
Name...... SNSMAT
Entry..... A=Keyboard row number
Exit...... A=Column data of keyboard row
Modifies.. AF, C, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to read a complete row of the keyboard matrix. <a href="/gseidler/The-MSX-Red-Book/blob/master/ppi_port_c">PPI Port C</a> is read in then written back with the row number occupying the four Keyboard Row Select bits. <a href="/gseidler/The-MSX-Red-Book/blob/master/ppi_port_b">PPI Port B</a> is then read into register A to return the eight column inputs. The four miscellaneous control outputs of <a href="/gseidler/The-MSX-Red-Book/blob/master/ppi_port_c">PPI Port C</a> are unaffected by this routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-145fh"></a><a name="user-content-isflio"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 145FH
Name...... ISFLIO
Entry..... None
Exit...... Flag NZ if file I/O active
Modifies.. AF
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to check whether the BASIC Interpreter is currently directing its input or output via an I/O buffer. This is determined by examining <a href="#ptrfil">PTRFIL</a>. It is normally zero but will contain a buffer FCB (File Control Block) address while statements such as "<code>PRINT#1</code>", "<code>INPUT#1</code>", etc. are being executed by the Interpreter.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-146ah"></a><a name="user-content-dcompr"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 146AH
Name...... DCOMPR
Entry..... HL, DE
Exit...... Flag NC if HL&gt;DE, Flag Z if HL=DE, Flag C if HL&lt;DE
Modifies.. AF
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine used by the BASIC Interpreter to check the relative values of register pairs HL and DE.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-1470h"></a><a name="user-content-getvcp"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 1470H
Name...... GETVCP
Entry..... A=Voice number (0, 1, 2)
Exit...... HL=Address in voice buffer
Modifies.. AF, HL
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to return the address of byte 2 in the specified voice buffer (<a href="#vcba">VCBA</a>, <a href="#vcbb">VCBB</a> or <a href="#vcbc">VCBC</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-1474h"></a><a name="user-content-getvc2"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 1474H
Name...... GETVC2
Entry..... L=Byte number (0 to 36)
Exit...... HL=Address in voice buffer
Modifies.. AF, HL
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to return the address of any byte in the voice buffer (<a href="#vcba">VCBA</a>, <a href="#vcbb">VCBB</a> or <a href="#vcbc">VCBC</a>) specified by the voice number in <a href="#voicen">VOICEN</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-148ah"></a><a name="user-content-phydio"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 148AH
Name...... PHYDIO
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. None
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine for use by Disk BASIC, simply returns on standard MSX machines.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-148eh"></a><a name="user-content-format"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 148EH
Name...... FORMAT
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. None
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine for use by Disk BASIC, simply returns on standard MSX machines.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-1492h"></a><a name="user-content-putq"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 1492H
Name...... PUTQ
Entry..... A=Queue number, E=Data byte
Exit...... Flag Z if queue full
Modifies.. AF, BC, HL
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to place a data byte in one of the three music queues. The queue's get and put positions are first taken from <a href="#quetab">QUETAB</a> (<a href="#14fah">14FAH</a>). The put position is temporarily incremented and compared with the get position, if they are equal the routine terminates as the queue is full. Otherwise the queue's address is taken from <a href="#quetab">QUETAB</a> and the put position added to it. The data byte is placed at this location in the queue, the put position is incremented and the routine terminates. Note that the music queues are circular, if the get or put pointers reach the last position in the queue they wrap around back to the start.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-14adh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 14ADH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the interrupt handler to read a byte from one of the three music queues. The queue number is supplied in register A, the data byte is returned in register A and the routine returns Flag Z if the queue is empty. The queue's get and put positions are first taken from <a href="#quetab">QUETAB</a> (<a href="#14fah">14FAH</a>). If the putback flag is active then the data byte is taken from <a href="#quebak">QUEBAK</a> and the routine terminates (14D1H), this facility is unused in the current versions of the MSX ROM. The put position is then compared with the get position, if they are equal the routine terminates as the queue is empty. Otherwise the queue's address is taken from <a href="#quetab">QUETAB</a> and the get position added to it. The data byte is read from this location in the queue, the get position is incremented and the routine terminates.</p>
<pre><code>Address... 14DAH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the <a href="#gicini">GICINI</a> standard routine to initialize a queue's control block in <a href="#quetab">QUETAB</a>. The control block is first located in <a href="#quetab">QUETAB</a> (<a href="#1504h">1504H</a>) and the put, get and putback bytes zeroed. The size byte is set from register B and the queue address from register pair DE.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-14ebh"></a><a name="user-content-lftq"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 14EBH
Name...... LFTQ
Entry..... A=Queue number
Exit...... HL=Free space left in queue
Modifies.. AF, BC, HL
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to return the number of free bytes left in a music queue. The queue's get and put positions are taken from <a href="#quetab">QUETAB</a> (<a href="#14fah">14FAH</a>) and the free space determined by subtracting put from get.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-14fah"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 14FAH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine returns a queue's control parameters from <a href="#quetab">QUETAB</a>, the queue number is supplied in register A. The control block is first located in <a href="#quetab">QUETAB</a> (<a href="#1504h">1504H</a>), the put position is then placed in register B, the get position in register C and the putback flag in register A.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-1504h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 1504H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine locates a queue's control block in <a href="#quetab">QUETAB</a>. The queue number is supplied in register A and the control block address returned in register pair HL. The queue number is simply multiplied by six, as there are six bytes per block, and added to the address of <a href="#quetab">QUETAB</a> as held in <a href="#queues">QUEUES</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-1510h"></a><a name="user-content-grpprt"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 1510H
Name...... GRPPRT
Entry..... A=Character
Exit...... None
Modifies.. EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to display a character on the screen in either <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> or <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a>, it is functionally equivalent to the <a href="#chput">CHPUT</a> standard routine.</p>
<p>The <a href="#cnvchr">CNVCHR</a> standard routine is first used to check for a graphic character, if the character is a header code (01H) then the routine terminates with no action. If the character is a converted graphic one then the control code decoding section is skipped. Otherwise the character is checked to see if it is a control code. Only the CR code (0DH) is recognized (<a href="#157eh">157EH</a>), all other characters smaller than 20H are ignored.</p>
<p>Assuming the character is displayable its eight byte pixel pattern is copied from the ROM character set into the <a href="#patwrk">PATWRK</a> buffer (0752H) and <a href="#forclr">FORCLR</a> copied to <a href="#atrbyt">ATRBYT</a> to set its colour. The current graphics coordinates are then taken from <a href="#grpacx">GRPACX</a> and <a href="#grpacy">GRPACY</a> and used to set the current pixel physical address via the <a href="#scalxy">SCALXY</a> and <a href="#mapxyc">MAPXYC</a> standard routines.</p>
<p>The eight byte pattern in <a href="#patwrk">PATWRK</a> is processed a byte at a time. At the start of each byte the current pixel physical address is obtained via the <a href="#fetchc">FETCHC</a> standard routine and saved. The eight bits are then examined in turn. If the bit is a 1 the associated pixel is set by the <a href="#setc">SETC</a> standard routine, if it is a 0 no action is taken. After each bit the current pixel physical address is moved right (<a href="#16ach">16ACH</a>). When the byte is finished, or the right hand edge of the screen is reached, the initial current pixel physical address is restored and moved down one position by the <a href="#tdownc">TDOWNC</a> standard routine.</p>
<p>When the pattern is complete, or the bottom of the screen has been reached, <a href="#grpacx">GRPACX</a> is updated. In <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> its value is increased by eight, in <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a> by thirty-two. If <a href="#grpacx">GRPACX</a> then exceeds 255, the right hand edge of the screen, a CR operation is performed (<a href="#157eh">157EH</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-157eh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 157EH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine performs the CR operation for the <a href="#grpprt">GRPPRT</a> standard routine, this code functions as a combined CR,LF. <a href="#grpacx">GRPACX</a> is zeroed and eight or thirty-two, depending on the screen mode, added to <a href="#grpacy">GRPACY</a>. If <a href="#grpacy">GRPACY</a> then exceeds 191, the bottom of the screen, it is set to zero.</p>
<p><a href="#grpacx">GRPACX</a> and <a href="#grpacy">GRPACY</a> may be manipulated directly by an application program to compensate for the limited number of control functions available.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-1599h"></a><a name="user-content-scalxy"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 1599H
Name...... SCALXY
Entry..... BC=X coordinate, DE=Y coordinate
Exit...... Flag NC if clipped
Modifies.. AF
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to clip a pair of graphics coordinates if necessary. The BASIC Interpreter can produce coordinates in the range -32768 to +32767 even though this far exceeds the actual screen size. This routine modifies excessive coordinate values to fit within the physically realizable range. If the X coordinate is greater than 255 it is set to 255, if the Y coordinate is greater than 191 it is set to 191. If either coordinate is negative (greater than 7FFFH) it is set to zero. Finally if the screen is in <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a> both coordinates are divided by four as required by the <a href="#mapxyc">MAPXYC</a> standard routine.</p>
<pre><code>Address... 15D9H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used to check the current screen mode, it returns Flag Z if the screen is in <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-15dfh"></a><a name="user-content-mapxyc"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 15DFH
Name...... MAPXYC
Entry..... BC=X coordinate, DE=Y coordinate
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, D, HL
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to convert a graphics coordinate pair into the current pixel physical address. The location in the Character Pattern Table of the byte containing the pixel is placed in <a href="#cloc">CLOC</a>. The bit mask identifying the pixel within that byte is placed in <a href="#cmask">CMASK</a>. Slightly different conversion methods are used for <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> and <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a>, equivalent programs in BASIC are:</p>
<pre><code>Graphics Mode

10 INPUT"X,Y Coordinates";X,Y
20 A=(Y\8)*256+(Y AND 7)+(X AND &amp;HF8)
30 PRINT"ADDR=";HEX$(Base(12)+A);"H ";
40 RESTORE 100
50 FOR N=0 TO (X AND 7):READ M$: NEXT N
60 PRINT"MASK=";M$
70 GOTO 10
100 DATA 10000000
110 DATA 01000000
120 DATA 00100000
130 DATA 00010000
140 DATA 00001000
150 DATA 00000100
160 DATA 00000010
170 DATA 00000001
</code></pre>

<pre><code>Multicolour Mode

10 INPUT"X,Y Coordinates";X,Y
20 X=X\4:Y-Y\4
30 A=(Y\8)*256+(Y AND 7)+(X*4 AND &amp;HF8)
40 PRINT"ADDR=";HEX$(BASE(17)+A);"H ";
50 IF X MOD 2=0 THEN MS="11110000" ELSE MS="00001111"
60 PRINT"MASK=";M$
70 GOTO 10
</code></pre>
<p>The allowable input range for both programs is X=0 to 255 and Y=0 to 191. The data statements in the <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> program correspond to the eight byte mask table commencing at 160BH in the MSX ROM. Line 20 in the <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a> program actually corresponds to the division by four in the <a href="#scalxy">SCALXY</a> standard routine. It is included to make the coordinate system consistent for both programs.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-1639h"></a><a name="user-content-fetchc"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 1639H
Name...... FETCHC
Entry..... None
Exit...... A=CMASK, HL=CLOC
Modifies.. A, HL
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to return the current pixel physical address, register pair HL is loaded from <a href="#cloc">CLOC</a> and register A from <a href="#cmask">CMASK</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-1640h"></a><a name="user-content-storec"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 1640H
Name...... STOREC
Entry..... A=CMASK, HL=CLOC
Exit...... None
Modifies.. None
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to set the current pixel physical address, register pair HL is copied to <a href="#cloc">CLOC</a> and register A is copied to <a href="#cmask">CMASK</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-1647h"></a><a name="user-content-readc"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 1647H
Name...... READC
Entry..... None
Exit...... A=Colour code of current pixel
Modifies.. AF, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to return the colour of the current pixel. The VRAM physical address is first obtained via the <a href="#fetchc">FETCHC</a> standard routine. If the screen is in <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> the byte pointed to by <a href="#cloc">CLOC</a> is read from the Character Pattern Table via the <a href="#rdvrm">RDVRM</a> standard routine. The required bit is then isolated by <a href="#cmask">CMASK</a> and used to select either the upper or lower four bits of the corresponding entry in the Colour Table.</p>
<p>If the screen is in <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a> the byte pointed to by <a href="#cloc">CLOC</a> is read from the Character Pattern Table via the <a href="#rdvrm">RDVRM</a> standard routine. <a href="#cmask">CMASK</a> is then used to select either the upper or lower four bits of this byte. The value returned in either case will be a normal VDP colour code from zero to fifteen.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-1676h"></a><a name="user-content-setatr"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 1676H
Name...... SETATR
Entry..... A=Colour code
Exit...... Flag C if illegal code
Modifies.. Flags
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to set the graphics ink colour used by the <a href="#setc">SETC</a> and <a href="#nsetcx">NSETCX</a> standard routines. The colour code, from zero to fifteen, is simply placed in <a href="#atrbyt">ATRBYT</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-167eh"></a><a name="user-content-setc"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 167EH
Name...... SETC
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to set the current pixel to any colour, the colour code is taken from <a href="#atrbyt">ATRBYT</a>. The pixel's VRAM physical address is first obtained via the <a href="#fetchc">FETCHC</a> standard routine. In <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> both the Character Pattern Table and Colour Table are then modified (<a href="#186ch">186CH</a>).</p>
<p>In <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a> the byte pointed to by <a href="#cloc">CLOC</a> is read from the Character Pattern Table by the <a href="#rdvrm">RDVRM</a> standard routine. The contents of <a href="#atrbyt">ATRBYT</a> are then placed in the upper or lower four bits, as determined by <a href="#cmask">CMASK</a>, and the byte written back via the <a href="#wrtvrm">WRTVRM</a> standard routine</p>
<p><a name="user-content-16ach"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 16ACH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine moves the current pixel physical address one position right. If the right hand edge of the screen is exceeded it returns with Flag C and the physical address is unchanged. In <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> <a href="#cmask">CMASK</a> is first shifted one bit right, if the pixel still remains within the byte the routine terminates. If <a href="#cloc">CLOC</a> is at the rightmost character cell (LSB=F8H to FFH) then the routine terminates with Flag C (175AH). Otherwise <a href="#cmask">CMASK</a> is set to 80H, the leftmost pixel, and 0008H added to <a href="#cloc">CLOC</a>.</p>
<p>In <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a> control transfers to a separate routine (<a href="#1779h">1779H</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-16c5h"></a><a name="user-content-rightc"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 16C5H
Name...... RIGHTC
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to move the current pixel physical address one position right. In <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> <a href="#cmask">CMASK</a> is first shifted one bit right, if the pixel still remains within the byte the routine terminates. Otherwise <a href="#cmask">CMASK</a> is set to 80H, the leftmost pixel, and 0008H added to <a href="#cloc">CLOC</a>. Note that incorrect addresses will be produced if the right hand edge of the screen is exceeded.</p>
<p>In <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a> control transfers to a separate routine (<a href="#178bh">178BH</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-16d8h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 16D8H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine moves the current pixel physical address one position left. If the left hand edge of the screen is exceeded it returns Flag C and the physical address is unchanged. In <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> <a href="#cmask">CMASK</a> is first shifted one bit left, if the pixel still remains within the byte the routine terminates. If <a href="#cloc">CLOC</a> is at the leftmost character cell (LSB=00H to 07H) then the routine terminates with Flag C (175AH). Otherwise <a href="#cmask">CMASK</a> is set to 01H, the rightmost pixel, and 0008H subtracted from <a href="#cloc">CLOC</a>.</p>
<p>In <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a> control transfers to a separate routine (<a href="#179ch">179CH</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-16eeh"></a><a name="user-content-leftc"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 16EEH
Name...... LEFTC
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to move the current pixel physical address one position left. In <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> <a href="#cmask">CMASK</a> is first shifted one bit left, if the pixel still remains within the byte the routine terminates. Otherwise <a href="#cmask">CMASK</a> is set to 01H, the leftmost pixel, and 0008H subtracted from <a href="#cloc">CLOC</a>. Note that incorrect addresses will be produced if the left hand edge of the screen is exceeded.</p>
<p>In <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a> control transfers to a separate routine (<a href="#17ach">17ACH</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-170ah"></a><a name="user-content-tdownc"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 170AH
Name...... TDOWNC
Entry..... None
Exit...... Flag C if off screen
Modifies.. AF
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to move the current pixel physical address one position down. If the bottom edge of the screen is exceeded it returns Flag C and the physical address is unchanged. In <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> <a href="#cloc">CLOC</a> is first incremented, if it still remains within an eight byte boundary the routine terminates. If <a href="#cloc">CLOC</a> was in the bottom character row (<a href="#cloc">CLOC</a>&gt;=1700H) then the routine terminates with Flag C (1759H). Otherwise 00F8H is added to <a href="#cloc">CLOC</a>.</p>
<p>In <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a> control transfers to a separate routine (<a href="#17c6h">17C6H</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-172ah"></a><a name="user-content-downc"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 172AH
Name...... DOWNC
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to move the current pixel physical address one position down. In <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> <a href="#cloc">CLOC</a> is first incremented, if it still remains within an eight byte boundary the routine terminates. Otherwise 00F8H is added to <a href="#cloc">CLOC</a>. Note that incorrect addresses will be produced if the bottom edge of the screen is exceeded.</p>
<p>In <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a> control transfers to a separate routine (<a href="#17dch">17DCH</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-173ch"></a><a name="user-content-tupc"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 173CH
Name...... TUPC
Entry..... None
Exit...... Flag C if off screen
Modifies.. AF
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to move the current pixel physical address one position up. If the top edge of the screen is exceeded it returns with Flag C and the physical address is unchanged. In <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> <a href="#cloc">CLOC</a> is first decremented, if it still remains within an eight byte boundary the routine terminates. If <a href="#cloc">CLOC</a> was in the top character row (<a href="#cloc">CLOC</a>&lt;0100H) then the routine terminates with Flag C. Otherwise 00F8H is subtracted from <a href="#cloc">CLOC</a>.</p>
<p>In <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a> control transfers to a separate routine (<a href="#17e3h">17E3H</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-175dh"></a><a name="user-content-upc"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 175DH
Name...... UPC
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to move the current pixel physical address one position up. In <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> <a href="#cloc">CLOC</a> is first decremented, if it still remains within an eight byte boundary the routine terminates. Otherwise 00F8H is subtracted from <a href="#cloc">CLOC</a>. Note that incorrect addresses will be produced if the top edge of the screen is exceeded.</p>
<p>In <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a> control transfers to a separate routine (<a href="#17f8h">17F8H</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-1779h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 1779H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a> version of the routine at <a href="#16ach">16ACH</a>. It is identical to the <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> version except that <a href="#cmask">CMASK</a> is shifted four bit positions right and becomes F0H if a cell boundary is crossed.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-178bh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 178BH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a> version of the <a href="#rightc">RIGHTC</a> standard routine. It is identical to the <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> version except that <a href="#cmask">CMASK</a> is shifted four bit positions right and becomes F0H if a cell boundary is crossed.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-179ch"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 179CH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a> version of the routine at <a href="#16d8h">16D8H</a>. It is identical to the <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> version except that <a href="#cmask">CMASK</a> is shifted four bit positions left and becomes 0FH if a cell boundary is crossed.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-17ach"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 17ACH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a> version of the <a href="#leftc">LEFTC</a> standard routine. It is identical to the <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> version except that <a href="#cmask">CMASK</a> is shifted four bit positions left and becomes 0FH if a cell boundary is crossed.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-17c6h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 17C6H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a> version of the <a href="#tdownc">TDOWNC</a> standard routine. It is identical to the <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> version except that the bottom boundary address is 0500H instead of 1700H. There is a bug in this routine which will cause it to behave unpredictably if <a href="#mltcgp">MLTCGP</a>, the Character Pattern Table base address, is changed from its normal value of zero. There should be an <code>EX DE,HL</code> instruction inserted at address 17CEH.</p>
<p>If the Character Pattern Table base is increased the routine will think it has reached the bottom of the screen when it actually has not. This routine is used by the "<code>PAINT</code>" statement so the following demonstrates the fault:</p>
<pre><code>10 BASE(17)=&amp;H1000
20 SCREEN 3
30 PSET(200,0)
40 DRAW"D180L100U180R100"
50 PAINT(150,90)
60 GOTO 60
</code></pre>

<p><a name="user-content-17dch"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 17DCH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a> version of the <a href="#downc">DOWNC</a> standard routine, it is identical to the <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> version.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-17e3h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 17E3H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a> version of the <a href="#tupc">TUPC</a> standard routine. It is identical to the <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> version except that is has a bug as above, this time there should be an <code>EX DE,HL</code> instruction at address 17EBH.</p>
<p>If the Character Pattern Table base address is increased the routine will think it is within the table when it has actually exceeded the top edge of the screen. This may be demonstrated by removing the "<code>R100</code>" part of Line 40 in the previous program.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-17f8h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 17F8H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a> version of the <a href="#upc">UPC</a> standard routine, it is identical to the <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> version.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-1809h"></a><a name="user-content-nsetcx"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 1809H
Name...... NSETCX
Entry..... HL=Pixel fill count
Exit...... None
Modifies.. AF, BC, DE, HL, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to set the colour of multiple pixels horizontally rightwards from the current pixel physical address. Although its function can be duplicated by the <a href="#setc">SETC</a> and <a href="#rightc">RIGHTC</a> standard routines this would result in significantly slower operation. The supplied pixel count should be chosen so that the right-hand edge of the screen is not passed as this will produce anomalous behaviour. The current pixel physical address is unchanged by this routine.</p>
<p>In <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> <a href="#cmask">CMASK</a> is first examined to determine the number of pixels to the right within the current character cell. Assuming the fill count is large enough these are then set (<a href="#186ch">186CH</a>). The remaining fill count is divided by eight to determine the number of whole character cells. Successive bytes in the Character Pattern Table are then zeroed and the corresponding bytes in the Colour Table set from <a href="#atrbyt">ATRBYT</a> to fill these whole cells. The remaining fill count is then converted to a bit mask, using the seven byte table at 185DH, and these pixels are set (<a href="#186ch">186CH</a>).</p>
<p>In <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a> control transfers to a separate routine (<a href="#18bbh">18BBH</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-186ch"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 186CH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine sets up to eight pixels within a cell to a specified colour in <a href="#graphicsmod">Graphics Mode</a>. <a href="#atrbyt">ATRBYT</a> contains the colour code, register pair HL the address of the relevant byte in the Character Pattern Table and register A a bit mask, 11100000 for example, where every 1 specifies a bit to be set.</p>
<p>If <a href="#atrbyt">ATRBYT</a> matches the existing 1 pixel colour in the corresponding Colour Table byte then each specified bit is set to 1 in the Character Pattern Table byte. If <a href="#atrbyt">ATRBYT</a> matches the existing 0 pixel colour in the corresponding Colour Table byte then each specified bit is set to 0 in the Character Pattern Table byte.</p>
<p>If <a href="#atrbyt">ATRBYT</a> does not match either of the existing colours in the Colour Table Byte then normally each specified bit is set to 1 in the Character Pattern Table byte and the 1 pixel colour changed in the Colour Table byte. However if this would result in all bits being set to 1 in the Character Pattern Table byte then each specified bit is set to 0 and the 0 pixel colour changed in the Colour Table byte.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-18bbh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 18BBH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a> version of the <a href="#nsetcx">NSETCX</a> standard routine. The <a href="#setc">SETC</a> and <a href="#rightc">RIGHTC</a> standard routines are called until the fill count is exhausted. Speed of operation is not so important in <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a> because of the lower screen resolution and the consequent reduction in the number of operations required.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-18c7h"></a><a name="user-content-gtaspc"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 18C7H
Name...... GTASPC
Entry..... None
Exit...... DE=ASPCT1, HL=ASPCT2
Modifies.. DE, HL
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to return the "<code>CIRCLE</code>" statement default aspect ratios.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-18cfh"></a><a name="user-content-pntini"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 18CFH
Name...... PNTINI
Entry..... A=Boundary colour (0 to 15)
Exit...... Flag C if illegal colour
Modifies.. AF
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to set the boundary colour for the "<code>PAINT</code>" statement. In <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a> the supplied colour code is placed in <a href="#bdratr">BDRATR</a>. In <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> <a href="#bdratr">BDRATR</a> is copied from <a href="#atrbyt">ATRBYT</a> as it is not possible to have separate paint and boundary colours.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-18e4h"></a><a name="user-content-scanr"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 18E4H
Name...... SCANR
Entry..... B=Fill switch, DE=Skip count
Exit...... DE=Skip remainder, HL=Pixel count
Modifies.. AF, BC, DE, HL, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine used by the "<code>PAINT</code>" statement handler to search rightwards from the current pixel physical address until a colour code equal to <a href="#bdratr">BDRATR</a> is found or the edge of the screen is reached. The terminating position becomes the current pixel physical address and the initial position is returned in <a href="#csavea">CSAVEA</a> and <a href="#csavem">CSAVEM</a>. The size of the traversed region is returned in register pair HL and <a href="#filnam">FILNAM</a>+1. The traversed region is normally filled in but this can be inhibited, in <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> only, by using an entry parameter of zero in register B. The skip count in register pair DE determines the maximum number of pixels of the required colour that may be ignored from the initial starting position. This facility is used by the "<code>PAINT</code>" statement handler to search for gaps in a horizontal boundary blocking its upward progress.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-197ah"></a><a name="user-content-scanl"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 197AH
Name...... SCANL
Entry..... None
Exit...... HL=Pixel count
Modifies.. AF, BC, DE, HL, EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to search leftwards from the current pixel physical address until a colour code equal to <a href="#bdratr">BDRATR</a> is found or the edge of the screen is reached. The terminating position becomes the current pixel physical address and the size of the traversed region is returned in register pair HL. The traversed region is always filled in.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-19c7h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 19C7H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the <a href="#scanl">SCANL</a> and <a href="#scanr">SCANR</a> standard routines to check the current pixel's colour against the boundary colour in <a href="#bdratr">BDRATR</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-19ddh"></a><a name="user-content-tapoof"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 19DDH
Name...... TAPOOF
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to stop the cassette motor after data has been written to the cassette. After a delay of 550 ms, on MSX machines with one wait state, control drops into the <a href="#tapiof">TAPIOF</a> standard routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-19e9h"></a><a name="user-content-tapiof"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 19E9H
Name...... TAPIOF
Entry..... None
Exit...... None
Modifies.. EI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to stop the cassette motor after data has been read from the cassette. The motor relay is opened via the <a href="#ppi_mode_port">PPI Mode Port</a>. Note that interrupts, which must be disabled during cassette data transfers for timing reasons, are enabled as this routine terminates.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-19f1h"></a><a name="user-content-tapoon"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 19F1H
Name...... TAPOON
Entry..... A=Header length switch
Exit...... Flag C if CTRL-STOP termination
Modifies.. AF, BC, HL, DI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to turn the cassette motor on, wait 550 ms for the tape to come up to speed and then write a header to the cassette. A header is a burst of HI cycles written in front of every data block so the baud rate can be determined when the data is read back.</p>
<p>The length of the header is determined by the contents of register A: 00H=Short header, NZ=Long header. The BASIC cassette statements "<code>SAVE</code>", "<code>CSAVE</code>" and "<code>BSAVE</code>" all generate a long header at the start of the file, in front of the identification block, and thereafter use short headers between data blocks. The number of cycles in the header is also modified by the current baud rate so as to keep its duration constant:</p>
<pre><code>1200 Baud SHORT ... 3840 Cycles ... 1.5 Seconds
1200 Baud LONG ... 15360 Cycles ... 6.1 Seconds
2400 Baud SHORT ... 7936 Cycles ... 1.6 Seconds
2400 Baud LONG ... 31744 Cycles ... 6.3 Seconds
</code></pre>
<p>After the motor has been turned on and the delay has expired the contents of <a href="#header">HEADER</a> are multiplied by two hundred and fifty-six and, if register A is non-zero, by a further factor of four to produce the cycle count. HI cycles are then generated (<a href="#1a4dh">1A4DH</a>) until the count is exhausted whereupon control transfers to the <a href="#breakx">BREAKX</a> standard routine. Because the CTRL-STOP key is only examined at termination it is impossible to break out part way through this routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-1a19h"></a><a name="user-content-tapout"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 1A19H
Name...... TAPOUT
Entry..... A=Data byte
Exit...... Flag C if CTRL-STOP termination
Modifies.. AF, B, HL
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to write a single byte of data to the cassette. The MSX ROM uses a software driven FSK (Frequency Shift Keyed) method for storing information on the cassette. At the 1200 baud rate this is identical to the Kansas City Standard used by the BBC for the distribution of BASICODE programs.</p>
<p>At 1200 baud each 0 bit is written as one complete 1200 Hz LO cycle and each 1 bit as two complete 2400 Hz HI cycles. The data rate is thus constant as 0 and 1 bits have the same duration. When the 2400 baud rate is selected the two frequencies change to 2400 Hz and 4800 Hz but the format is otherwise unchanged.</p>
<p>A byte of data is written with a 0 start bit (<a href="#1a50h">1A50H</a>), eight data bits with the least significant bit first, and two 1 stop bits (<a href="#1a40h">1A40H</a>). At the 1200 baud rate a single byte will have a nominal duration of 11 x 833 µs = 9.2 ms. After the stop bits have been written control transfers to the <a href="#breakx">BREAKX</a> standard routine to check the CTRL-STOP key. The byte 43H is shown below as it would be written to cassette:</p>
<p><a name="user-content-figure39b"></a><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/294a5ad578c25ddae20a935bc505bf85bffda975/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f43483034463339622e737667"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/294a5ad578c25ddae20a935bc505bf85bffda975/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f43483034463339622e737667" alt="" data-canonical-src="https://rawgit.com/oraculo666/the-msx-red-book/master/images/CH04F39b.svg" style="max-width:100%;"></a></p>
<p><strong>Figure 39:</strong> Cassette Data Byte</p>
<p>It is important not to leave too long an interval between bytes when writing data as this will increase the error rate. An inter-byte gap of 80 µs, for example, produces a read failure rate of approximately twelve percent. If a substantial amount of processing is required between each byte then buffering should be used to lump data into headered blocks. The BASIC "<code>SAVE</code>" format is of this type.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-1a39h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 1A39H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine writes a single LO cycle with a length of approximately 816 µs to the cassette. The length of each half of the cycle is taken from <a href="#low">LOW</a> and control transfers to the general cycle generator (<a href="#1a50h">1A50H</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-1a40h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 1A40H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine writes two HI cycles to the cassette. The first cycle is generated (<a href="#1a4dh">1A4DH</a>) followed by a 17 µs delay and then the second cycle (<a href="#1a4dh">1A4DH</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-1a4dh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 1A4DH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine writes a single HI cycle with a length of approximately 396 µs to the cassette. The length of each half of the cycle is taken from <a href="#high">HIGH</a> and control drops into the general cycle generator.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-1a50h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 1A50H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine writes a single cycle to the cassette. The length of the cycle's first half is supplied in register L and its second half in register H. The first length is counted down and then the Cas Out bit set via the <a href="#ppi_mode_port">PPI Mode Port</a>. The second length is counted down and the Cas Out bit reset.</p>
<p>On all MSX machines the Z80 runs at a clock frequency of 3.579545 MHz (280 ns) with one wait state during the M1 cycle. As this routine counts every 16T states each unit increment in the length count represents a period of 4.47 µs. There is also a fixed overhead of 20.7 µs associated with the routine whatever the length count.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-1a63h"></a><a name="user-content-tapion"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 1A63H
Name...... TAPION
Entry..... None
Exit...... Flag C if CTRL-STOP termination
Modifies.. AF, BC, DE, HL, DI
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to turn the cassette motor on, read the cassette until a header is found and then determine the baud rate. Successive cycles are read from the cassette and the length of each one measured (<a href="#1b34h">1B34H</a>). When 1,111 cycles have been found with less than 35 µs variation in their lengths a header has been located.</p>
<p>The next 256 cycles are then read (<a href="#1b34h">1B34H</a>) and averaged to determine the cassette HI cycle length. This figure is multiplied by 1.5 and placed in <a href="#lowlim">LOWLIM</a> where it defines the minimum acceptable length of a 0 start bit. The HI cycle length is placed in <a href="#winwid">WINWID</a> and will be used to discriminate between LO and HI cycles.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-1abch"></a><a name="user-content-tapin"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 1ABCH
Name...... TAPIN
Entry..... None
Exit...... A=Byte read, Flag C if CTRL-STOP or I/O error
Modifies.. AF, BC, DE, L
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to read a byte of data from the cassette. The cassette is first read continuously until a start bit is found. This is done by locating a negative transition, measuring the following cycle length (<a href="#1b1fh">1B1FH</a>) and comparing this to see if it is greater than <a href="#lowlim">LOWLIM</a>.</p>
<p>Each of the eight data bits is then read by counting the number of transitions within a fixed period of time (<a href="#1b03h">1B03H</a>). If zero or one transitions are found it is a 0 bit, if two or three are found it is a 1 bit. If more than three transitions are found the routine terminates with Flag C as this is presumed to be a hardware error of some sort. After the value of each bit has been determined a further one or two transitions are read (1B23H) to retain synchronization. With an odd transition count one more will be read, with an even transition count two more.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-1b03h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 1B03H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the <a href="#tapin">TAPIN</a> standard routine to count the number of cassette transitions within a fixed period of time. The window duration is contained in <a href="#winwid">WINWID</a> and is approximately 1.5 times the length of a HI cycle as shown below:</p>
