<p>This twenty-one byte table is used by the Interpreter during program tokenization. It contains the ten single character keywords and their tokens:</p>
<pre><code>+ ... F1H    * ... F3H   ^ ... F5H    ' ... E6H = ... EFH
- ... F2H    / ... F4H   \ ... FCH    &gt; ... EEH &lt; ... F0H
</code></pre>

<p><a name="user-content-3d3bh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 3D3BH
</code></pre>
<p>This table is used by the Expression Evaluator to determine the precedence level for a given infix operator, the higher the table value the greater the operator's precedence. Not included are the precedences for the relational operators (64H), the "<code>NOT</code>" operator (5AH) and the negation operator (7DH), these are defined directly by the Expression and Factor Evaluators.</p>
<pre><code>79H ... +       46H ... OR
79H ... -       3CH ... XOR
7CH ... *       32H ... EQV
7CH ... /       28H ... IMP
7FH ... ^       7AH ... MOD
50H ... AND     7BH ... \
</code></pre>

<p><a name="user-content-3d47h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 3D47H
</code></pre>
<p>This table is used to convert the result of a user defined function to the same type as the Variable used in the function definition. It contains the addresses of the type conversion routines:</p>
<pre><code>303AH ... CDBL
0000H ... Not used
2F8AH ... CINT
3058H ... Check string type
2FB2H ... CSNG
</code></pre>

<p><a name="user-content-3d51h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 3D51H
</code></pre>
<p>This table of addresses is used by the Expression Evaluator to find the handler for a particular infix math operator when both operands are double precision:</p>
<pre><code>269AH ... +
268CH ... -
27E6H ... *
289FH ... /
37D7H ... ^
2F83H ... Relation
</code></pre>

<p><a name="user-content-3d5dh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 3D5DH
</code></pre>
<p>This table of addresses is used by the Expression Evaluator to find the handler for a particular infix math operator when both operands are single precision:</p>
<pre><code>324EH ... +
3257H ... -
325CH ... *
3267H ... /
37C8H ... ^
2F21H ... Relation
</code></pre>

<p><a name="user-content-3d69h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 3D69H
</code></pre>
<p>This table of addresses is used by the Expression Evaluator to find the handler for a particular infix math operator when both operands are integer:</p>
<pre><code>3172H ... +
3167H ... -
3193H ... *
4DB8H ... /
383FH ... ^
2F4DH ... Relation
</code></pre>

<p><a name="user-content-3d75h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 3D75H
</code></pre>
<p>This table contains the Interpreter error messages, each one is stored in plain text with a zero byte terminator. The associated error codes are shown below for reference only, they do not form part of the table:</p>
<pre><code>01 NEXT without FOR             19 Device I/O error
02 Syntax error                 20 Verify error
03 RETURN without GOSUB         21 No RESUME
04 Out of DATA                  22 RESUME without error
05 Illegal function call        23 Unprintable error
06 Overflow                     24 Missing operand
07 Out of memory                25 Line buffer overflow
08 Undefined line number        50 FIELD overflow
09 Subscript out of range       51 Internal error
10 Redimensioned array          52 Bad file number
11 Division by zero             53 File not found
12 Illegal direct               54 File already open
13 Type mismatch                55 Input past end
14 Out of string space          56 Bad file name
15 String too long              57 Direct statement in file
16 String formula too complex   58 Sequential I/O only
17 Can't CONTINUE               59 File not OPEN
18 Undefined user function
</code></pre>

<p><a name="user-content-3fd2h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 3FD2H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the plain text message "<code>in</code>" terminated by a zero byte.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-3fd7h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 3FD7H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the plain text message "<code>Ok</code>", CR, LF terminated by a zero byte.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-3fdch"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 3FDCH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the plain text message "<code>Break</code>" terminated by a zero byte.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-3fe2h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 3FE2H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine searches the Z80 stack for the "<code>FOR</code>" loop parameter block whose loop Variable address is supplied in register pair DE. The search is started four bytes above the current Z80 SP to allow for the caller's return address and the Runloop return address. If no "<code>FOR</code>" token (82H) exists the routine terminates Flag NZ, if one is found the loop Variable address is taken from the parameter block and checked. The routine terminates Flag Z upon a successful match with register pair HL pointing to the type byte of the parameter block. Otherwise the search moves up twenty-two bytes to the start of the next parameter block.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4001h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4001H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>INP</code>" function to an operand contained in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. The port number is checked (<a href="#5439h">5439H</a>), the port read and the result placed in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> as an integer (4FCFH).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-400bh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 400BH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine first evaluates an operand in the range -32768 to +65535 (<a href="#542fh">542FH</a>) and places it in register pair BC. After checking for a comma, via the <a href="#synchr">SYNCHR</a> standard routine, it evaluates a second operand in the range 0 to 255 (521CH) and places this in register A.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4016h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4016H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>OUT</code>" statement handler. The port number and data byte are evaluated (<a href="#400bh">400BH</a>) and the data byte written to the relevant Z80 port.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-401ch"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 401CH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>WAIT</code>" statement handler. The port number and "<code>AND</code>" operands are first evaluated (<a href="#400bh">400BH</a>) followed by the optional "<code>XOR</code>" operand (521CH). The port is then repeatedly read and the operands applied, XOR then AND, until a non-zero result is obtained. Contrary to the information given in some MSX manuals the loop can be broken by the CTRL-STOP key as the <a href="#ckcntc">CKCNTC</a> standard routine is called from inside it.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4039h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4039H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Runloop when it encounters the end of the program text while in program mode. <a href="#oneflag">ONEFLAG</a> is checked to see whether it still contains an active error code. If so a "<code>No RESUME</code>" error is generated, otherwise program termination continues normally (6401H). The idea behind this routine is to catch any "<code>ON ERROR</code>" handlers without a "<code>RESUME</code>" statement at the end.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-404fh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 404FH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the "<code>READ</code>" statement handler when an error is found in a "<code>DATA</code>" statement. The line number contained in <a href="#datlin">DATLIN</a> is copied to <a href="#curlin">CURLIN</a> so the error handler will flag the "<code>DATA</code>" line as the illegal statement rather than the program line. Control then drops into the "<code>Syntax error</code>" generator.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4055h"></a>
<a name="user-content-4058h"></a>
<a name="user-content-405bh"></a>
<a name="user-content-405eh"></a>
<a name="user-content-4061h"></a>
<a name="user-content-4064h"></a>
<a name="user-content-4067h"></a>
<a name="user-content-406ah"></a>
<a name="user-content-406dh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4055H
</code></pre>
<p>This is a group of nine error generators, register E is loaded with the relevant error code and control drops into the error handler:</p>
<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>ADDRESS</th>
<th>ERROR</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>4055H</td>
<td>Syntax error</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>4058H</td>
<td>Division by zero</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>405BH</td>
<td>NEXT without FOR</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>405EH</td>
<td>Redimensioned array</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>4061H</td>
<td>Undefined user function</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>4064H</td>
<td>RESUME without error</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>4067H</td>
<td>Overflow error</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>406AH</td>
<td>Missing operand</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>406DH</td>
<td>Type mismatch</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<p><a name="user-content-406fh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 406FH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the Interpreter error handler, all error generators transfer to here with an error code in register E. <a href="#vlzadr">VLZADR</a> is first checked to see if the "<code>VAL</code>" statement handler has changed the program text, if so the original character is restored from <a href="#vlzdat">VLZDAT</a>. The current line number is then copied from <a href="#curlin">CURLIN</a> to <a href="#errlin">ERRLIN</a> and <a href="#dot">DOT</a> and the Z80 stack is restored from <a href="#savstk">SAVSTK</a> (62F0H). The error code is placed in <a href="#errflg">ERRFLG</a>, for use by the "<code>ERR</code>" function, and the current program text position copied from <a href="#savtxt">SAVTXT</a> to <a href="#errtxt">ERRTXT</a> for use by the "<code>RESUME</code>" statement handler. The error line number and program text position are also copied to <a href="#oldlin">OLDLIN</a> and <a href="#oldtxt">OLDTXT</a> for use by the "<code>CONT</code>" statement handler. <a href="#onelin">ONELIN</a> is then checked to see if a previous "<code>ON ERROR</code>" statement has been executed. If so, and providing no error code is already active, control transfers to the Runloop (4620H) to execute the BASIC error recovery statements.</p>
<p>Otherwise the error code is used to count through the error message table at <a href="#3d75h">3D75H</a> until the required one is reached. A CR,LF is issued (<a href="#7323h">7323H</a>) and the screen forced back to text mode via the <a href="#totext">TOTEXT</a> standard routine. A BELL code is then issued and the error message displayed (<a href="#6678h">6678H</a>). Assuming the Interpreter is in program mode, rather than direct mode, this is followed by the line number (<a href="#340ah">340AH</a>) and control drops into the "<code>OK</code>" point.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-411fh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 411FH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the re-entry point to the Interpreter Mainloop for a terminating program. The screen is forced to text mode via the <a href="#totext">TOTEXT</a> standard routine, the printer is cleared (<a href="#7304h">7304H</a>) and I/O buffer 0 closed (6D7BH). A CR,LF is then issued to the screen (<a href="#7323h">7323H</a>), the message "<code>OK</code>" is displayed (<a href="#6678h">6678H</a>) and control drops into the Mainloop.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4134h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4134H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the Interpreter Mainloop. <a href="#curlin">CURLIN</a> is first set to FFFFH to indicate direct mode and <a href="#autflg">AUTFLG</a> checked to see if "<code>AUTO</code>" mode is on. If so the next line number is taken from <a href="#autlin">AUTLIN</a> and displayed (<a href="#3412h">3412H</a>). The Program Text Area is then searched to see if this line already exists (<a href="#4295h">4295H</a>) and either an asterisk or space displayed accordingly.</p>
<p>The <a href="#isflio">ISFLIO</a> standard routine is then used to determine whether a "<code>LOAD</code>" statement is active. If so the program line is collected from the cassette (<a href="#7374h">7374H</a>), otherwise it is taken from the console via the <a href="#pinlin">PINLIN</a> standard routine. If the line is empty or the CTRL-STOP key has been pressed control transfers back to the start of the Mainloop (<a href="#4134h">4134H</a>) with no further action. If the line commences with a line number this is converted to an unsigned integer in register pair DE (4769H). The line is then converted to tokenized form and placed in <a href="#kbuf">KBUF</a> (<a href="#42b2h">42B2H</a>). If no line number was found at the start of the line control then transfers to the Runloop (<a href="#6d48h">6D48H</a>) to execute the statement.</p>
<p>Assuming the line commences with a line number it is tested to see if it is otherwise empty and the result temporarily saved. The line number is copied to <a href="#dot">DOT</a> and <a href="#autlin">AUTLIN</a> increased by the contents of <a href="#autinc">AUTINC</a>, if <a href="#autlin">AUTLIN</a> now exceeds 65530 the "<code>AUTO</code>" mode is turned off. The Program Text Area is then searched (<a href="#4295h">4295H</a>) to find a matching line number or, failing this, the position of the next highest line number. If no matching line number is found and the line is empty and "<code>AUTO</code>" mode is off an "<code>Undefined line number</code>" error is generated (<a href="#481ch">481CH</a>). If a matching line number is found and the line is empty and "<code>AUTO</code>" mode is on the Mainloop simply skips to the next statement (4237H).</p>
<p>Otherwise any pointers in the Program Text Area are converted back to line numbers (54EAH) and any existing program line deleted (5405H). Assuming the new program line is non-empty the Program Text Area is opened up by the required amount (<a href="#6250h">6250H</a>) and the tokenized program line copied from <a href="#kbuf">KBUF</a>.</p>
<p>The Program Text Area links are then recalculated (4257H), the Variable Storage Areas are cleared (<a href="#629ah">629AH</a>) and control transfers back to the start of the Mainloop.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4253h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4253H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine recalculates the Program Text Area links after a program modification. The first two bytes of each program line contain the starting address of the following line, this is called the link. Although the link increases the amount of storage required per program line it greatly reduces the time required by the Interpreter to locate a given line.</p>
<p>An example of a typical program line is shown below, in this case the line "<code>10 PRINT 9</code>" situated at the start of the Program Text Area (8001H):</p>
<p><a name="user-content-figure43"></a><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/e340285909ffa613e463d5a9b8daf8ab2c56a2ad/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830354634332e737667"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/e340285909ffa613e463d5a9b8daf8ab2c56a2ad/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830354634332e737667" alt="" data-canonical-src="https://rawgit.com/oraculo666/the-msx-red-book/master/images/CH05F43.svg" style="max-width:100%;"></a></p>
<p><strong>Figure 43:</strong> Program Line</p>
<p>In the above example the link is stored in Z80 word order (LSB,MSB) and is immediately followed by the binary line number, also in word order. The statement itself is composed of a "<code>PRINT</code>" token (91H), a single space, the number nine and the end of line character (00H). Further details of the storage format can be found in the tokenizing routine (<a href="#42b2h">42B2H</a>).</p>
<p>Each link is recalculated simply by scanning through the line until the end of line character is found. The process is complete when the end of the Program Storage Area, marked by the special link of 0000H, is reached.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4279h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4279H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the "<code>LIST</code>" statement handler to collect up to two line number operands from the program text. If the first line number is present it is converted to an unsigned integer in register pair DE (<a href="#475fh">475FH</a>), if not a default value of 0000H is returned. If the second line number is present it must be preceded by a "-" token (F2H) and is returned on the Z80 stack, if not a default value of 65530 is returned. Control then drops into the program text search routine to find the first referenced program line.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4295h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4295H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine searches the Program Text Area for the program line whose line number is supplied in register pair DE. Starting at the address contained in <a href="#txttab">TXTTAB</a> each program line is examined for a match. If an equal line number is found the routine terminates with Flag Z,C and register pair BC pointing to the start of the program line. If a higher line number is found the routine terminates Flag NZ,NC and if the end link is reached the routine terminates Flag Z,NC.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-42b2h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 42B2H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Interpreter Mainloop to tokenize a line of text. On entry register pair HL points to the first text character in <a href="#buf">BUF</a>. On exit the tokenized line is in <a href="#kbuf">KBUF</a>, register pair BC holds its length and register pair HL points to its start.</p>
<p>Except after opening quotes or after the "<code>REM</code>", "<code>CALL</code>" or "<code>DATA</code>" keywords any string of characters matching a keyword is replaced by that keyword's token. Lower case alphabetics are changed to upper case for keyword comparison. The character "<code>?</code>" is replaced by the "<code>PRINT</code>" token (91H) and the character "'" by ":" (3AH), "<code>REM</code>" token (8FH), "'" token (E6H). The "<code>ELSE</code>" token (A1H) is preceded by a statement separator (3AH). Any other miscellaneous characters in the text are copied without alteration except that lower case alphabetics are converted to upper case. Those tokens smaller than 80H, the function tokens, cannot be stored directly in <a href="#kbuf">KBUF</a> as they will conflict with ordinary text. Instead the sequence FFH, token+80H is used.</p>
<p>Numeric constants are first converted into one of the standard types in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> (<a href="#3299h">3299H</a>). They are then stored in one of several ways depending upon their type and magnitude, the general idea being to minimize memory usage:</p>
<pre><code>0BH LSB MSB ................... Octal number
0CH LSB MSB ................... Hex number
11H to 1AH .................... Integer 0 to 9
0FH LSB ....................... Integer 10 to 255
1CH LSB MSB ................... Integer 256 to 32767
1DH EE DD DD DD ............... Single Precision
1FH EE DD DD DD DD DD DD DD ... Double Precision
</code></pre>
<p>There is no specific token for binary numbers, these are left as character strings. This would appear to be a legacy from earlier versions of Microsoft BASIC. Any sign prefixing a number is regarded as an operator and is stored as a separate token, negative numbers are not produced during tokenization. As double precision numbers occupy so much space a line containing too many, for example PRINT 1#,1#,1# etc. may cause <a href="#kbuf">KBUF</a> to fill up. If this happens a "<code>Line buffer overflow</code>" error is generated.</p>
<p>Any number following one of the keyword tokens in the table at <a href="#43b5h">43B5H</a> is considered to be a line number operand and is stored with a different token:</p>
<pre><code>0DH LSB MSB ................... Pointer
0EH LSB MSB ................... Line number
</code></pre>
<p>During tokenization only the normal type (0EH) is generated, when a program actually runs these line number operands are converted to the address pointer type (0DH).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-43b5h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 43B5H
</code></pre>
<p>This table of tokens is used during tokenization to check for the keywords which take line number operands. The keywords themselves are listed below:</p>
<pre><code>RESTORE    RUN
AUTO       LIST
RENUM      LLIST
DELETE     GOTO
RESUME     RETURN
ERL        THEN
ELSE       GOSUB
</code></pre>

<p><a name="user-content-4524h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4524H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>FOR</code>" statement handler. The loop Variable is first located and assigned its initial value by the "<code>LET</code>" handler (<a href="#4880h">4880H</a>), the address of the loop Variable is returned in register pair DE. The end of the statement is found (<a href="#485bh">485BH</a>) and its address placed in <a href="#endfor">ENDFOR</a>. The Z80 stack is then searched (3FE6H) for any parameter blocks using the same loop Variable. For each one found the current <a href="#endfor">ENDFOR</a> address is compared with that of the parameter block, if there is a match that section of the stack is discarded. This is done in case there are any incomplete loops as a result of a "<code>GOTO</code>" back to the "<code>FOR</code>" statement from inside the loop.</p>
<p>The termination operand and optional "<code>STEP</code>" operand are then evaluated and converted to the same type as the loop Variable. After checking that stack space is available (<a href="#625eh">625EH</a>) a twenty-five byte parameter block is pushed onto the Z80 stack. This is made up of the following:</p>
<pre><code>2 bytes ... ENDFOR address
2 bytes ... Current line number
8 bytes ... Loop termination value
8 bytes ... STEP value
1 byte  ... Loop type
1 byte  ... STEP direction
2 bytes ... Address of loop Variable
1 byte  ... FOR token (82H)
</code></pre>
<p>The parameter block remains on the stack for use by the "<code>NEXT</code>" statement handler until termination is reached, it is then discarded. The size of the block remains constant even though, for integer and single precision loop Variables, the full eight bytes are not required for the termination and STEP values. In these cases the least significant bytes are packed out with garbage.</p>
<p>It should be noted that the type of arithmetic operation performed by the "<code>NEXT</code>" statement handler, and hence the loop execution speed, depends entirely upon the loop Variable type and not the operand types. For the fastest program execution integer type Variables, N% for example, should be used.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4601h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4601H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the Runloop, each statement handler returns here upon completion so the Interpreter can proceed to the next statement. The current Z80 SP is copied to <a href="#savstk">SAVSTK</a> for error recovery purposes and the CTRL-STOP key checked via the <a href="#iscntc">ISCNTC</a> standard routine. Any pending interrupts are processed (<a href="#6389h">6389H</a>) and the current program text position, held in register pair HL throughout the Interpreter, is copied to <a href="#savtxt">SAVTXT</a>.</p>
<p>The current program character is then examined, if this is a statement separator (3AH) control transfers immediately to the execution point (<a href="#4640h">4640H</a>). If it is anything else but an end of line character (00H) a "<code>Syntax error</code>" is generated (<a href="#4055h">4055H</a>) as there is spurious text at the end of the statement. Register pair HL is advanced to the first character of the new program line and the link examined, if this is zero the program is terminated (<a href="#4039h">4039H</a>). Otherwise the line number is taken from the new line and placed in <a href="#curlin">CURLIN</a>. If <a href="#trcflg">TRCFLG</a> is non-zero the line number is displayed (<a href="#3412h">3412H</a>) enclosed by square brackets, control then drops into the execution point.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4640h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4640H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the Runloop execution point. A return to the start of the Runloop (<a href="#4601h">4601H</a>) is pushed onto the Z80 stack and the first character taken from the new statement via the <a href="#chrgtr">CHRGTR</a> standard routine. If it is an underline character (5FH) control transfers to the "<code>CALL</code>" statement handler (55A7H). If it is smaller than 81H, the smallest statement token, control transfers to the "<code>LET</code>" handler (<a href="#4880h">4880H</a>). If it is larger than D8H, the largest statement token, it is checked to see if it is one of the function tokens allowed as a statement (<a href="#51adh">51ADH</a>). Otherwise the handler address is taken from the table at <a href="#392eh">392EH</a> and pushed onto the stack. Control then drops into the <a href="#chrgtr">CHRGTR</a> standard routine to fetch the next program character before control transfers to the statement handler.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4666h"></a><a name="user-content-chrgtr"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4666H
Name...... CHRGTR
Entry..... HL points to current program character
Exit...... A=Next program character
Modifies.. AF, HL
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to fetch the next character from the program text. Register pair HL is incremented and the character placed in register A. If it is a space, TAB code (09H) or LF code (0AH) it is skipped over. If it is a statement separator (3AH) or end of line character (00H) the routine terminates with Flag Z,NC. If it is a digit from "0" to "9" the routine terminates with Flag NZ,C. If it is any other character apart from the numeric prefix tokens the routine terminates Flag NZ,NC. If the character is one of the numeric prefix tokens then it is placed in <a href="#consav">CONSAV</a> and the operand copied to <a href="#conlo">CONLO</a>. The type code is placed in <a href="#contyp">CONTYP</a> and the address of the trailing program character in <a href="#contxt">CONTXT</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-46e8h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 46E8H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator and during detokenization to recover a numeric operand when one of the prefix tokens is returned by the <a href="#chrgtr">CHRGTR</a> standard routine. The prefix token is first taken from <a href="#consav">CONSAV</a>, if it is anything but a line number or pointer token the operand is copied from <a href="#conlo">CONLO</a> to <a href="#dac">DAC</a> and the type code copied from <a href="#contyp">CONTYP</a> to <a href="#valtyp">VALTYP</a>. If it is a line number it is converted to single precision and placed in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> (3236H). If it is a pointer the original line number is recovered from the referenced program line, converted to single precision and placed in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> (3236H).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4718h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4718H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>DEFSTR</code>" statement handler. Register E is loaded with the string type code (03H) and control drops into the general type definition routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-471bh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 471BH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>DEFINT</code>" statement handler. Register E is loaded with the integer type code (02H) and control drops into the general type definition routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-471eh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 471EH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>DEFSNG</code>" statement handler. Register E is loaded with the single precision type code (04H) and control drops into the general type definition routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4721h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4721H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>DEFDBL</code>" statement handler. Register E is loaded with the double precision type code (08H) and the first range definition character checked (<a href="#64a7h">64A7H</a>). If this is not upper case alphabetic a "<code>Syntax error</code>" is generated (<a href="#4055h">4055H</a>). If a "-" token (F2H) follows the second range definition character is taken and checked (<a href="#64a7h">64A7H</a>), the difference between the two determines the number of entries in <a href="#deftbl">DEFTBL</a> that are filled with the type code.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4755h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4755H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine evaluates an operand and converts it to an integer in register pair DE (520FH). If the operand is negative an "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-475fh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 475FH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the statement handlers shown in the table at <a href="#43b5h">43B5H</a> to collect a single line number operand from the program text and convert it to an unsigned integer in register pair DE. If the first character in the text is a "." (2EH) the routine terminates with the contents of <a href="#dot">DOT</a>. If it is one of the line number tokens (0DH or 0EH) the routine terminates with the contents of <a href="#conlo">CONLO</a>. Otherwise successive digits are taken and added to the product, with appropriate multiplications by ten, until a non-numeric character is found.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-479eh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 479EH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>RUN</code>" statement handler. If no line number operand is present in the program text the system is cleared (<a href="#629ah">629AH</a>) and control returns to the Runloop with register pair HL pointing to the start of the Program Storage Area. If a line number operand is present the system is cleared (62A1H) and control transfers to the "<code>GOTO</code>" statement handler (47E7H). Otherwise a following filename is assumed, for example <code>RUN "CAS:FILE"</code>, and control transfers to the "<code>LOAD</code>" statement handler (<a href="#6b5bh">6B5BH</a>);</p>
<p><a name="user-content-47b2h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 47B2H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>GOSUB</code>" statement handler. After checking that stack space is available (<a href="#625eh">625EH</a>) the line number operand is collected and placed in register pair DE (4769H). The seven byte parameter block is then pushed onto the stack and control transfers to the "<code>GOTO</code>" handler (47EBH). The parameter block is made up of the following:</p>
<pre><code>2 bytes ... End of statement address
2 bytes ... Current line number
2 bytes ... 0000H
1 byte  ... GOSUB token (8DH)
</code></pre>
<p>The parameter block remains on the stack until a "<code>RETURN</code>" statement is executed. It is then used to determine the original program text position after which it is discarded.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-47cfh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 47CFH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Runloop interrupt processor (<a href="#6389h">6389H</a>) to create a "<code>GOSUB</code>" type parameter block on the Z80 stack. An interrupt block is identical to a normal block except that the two zero bytes shown above are replaced by the address of the device's entry in <a href="#trptbl">TRPTBL</a>. This address will be used by the "<code>RETURN</code>" statement handler to update the device's interrupt status once a subroutine has terminated. After pushing the parameter block control transfers to the Runloop to execute the program line whose address is supplied in register pair DE.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-47e8h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 47E8H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>GOTO</code>" statement handler. The line number operand is collected (4769H) and placed in register pair HL. If it is a pointer control transfers immediately to the Runloop to begin execution at the new program text position. Otherwise the line number is compared with the current line number to determine the starting position for the program text search. If it is greater the search starts from the end of this line (4298H), if it is smaller it starts from the beginning of the Program Text Area (<a href="#4295h">4295H</a>). If the referenced line cannot be found an "<code>Undefined line number</code>" error is generated (<a href="#481ch">481CH</a>). Otherwise the line number operand is replaced by the referenced program line's address and its token changed to the pointer type (5583H). Control then transfers to the Runloop to execute the referenced program line.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-481ch"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 481CH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>Undefined line number</code>" error generator.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4821h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4821H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>RETURN</code>" statement handler. A dummy loop Variable address is placed in register pair DE and the Z80 stack searched (<a href="#3fe2h">3FE2H</a>) to find the first parameter block not belonging to a "<code>FOR</code>" loop, this section of stack is then discarded. If no "<code>GOSUB</code>" token (8DH) is found at this point a "<code>RETURN without GOSUB</code>" error is generated.</p>
<p>The next two bytes are then taken from the block, if they are non-zero the block was generated by an interrupt and the temporary "<code>STOP</code>" condition is removed (<a href="#633eh">633EH</a>). The program text is then examined, if anything follows the "<code>RETURN</code>" token itself it is assumed to be a line number operand and control transfers to the "<code>GOTO</code>" handler (<a href="#47e8h">47E8H</a>). Otherwise the old line number and program text address are taken from the block and control returns to the Runloop.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-485bh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 485BH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>DATA</code>" statement handler. The program text is skipped over until a statement separator (3AH) or end of line character (00H) is found. This routine is also the "<code>REM</code>" and "<code>ELSE</code>" statement handler via the entry point at 485DH, in this case only the end of line character acts as a terminator.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4880h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4880H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>LET</code>" statement handler. The Variable is first located (<a href="#5ea4h">5EA4H</a>), its address saved in <a href="#temp">TEMP</a> and the operand evaluated (<a href="#4c64h">4C64H</a>). If necessary the operand's type is then changed to match that of the Variable (517AH). Assuming the operand is one of the three numeric types it is simply copied from <a href="#dac">DAC</a> to the Variable in the Variable Storage Area (2EF3H). If the operand is a string type the address of the string body is taken from the descriptor and checked. If it is in <a href="#kbuf">KBUF</a>, as would be the case for an explicit string in a direct statement, the body is first copied to the String Storage Area and a new descriptor created (6611H). The descriptor is then freed from <a href="#tempst">TEMPST</a> (67EEH) and copied to the Variable in the Variable Storage Area (2EF3H).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-48e4h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 48E4H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>ON ERROR</code>", "<code>ON DEVICE GOSUB</code>" and "<code>ON EXPRESSION</code>" statement handler. If the next program text character is not an "<code>ERROR</code>" token (A6H) control transfers to the "<code>ON DEVICE GOSUB</code>" and "<code>ON EXPRESSION</code>" handler (<a href="#490dh">490DH</a>). The program text is checked to ensure that a "<code>GOTO</code>" token (89H) follows and then the line number operand collected (4769H). The program text is searched to obtain the address of the referenced line (4293H) and this is placed in <a href="#onelin">ONELIN</a>. If the line number operand is non-zero the routine then terminates. If the line number operand is zero <a href="#oneflg">ONEFLG</a> is checked to see if an error situation already exists (implying that the statement is inside a BASIC error recovery routine). If so control transfers to the error handler (4096H) to force an immediate error, otherwise the routine terminates normally.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-490dh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 490DH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>ON DEVICE GOSUB</code>" and "<code>ON EXPRESSION</code>" statement handler. If the next program text character is not a device token (<a href="#7810h">7810H</a>) control transfers to the "<code>ON EXPRESSION</code>" handler (<a href="#4943h">4943H</a>). After checking the program text for a "<code>GOSUB</code>" token (8DH) each of the line number operands required for a particular device is collected in turn (4769H). Assuming a given line number operand is non-zero the program text is searched to find the address of the referenced line (4293H) and this is placed in the device's entry in <a href="#trptbl">TRPTBL</a> (<a href="#785ch">785CH</a>). The routine terminates when no more line number operands are found.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4943h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4943H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>ON EXPRESSION</code>" statement handler. The operand is evaluated (521CH) and the following "<code>GOSUB</code>" token (8DH) or "<code>GOTO</code>" token (89H) placed in register A. The operand is then used to count along the program text until register pair HL points to the required line number operand. Control then transfers back to the Runloop execution point (4646H) to decode the "<code>GOSUB</code>" or "<code>GOTO</code>" token.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-495dh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 495DH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>RESUME</code>" statement handler. <a href="#oneflg">ONEFLG</a> is first checked to make sure that an error condition already exists, if not a "<code>RESUME without error</code>" is generated (<a href="#4064h">4064H</a>). If a non- zero line number operand follows control transfers to the "<code>GOTO</code>" handler (47EBH). If a "<code>NEXT</code>" token (83H) follows the position of the error is restored from <a href="#errtxt">ERRTXT</a> and <a href="#errlin">ERRLIN</a>, the start of the next statement is found (<a href="#485bh">485BH</a>) and the routine terminates. If there is no line number operand or if it is zero the position of the error is found from <a href="#errtxt">ERRTXT</a> and <a href="#errlin">ERRLIN</a> and the routine terminates.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-49aah"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 49AAH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>ERROR</code>" statement handler. The operand is evaluated and placed in register E (521CH). If it is zero an "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH), otherwise control transfers to the error handler (<a href="#406fh">406FH</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-49b5h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 49B5H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>AUTO</code>" Statement handler. The optional start and increment line number operands, both with a default value of ten, are collected (<a href="#475fh">475FH</a>) and placed in <a href="#autlin">AUTLIN</a> and <a href="#autinc">AUTINC</a>. After making <a href="#autflg">AUTFLG</a> non-zero the Runloop return is destroyed and control transfers directly to the Mainloop (<a href="#4134h">4134H</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-49e5h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 49E5H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>IF</code>" statement handler. The operand is evaluated (<a href="#4c64h">4C64H</a>) and, after checking for a "<code>GOTO</code>" token (89H) or "<code>THEN</code>" token (DAH), its sign is tested (<a href="#2ea1h">2EA1H</a>). If the operand is non- zero (true) the following text is executed either by an immediate transfer to the Runloop (4646H) or, for a line number operand, the "<code>GOTO</code>" handler (<a href="#47e8h">47E8H</a>). If the operand is zero (false) the statement text is scanned (<a href="#485bh">485BH</a>) until an "<code>ELSE</code>" token (A1H) is found not balanced by an "<code>IF</code>" token (8BH) and execution re-commences.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4a1dh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4A1DH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>LPRINT</code>" statement handler. <a href="#prtflg">PRTFLG</a> is set to 01H, to direct output to the printer, and control transfers to the "<code>PRINT</code>" handler (4A29H).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4a24h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4A24H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>PRINT</code>" statement handler. The program text is first checked for a trailing buffer number and, if necessary, <a href="#ptrfil">PTRFIL</a> set to direct output to the required I/O buffer (<a href="#6d57h">6D57H</a>). If no more program text exists a CR,LF is issued (7328H) and the routine terminates (<a href="#4affh">4AFFH</a>). Otherwise successive characters are taken from the program text and analyzed. If a "<code>USING</code>" token (E4H) is found control transfers to the "<code>PRINT USING</code>" handler (<a href="#60b1h">60B1H</a>). If a ";" character is found control just transfers back to the start to fetch the next item (4A2EH). If a comma is found sufficient spaces are issued to bring the current print position, from <a href="#ttypos">TTYPOS</a>, <a href="#lptpos">LPTPOS</a> or an I/O buffer FCB, to an integral multiple of fourteen. If output is directed to the screen and the print position is equal to or greater than the contents of <a href="#clmlst">CLMLST</a> or if output is directed to the printer and it is equal to or greater than 238 then a CR,LF is issued instead (7328H). If a "<code>SPC(</code>" token (DFH) is found the operand is evaluated (<a href="#521bh">521BH</a>) and the required number of spaces are output. If a "<code>TAB(</code>" token (DBH) is found the operand is evaluated (<a href="#521bh">521BH</a>) and sufficient spaces issued to bring the current print position, from <a href="#ttypos">TTYPOS</a>, <a href="#lptpos">LPTPOS</a> or an I/O buffer FCB, to the required point.</p>
<p>If none of these characters is found the program text contains a data item which is then evaluated (<a href="#4c64h">4C64H</a>). If the operand is a string it is simply displayed (667BH). If it is numeric it is first converted to text in <a href="#fbuffr">FBUFFR</a> (<a href="#3425h">3425H</a>) and a string descriptor created (6635H). If output is directed to an I/O buffer the resulting string is then displayed (667BH). If output is directed to the screen or printer the current print position, from <a href="#ttypos">TTYPOS</a> or <a href="#lptpos">LPTPOS</a>, is compared with the line length and a CR,LF issued (7328H) if the output will not fit on the line. The maximum line length is 255 for the printer and is taken from <a href="#linlen">LINLEN</a> for the screen. Once the string has been displayed control transfers back to the start of the handler.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4affh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4AFFH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine zeroes <a href="#prtflg">PRTFLG</a> and <a href="#ptrfil">PTRFIL</a> to return the Interpreter's output to the screen.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4b0eh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4B0EH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>LINE INPUT</code>", "<code>LINE INPUT#</code>" and "<code>LINE</code>" statement handler. If the following program text character is anything other than an "<code>INPUT</code>" token (85H) control transfers to the "<code>LINE</code>" statement handler (<a href="#58a7h">58A7H</a>). If the following program text character is a "#" (23H) control transfers to the "<code>LINE INPUT#</code>" statement handler (<a href="#6d8fh">6D8FH</a>).</p>
<p>Any following prompt string is evaluated and displayed (4B7BH) and the Variable located (<a href="#5ea4h">5EA4H</a>) and checked to ensure that it is a string type (<a href="#3058h">3058H</a>). The line of text is collected from the console via the <a href="#inlin">INLIN</a> standard routine, if Flag C (CTRL-STOP) is returned control transfers to the "<code>STOP</code>" statement handler (63FEH). Otherwise the input string is analyzed and a descriptor created (6638H), control then transfers to the "<code>LET</code>" statement handler for assignment (4892H). It should be noted that the screen is not forced to text mode before the input is collected.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4b3ah"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4B3AH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the plain text message "<code>?Redo from start</code>", CR, LF terminated by a zero byte.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4b4dh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4B4DH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the "<code>READ/INPUT</code>" statement handler if it has failed to convert a data item to numeric form. If in "<code>READ</code>" mode (<a href="#flginp">FLGINP</a> is non-zero) a "<code>Syntax error</code>" is generated (<a href="#404fh">404FH</a>). Otherwise the message "<code>?Redo from start</code>" is displayed (<a href="#6678h">6678H</a>) and control returns to the statement handler.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4b62h"></a><a name="user-content-input#"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4B62H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>INPUT#</code>" Statement handler. The buffer number is evaluated and <a href="#ptrfil">PTRFIL</a> set to direct input from the required I/O buffer (6D55H), control then transfers to the combined "<code>READ/INPUT</code>" statement handler (4B9BH).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4b6ch"></a><a name="user-content-input"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4B6CH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>INPUT</code>" statement handler. If the next program text character is a "#" control transfers to the "<code>INPUT#</code>" statement handler (<a href="#4b62h">4B62H</a>). Otherwise the screen is forced to text mode, via the <a href="#totxt">TOTXT</a> standard routine, and any prompt string analyzed (<a href="#6636h">6636H</a>) and displayed (667BH). A question mark is then displayed and a line of text collected from the console via the <a href="#qinlin">QINLIN</a> standard routine. If this returns Flag C (CTRL-STOP) control transfers to the "<code>STOP</code>" handler (63FEH). If the first character in <a href="#buf">BUF</a> is zero (null input) the handler terminates by skipping to the end of the statement (485AH), otherwise control drops into the combined "<code>READ/INPUT</code>" handler.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4b9fh"></a><a name="user-content-read"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4B9FH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>READ</code>" statement handler, a large section is also used by the "<code>INPUT</code>" and "<code>INPUT#</code>" statements so the structure is rather awkward. Each Variable found in the program text is located in turn (<a href="#5ea4h">5EA4H</a>), for each one the corresponding data item is obtained and assigned to the Variable by the "<code>LET</code>" handler (4893H). When in "<code>READ</code>" mode the data items are taken from the program text using the initial contents of <a href="#datptr">DATPTR</a> (<a href="#4c40h">4C40H</a>). When in "<code>INPUT</code>" or "<code>INPUT#</code>" mode the data items are taken from the text buffer <a href="#buf">BUF</a>.</p>
<p>If the data items are exhausted in "<code>READ</code>" mode an "<code>Out of DATA</code>" error is generated. If they are exhausted in "<code>INPUT</code>" mode two question marks are displayed and another line fetched from the console via the <a href="#qinlin">QINLIN</a> standard routine. If they are exhausted in "<code>INPUT#</code>" mode another line of text is copied to <a href="#buf">BUF</a> from the relevant I/O buffer (<a href="#6d83h">6D83H</a>). If the Variable list is exhausted while in "<code>INPUT</code>" mode the message "<code>Extra ignored</code>" is displayed (<a href="#6678h">6678H</a>) and the handler terminates (<a href="#4affh">4AFFH</a>). In "<code>INPUT#</code>" mode no message is displayed while in "<code>READ</code>" mode control terminates by updating <a href="#datptr">DATPTR</a> (63DEH). If a data item cannot be converted to numeric form (<a href="#3299h">3299H</a>) to match a numeric Variable control transfers to the "<code>?Redo from start</code>" routine (<a href="#4b4dh">4B4DH</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4c2fh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4C2FH
</code></pre>
<p>The is the plain text message "<code>?Extra ignored</code>", CR, LF terminated by a zero byte.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4c40h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4C40H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the "<code>READ</code>" handler to locate the next "<code>DATA</code>" statement in the program text, the address to start from is supplied in register pair HL. Each program statement is examined until a "<code>DATA</code>" token (84H) is found whereupon the routine terminates (4BD1H). If the end link is reached an "<code>Out of DATA</code>" error is generated. As the search proceeds the line number of each program line is placed in <a href="#datlin">DATLIN</a> for use by the error handler.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4c5fh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4C5FH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine checks that the next character in the program text is the "=" token (EFH) and then drops into the Expression Evaluator. When entered at 4C62H it checks for "(".</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4c64h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4C64H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the Expression Evaluator. On entry register pair HL points to the first character of the expression to be evaluated. On exit register pair HL points to the character following the expression, the result is in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> and the type code in <a href="#valtyp">VALTYP</a>. For a string result the address of the string descriptor is returned at <a href="#dac">DAC</a>+2. The descriptor itself comprising a single byte for the string length and two bytes for its address, will be in <a href="#tempst">TEMPST</a> or inside a string Variable.</p>
<p>An expression is a list of factors (<a href="#4dc7h">4DC7H</a>) linked together by operators with differing precedence levels. To process such an expression correctly the Expression Evaluator must be able to temporarily stack an intermediate result, if the next operator has a higher precedence than the current operator, and start afresh on a new calculation. It therefore has two basic operations, STACK and APPLY. For example:</p>
<pre><code>3+250\2^2*3^3+1,

STACK:    3+        (\ follows)
STACK:    250\      (^ follows)
APPLY:    2^2=4     (* follows)
STACK:    4*        (^ follows)
APPLY:    3^3=27    (+ follows)
APPLY:    4*27=108  (+ follows)
APPLY:    250\108=2 (+ follows)
APPLY:    3+2=5     (+ follows)
APPLY:    5+1=6     (, follows)
</code></pre>
<p>Evaluation terminates when the next operator has a precedence equal to or lower than the initial precedence and the stack is empty. The expression delimiter, shown as a comma in the example, is regarded as having a precedence of zero and so will always halt evaluation. Normally the Expression Evaluator starts off with an initial precedence of zero but the entry point at 4C67H may be used to supply an alternative value in register D. This facility is used by the Factor Evaluator to restrict the range of evaluation when applying the monadic negation and "<code>NOT</code>" operators.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4d22h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4D22H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Expression Evaluator to apply an infix math operator (+-*/ ) to a pair of numeric operands. There are separate routines for the relational operators (<a href="#4f57h">4F57H</a>) and the logical operators (<a href="#4f78h">4F78H</a>). The first operand, its type code, and the operator token are supplied on the Z80 stack, the second operand and its type code are supplied in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> and <a href="#valtyp">VALTYP</a>. The types of both operands are first compared, if they differ the lowest precision operand is converted to match the higher. The operands are then moved to the positions required by the math routines. For integers the first operand is placed in register pair DE and the second in register pair HL. For single precision the first operand is placed in registers C, B, E, D and the second in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. For double precision the first operand is placed in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> and the second in <a href="#arg">ARG</a>. The operator token is then used to obtain the required address from the table at 3D51H, 3D5DH or 3D69H, depending upon the operand type, and control transfers to the relevant math routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4db8h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4DB8H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Expression Evaluator to divide two integer operands. The first operand is contained in register pair DE and the second in register pair HL, the result is returned in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. Both operands are converted to single precision (2FCBH) and control transfers to the single precision division routine (<a href="#3265h">3265H</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4dc7h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4DC7H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the Factor Evaluator. On entry register pair HL points to the character before the factor to be evaluated. On exit register pair HL points to the character following the factor, the result is in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> and the type code in <a href="#valtyp">VALTYP</a>. A factor may be one of the following:</p>
<ol>
<li>A numeric or string constant</li>
<li>A numeric or string Variable</li>
<li>A function</li>
<li>A monadic operator (+-NOT)</li>
<li>A parenthesized expression</li>
</ol>
<p>The first character is taken from the program text via the <a href="#chrgtr">CHRGTR</a> standard routine and examined. If it is an end of Statement character a "<code>Missing operand</code>" error is generated (<a href="#406ah">406AH</a>). If it is an ASCII digit it is converted from textual form to one of the standard numeric types in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> (<a href="#3299h">3299H</a>).</p>
<p>If it is upper case alphabetic (64A8H) it is a Variable and its current value is returned (<a href="#4e9bh">4E9BH</a>). If it is a numeric token the number is copied from <a href="#conlo">CONLO</a> to <a href="#dac">DAC</a> (46B8H). If it is one of the FFH prefixed function tokens shown in the table at 39DEH it is decoded to transfer control to the relevant function handler (4ECFH). If it is the monadic "+" operator it is simply skipped over, only the monadic "-" operator (<a href="#4e8dh">4E8DH</a>) and monadic "<code>NOT</code>" operator (<a href="#4f63h">4F63H</a>) require any action.</p>
<p>If it is an opening quote the following explicit string is analyzed and a descriptor created (<a href="#6636h">6636H</a>). If it is an "&amp;" it is a non-decimal numeric constant and it is converted to one of the standard numeric types in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> (<a href="#4eb8h">4EB8H</a>). If it is not one of the functions shown below then it must be a parenthesized expression (4E87H), otherwise a "<code>Syntax error</code>" is generated. The following function tokens are tested for directly and control transferred to the address shown:</p>
<pre><code>ERR .... 4DFDH   ATTR$ .... 7C43H
ERL .... 4E0BH   VARPTR ... 4E41H
POINT .. 5803H   USR....... 4FD5H
TIME ... 7900H   INSTR .... 68EBH
SPRITE . 7A84H   INKEY$ ... 7347H
VDP .... 7B47H   STRING$ .. 6829H
BASE ... 7BCBH   INPUT$ ... 6C87H
PLAY ... 791BH   CSRLIN ... 790AH
DSKI$ .. 7C3EH   FN ....... 5040H
</code></pre>

<p><a name="user-content-4dfdh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4DFDH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>ERR</code>" function. The contents of <a href="#errflg">ERRFLG</a> are placed in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> as an integer (4FCFH).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4e0bh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4E0BH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>ERL</code>" function. The contents of <a href="#errlin">ERRLIN</a> are copied to <a href="#dac">DAC</a> as a single precision number (3236H).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4e41h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4E41H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>VARPTR</code>" function. If the function token is followed by a "#" the buffer number is evaluated (<a href="#521bh">521BH</a>), the I/O buffer FCB located (<a href="#6a6dh">6A6DH</a>) and its address placed in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> as an integer (2F99H). Otherwise the Variable is located (5F5DH) and its address placed in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> as an integer (2F99H).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4e8dh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4E8DH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the monadic "-" operator. Register D is set to a precedence value of 7DH, the factor evaluated (4C67H) and then negated (2E86H).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4e9bh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4E9BH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to return the current value of a Variable. The Variable is first located (<a href="#5ea4h">5EA4H</a>). If it is a string Variable its address is placed in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> to point to the descriptor. Otherwise the contents of the Variable are copied to <a href="#dac">DAC</a> (2F08).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4ea9h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4EA9H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine returns the single character pointed to by register pair HL in register A, if it is a lower case alphabetic it converts it to upper case.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4eb8h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4EB8H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator and the numeric input routine (<a href="#3299h">3299H</a>) to convert an ampersand ("&amp;") Prefixed number from textual form to an integer in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. As each legal character is found the product is multiplied by 2, 8 or 16, depending upon the character which initially followed the ampersand, and the new digit added to it. If the product overflows an "<code>Overflow</code>" error is generated (<a href="#4067h">4067H</a>). The routine terminates when an unacceptable character is found.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4efch"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4EFCH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to process the FFH prefixed function tokens. If the token is either "<code>LEFT$</code>", "<code>RIGHT$</code>" or "<code>MID$</code>" the string operand is evaluated (4C62H), the address of its descriptor pushed onto the Z80 stack and the following numeric operand also evaluated (521CH) and stacked. Otherwise the function's parenthesized operand is evaluated (4E87H) and, for "<code>SQR</code>", "<code>RND</code>", "<code>SIN</code>", "<code>LOG</code>", "<code>EXP</code>", "<code>COS</code>", "<code>TAN</code>" or "<code>ATN</code>" only, converted to double precision (<a href="#303ah">303AH</a>). The function token is then used to obtain the required address from the table at 39DEH and control transfers to the function handler.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4f47h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4F47H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the numeric input conversion routine (<a href="#3299h">3299H</a>) to test for a "+" or "-" character or token. It returns register D=0 for positive and register D=FFH for negative.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4f57h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4F57H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Expression Evaluator to apply a relational operator (&lt;&gt;= or combinations) to a pair of operands. If the operands are numeric the Expression Evaluator first uses the math operator routine (<a href="#4d22h">4D22H</a>) to apply the general relation operation to the operands. If the operands are strings the string comparison routine (<a href="#65c8h">65C8H</a>) is used first. When control arrives here the relation result is in register A and the Z80 Flags:</p>
<pre><code>Operand 1=Operand 2 ... A=00H, Flag Z,NC
Operand 1&lt;Operand 2 ... A=01H, Flag NZ,NC
Operand 1&gt;Operand 2 ... A=FFH, Flag NZ,C
</code></pre>
<p>The Expression Evaluator also supplies a bit mask defining the original operators on the Z80 stack. This has a 1 in each position if the associated operation is required: 00000&lt;=&gt;. The mask is applied to the relation result producing zero if none of the conditions is satisfied. This is then placed in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> as a true (-1) or false (0) integer (2E9AH).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4f63h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4F63H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the monadic "<code>NOT</code>" operator. Register D is set to an initial precedence level of 5AH and the expression evaluated (4C67H) and converted to an integer (<a href="#2f8ah">2F8AH</a>). It is then inverted and restored to <a href="#dac">DAC</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4f78h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4F78H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Expression Evaluator to apply a logical operator ("<code>OR</code>", "<code>AND</code>", "<code>XOR</code>", "<code>EQV</code>" and "<code>IMP</code>") or the "<code>MOD</code>" and "" operators to a pair of numeric operands. The first operand, which has already been converted to an integer, is supplied on the Z80 stack and the second is supplied in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. The operator token (actually its precedence level) is supplied in register B. After converting the second operand to an integer (<a href="#2f8ah">2F8AH</a>) the operator is examined. There are separate routines for "<code>MOD</code>" (<a href="#323ah">323AH</a>) and "" (<a href="#31e6h">31E6H</a>) but the logical operators are processed locally using the corresponding Z80 logical instructions on register pairs DE and HL. The result is stored in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> as an integer (2F99H).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4fc7h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4FC7H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>LPOS</code>" function to an operand contained in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. The contents of <a href="#lptpos">LPTPOS</a> are placed in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> as an integer (4FCFH).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4fcch"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4FCCH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>POS</code>" function to an operand contained in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. The contents of <a href="#ttypos">TTYPOS</a> are placed in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> as an integer (2F99).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-4fd5h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 4FD5H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>USR</code>" function. The user number is collected directly from the program text, it cannot be an expression, and the associated address taken from <a href="#usrtab">USRTAB</a> (4FF4H). The following parenthesized operand is then evaluated (4E87H) and left in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> as the passed parameter. If it is a string type its storage is freed (67D3H). The current program text position is pushed onto the Z80 stack followed by a return to 3297H, the routine at this address will restore the program text position after the user function has terminated. Control then transfers to the user address with register pair HL pointing to the first byte of <a href="#dac">DAC</a> and the type code, from <a href="#valtyp">VALTYP</a>, in register A. Additionally, for a string parameter, the descriptor address is taken from <a href="#dac">DAC</a> and placed in register pair DE.</p>
<p>The user routine may modify any register except the Z80 SP and should terminate with a RET instruction, interrupts may be left disabled if necessary as the Runloop will re-enable them. Any numeric parameter to be returned to the Interpreter should be placed in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. Strictly speaking this should be the same numeric type as the passed parameter, however if <a href="#valtyp">VALTYP</a> is modified the Interpreter will always accept it.</p>
<p>Returning a string type is more difficult. Using the same method as the Factor Evaluator string functions, which involves copying the string to the String Storage Area and pushing a new descriptor onto <a href="#tempst">TEMPST</a>, is complicated and vulnerable to changes in the MSX system. A simpler and more reliable method is to use the passed parameter to create the space for the result. This should not be an explicitly stated string as the program text will have to be modified, instead an implicit parameter should be used. This must be done with care however, it is very easy to gain the impression that the Interpreter has accepted the string when in fact it has not. Take the following example which does nothing but return the passed parameter:</p>
<pre><code>10 POKE &amp;H9000,&amp;HC9
20 DEFUSR=&amp;H9000
30 A$=USR(STRING$(12,"!"))
40 PRINT A$
50 B$=STRING$(9,"X")
60 PRINT A$
</code></pre>
<p>At first it seems that the passed string has been correctly assigned to A$. When line 60 is reached however it becomes apparent that A$ has been corrupted by the subsequent assignment of a string to B$. What has happened is that the temporary storage allocated to the passed parameter was reclaimed from the String Storage Area before control transferred to the user routine. This region was then used to store the string belonging to B$ thus modifying A$.</p>
<p>This situation can be avoided by assigning the parameter to a Variable beforehand and then passing the Variable, for example:</p>
<pre><code>10 A$=STRING$(12,"!")
20 A$=USR(A$)
</code></pre>
<p>Line 10 results in twelve bytes of the String Storage Area being permanently allocated to A$. When the user function is entered the descriptor, which is pointed to by register pair DE, will contain the starting address of the twelve byte region where the result should be placed. If the returned string is shorter than the passed one the length byte of the descriptor may be changed without any side effects. For further details on string storage see the garbage collector (<a href="#66b6h">66B6H</a>).</p>
<p>A point worth noting is that a "<code>CLEAR</code>" operation is not strictly necessary before a machine language program is loaded. The region between the top of the Array Storage Area and the base of the Z80 stack is never used by the Interpreter. A program can exist in this region provided that the two enclosing areas do not overlap it.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-500eh"></a><a name="user-content-defusr"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 500EH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>DEFUSR</code>" statement handler. The user number is collected directly from the program text, it cannot be an expression, and the associated entry in <a href="#usrtab">USRTAB</a> located (4FF4H). The address operand is then evaluated (<a href="#542fh">542FH</a>) and placed in <a href="#usrtab">USRTAB</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-501dh"></a><a name="user-content-def fn"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 501DH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>DEF FN</code>" and "<code>DEFUSR</code>" statement handler. If the following character is a "<code>USR</code>" token (DDH) control transfers to the "<code>DEFUSR</code>" statement handler (<a href="#500eh">500EH</a>), otherwise the program text is checked for a trailing "<code>FN</code>" token (DEH). The function name Variable is located (<a href="#51a1h">51A1H</a>) and, after checking that the Interpreter is in program mode (<a href="#5193h">5193H</a>), the current program text position is placed there. Each of the Variables in the formal parameter list is then located in succession (<a href="#5ea4h">5EA4H</a>), this is simply to ensure that they are created. The routine terminates by skipping over the remainder of the statement (<a href="#485bh">485BH</a>) as the function body is not required at this time.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5040h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5040H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>FN</code>" function. The function name Variable is first located (<a href="#51a1h">51A1H</a>) to obtain the address of the function definition in the program text. Each formal Variable from the function definition is located in turn (<a href="#5ea4h">5EA4H</a>) and its address pushed onto the Z80 stack. As each one is found the corresponding actual parameter is evaluated (<a href="#4c64h">4C64H</a>) and pushed onto the stack with it. If necessary the type of the actual parameter is converted to match that of the formal parameter (517AH)'</p>
<p>When both lists are exhausted each formal Variable address and actual parameter are popped from the stack in turn. Each Variable is then copied from the Variable Storage Area to <a href="#parm2">PARM2</a> with its value replaced by the actual parameter. It should be noted that, because <a href="#parm2">PARM2</a> is only a hundred bytes long, a maximum of nine double precision parameters is allowed. When all the actual parameters have been copied to <a href="#parm2">PARM2</a> the entire contents of <a href="#parm1">PARM1</a> (the current parameter area) are pushed onto the Z80 stack and <a href="#parm2">PARM2</a> is copied to <a href="#parm1">PARM1</a> (518EH). Register pair HL is then set to the start of the function body in the program text and the expression is evaluated (<a href="#4c5fh">4C5FH</a>). The old contents of <a href="#parm1">PARM1</a> are popped from the stack and restored. Finally the result of the evaluation is type converted if necessary to match the function name type (517AH).</p>
<p>A user defined function differs from a normal expression in only one respect, it has its own set of local Variables. These Variables are created in <a href="#parm1">PARM1</a> when the function is invoked and disappear when it terminates. When a normal Variable search is initiated by the Expression Evaluator the region examined is the Variable Storage Area. However, if <a href="#nofuns">NOFUNS</a> is non-zero, indicating at least one active user function, <a href="#parm1">PARM1</a> will be searched instead, only if this fails will the search move on to the global Variables in the Variable Storage Area. Using a local Variable area specific to each invocation of a function means that the same Variable names can be used throughout without the Variables overwriting each other or the global Variables.</p>
<p>It is worth noting that a user defined function is slower than an inline expression or even a subroutine. The search carried out to find the function name Variable, plus the large amount of stacking and destacking, are significant overheads.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5189h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5189H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine moves a block of memory from the address pointed to by register pair DE to that pointed to by register pair HL, register pair BC defines the length.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5193h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5193H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine generate an "<code>Illegal direct</code>" error if <a href="#curlin">CURLIN</a> shows the Interpreter to be in direct mode.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-51a1h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 51A1H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine checks the program text for an "<code>FN</code>" token (DEH) and then creates the function name Variable (5EA9H). These are distinguished from ordinary Variables by having bit 7 set in the first character of the Variable's name.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-51adh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 51ADH
</code></pre>
<p>Control transfers to this routine from the Runloop execution point (<a href="#4640h">4640H</a>) if a token greater than D8H is found at the start of a statement. If the token is not an FFH prefixed function token a "<code>Syntax error</code>" is generated (<a href="#4055h">4055H</a>). If the function token is one of those which double as statements control transfers to the relevant handler, otherwise a "<code>Syntax error</code>" is generated. The statements in question are "<code>MID$</code>" (<a href="#696eh">696EH</a>), "<code>STRIG</code>" (<a href="#77bfh">77BFH</a>) and "<code>INTERVAL</code>" (<a href="#77b1h">77B1H</a>). There is actually no separate token for "<code>INTERVAL</code>", the "<code>INT</code>" token (85H) suffices with the remaining characters being checked by the statement handler.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-51c9h"></a><a name="user-content-width"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 51C9H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>WIDTH</code>" statement handler. The operand is evaluated (521CH) and its magnitude checked. If it is zero or greater than thirty-two or forty, depending upon the screen mode held in <a href="#oldscr">OLDSCR</a> an "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH). If it is the same as the current contents of <a href="#linlen">LINLEN</a> the routine terminates with no further action. Otherwise the current screen is cleared with a FORMFEED control code (0CH) via the <a href="#outdo">OUTDO</a> standard routine in case the screen is to be made smaller. The operand is then placed in <a href="#linlen">LINLEN</a> and either <a href="#linl32">LINL32</a> or <a href="#linl40">LINL40</a>, depending upon the screen mode held in <a href="#oldscr">OLDSCR</a>, and the screen cleared again in case it has been made larger. Because the line length variable to be changed is selected by <a href="#oldscr">OLDSCR</a>, rather than <a href="#scrmod">SCRMOD</a>, the width can still be changed even if the screen is currently in <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> or <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a>. In this case the change is effective when a return is made to the Interpreter Mainloop or an "<code>INPUT</code>" statement is executed.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-520eh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 520EH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine evaluates the next expression in the program text (<a href="#4c64h">4C64H</a>), converts it to an integer (<a href="#2f8ah">2F8AH</a>) and places the result in register pair DE. The magnitude and sign of the MSB are then tested and the routine terminates.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-521bh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 521BH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine evaluates the next operand in the program text (<a href="#4c64h">4C64H</a>) and converts it to an integer (5212H). If the operand is greater than 255 an "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5229h"></a><a name="user-content-llist"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5229H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>LLIST</code>" statement handler. <a href="#prtflg">PRTFLG</a> is set to 01H, to direct output to the printer, and control drops into the "<code>LIST</code>" statement handler.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-522eh"></a><a name="user-content-list"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 522EH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>LIST</code>" statement handler. The optional start and termination line number operands are collected and the starting position found in the program text (<a href="#4279h">4279H</a>). Successive program lines are listed until the end link is found, the CTRL-STOP key is pressed or the termination line number is reached, control then transfers directly to the Mainloop "<code>OK</code>" point (<a href="#411fh">411FH</a>). Each program line is listed by displaying its line number (<a href="#3412h">3412H</a>), detokenizing (<a href="#5284h">5284H</a>) and displaying (527BH) the line itself and then issuing a CR,LF (7328H).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5284h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5284H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the "<code>LIST</code>" statement handler to convert a tokenized program line to textual form. On entry register pair HL points to the first character of the tokenized line. On exit the line of text is in <a href="#buf">BUF</a> and is terminated by a zero byte.</p>
<p>Any normal or FFH prefixed token is converted to the corresponding keyword by a simple linear search of the tokens in the table at 3A72H. Exceptions are made if either an opening quote character, a "<code>REM</code>" token, or a "<code>DATA</code>" token has previously been found. Normally these tokens will be followed by plain text anyway, the check is made to stop graphics characters being interpreted as tokens. The three byte sequence ":" (3AH), "<code>REM</code>" token (8FH), " " token (E6H) is converted to the single " " character (27H) and the statement separator (3AH) preceding an "<code>ELSE</code>" token (A1H) is scrubbed out.</p>
<p>If one of the numeric tokens is found its value and type are first copied from <a href="#conlo">CONLO</a> and <a href="#contyp">CONTYP</a> to <a href="#dac">DAC</a> and <a href="#valtyp">VALTYP</a> (<a href="#46e8h">46E8H</a>). It is then converted to textual form in <a href="#fbuffr">FBUFFR</a> by the decimal (<a href="#3425h">3425H</a>), octal (<a href="#371eh">371EH</a>) or hex (<a href="#3722h">3722H</a>) conversion routines. For octal and hex types the number is prefixed by an ampersand and an "<code>O</code>" or "<code>H</code>" letter. A type suffix, "'" or "#", is added to single precision or double precision numbers only if there is no decimal part and no exponent part ("<code>E</code>" or "<code>D</code>").</p>
<p><a name="user-content-53e2h"></a><a name="user-content-delete"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 53E2H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>DELETE</code>" statement handler. The optional start and termination line number operands are collected and the starting position found in the program text (<a href="#4279h">4279H</a>). If any pointers exist in the program text they are converted back to line numbers (54EAH). The terminating program line is found by a search of the program text (<a href="#4295h">4295H</a>), if this address is smaller than that of the starting program line an "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH), otherwise the message "<code>OK</code>" is displayed (<a href="#6678h">6678H</a>). The block of memory from the end of the terminating line to the start of the Variable Storage Area is copied down to the beginning of the starting line and <a href="#vartab">VARTAB</a>, <a href="#arytab">ARYTAB</a> and <a href="#strend">STREND</a> are reset to the new (lower) end of the program text. Control then transfers directly to the end of the Mainloop (4237H) to reset the remaining pointers and to relink the Program Text Area. Note that, because control does not return to the normal "<code>OK</code>" point, the screen will not be returned to text mode. If the screen is in <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> or <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour mode</a> when a "<code>DELETE</code>" is executed, which is admittedly rather unlikely, the system will crash.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-541ch"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 541CH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>PEEK</code>" function to an operand contained in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. The address operand is checked (<a href="#5439h">5439H</a>) then the byte read from memory and placed in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> as an integer (4FCFH).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5423h"></a><a name="user-content-poke"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5423H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>POKE</code>" statement handler. The address operand is evaluated (<a href="#542fh">542FH</a>) then the data operand evaluated (521CH) and written to memory.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-542fh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 542FH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine evaluates the next operand in the program text (<a href="#4c64h">4C64H</a>) and places it in register pair DE as an integer (<a href="#5439h">5439H</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5439h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5439H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine converts the numeric operand contained in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> into an integer in register pair HL.
