The operand must be in the range -32768 to +65535 and is normally an address as required by "<code>POKE</code>", "<code>PEEK</code>", "<code>BLOAD</code>", etc. The operand's type is first checked via the <a href="#getypr">GETYPR</a> standard routine, if it is already an integer it is simply placed in register pair HL (<a href="#2f8ah">2F8AH</a>). Assuming the operand is single precision or double precision its sign is checked, if it is negative it is converted to integer (<a href="#2f8ah">2F8AH</a>). Otherwise it is converted to single precision (<a href="#2fb2h">2FB2H</a>) and its magnitude checked (<a href="#2f21h">2F21H</a>). If it is greater than 32767 and smaller than 65536 then -65536 is added (<a href="#324eh">324EH</a>) before it is converted to integer (<a href="#2f8ah">2F8AH</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5468h"></a><a name="user-content-renum"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5468H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>RENUM</code>" statement handler. If a new initial line number operand exists it is collected (<a href="#475fh">475FH</a>), otherwise a default value of ten of taken. If an old initial line number operand exists it is collected (<a href="#475fh">475FH</a>), otherwise a default value of zero is taken. If an increment line number operand exists it is collected (4769H), otherwise a default value of ten is taken.</p>
<p>The program text is then searched for existing line numbers equal to or greater than the new initial line number (<a href="#4295h">4295H</a>) and the old initial line number (<a href="#4295h">4295H</a>), an "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH) if the new address is smaller than the old address. This is to catch any attempt to renumber high program lines down to existing low ones.</p>
<p>A dummy renumbering run of the program text is first carried out to check than no new line number will be generated with a value greater than 65529. This must be done as an error midway through the conversion would leave the program text in a confused state. Assuming all is well any line number operands in the program text are converted to pointers (<a href="#54f6h">54F6H</a>). This neatly solves the problem of line number references, <code>GOTO 50</code> for example, as the program text is not moved during renumbering. Starting at the old initial program text position each existing program line number is replaced with its new value. When the end link is reached any program text pointers are converted back to line number operands (54F1H) and control transfers directly to the Mainloop "<code>OK</code>" point (411EH).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-54f6h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 54F6H
</code></pre>
<p>When entered at 54F6H this routine converts every line number operand in the program text to a pointer. When entered at 54F7H it performs the reverse operation and converts every pointer in the program text back to a line number operand. Starting at the beginning of the Program Text Area each line is examined for a pointer token (0DH) or a line number operand token (0EH) depending upon the mode. In pointer to line number operand mode the pointer is replaced by the line number from the referenced program line and the token changed to 0EH. In line number operand to pointer mode the program text is searched (<a href="#4295h">4295H</a>) to find the relevant line, its address replaces the line number operand and the token is changed to 0DH. If the search is unsuccessful a message of the form "<code>Undefined line NNNN in NNNN</code>" is displayed (<a href="#6678h">6678H</a>) and the conversion process continues. A special check is made for the "<code>ON ERROR GOTO 0</code>" statement, to prevent the generation of a spurious error message, but no check is made for the similar "<code>RESUME 0</code>" statement. In this case an error message will be displayed, this should be ignored.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-555ah"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 555AH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the plain text message "<code>Undefined line </code>" terminated by a zero byte.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-558ch"></a><a name="user-content-synchr"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 558CH
Name...... SYNCHR
Entry..... HL points to character to check
Exit...... A=Next program character
Modifies.. AF, HL
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to check the current program text character, whose address is supplied in register pair HL, against a reference character. The reference character is supplied as a single byte immediately following the <code>CALL</code> or <code>RST</code> instruction, for example:</p>
<pre><code>RST 08H
DEFB ","
</code></pre>
<p>If the characters do not match a "<code>Syntax error</code>" is generated (<a href="#4055h">4055H</a>), otherwise control transfers to the <a href="#chrgtr">CHRGTR</a> standard routine to fetch the next program character (<a href="#4666h">4666H</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5597h"></a><a name="user-content-getypr"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5597H
Name...... GETYPR
Entry..... None
Exit...... AF=Type
Modifies.. AF
</code></pre>
<p>Standard routine to return the type of the current operand, determined by <a href="#valtyp">VALTYP</a>, as follows:</p>
<pre><code>Integer..............A=FFH, Flag M,NZ,C
String...............A=00H, Flag P,Z,C
Single Precision ... A=01H, Flag P,NZ,C
Double Precision ... A=05H, Flag P,NZ,NC
</code></pre>

<p><a name="user-content-55a8h"></a><a name="user-content-call"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 55A8H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>CALL</code>" statement handler. The extended statement name, which is an unquoted string up to fifteen characters long terminated by a "(", ":" or end of line character (00H), is first copied from the program text to <a href="#procnm">PROCNM</a>, any unused bytes are zero filled. Bit 5 of each entry in <a href="#sltatr">SLTATR</a> is then examined for an extension ROM with a statement handler. If a suitable ROM is found its position in <a href="#sltatr">SLTATR</a> is converted to a Slot ID in register A and a ROM base address in register H (<a href="#7e2ah">7E2AH</a>). The statement handler address is read from ROM locations four and five (<a href="#7e1ah">7E1AH</a>) and placed in register pair IX. The Slot ID is placed in the high byte of register pair IY and the ROM statement handler called via the <a href="#calslt">CALSLT</a> standard routine.</p>
<p>The ROM will examine the statement name and return Flag C if it does not recognize it, otherwise it performs the required operation. If the ROM call fails the search of <a href="#sltatr">SLTATR</a> continues until the table is exhausted whereupon a "<code>Syntax error</code>" is generated (<a href="#4055h">4055H</a>). If the ROM call is successful the handler terminates.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-55f8h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 55F8H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the device name parser (<a href="#6f15h">6F15H</a>) when it cannot recognize a device name found in the program text. Upon entry register pair HL points to the first character of the name and register B holds its length. The name is first copied to <a href="#procnm">PROCNM</a> and terminated by a zero byte. Bit 6 of each entry in <a href="#sltatr">SLTATR</a> is then examined for an extension ROM with a device handler. If a suitable ROM is found its position in <a href="#sltatr">SLTATR</a> is converted to a Slot ID in register A and a ROM base address in register H (<a href="#7e2ah">7E2AH</a>). The device handler address is read from ROM locations six and seven (<a href="#7e1ah">7E1AH</a>) and placed in register pair IX. The Slot ID is placed in the high byte of register pair IY, the unknown device code (FFH) in register A and the ROM device handler called via the <a href="#calslt">CALSLT</a> standard routine.</p>
<p>The ROM will examine the device name and return Flag C if it does not recognize it, otherwise it returns its own internal code from zero to three. If the ROM call fails the search of <a href="#sltatr">SLTATR</a> continues until the table is exhausted whereupon a "<code>Bad file name</code>" error is generated (<a href="#6e6bh">6E6BH</a>). If the ROM call is successful the ROM's internal code is added to its <a href="#sltatr">SLTATR</a> position, multiplied by a factor of four, to produce a global device code' The base code for each entry in <a href="#sltatr">SLTATR</a> is shown below in hexadecimal. The "SS" and "PS" markers show the corresponding Secondary and Primary Slot numbers, each slot is composed of four pages:</p>
<p><a name="user-content-figure44"></a><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/a7bf212de1acb533cf144d7dc93ce6c7654563d1/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830354634342e737667"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/a7bf212de1acb533cf144d7dc93ce6c7654563d1/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830354634342e737667" alt="" data-canonical-src="https://rawgit.com/oraculo666/the-msx-red-book/master/images/CH05F44.svg" style="max-width:100%;"></a></p>
<p><strong>Figure 44:</strong> Device Codes</p>
<p>The global device code is used by the Interpreter until the time comes for the ROM to perform an actual device operation. It is then converted back into the ROM's Slot ID, base address and internal device code to perform the ROM access. Note that the codes from 0 to 8 are reserved for disk drive identifiers and those from FCH to FFH for the standard devices GRP, CRT, LPT and CAS. With the current MSX hardware structure these codes correspond to physically improbable ROM configurations and are therefore safe to be used for specific purposes by the Interpreter.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-564ah"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 564AH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the function dispatcher (<a href="#6f8fh">6F8FH</a>) when it encounters a device code not belonging to one of the standard devices. The device code is first converted to a <a href="#sltatr">SLTATR</a> position and then to a Slot ID in register A and ROM base address in register H (7E2DH). The ROM device handler address is read from ROM locations six and seven (<a href="#7e1ah">7E1AH</a>) and placed in register pair IX. The Slot ID is placed in the high byte of register pair IY, the ROM's internal device code in DEVICE and the ROM device handler called via the <a href="#calslt">CALSLT</a> standard routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-566ch"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 566CH
</code></pre>
<p>This entry point to the macro language parser is used by the "<code>DRAW</code>" statement handler, a later entry point (<a href="#56a2h">56A2H</a>) is used by the "<code>PLAY</code>" statement handler. The command string is evaluated (<a href="#4c64h">4C64H</a>) and its storage freed (<a href="#67d0h">67D0H</a>). After pushing a zero termination block onto the Z80 stack the length and address of the string body are placed in <a href="#mcllen">MCLLEN</a> and <a href="#mclptr">MCLPTR</a> and control drops into the parser mainloop.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-56a2h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 56A2H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the macro language parser mainloop, it is used to process the command string associated with a "<code>DRAW</code>" or "<code>PLAY</code>" statement' On entry the string length is in <a href="#mcllen">MCLLEN</a>, the string address is in <a href="#mclptr">MCLPTR</a> and the address of the relevant command table is in <a href="#mcltab">MCLTAB</a>. The command tables contain the legal command letters, together with the associated command handler addresses, for each statement. The "<code>DRAW</code>" table is at 5D83H and the "<code>PLAY</code>" table at 752EH.</p>
<p>The parser mainloop first fetches the next character from the command string (<a href="#56eeh">56EEH</a>). If there are no more characters left the next string descriptor is popped from the stack (568CH). If this is zero the parser terminates (5709H) if <a href="#mclflg">MCLFLG</a> shows a "<code>DRAW</code>" statement to be active, otherwise control transfers back to the "<code>PLAY</code>" statement handler (7494H).</p>
<p>Assuming a command character exists the current command table is searched to check its legality, if no match is found an "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH). The command table entry is then examined, if bit 7 is set the command takes an optional numeric parameter. If this is present it is collected and placed in register pair DE (571CH), otherwise a default value of one is taken. After pushing a return to the start of the parser mainloop onto the Z80 stack control transfers to the command handler at the address taken from the command table.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-56eeh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 56EEH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the macro language parser to fetch the next character from the command string. If <a href="#mcllen">MCLLEN</a> is zero the routine terminates with Flag Z, there are no characters left. Otherwise the next character is taken from the address contained in <a href="#mclptr">MCLPTR</a> and returned in register A, if the character is lower case it is converted to upper case. <a href="#mclptr">MCLPTR</a> is then incremented and <a href="#mcllen">MCLLEN</a> decrement Ed.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-570bh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 570BH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the macro language parser to return an unwanted character to the command string. <a href="#mcllen">MCLLEN</a> is incremented and <a href="#mclptr">MCLPTR</a> decremented.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5719h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5719H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the macro language parser to collect a numeric parameter from the command string. The result is a signed integer and is returned in register pair DE, it cannot be an expression. The first character is taken and examined, if it is a "+" it is ignored and the next character taken (<a href="#5719h">5719H</a>). If it is a "-" a return is set up to the negation routine (5795H) and the next character taken (<a href="#5719h">5719H</a>). If it is an "=" the value of the following Variable is returned (<a href="#577ah">577AH</a>). Otherwise successive characters are taken and a binary product accumulated until a non-numeric character is found.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-575ah"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 575AH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the macro language parser "=" and "X" handlers. The Variable name is copied to <a href="#buf">BUF</a> until the ";" delimiter is found, if this takes more than thirty-nine characters to find an "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH). Otherwise control transfers to the Factor Evaluator Variable handler (<a href="#4e9bh">4E9BH</a>) and the Variable contents are returned in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-577ah"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 577AH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the macro language parser to process the "=" character in a command parameter. The Variable's value is obtained (<a href="#575ah">575AH</a>), converted to an integer (<a href="#2f8ah">2F8AH</a>) and placed in register pair DE.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5782h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5782H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the macro language parser to process the "X" command. The Variable is processed (<a href="#575ah">575AH</a>) and, after checking that stack space is available (<a href="#625eh">625EH</a>), the current contents of <a href="#mcllen">MCLLEN</a> and <a href="#mclptr">MCLPTR</a> are stacked. Control then transfers to the parser entry point (5679H) to obtain the Variable's descriptor and process the new command string.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-579ch"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 579CH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by various graphics statements to evaluate a coordinate pair in the program text. The coordinates must be parenthesized with a comma separating the component operands. If the coordinate pair is preceded by a "<code>STEP</code>" token (DCH) each component value is added to the corresponding component of the current graphics coordinates in <a href="#grpacx">GRPACX</a> and <a href="#grpacy">GRPACY</a>, otherwise the absolute values are returned. The X coordinate is returned in <a href="#grpacx">GRPACX</a>, <a href="#gxpos">GXPOS</a> and register pair BC. The Y coordinate is returned in <a href="#grpacy">GRPACY</a>, <a href="#gypos">GYPOS</a> and register pair DE.</p>
<p>There are two entry points to the routine, the one which is used depends on whether the caller is expecting more than one coordinate pair. The "<code>LINE</code>" statement, for example, expects two coordinate pairs the first of which is the more flexible. The entry point at 579CH is used to collect the first coordinate pair and will accept the characters "-" or "@-" as representing the current graphics coordinates. The entry point at 57ABH is used for the second coordinate pair and requires an explicit operand.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-57e5h"></a><a name="user-content-preset"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 57E5H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>PRESET</code>" statement handler. The current background colour is taken from <a href="#bakclr">BAKCLR</a> and control drops into the "<code>PSET</code>" handler.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-57eah"></a><a name="user-content-pset"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 57EAH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>PSET</code>" statement handler. After the coordinate pair has been evaluated (57ABH) the current foreground colour is taken from <a href="#forclr">FORCLR</a> and used as the default when setting the ink colour (<a href="#5850h">5850H</a>). The current graphics coordinates are converted to a physical address, via the <a href="#scalxy">SCALXY</a> and <a href="#mapxyc">MAPXYC</a> standard routines, and the colour of the current pixel set via the <a href="#setc">SETC</a> standard routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5803h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5803H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>POINT</code>" function. The current contents of <a href="#cloc">CLOC</a>, <a href="#cmask">CMASK</a>, <a href="#gypos">GYPOS</a>, <a href="#gxpos">GXPOS</a>, <a href="#grpacy">GRPACY</a> and <a href="#grpacx">GRPACX</a> are stacked and the coordinate pair operand evaluated (57ABH). The colour of the new pixel is read via the <a href="#scalxy">SCALXY</a>, <a href="#mapxyc">MAPXYC</a> and <a href="#readc">READC</a> standard routines and placed in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> as an integer (2F99H), the old coordinate values are then popped and restored. Note that a value of -1 is returned if the point coordinates are outside the screen.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5850h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5850H
</code></pre>
<p>This graphics routine is used to evaluate an optional colour operand in the program text and to make it the current ink colour. After checking the screen mode (<a href="#59bch">59BCH</a>) the colour operand is evaluated (521CH) and placed in <a href="#atrbyt">ATRBYT</a>. If no operand exists the colour code supplied in register A is placed in <a href="#atrbyt">ATRBYT</a> instead.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5871h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5871H
</code></pre>
<p>This graphics routine returns the difference between the contents of <a href="#gxpos">GXPOS</a> and register pair BC in register pair HL. If the result is negative (<a href="#gxpos">GXPOS</a>&lt;BC) it is negated to produce the absolute magnitude and Flag C is returned.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5883h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5883H
</code></pre>
<p>This graphics routine returns the difference between the contents of <a href="#gypos">GYPOS</a> and register pair DE in register pair HL. If the result is negative (<a href="#gypos">GYPOS</a>&lt;DE) it is negated to produce the absolute magnitude and Flag C is returned.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-588eh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 588EH
</code></pre>
<p>This graphics routine swaps the contents of <a href="#gypos">GYPOS</a> and register pair DE.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5898h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5898H
</code></pre>
<p>This graphics routine first swaps the contents of <a href="#gypos">GYPOS</a> and register pair DE (<a href="#588eh">588EH</a>) then swaps the contents of <a href="#gxpos">GXPOS</a> and register pair BC. When entered at 589BH only the second operation is performed.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-58a7h"></a><a name="user-content-line"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 58A7H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>LINE</code>" statement handler. The first coordinate pair (X1,Y1) is evaluated (<a href="#579ch">579CH</a>) and placed in register pairs BC,DE. After checking for the "-" token (F2H) the second coordinate pair (X2,Y2) is evaluated (57ABH) and left in <a href="#grpacx">GRPACX</a>, <a href="#grpacy">GRPACY</a> and <a href="#gxpos">GXPOS</a>, <a href="#gypos">GYPOS</a>. After setting the ink colour (584DH) the program text is checked for a following "B" or "BF" option and either the box (<a href="#5912h">5912H</a>), boxfill (<a href="#58bfh">58BFH</a>) or linedraw (<a href="#58fch">58FCH</a>) operation performed. None of these operations affects the current graphics coordinates in <a href="#grpacx">GRPACX</a> and <a href="#grpacy">GRPACY</a>, these are left at X2,Y2.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-58bfh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 58BFH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine performs the boxfill operation. Given that the supplied coordinate pairs define diagonally opposed points of the box two quantities must be derived from them. The horizontal size of the box is obtained from the difference between X1 and X2, this gives the number of pixels to set per row. The vertical size is obtained from the difference between Y1 and Y2 giving the number of rows required. Starting at the physical address of X1,Y1, and moving successively lower via the <a href="#downc">DOWNC</a> standard routine, the required number of pixel rows are filled in by repeated use of the <a href="#nsetcx">NSETCX</a> standard routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-58fch"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 58FCH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine performs the linedraw operation. After drawing the line (<a href="#593ch">593CH</a>) <a href="#gxpos">GXPOS</a> and <a href="#gypos">GYPOS</a> are reset to X2,Y2 from <a href="#grpacx">GRPACX</a> and <a href="#grpacy">GRPACY</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5912h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5912H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine performs the box operation. The box is produced by drawing a line (<a href="#58fch">58FCH</a>) between each of the four corner points. The coordinates of each corner are derived from the initial operands by interchanging the relevant component of the pair. The drawing sequence is:</p>
<ol>
<li>X1,Y2 to X2,Y2</li>
<li>X1,Y1 to X2,Y1</li>
<li>X2,Y1 to X2,Y2</li>
<li>X1,Y1 to X1,Y2</li>
</ol>

<p><a name="user-content-593ch"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 593CH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine draws a line between the points X1,Y1, supplied in register pairs BC and DE and X2,Y2, supplied in <a href="#gxpos">GXPOS</a> and <a href="#gypos">GYPOS</a>. The operation of the drawing mainloop (5993H) is best illustrated by an example, say LINE(0,0)-(10,4). To reach the end point of the line from its start ten horizontal steps (X2- X1) and four downward steps (Y2-Y1) must be taken altogether. The best approximation to a straight line therefore requires two and a half horizontal steps for every downward step (X2-X1/Y2-Y1). While this is impossible in practice, as only integral steps can be taken, the correct ratio can be achieved on average.</p>
<p>The method employed is to add the Y difference to a counter each time a rightward step is taken. When the counter exceeds the value of the X difference it is reset and one downward step is taken, this is in effect an integer division of the two difference values. Sometimes downward steps will be produced every two rightward steps and sometimes every three rightward steps. The average, however, will be one downward step every two and a half rightward steps. An equivalent BASIC program is shown below with a slightly offset BASIC line for comparison:</p>
<pre><code>10 SCREEN 0
20 INPUT"START X,Y";X1,Y1
30 INPUT"END X,Y",X2,Y2
40 SCREEN 2
50 X=X1:Y=Y1:L=X2-X1:S=Y2-Y1:CTR=L/2
60 PSET(X,Y)
70 CTR=CTR+S:IF CTR&lt;L THEN 90
80 CTR=CTR-L:Y=Y+1
90 X=X+1:IF X&lt;=X2 THEN 60
100 LINE(X1,Y1+5)-(X2,Y2+5)
110 GOTO 110
</code></pre>
<p>The above example suffers from three limitations. The line must slope downwards, it must slope to the right and the slope cannot exceed forty-five degrees from the horizontal (one downward step for one rightward step).</p>
<p>The routine overcomes the first limitation by examining the Y1 and Y2 coordinates before drawing commences. If Y2 is greater than or equal to Y1, showing the line to slope upwards or to be horizontal, both coordinate pairs are exchanged. The line is now sloping downwards and will be drawn from the end point to the start.</p>
<p>The second limitation is overcome by examining X1 and X2 beforehand to determine which way the line is sloping. If X2 is greater than or equal to X1 the line slopes to the right and a Z80 JP to the <a href="#rightc">RIGHTC</a> standard routine is placed in <a href="#minupd">MINUPD</a>/<a href="#maxupd">MAXUPD</a> (see below) for use by the drawing mainloop, otherwise a JP to the <a href="#leftc">LEFTC</a> standard routine is placed there.</p>
<p>The third limitation is overcome by comparing the X coordinate difference to the Y coordinate difference before drawing to determine the slope steepness. If X2-X1 is smaller than Y2-Y1 the slope of the line is less than forty-five degrees from the horizontal. The simple method shown above for LINE(0,0)-(10,4) will not work for slopes greater than forty- five degrees as the maximum rate of descent is achieved when one downward step is taken for every horizontal step. It will work however if the step directions are exchanged. Thus LINE(0,0)-(4,10) requires one rightward step for every two and a half downward steps. <a href="#minupd">MINUPD</a> holds a Z80 JP to the "normal" step direction standard routine for the drawing mainloop and <a href="#maxupd">MAXUPD</a> holds a JP to the "slope" step direction standard routine. For shallow angles <a href="#minupd">MINUPD</a> will vector to <a href="#downc">DOWNC</a> and <a href="#maxupd">MAXUPD</a> to <a href="#leftc">LEFTC</a> or <a href="#rightc">RIGHTC</a>. For steep angles <a href="#minupd">MINUPD</a> will vector to <a href="#leftc">LEFTC</a> or <a href="#rightc">RIGHTC</a> and <a href="#maxupd">MAXUPD</a> to <a href="#downc">DOWNC</a>. For steep angles the counter values must also be exchanged, the X difference must now be added to the counter and the Y difference used as the counter limit. The variables <a href="#mindel">MINDEL</a> and <a href="#maxdel">MAXDEL</a> are used by the drawing mainloop to hold these counter values, <a href="#mindel">MINDEL</a> holds the smaller end point difference and <a href="#maxdel">MAXDEL</a> the larger.</p>
<p>An interesting point is that the reference counter, held in CTR in the above program and in register pair DE in the ROM, is preloaded with half the largest end point difference rather than being set to zero. This has the effect of splitting the first "stair" in the line into two sections, one at the start of the line and one at its end, and improving the line's appearance.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-59b4h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 59B4H
</code></pre>
<p>This graphics routine shifts the contents of register pair DE one bit to the right.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-59bch"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 59BCH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine generates an "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error (475AH) if the screen is not in <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> or <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-59c5h"></a><a name="user-content-paint"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 59C5H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>PAINT</code>" statement handler. The starting coordinate pair is evaluated (<a href="#579ch">579CH</a>), the ink colour set (584DH) and the optional boundary colour operand evaluated (521CH) and placed in <a href="#bdratr">BDRATR</a>. The starting coordinate pair is checked to ensure that it is within the screen (<a href="#5e91h">5E91H</a>) and is made the current pixel physical address by the <a href="#mapxyc">MAPXYC</a> standard routine. The distance to the right hand boundary is then measured (<a href="#5adch">5ADCH</a>) and, if it is zero, the handler terminates. Otherwise the distance to the left hand boundary is measured (<a href="#5aedh">5AEDH</a>) and the sum of the two placed in register pair DE as the zone width. The current position is then stacked twice (5ACEH), first with a termination flag (00H) and then with a down direction flag (40H). Control then transfers to the paint mainloop (<a href="#5a26h">5A26H</a>) with an up direction flag (C0H) in register B.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5a26h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5A26H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the paint mainloop. The zone width is held in register pair DE, the paint direction, up or down, in register B and the current pixel physical address is that of the pixel adjacent to the left hand boundary. A vertical step is taken to the next line, via the <a href="#tupc">TUPC</a> or <a href="#tdownc">TDOWNC</a> standard routines, and the distance to the right hand boundary measured (<a href="#5adch">5ADCH</a>). The distance to the left hand boundary is then measured and the line between the boundaries filled in (<a href="#5aedh">5AEDH</a>). If no change is found in the position of either boundary control transfers to the start of the mainloop to continue painting in the same direction. If a change is found an inflection has occurred and the appropriate action must be taken.</p>
<p>There are four types of inflection, LH or RH incursive, where the relevant boundary moves inward, and LH or RH excursive, where it moves outward. An example of each type is shown below with numbered zones indicating the order of painting during upward movement. A secondary zone is shown within each inflective region for completeness:</p>
<p><a name="user-content-figure45"></a><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/6df91f01aab8c89432dbe16ae0189de8e6d61e28/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830354634352e737667"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/6df91f01aab8c89432dbe16ae0189de8e6d61e28/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830354634352e737667" alt="" data-canonical-src="https://rawgit.com/oraculo666/the-msx-red-book/master/images/CH05F45.svg" style="max-width:100%;"></a></p>
<p><strong>Figure 45:</strong> Boundary Inflections</p>
<p>A LH excursion has occurred when the distance to the left hand boundary is non-zero, a RH excursion has occurred when the current zone width is greater than that of the previous line. Unless the excursion is less than two pixels, in which case it will be ignored, the current position (the bottom left of zone 3 in figure 45) is stacked (<a href="#5ac2h">5AC2H</a>), the paint direction reversed and painting restarts at the top left of the excursive region .</p>
<p>A RH incursion has occurred when the current zone width is smaller than that of the previous line. If the incursion is total, that is the current zone width is zero, a dead end has been reached and the last position and direction are popped (5AIFH) and painting restarts at that point. Otherwise the current position and direction are stacked (<a href="#5ac2h">5AC2H</a>) and painting restarts at the bottom left of the incursive region.</p>
<p>A LH incursion is dealt with automatically during the search for the right hand boundary and requires no explicit action by the paint mainloop.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5ac2h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5AC2H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the "<code>PAINT</code>" statement handler to save the current paint position and direction on the Z80 stack. The six byte parameter block is made up of the following:</p>
<pre><code>2 bytes ... Current contents of CLOC
1 byte  ... Current direction
1 byte  ... Current contents of CMASK
2 bytes ... Current zone width
</code></pre>
<p>After the parameters have been stacked a check is made that sufficient stack space still exists (<a href="#625eh">625EH</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5adch"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5ADCH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the "<code>PAINT</code>" statement handler to locate the right hand boundary. The zone width of the previous line is passed to the <a href="#scanr">SCANR</a> standard routine in register pair DE, this determines the maximum number of boundary colour pixels that may initially be skipped over. The returned skip count remainder is placed in <a href="#skpcnt">SKPCNT</a> and the number of non-boundary colour pixels traversed in <a href="#movcnt">MOVCNT</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5aedh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5AEDH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the "<code>PAINT</code>" statement handler to locate the left hand boundary. The end point of the right hand boundary search is temporarily saved and the starting point taken from <a href="#csavea">CSAVEA</a> and <a href="#csavem">CSAVEM</a> and made the current pixel physical address. The left hand boundary is then located via the <a href="#scanl">SCANL</a> standard routine, which also fills in the entire zone, and the right hand end point recovered and placed in <a href="#csavea">CSAVEA</a> and <a href="#csavem">CSAVEM</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5b0bh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5B0BH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the "<code>CIRCLE</code>" statement handler to negate the contents of register pair DE.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5b11h"></a><a name="user-content-circle"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5B11H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>CIRCLE</code>" statement handler. After evaluating the centre coordinate pair (<a href="#579ch">579CH</a>) the radius is evaluated (520FH), multiplied (<a href="#325ch">325CH</a>) by SIN(PI/4) and placed in <a href="#cnpnts">CNPNTS</a>. The ink colour is set (584DH), the start angle evaluated (<a href="#5d17h">5D17H</a>) and placed in <a href="#cstcnt">CSTCNT</a> and the end angle evaluated (<a href="#5d17h">5D17H</a>) and placed in <a href="#cencnt">CENCNT</a>. If the end angle is smaller than the start angle the two values are swapped and <a href="#cplotf">CPLOTF</a> is made non-zero. The aspect ratio is evaluated (<a href="#4c64h">4C64H</a>) and, if it is greater than one, its reciprocal is taken (3267H) and <a href="#csclxy">CSCLXY</a> is made non-zero to indicate an X axis squash. The aspect ratio is multiplied (<a href="#325ch">325CH</a>) by 256, converted to an integer (<a href="#2f8ah">2F8AH</a>) and placed in <a href="#aspect">ASPECT</a> as a single byte binary fraction. Register pairs HL and DE are set to the starting position on the circle perimeter (X=RADIUS,Y=0) and control drops into the circle mainloop.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5bbdh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5BBDH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the circle mainloop. Because of the high degree of symmetry in a circle it is only necessary to compute the coordinates of the arc from zero to forty-five degrees. The other seven segments are produced by rotation and reflection of these points. The parametric equation for a unit circle, with T the angle from zero to PI/4, is:</p>
<pre><code>X=COS(T)
Y=SIN(T)
</code></pre>
<p>Direct computation using this equation, or the corresponding functional form X=SQR(1-Y^2), is too slow, instead the first derivative is used:</p>
<pre><code> dx
---- = -Y/X
 dy
</code></pre>
<p>Given that the starting position is known (X=RADIUS,Y=0), the X coordinate change for each unit Y coordinate change may be computed using the derivative. Furthermore, because graphics resolution is limited to one pixel, it is only necessary to know when the sum of the X coordinate changes reaches unity and then to decrement the X coordinate. Therefore:</p>
<pre><code>Decrement X when (Y1/X)+(Y2/X)+(Y3/X)+... =&gt; 1
Therefore decrement when (Y1+Y2+Y3+...)/X =&gt; 1
Therefore decrement when     Y1+Y2+Y3+... =&gt; X
</code></pre>
<p>All that is required to identify an X coordinate change is to totalize the Y coordinate values from each step until the X coordinate value is exceeded. The circle mainloop holds the X coordinate in register pair HL, the Y coordinate in register pair DE and the running total in <a href="#crcsum">CRCSUM</a>. An equivalent BASIC program for a circle of arbitrary radius 160 pixels is:</p>
<pre><code>10 SCREEN 2
20 X=160:Y=0:CRCSUM=0
30 PSET(X,191-Y)
40 CRCSUM=CRCSUM+Y :Y=Y+1
50 IF CRCSUM&lt;X THEN 30
60 CRCSUM=CRCSUM-X:X=X-1
70 IF X&gt;Y THEN 30
80 CIRCLE(0,191),155
90 GOTO 90
</code></pre>
<p>The coordinate pairs generated by the mainloop are those of a "virtual" circle, such tasks as axial reflection, elliptic squash and centre translation are handled at a lower level (<a href="#5c06h">5C06H</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5c06h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5C06H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used to by the circle mainloop to convert a coordinate pair, in register pairs HL and DE, into eight symmetric points on the screen. The Y coordinate is initially negated (<a href="#5b0bh">5B0BH</a>), reflecting it about the X axis, and the first four points produced by successive clockwise rotations through ninety degrees (5C48H). The Y coordinate is then negated again (<a href="#5b0bh">5B0BH</a>) and a further four points produced (5C48H).</p>
<p>Clockwise rotation is performed by exchanging the X and Y coordinates and negating the new Y coordinate, thus a point (40,10) would become (10,-40). Assuming an aspect ratio of 0.5, for example, the complete sequence of eight points would therefore be:</p>
<ol>
<li>X,-Y*0.5</li>
<li>-Y,-X*0.5</li>
<li>-X, Y*0.5</li>
<li>Y, X*0.5</li>
<li>Y,-X*0.5</li>
<li>-X,-Y*0.5</li>
<li>-Y, X*0.5</li>
<li>X, Y*0.5</li>
</ol>
<p>It can be seen from the above that, ignoring the sign of the coordinates for the moment, there are only four terms involved. Therefore, rather than performing the relatively slow aspect ratio multiplication (<a href="#5cebh">5CEBH</a>) for each point, the terms X*0.5 and Y*0.5 can be prepared in advance and the complete sequence generated by interchanging and negating the four terms. With the aspect ratio shown above the initial conditions are set up so that register pair HL=X, register pair DE=-Y*0.5, CXOFF=Y and CYOFF=X*0.5 and successive points are produced by the operations:</p>
<ol>
<li>Exchange HL and CXOFF, negate HL.</li>
<li>Exchange DE and CYOFF, negate DE.</li>
</ol>
<p>In parallel with the computation of each circle coordinate the number of points required to reach the start of the segment containing the point is kept in <a href="#cpcnt8">CPCNT8</a>. This will initially be zero and will increase by 2*RADIUS*SIN(PI/4) as each ninety degree rotation is made. As each of the eight points is produced its Y coordinate value is added to the contents of <a href="#cpcnt8">CPCNT8</a> and compared to the start and end angles to determine the appropriate course of action. If the point is between the two angles and <a href="#cplotf">CPLOTF</a> is zero, or if it is outside the angles and <a href="#cplotf">CPLOTF</a> is non-zero, the coordinates are added to the circle centre coordinates (5CDCH) and the point set via the <a href="#scalxy">SCALXY</a>, <a href="#mapxyc">MAPXYC</a> and <a href="#setc">SETC</a> standard routines. If the point is equal to either of the two angles, and the associated bit is set in <a href="#clinef">CLINEF</a>, the coordinates are added to the circle centre coordinates (5CDCH) and a line drawn to the centre (<a href="#593ch">593CH</a>). If none of these conditions is applicable no action is taken other than to proceed to the next point.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5cebh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5CEBH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine multiplies the coordinate value supplied in register pair DE by the aspect ratio contained in <a href="#aspect">ASPECT</a>, the result is returned in register pair DE. The standard binary shift and add method is used but the operation is performed as two single byte multiplications to avoid overflow problems.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5d17h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5D17H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the "<code>CIRCLE</code>" statement handler to convert an angle operand to the form required by the circle mainloop, the result is returned in register pair DE. While the method used is basically sound, and eliminates one trigonometric computation per angle, the results produced are inaccurate. This is demonstrated by the following example which draws a line to the true thirty degree point on a circle's perimeter:</p>
<pre><code>10 SCREEN 2
20 PI = 4 * ATN(1)
30 CIRCLE(100,100),80,,PI/6
40 LINE(100,100)-(100+80*COS(PI/6),100-80*SIN(PI/6))
50 GOTO 50
</code></pre>
<p>The result that the routine should produce is the number of points that must be produced by the circle mainloop before the required angle is reached. This can be computed by first noting that there will be INT(ANGLE/(PI/4)) forty-five degree segments prior to the segment containing the required angle. Furthermore each forty-five segment will contain RADIUS*SIN(PI/4) points as this is the value of the terminating Y coordinate. Therefore the number of points required to reach the start of the segment containing the angle is the product of these two numbers. The total count is produced by adding this figure to the number of points required to cover any remaining angle within the final segment, that is RADIUS*SIN(REMAINING ANGLE) points.</p>
<p>Unfortunately the routine computes the number of points within a segment by linear approximation from the total segment size on the mistaken assumption that successive points subtend equal angles. Thus in the above example the point count computed for the angle is 30/45*(80*0.707107)=37 instead of the correct value of forty. The error produced by the routine is therefore at a maximum at the centre of each forty-five degree segment and reduces to zero at the end points.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5d6eh"></a><a name="user-content-draw"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5D6EH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>DRAW</code>" statement handler. Register pair DE is set to point to the command table at 5D83H and control transfers to the macro language parser (<a href="#566ch">566CH</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5d83h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5D83H
</code></pre>
<p>This table contains the valid command letters and associated addresses for the "<code>DRAW</code>" statement commands. Those commands which takes a parameter, and consequently have bit 7 set in the table, are shown with an asterisk:</p>
<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>CMD</th>
<th>TO</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>

<td>U*</td>

</tr>
<tr>
<td>D*</td>
<td>5DB4H</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>L*</td>
<td>5DB9H</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>R*</td>
<td>5DBCH</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>M</td>
<td>5DD8H</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>E*</td>
<td>5DCAH</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>F*</td>

</tr>
<tr>

</tr>

</tr>

</tr>

</tr>

</tr>

</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<p><a name="user-content-5db1h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5DB1H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>DRAW</code>" statement "<code>U</code>" command handler. The operation of the "<code>D</code>", "<code>L</code>", "<code>R</code>", "<code>E</code>", "<code>F</code>", "<code>G</code>" and "<code>H</code>" commands is very similar so no separate description of their handlers is given. The optional numeric parameter is supplied by the macro language parser in register pair DE. This initial parameter is modified by a given handler into a horizontal offset in register pair BC and a vertical offset in register pair DE. For example if leftward or upward movement is required the parameter is negated (<a href="#5b0bh">5B0BH</a>), if diagonal movement is required the parameter is duplicated so that equal horizontal and vertical offsets are produced. Once the offsets have been prepared control transfers to the line drawing routine (5DFFH).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5dd8h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5DD8H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>DRAW</code>" statement "<code>M</code>" command handler. The character following the command letter is examined then the two parameters collected from the command string (<a href="#5719h">5719H</a>). If the initial character is "+" or "-" the parameters are regarded as offsets and are scaled (<a href="#5e66h">5E66H</a>), rotated through successive ninety degree steps as determined by <a href="#drwang">DRWANG</a> and then added to the current graphics coordinates (5CDCH) to determine the termination point. If <a href="#drwflg">DRWFLG</a> shows the "<code>B</code>" mode to be inactive a line is then drawn (5CCDH) from the current graphics coordinates to the termination point. If <a href="#drwflg">DRWFLG</a> shows the "<code>N</code>" mode to be inactive the termination coordinates are placed in <a href="#grpacx">GRPACX</a> and <a href="#grpacy">GRPACY</a> to become the new current graphics coordinates. Finally <a href="#drwflg">DRWFLG</a> is zeroed, turning the "<code>B</code>" and "<code>N</code>" modes off, and the handler terminates.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5e42h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5E42H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>DRAW</code>" statement "<code>N</code>" command handler, <a href="#drwflg">DRWFLG</a> is simply set to 40H.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5e46h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5E46H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>DRAW</code>" statement "<code>B</code>" command handler, <a href="#drwflg">DRWFLG</a> is simply set to 80H.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5e4eh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5E4EH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>DRAW</code>" statement "<code>A</code>" command handler. The parameter is checked for magnitude and placed in <a href="#drwang">DRWANG</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5e59h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5E59H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>DRAW</code>" statement "<code>S</code>" command handler. The parameter is checked for magnitude and placed in <a href="#drwscl">DRWSCL</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5e66h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5E66H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the "<code>DRAW</code>" statement "<code>U</code>", "<code>D</code>", "<code>L</code>", "<code>R</code>", "<code>E</code>", "<code>F</code>", "<code>G</code>", "<code>H</code>" and "<code>M</code>" (in offset mode) command handlers to scale the offset supplied in register pair DE by the contents of <a href="#drwscl">DRWSCL</a>. Unless <a href="#drwscl">DRWSCL</a> is zero, in which case the routine simply terminates, the offset is multiplied using repeated addition and then divided by four (<a href="#59b4h">59B4H</a>). To eliminate scaling an "<code>S0</code>" or "<code>S4</code>" command should be used.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5e87h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5E87H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>DRAW</code>" statement "<code>C</code>" command handler. The parameter is placed in <a href="#atrbyt">ATRBYT</a> via the <a href="#setatr">SETATR</a> standard routine. There is no check on the MSB of the parameter so illegal values such as "<code>C265</code>" will be accepted without an error message.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5e91h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5E91H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the "<code>PAINT</code>" statement handler to check, via the <a href="#scalxy">SCALXY</a> standard routine, that the coordinates in register pairs BC and DE are within the screen. If not an "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5e9fh"></a><a name="user-content-dim"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5E9FH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>DIM</code>" statement handler. A return is set up to 5E9AH, so that multiple Arrays can be processed, <a href="#dimflg">DIMFLG</a> is made non-zero and control drops into the Variable search routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5ea4h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5EA4H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the Variable search routine. On entry register pair HL points to the first character of the Variable name in the program text. On exit register pair HL points to the character following the name and register pair DE to the first byte of the Variable contents in the Variable Storage Area. The first character of the name is taken from the program text, checked to ensure that it is upper case alphabetic (<a href="#64a7h">64A7H</a>) and placed in register C. The optional second character, with a default value of zero, is placed in register B, this character may be alphabetic or numeric. Any further alphanumeric characters are then simply skipped over. If a type suffix character ("%", "$", "!" or "#") follows the name this is converted to the corresponding type code (2, 3, 4 or 8) and placed in <a href="#valtyp">VALTYP</a>. Otherwise the Variable's default type is taken from <a href="#deftbl">DEFTBL</a> using the first letter of the name to locate the appropriate entry.</p>
<p><a href="#subflg">SUBFLG</a> is then checked to determine how any parenthesized subscript following the name should be treated. This flag is normally zero but is modified by the "<code>ERASE</code>" (01H), "<code>FOR</code>" (64H), "<code>FN</code>" (80H) or "<code>DEF FN</code>" (80H) statement handlers to force a particular course of action. In the "<code>ERASE</code>" case control transfers straight to the Array search routine (5FE8H), no parenthesized subscript need be present. In the "<code>FOR</code>", "<code>FN</code>" and "<code>DEF FN</code>" cases control transfers straight to the simple Variable search routine (<a href="#5f08h">5F08H</a>), no check is made for a parenthesized subscript. Assuming that the situation is normal the program text is checked for the characters "(" or "[". If either is present control transfers to the Array search routine (<a href="#5fbah">5FBAH</a>), otherwise control drops into the simple Variable search routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5f08h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5F08H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the simple Variable search routine. There are four types of simple Variable each composed of a header followed by the Variable contents. The first byte of the header contains the type code and the next two bytes the Variable name. The contents of the Variable will be one of the three standard numeric forms or, for the string type, the length and address of the string. Each of the four types is shown below:</p>
<p><a name="user-content-figure46"></a><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/4b3dccae6a7aa80bbab4a5dddedcbf1891839b38/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830354634362e737667"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/4b3dccae6a7aa80bbab4a5dddedcbf1891839b38/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830354634362e737667" alt="" data-canonical-src="https://rawgit.com/oraculo666/the-msx-red-book/master/images/CH05F46.svg" style="max-width:100%;"></a></p>
<p><strong>Figure 46:</strong> Simple Variables</p>
<p><a href="#nofuns">NOFUNS</a> is first checked to determine whether a user defined function is currently being evaluated. If so the search is carried out on the contents of <a href="#parm1">PARM1</a> first of all, only if this fails will it move onto the main Variable Storage Area. A linear search method is used, the two name characters and type byte of each Variable in the storage area are compared to the reference characters and type until a match is found or the end of the storage area is reached. If the search is successful the routine terminates with the address of the first byte of the Variable contents in register pair DE. If the search is unsuccessful the Array Storage Area is moved upwards and the new Variable is added to the end of the existing ones and initialized to zero.</p>
<p>There are two exceptions to this automatic creation of a new Variable. If the search is being carried out by the "<code>VARPTR</code>" function, and this is determined by examining the return address, no Variable will be created. Instead the routine terminates with register pair DE set to zero (5F61H) causing a subsequent "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error. The second exception occurs when the search is being carried out by the Factor Evaluator, that is when the Variable is newly declared inside an expression. In this case <a href="#dac">DAC</a> is zeroed for numeric types, and loaded with the address of a dummy zero length descriptor for a string type, thus returning a zero result (5FA7H). These actions are designed to prevent the Expression Evaluator creating a new Variable ("<code>VARPTR</code>") is the only function to take a Variable argument directly rather than via an expression and so requires separate protection). If this were not so then assignment to an Array, via the "<code>LET</code>" statement handler, would fail as any simple Variable created during expression evaluation would change the Array's address.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-5fbah"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 5FBAH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the Array search routine. There are four types of Array each composed of a header plus a number of elements. The first byte of the header contains the type code, the next two bytes the Array name and the next two the offset to the start of the following Array. This is followed by a single byte containing the dimensionality of the Array and the element count list. Each two byte element count contains the maximum number of elements per dimension. These are stored in reverse order with the first one corresponding to the last subscript. The contents of each Array element are identical to the contents of the corresponding simple Variable. The integer Array AB%(3,4) is shown below with each element identified by its subscripts, high memory is towards the top of the page:</p>
<p><a name="user-content-figure47"></a><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/fa7cf27704ed59008e2d36ac6843cdb709b60784/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830354634372e737667"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/fa7cf27704ed59008e2d36ac6843cdb709b60784/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830354634372e737667" alt="" data-canonical-src="https://rawgit.com/oraculo666/the-msx-red-book/master/images/CH05F47.svg" style="max-width:100%;"></a></p>
<p><strong>Figure 47:</strong> Integer Array</p>
<p>Each subscript is evaluated, converted to an integer (<a href="#4755h">4755H</a>) and pushed onto the Z80 stack until a closing parenthesis is found, it need not match the opening one. A linear search is then carried out on the Array Storage Area for a match with the two name characters and the type. If the search is successful <a href="#dimflg">DIMFLG</a> is checked and a "<code>Redimensioned array</code>" error generated (<a href="#405eh">405EH</a>) if it shows a "<code>DIM</code>" statement to be active. Unless an "<code>ERASE</code>" statement is active, in which case the routine terminates with register pair BC pointing to the start of the Array (3297H), the dimensionality of the Array is then checked against the subscript count and a "<code>Subscript out of range</code>" error generated if they fail to match. Assuming these tests are passed control transfers to the element address computation point (607DH).</p>
<p>If the search is unsuccessful and an "<code>ERASE</code>" statement is active an "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH), otherwise the new Array is added to the end of the existing Array Storage Area. Initialization of the new Array proceeds by storing the two name characters, the type code and the dimensionality (the subscript count) followed by the element count for each dimension. If <a href="#dimflg">DIMFLG</a> shows a "<code>DIM</code>" statement to be active the element counts are determined by the subscripts. If the Array is being created by default, with a statement such as "<code>A(1,2,3)=5</code>" for example, a default value of eleven is used. As each element count is stored the total size of the Array is accumulated in register pair DE by successive multiplications (<a href="#314ah">314AH</a>) of the element counts and the element size (the Array type). After a check that this amount of memory is available (6267H) <a href="#strend">STREND</a> is increased the new area is zeroed and the Array size is stored, in slightly modified form, immediately after the two name characters. Unless the Array is being created by default, in which case the element address must be computed, the routine then terminates.</p>
<p>This is the element address computation point of the Array search routine. The location of a particular element within an Array involves the multiplication (<a href="#314ah">314AH</a>) of subscripts, element counts and element sizes. As there are a variety of ways this could be done the actual method used is best illustrated with an example. The location of element (1,2,3) in a 4*5*6 Array would initially be computed as (((3*5)+2)*4)+1. This is then multiplied by the element size (type) and added to the Array base address to obtain the address of the required element. The computation method is an optimized form which minimizes the number of steps needed, it is equivalent to evaluating (3*(4*5))+(2*4)+(1). The element address is returned in register pair DE.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-60b1h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 60B1H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>PRINT USING</code>" statement handler. Control transfers here from the general "<code>PRINT</code>" statement handler after the applicable output device has been set up. Upon termination control passes back to the general "<code>PRINT</code>" statement exit point (<a href="#4affh">4AFFH</a>) to restore the normal video output. The format string is evaluated (4C65H) and the address and length of the string body obtained from the descriptor. The program text pointer is then temporarily saved. Each character of the format string is examined until one of the possible template characters is found. If the character does not belong in a template it is simply output via the <a href="#outdo">OUTDO</a> standard routine. Once the start of a template is found this is scanned along until a non-template character is found. Control then passes to the numeric output routine (6192H) or the string output routine (6211H).</p>
<p>In either case the program text pointer is restored to register pair HL and the next operand evaluated (<a href="#4c64h">4C64H</a>). For numeric output the information gained from the template scan is passed to the numeric conversion routine (3426H) in registers A, B and C and the resulting string displayed (<a href="#6678h">6678H</a>). For string output the required character count is passed to the "<code>LEFT$</code>" statement handler (6868H) in register C and the resulting string displayed (667BH). For either type of output the program text and format string are then examined to determine whether there are any further characters. If no operands exist the handler terminates. If the format string has been exhausted then it is restarted from the beginning (60BFH), otherwise scanning continues from the current position for the next operand (60f6H).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6250h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6250H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Interpreter Mainloop and the Variable search routine to move a block of memory upwards. A check is first made to ensure that sufficient memory exists (6267H) and then the block of memory is moved. The top source address is supplied in register pair BC and the top destination address in register pair HL. Copying stops when the contents of register pair BC equal those of register pair DE.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-625eh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 625EH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used to check that sufficient memory is available between the top of the Array Storage Area and the base of the Z80 stack. On entry register C contains the number of words the caller requires. If this would narrow the gap to less than two hundred bytes an "<code>Out of memory</code>" error is generated.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6286h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6286H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>NEW</code>" statement handler. <a href="#trcflg">TRCFLG</a>, <a href="#autflg">AUTFLG</a> and <a href="#ptrflg">PTRFLG</a> are zeroed and the zero end link is placed at the start of the Program Text Area. <a href="#vartab">VARTAB</a> is set to point to the byte following the end link and control drops into the run-clear routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-629ah"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 629AH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the "<code>NEW</code>", "<code>RUN</code>" and "<code>CLEAR</code>" statement handlers to initialize the Interpreter variables. All interrupts are cleared (636EH) and the default Variable types in <a href="#deftbl">DEFTBL</a> set to double precision. <a href="#rndx">RNDX</a> is reset (<a href="#2c24h">2C24H</a>) and <a href="#oneflg">ONEFLG</a>, <a href="#onelin">ONELIN</a> and <a href="#oldtxt">OLDTXT</a> are zeroed. <a href="#memsiz">MEMSIZ</a> is copied to <a href="#fretop">FRETOP</a> to clear the String Storage Area and <a href="#datptr">DATPTR</a> set to the start of the Program Text Area (<a href="#63c9h">63C9H</a>). The contents of <a href="#vartab">VARTAB</a> are copied into <a href="#arytab">ARYTAB</a> and <a href="#strend">STREND</a>, to clear any Variables, all the I/O buffers are closed (<a href="#6c1ch">6C1CH</a>) and <a href="#nlonly">NLONLY</a> is reset. <a href="#savstk">SAVSTK</a> and the Z80 SP are reset from <a href="#stktop">STKTOP</a> and <a href="#temppt">TEMPPT</a> is reset to the start of <a href="#tempst">TEMPST</a> to clear any string descriptors. The printer is shut down (<a href="#7304h">7304H</a>) and output restored to the screen (<a href="#4affh">4AFFH</a>). Finally <a href="#prmlen">PRMLEN</a>, <a href="#nofuns">NOFUNS</a>, <a href="#prmln2">PRMLN2</a>, <a href="#funact">FUNACT</a>, <a href="#prmstk">PRMSTK</a> and <a href="#subflg">SUBFLG</a> are zeroed and the routine terminates.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-631bh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 631BH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the "<code>DEVICE ON</code>" statement handlers to enable an interrupt source, the address of the relevant device's <a href="#trptbl">TRPTBL</a>. status byte is supplied in register pair HL. Interrupts are enabled by setting bit 0 of the status byte. Bits 1 and 2 are then examined and, if the device has been stopped and an interrupt has occurred, <a href="#ongsbf">ONGSBF</a> is incremented (634FH) so that the Runloop will process it at the end of the statement. Finally bit 1 of the status byte is reset to release any existing stop condition.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-632eh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 632EH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the "<code>DEVICE OFF</code>" statement handlers to disable an interrupt source, the address of the relevant device's <a href="#trptbl">TRPTBL</a> status byte is supplied in register pair HL. Bits 0 and 2 are examined to determine whether an interrupt has occurred since the end of the last statement, if so <a href="#ongsbf">ONGSBF</a> is decremented (6362H) to prevent the Runloop from picking it up. The status byte is then zeroed.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6331h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6331H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the "<code>DEVICE STOP</code>" statement handlers to suspend processing of interrupts from an interrupt source, the address of the relevant device's <a href="#trptbl">TRPTBL</a> status byte is supplied in register pair HL. Bits 0 and 2 are examined to determine whether an interrupt has occurred since the end of the last statement, if so <a href="#ongsbf">ONGSBF</a> is decremented (6362H) to prevent the Runloop from picking it up. Bit 1 of the status byte is then set.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-633eh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 633EH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the "<code>RETURN</code>" statement handler to release the temporary stop condition imposed during interrupt driven BASIC subroutines, the address of the relevant device's <a href="#trptbl">TRPTBL</a> status byte is supplied in register pair HL. Bits 0, and 2 are examined to determine whether a stopped interrupt has occurred since the subroutine was first activated. If so <a href="#ongsbf">ONGSBF</a> is incremented (634FH) so that the Runloop will pick it up at the end of the statement. Bit 1 of the status byte is then reset. It should be noted that any "<code>DEVICE STOP</code>" Statement within an interrupt driven subroutine will therefore be ineffective.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6358h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6358H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Runloop interrupt processor (<a href="#6389h">6389H</a>) to clear an interrupt prior to activating the BASIC subroutine, the address of the relevant device's <a href="#trptbl">TRPTBL</a> status byte is supplied in register pair HL. <a href="#ongsbf">ONGSBF</a> is decremented and bit 2 of the status byte is reset.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-636eh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 636EH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the run-clear routine (<a href="#629ah">629AH</a>) to clear all interrupts. The seventy-eight bytes of <a href="#trptbl">TRPTBL</a> and the ten bytes of <a href="#fnkflg">FNKFLG</a> are zeroed.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6389h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6389H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the Runloop interrupt processor. <a href="#oneflg">ONEFLG</a> is first examined to determine whether an error condition currently exists. If so the routine terminates, no interrupts will be processed until the error clears. <a href="#curlin">CURLIN</a> is then examined and, if the Interpreter is in direct mode, the routine terminates. Assuming all is well a search is made of the twenty-six status bytes in <a href="#trptbl">TRPTBL</a> to find the first active interrupt. Note that devices near the start of the table will consequently have a higher priority than those lower down. When the first active status byte is found, that is one with bits 0 and 2 set, the associated address is taken from <a href="#trptbl">TRPTBL</a> and placed in register pair DE. The interrupt is then cleared (<a href="#6358h">6358H</a>) and the device stopped (<a href="#6331h">6331H</a>) before control transfers to the "<code>GOSUB</code>" handler (<a href="#47cfh">47CFH</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-63c9h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 63C9H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>RESTORE</code>" statement handler. If no line number operand exists <a href="#datptr">DATPTR</a> is set to the start of the Program Storage Area. Otherwise the operand is collected (4769H), the program text searched to find the relevant line (<a href="#4295h">4295H</a>) and its address placed in <a href="#datptr">DATPTR</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-63e3h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 63E3H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>STOP</code>" statement handler. If further text exists in the statement control transfers to the "<code>STOP ON/OFF/STOP</code>" statement handler (<a href="#77a5h">77A5H</a>). Otherwise register A is set to 01H and control drops into the "<code>END</code>" statement handler.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-63eah"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 63EAH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>END</code>" statement handler. It is also used, with differing entry points, by the "<code>STOP</code>" statement and for CTRL- STOP and end of text program termination. <a href="#oneflg">ONEFLG</a> is first zeroed and then, for the "<code>END</code>" statement only, all I/O buffers are closed (<a href="#6c1ch">6C1CH</a>). The current program text position is placed in <a href="#savtxt">SAVTXT</a> and <a href="#oldtxt">OLDTXT</a> and the current line number in <a href="#oldlin">OLDLIN</a> for use by any subsequent "<code>CONT</code>" statement. The printer is shut down (<a href="#7304h">7304H</a>), a CR LF issued to the screen (<a href="#7323h">7323H</a>) and register pair HL set to point to the "<code>Break</code>" message at 3FDCH. For the "<code>END</code>" statement and end of text cases control then transfers to the Mainloop "<code>OK</code>" point (411EH). For the CTRL-STOP case control transfers to the end of the error handler (40FDH) to display the "<code>Break</code>" message.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6424h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6424H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>CONT</code>" statement handler. Unless they are zero, in which case a "<code>Can't CONTINUE</code>" error is generated, the contents of <a href="#oldtxt">OLDTXT</a> are placed in register pair HL and those of <a href="#oldlin">OLDLIN</a> in <a href="#curlin">CURLIN</a>. Control then returns to the Runloop to execute at the old program text position. A program cannot be continued after CTRL-STOP has been used to break from WITHIN a statement, via the <a href="#ckcntc">CKCNTC</a> standard routine, rather than from between statements.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6438h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6438H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>TRON</code>" statement handler, <a href="#trcflg">TRCFLG</a> is simply made non-zero.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6439h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6439H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>TROFF</code>" statement handler, <a href="#trcflg">TRCFLG</a> is simply made zero.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-643eh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 643EH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>SWAP</code>" statement handler. The first Variable is located (<a href="#5ea4h">5EA4H</a>) and its contents copied to <a href="#swptmp">SWPTMP</a>. The location of this Variable and of the end of the Variable Storage Area are temporarily saved. The second Variable is then located (<a href="#5ea4h">5EA4H</a>) and its type compared with that of the first. If the types fail to match a "<code>Type mismatch</code>" error is generated (<a href="#406dh">406DH</a>). The current end of the Variable Storage Area is then compared with the old end and an "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error generated (475AH) if they differ. Finally the contents of the second Variable are copied to the location of the first Variable (2EF3H) and the contents of <a href="#swptmp">SWPTMP</a> to the location of the second Variable (2EF3H).</p>
<p>The checks performed by the handler mean that the second Variable, if it is simple and not an Array, must always be in existence before a "<code>SWAP</code>" Statement is encountered or an error will be generated. The reason for this is that, supposing the first Variable was an Array, then the creation of a second (simple) Variable would move the Array Storage Area upwards invalidating its saved location. Note that the perfectly legal case of a simple first Variable and a newly created simple second Variable is also rejected.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6477h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6477H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>ERASE</code>" statement handler. <a href="#subflg">SUBFLG</a> is first set to 01H, to control the Variable search routine, and the Array located (<a href="#5ea4h">5EA4H</a>). All the following Arrays are moved downward and <a href="#strend">STREND</a> set to its new, lower value. The program text is then checked and, if a comma follows, control transfers back to the start of the handler.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-64a7h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 64A7H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine checks whether the character whose address is supplied in register pair HL is upper case alphabetic, if so it returns Flag NC.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-64afh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 64AFH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>CLEAR</code>" statement handler. If no operands are present control transfers to the run-clear routine (62A1H) to remove all current Variables. Otherwise the string space operand is evaluated (4756H) followed by the optional top of memory operand (<a href="#542fh">542FH</a>). The top of memory value is checked and an "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error generated (475AH) if it is less than 8000H or greater than F380H. The space required by the I/O buffers (267 bytes each) and the String Storage Area is subtracted from the top of memory value and an "<code>Out of memory</code>" error generated (6275H) if there is less than 160 bytes remaining to the base of the Variable Storage Area. Assuming all is well <a href="#himem">HIMEM</a>, <a href="#memsiz">MEMSIZ</a> and <a href="#stktop">STKTOP</a> are set to their new values and the remaining storage pointers reset via the run- clear routine (62A1H). The I/O buffer storage is re-allocated (<a href="#7e6bh">7E6BH</a>) and the handler terminates.</p>
<p>Unfortunately the computation of <a href="#memsiz">MEMSIZ</a> and <a href="#stktop">STKTOP</a>, when a new top of memory is specified, is incorrect resulting in the top of the String Storage Area being set one byte too high. This can be seen with the following where an illegal string is accepted:</p>
<pre><code>10 CLEAR 200,&amp;HF380
20 A$=STRING$(201,"A")
30 PRINT FRE("")
</code></pre>
<p>Because there should be an extra DEC HL instruction at 64EBH the new values of <a href="#memsiz">MEMSIZ</a> and <a href="#stktop">STKTOP</a> are initially set one byte too high. When the run-clear routine is called <a href="#memsiz">MEMSIZ</a> is copied into <a href="#fretop">FRETOP</a>, the top of the String Storage Area, which results in this being one byte too high as well. Although <a href="#memsiz">MEMSIZ</a> and <a href="#stktop">STKTOP</a> are correctly recomputed when the file pointers are reset, <a href="#fretop">FRETOP</a> is left with its incorrect value. When the "<code>FRE</code>" statement is executed in line thirty, and string garbage collection initiated, <a href="#fretop">FRETOP</a> is restored to its correct value but, because the string overflows the String Storage Area by one byte, the amount of free space displayed is -1 byte. To correctly set all the system pointers any alteration of the top of memory should be followed immediately by another "<code>CLEAR</code>" statement with no operands.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6520h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6520H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine computes the difference between the contents of register pairs HL and DE. It is a duplicate of the short section of code from 64ECH to 64F1H and is completely unused.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6527h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6527H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>NEXT</code>" statement handler. Assuming further text is present in the statement the loop Variable is located (<a href="#5ea4h">5EA4H</a>), otherwise a default address of zero is taken. The stack is then searched for the corresponding "<code>FOR</code>" parameter block (<a href="#3fe2h">3FE2H</a>). If no parameter block is found, or if a "<code>GOSUB</code>" parameter block is found first, a "<code>NEXT without FOR</code>" error is generated (<a href="#405bh">405BH</a>). Assuming the parameter block is found the intervening section of stack, together with any "<code>FOR</code>" blocks it may contain, is discarded. The loop Variable type is then taken from the parameter block and examined to determine the precision required during subsequent operations.</p>
<p>The STEP value is taken from the parameter block and added (3172H, 324EH or 2697H) to the current contents of the loop Variable which is then updated. The new value is compared (2F4DH, 2F21H or 2F5CH) with the termination value from the parameter block to determine whether the loop has terminated (65B6H). The loop will terminate for a positive STEP if the new loop value is GREATER than the termination value. The loop will terminate for a negative step if the new loop value is LESS than the termination value. If the loop has not terminated the original program text position and line number are taken from the parameter block and control transfers to the Runloop (45FDH). If the loop has terminated the parameter block is discarded from the stack and, unless further program text is present in which control transfers back to the start of the handler, control transfers to the Runloop to execute the next statement (<a href="#4601h">4601H</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-65c8h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 65C8H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Expression Evaluator to find the relation (&lt;&gt;=) between two string operands. The address of the first string descriptor is supplied on the Z80 stack and the address of the second in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. The result is returned in register A and the flags as for the numeric relation routines:</p>
<pre><code>String 1=String 2 ... A=00H, Flag Z,NC
String 1&lt;String 2 ... A=01H, Flag NZ,NC
String 1&gt;String 2 ... A=FFH, Flag NZ,C
</code></pre>
<p>Comparison commences at the first character of each string and continues until the two characters differ or one of the strings is exhausted. Control then returns to the Expression Evaluator (<a href="#4f57h">4F57H</a>) to place the true or false numeric result in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-65f5h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 65F5H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>OCT$</code>" function to an operand contained in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. The number is first converted to textual form in <a href="#fbuffr">FBUFFR</a> (<a href="#371eh">371EH</a>) and then the result string is created (6607H).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-65fah"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 65FAH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>HEX$</code>" function to an operand contained in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. The number is first converted to textual form in <a href="#fbuffr">FBUFFR</a> (<a href="#3722h">3722H</a>) and then the result string is created (6607H).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-65ffh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 65FFH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>BIN$</code>" function to an operand contained in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. The number is first converted to textual form in <a href="#fbuffr">FBUFFR</a> (<a href="#371ah">371AH</a>) and then the result string is created (6607H).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6604h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6604H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>STR$</code>" function to an operand contained in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. The number is first converted to textual form in <a href="#fbuffr">FBUFFR</a> (<a href="#3425h">3425H</a>) then analyzed to determine its length and address (6635H).
