After checking that sufficient space is available (<a href="#668eh">668EH</a>) the string is copied to the String Storage Area (67C7H) and the result descriptor created (<a href="#6654h">6654H</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6627h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6627H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine first checks that there is sufficient space in the String Storage Area for the string whose length is supplied in register A (668EH). The string length and the address where the string will be placed in the String Storage Area are then copied to <a href="#dsctmp">DSCTMP</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6636h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6636H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to analyze the character string whose address is supplied in register pair HL. The character string is scanned until a terminating character (00H or ") is found. The length and starting address are then placed in <a href="#dsctmp">DSCTMP</a> (662AH) and control drops into the descriptor creation routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6654h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6654H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the string functions to create a result descriptor. The descriptor is copied from <a href="#dsctmp">DSCTMP</a> to the next available position in <a href="#tempst">TEMPST</a> and its address placed in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. Unless <a href="#tempst">TEMPST</a> is full, in which case a "<code>String formula too complex</code>" error is generated, <a href="#temppt">TEMPPT</a> is increased by three bytes and the routine terminates.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6678h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6678H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine displays the message, or string, whose address is supplied in register pair HL. The string is analyzed (6635H) and its storage freed (67D3H). Successive characters are then taken from the string and displayed, via the <a href="#outdo">OUTDO</a> standard routine, until the string is exhausted.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-668eh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 668EH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine checks that there is room in the String Storage Area to add the string whose length is supplied in register A. On exit register pair DE points to the starting address in the String Storage Area where the string should be placed. The length of the string is first subtracted from the current free location contained in <a href="#fretop">FRETOP</a>. This is then compared with <a href="#stktop">STKTOP</a>, the lowest allowable location for string storage, to determine whether there is space for the string. If so <a href="#fretop">FRETOP</a> is updated with the new position and the routine terminates. If there is insufficient space for the string then garbage collection is initiated (<a href="#66b6h">66B6H</a>) to try and eliminate any dead strings. If, after garbage collection, there is still not enough space an "<code>Out of string space</code>" error is generated.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-66b6h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 66B6H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the string garbage collector, its function is to eliminate any dead strings from the String Storage Area. The basic problem with string Variables, as opposed to numeric ones, is that their lengths vary. If string bodies were stored with their Variables in the Variable Storage Area even such apparently simple statements as A$=A$+"X" would require the movement of thousands of bytes of memory and slow execution speeds dramatically. The method used by the Interpreter to overcome this problem is to keep the string bodies separate from the Variables. Thus strings are kept in the String Storage Area and each Variable holds a three byte descriptor containing the length and address of the associated string. Whenever a string is assigned to a Variable it is simply added to the heap of existing strings in the String Storage Area and the Variable's descriptor changed. No attempt is made to eliminate any previous string belonging to the Variable, by restructuring the heap, as this would wipe out any throughput gains.</p>
<p>If sufficient Variable assignments are made it is inevitable that the String Storage Area will fill up. In a typical program many of these strings will be unused, that is the result of previous assignments. Garbage collection is the process whereby these dead strings are removed. Every string Variable in memory, including Arrays and the local Variables present during evaluation of user defined functions, is examined until the one is found whose string is stored highest in the heap. This string is then moved to the top of the String Storage Area and the Variable contents modified to point to the new location. The owner of the next highest string is then found and the process repeated until every string belonging to a Variable has been compacted.</p>
<p>If a large number of Variables are present garbage collection may take an appreciable time. The process can be seen at work with the following program which repeatedly assigns the string "<code>AAAA</code>" to each element of the Array A$. The program will run at full speed for the first two hundred and fifty assignments and then pause to eliminate the fifty dead strings. A further fifty assignments can then be made before a further garbage collection is required:</p>
<pre><code>10 CLEAR 1000
20 DIM A$(200)
30 FOR N=0 TO 200
40 A$(N)=STRING$(4,"A")
50 PRINT".";
60 NEXT N
70 GOTO 30
</code></pre>
<p>The String Storage Area is also used to hold the intermediate strings produced during expression evaluation. Because so many string functions take multiple arguments, "<code>MID$</code>" takes three for example, the management of intermediate results is a major problem. To deal with it a standardized approach to string results is taken throughout the Interpreter. A producer of a string simply adds the string body to the heap in the String Storage Area, adds the descriptor to the descriptor heap in <a href="#tempst">TEMPST</a> and places the address of the descriptor in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. It is up to the user of the result to free this storage (<a href="#67d0h">67D0H</a>) once it has processed the string. This rule applies to all parts of the system, from the individual function handlers back through the Expression Evaluator to the statement handlers, with only two exceptions.</p>
<p>The first exception occurs when the Factor Evaluator finds an explicitly stated string, such as "<code>SOMETHING</code>" in the program text. In this case it is not necessary to copy the string to the String Storage Area as the original will suffice.</p>
<p>The second exception occurs when the Factor Evaluator finds a reference to a Variable. In this case it is not necessary to place a copy of the descriptor in <a href="#tempst">TEMPST</a> as one already exists inside the Variable.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6787h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6787H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Expression Evaluator to concatenate two string operands. Control transfers here when a "+" token is found following a string operand so the first action taken is to fetch the second string operand via the Factor Evaluator (<a href="#4dc7h">4DC7H</a>). The lengths are then taken from both string descriptors and added together to check the length of the combined string. If this is greater than two hundred and fifty-five characters a "<code>String too long</code>" error is generated. After checking that space is available in the String Storage Area (<a href="#6627h">6627H</a>) the storage of both operands is freed (67D6H). The first string is then copied to the String Storage Area (67BFH) and followed by the second one (67BFH). The result descriptor is created (<a href="#6654h">6654H</a>) and control transfers back to the Expression Evaluator (4C73H)'</p>
<p><a name="user-content-67d0h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 67D0H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine frees any storage occupied by the string whose descriptor address is contained in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. The address of the descriptor is taken from <a href="#dac">DAC</a> and examined to determine whether it is that of the last descriptor in <a href="#tempst">TEMPST</a> (67EEH), if not the routine terminates. Otherwise <a href="#temppt">TEMPPT</a> is reduced by three bytes clearing this descriptor from <a href="#tempst">TEMPST</a>. The address of the string body is then taken from the descriptor and compared with <a href="#fretop">FRETOP</a> to see if this is the lowest string in the String Storage Area, if not the routine terminates. Otherwise the length of the string is added to <a href="#fretop">FRETOP</a>, which is then updated with this new value, freeing the storage occupied by the string body.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-67ffh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 67FFH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>LEN</code>" function to an operand contained in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. The operand's storage is freed (<a href="#67d0h">67D0H</a>) and the string length taken from the descriptor and placed in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> as an integer (4FCFH).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-680bh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 680BH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>ASC</code>" function to an operand contained in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. The operand's storage is freed and the string length examined (6803H), if it is zero an "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH). Otherwise the first character is. taken from the string and placed in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> as an integer (4FCFH).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-681bh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 681BH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>CHR$</code>" function to an operand contained in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. After checking that sufficient space is available (6625H) the operand is converted to a single byte integer (521FH). This character is then placed in the String Storage Area and the result descriptor created (<a href="#6654h">6654H</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6829h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6829H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>STRING$</code>" function. After checking for the open parenthesis character the length operand is evaluated and placed in register E (521CH). The second operand is then evaluated (<a href="#4c64h">4C64H</a>). If it is numeric it is converted to a single byte integer (521FH) and placed in register A. If it is a string the first character is taken from it and placed in register A (680FH). Control then drops into the "<code>SPACE$</code>" function to create the result string.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6848h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6848H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>SPACE$</code>" function to an operand contained in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. The operand is first converted to a single byte integer in register E (521FH). After checking that sufficient space is available (<a href="#6627h">6627H</a>) the required number of spaces are copied to the String Storage Area and the result descriptor created (<a href="#6654h">6654H</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6861h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6861H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>LEFT$</code>" function. The first operand's descriptor address and the integer second operand are supplied on the Z80 stack. The slice size is taken from the stack (<a href="#68e3h">68E3H</a>) and compared to the source string length. If the source string length is less than the slice size it replaces it as the length to extract. After checking that sufficient space is available (<a href="#668eh">668EH</a>) the required number of characters are copied from the start of the source string to the String Storage Area (67C7H). The source string's storage is then freed (67D7H) and the result descriptor created (<a href="#6654h">6654H</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6891h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6891H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>RIGHT$</code>" function. The first operand's descriptor address and the integer second operand are supplied on the Z80 stack. The slice size is taken from the stack (<a href="#68e3h">68E3H</a>) and subtracted from the source string length to determine the slice starting position. Control then transfers to the "<code>LEFT$</code>" routine to extract the slice (6865H).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-689ah"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 689AH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>MID$</code>" function. The first operand's descriptor address and the integer second operand are supplied on the Z80 stack. The starting position is taken from the stack (68E6H) and checked, if it is zero an "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH). The optional slice size is then evaluated (<a href="#69e4h">69E4H</a>) and control transfers to the "<code>LEFT$</code>" routine to extract the slice (6869H).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-68bbh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 68BBH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>VAL</code>" function to an operand contained in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. The string length is taken from the descriptor (6803H) and checked, if it is zero it is placed in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> as an integer (4FCFH). The length is then added to the starting address of the string body to give the location of the character immediately following it. This is temporarily replaced with a zero byte and the string is converted to numeric form in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> (<a href="#3299h">3299H</a>). The original character is then restored and the routine terminates. The temporary zero byte delimiter is necessary because strings are packed together in the String Storage Area, without it the numeric converter would run on into succeeding strings.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-68e3h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 68E3H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the "<code>LEFT$</code>", "<code>MID$</code>" and "<code>RIGHT$</code>" function handlers to check that the next program text character is ")" and then to pop an operand from the Z80 stack into register pair DE.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-68ebh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 68EBH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>INSTR</code>" function. The first operand, which may be the starting position or the source string, is evaluated (4C62H) and its type tested. If it is the source string a default starting position of one is taken. If it is the starting position operand its value is checked and the source string operand evaluated (<a href="#4c64h">4C64H</a>). The pattern string is then evaluated (<a href="#4c64h">4C64H</a>) and the storage of both operands freed (<a href="#67d0h">67D0H</a>). The length of the pattern string is checked and, if zero, the starting position is placed in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> (4FCFH). The pattern string is then checked against successive characters from the source string, commencing at the starting position, until a match is found or the source string is exhausted. With a successful search the character position of the substring is placed in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> as an integer (4FCFH), otherwise a zero result is returned.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-696eh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 696EH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>MID$</code>" statement handler. After checking for the open parenthesis character the destination Variable is located (<a href="#5ea4h">5EA4H</a>) and checked to ensure that it is a string type (<a href="#3058h">3058H</a>). The address of the string body is then taken from the Variable and examined to determine whether it is inside the Program Text Area, as would be the case for an explicitly stated string. If this is the case the string body is copied to the String Storage Area (6611H) and a new descriptor copied to the Variable (2EF3H). This is done to avoid modifying the program text. The starting position is then evaluated (521CH) and checked, if it is zero an "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH). The optional slice length operand is evaluated (<a href="#69e4h">69E4H</a>) followed by the replacement string (4C5FH) whose storage is then freed (<a href="#67d0h">67D0H</a>). Characters are then copied from the replacement string to the destination string until either the slice length is completed or the replacement string is exhausted.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-69e4h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 69E4H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by various string functions to evaluate an optional operand (521CH) and return the result in register E. If no operand is present a default value of 255 is returned.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-69f2h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 69F2H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>FRE</code>" function to an operand contained in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. If the operand is numeric the single precision difference between the Z80 Stack Pointer and the contents of <a href="#strend">STREND</a> is placed in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> (4FC1H). If the operand is a string type its storage is freed (67D3H) and garbage collection initiated (<a href="#66b6h">66B6H</a>). The single precision difference between the contents of <a href="#fretop">FRETOP</a> and those of <a href="#stktop">STKTOP</a> is then placed in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> (4FC1H).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6a0eh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6A0EH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the file I/O handlers to analyze a filespec such as "<code>A:FILENAME.BAS</code>". The filespec consists of three parts, the device, the filename and the type extension. On entry register pair HL points to the start of the filespec in the program text. On exit register D holds the device code, the filename is in positions zero to seven of <a href="#filnam">FILNAM</a> and the type extension in positions eight to ten. Any unused positions are filled with spaces.</p>
<p>The filespec string is evaluated (<a href="#4c64h">4C64H</a>) and its storage freed (<a href="#67d0h">67D0H</a>), if the string is of zero length a "<code>Bad file name</code>" error is generated (<a href="#6e6bh">6E6BH</a>). The device name is parsed (<a href="#6f15h">6F15H</a>) and successive characters taken from the filespec and placed in <a href="#filnam">FILNAM</a> until the string is exhausted, a "." character is found or <a href="#filnam">FILNAM</a> is full. A "<code>Bad file name</code>" error is generated (<a href="#6e6bh">6E6BH</a>) if the filespec contains any control characters, that is those whose value is smaller than 20H. If the filespec contains a type extension a "<code>Bad file name</code>" error is generated (<a href="#6e6bh">6E6BH</a>) if it is longer than three characters or if the filename is longer than eight characters. If no type extension is present the filename may be any length, extra characters are simply ignored.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6a6dh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6A6DH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the file I/O handlers to locate the I/O buffer FCB whose number is supplied in register A. The buffer number is first checked against <a href="#maxfil">MAXFIL</a> and a "<code>Bad file number</code>" error generated (<a href="#6e7dh">6E7DH</a>) if it is too large. Otherwise the required address is taken from the file pointer block and placed in register pair HL and the buffer's mode taken from byte 0 of the FCB and placed in register A.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6a9eh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6A9EH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the file I/O handlers to evaluate an I/O buffer number and to locate its FCB. Any "#" character is skipped (<a href="#4666h">4666H</a>) and the buffer number evaluated (521CH). The FCB is located (<a href="#6a6dh">6A6DH</a>) and a "<code>File not open</code>" error generated (<a href="#6e77h">6E77H</a>) if the buffer mode byte is zero. Otherwise the FCB address is placed in <a href="#ptrfil">PTRFIL</a> to redirect the Interpreter's output.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6ab7h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6AB7H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>OPEN</code>" statement handler. The filespec is analyzed (<a href="#6a0eh">6A0EH</a>) and any following mode converted to the corresponding mode byte, these are: "<code>FOR INPUT</code>" (01H), "<code>FOR OUTPUT</code>" (02H) and "<code>FOR APPEND</code>" (08H). If no mode is explicitly stated random mode (04H) is assumed. The "<code>AS</code>" characters are checked and the buffer number evaluated (521CH), if this is zero a "<code>Bad file number</code>" error is generated (<a href="#6e7dh">6E7DH</a>). The FCB is then located (<a href="#6a6dh">6A6DH</a>) and a "<code>File already open</code>" error generated (<a href="#6e6eh">6E6EH</a>) if the buffer's mode byte is anything other than zero. The device code is placed in byte 4 of the FCB, the open function dispatched (<a href="#6f8fh">6F8FH</a>) and the Interpreter's output reset to the screen (<a href="#4affh">4AFFH</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6b24h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6B24H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the file I/O handlers to close the I/O buffer whose number is supplied in register A. The FCB is located (<a href="#6a6dh">6A6DH</a>) and, provided the buffer is in use, the close function dispatched (<a href="#6f8fh">6F8FH</a>) and the buffer filled with zeroes (<a href="#6ceah">6CEAH</a>). <a href="#ptrfil">PTRFIL</a> and the FCB mode byte are then zeroed to reset the Interpreter's output to the screen.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6b5bh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6B5BH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>LOAD</code>", "<code>MERGE</code>" and "<code>RUN filespec</code>" statement handler. The filespec is analyzed (<a href="#6a0eh">6A0EH</a>) and then, for "<code>LOAD</code>" and "<code>RUN</code>" only, the program text examined to determine whether the auto-run "<code>R</code>" option is specified. I/O buffer 0 is opened for input (6AFAH) and the first byte of <a href="#filnam">FILNAM</a> set to FFH if auto-run is required. For "<code>LOAD</code>" and "<code>RUN</code>" only any program text is then cleared via the "<code>NEW</code>" statement handler (6287H). As this will reset the Interpreter's output to the screen the buffer FCB is again located and placed in <a href="#ptrfil">PTRFIL</a> (6AAAH). Control then transfers directly to the Interpreter Mainloop (<a href="#4134h">4134H</a>) for the program text to be loaded as if typed from the keyboard. Note that no error checking of any sort is carried out on the data read.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6ba3h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6BA3H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>SAVE</code>" statement handler. The filespec is analyzed (<a href="#6a0eh">6A0EH</a>) and the program text examined to determine whether the ASCII "<code>A</code>" suffix is present. This is only relevant under Disk BASIC, it makes no difference on a standard MSX machine. I/O buffer 0 is opened for output (6AFAH) and control transfers to the "<code>LIST</code>" statement handler (<a href="#522eh">522EH</a>) to output the program text. Note that no error checking information of any sort accompanies the text.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6bdah"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6BDAH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the file I/O handlers to return the device code for the currently active I/O buffer. The FCB address is taken from <a href="#ptrfil">PTRFIL</a> then the device code taken from byte 4 of the FCB and placed in register A.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6be7h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6BE7H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the file I/O handlers to perform an operation on a number of I/O buffers. The address of the relevant routine is supplied in register pair BC and the buffer count in register A. For example if register pair BC contained 6B24H and register A contained 03H buffers 3, 2, 1 and 0 would be closed. The routine has a slightly different function if it is entered with FLAG NZ. In this case the I/O buffer numbers are taken sequentially from the program text and evaluated (521CH) before the operation is performed, a typical case might be "#1,#2".</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6c14h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6C14H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>CLOSE</code>" statement handler. Register pair BC is set to 6B24H, register A is loaded with the contents of <a href="#maxfil">MAXFIL</a> and the required number of buffers closed (<a href="#6be7h">6BE7H</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6c1ch"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6C1CH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the file I/O handlers to close every I/O buffer. Register pair BC is set to 6B24H, register A is loaded with the contents of <a href="#maxfil">MAXFIL</a> and all buffers closed (<a href="#6be7h">6BE7H</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6c2ah"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6C2AH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>LFILES</code>" statement handler. <a href="#prtflg">PRTFLG</a> is made non- zero, to direct output to the printer, and control drops into the "<code>FILES</code>" statement handler.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6c2fh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6C2FH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>FILES</code>" statement handler, an "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH) on a standard MSX machine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6c35h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6C35H
</code></pre>
<p>Control transfers here from the general "<code>PUT</code>" and "<code>GET</code>" handlers (<a href="#7758h">7758H</a>) when the program text contains anything other than a "<code>SPRITE</code>" token. A "<code>Sequential I/O only</code>" error is generated (<a href="#6e86h">6E86H</a>) on a standard MSX machine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6c48h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6C48H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the file I/O handlers to sequentially output the character supplied in register A. The character is placed in register C and the sequential output function dispatched (<a href="#6f8fh">6F8FH</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6c71h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6C71H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the file I/O handlers to sequentially input a single character. The sequential input function is dispatched (<a href="#6f8fh">6F8FH</a>) and the character returned in register A, FLAG C indicates an EOF (End Of File) condition.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6c87h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6C87H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>INPUT$</code>" function. The program text is checked for the "$" and "(" characters and the length operand evaluated (521CH). If an I/O buffer number is present it is evaluated, the FCB located (<a href="#6a9eh">6A9EH</a>) and the mode byte examined. An "<code>Input past end</code>" error is generated (<a href="#6e83h">6E83H</a>) if the buffer is not in input or random mode. After checking that sufficient space is available (<a href="#6627h">6627H</a>) the required number of characters are sequentially input (<a href="#6c71h">6C71H</a>), or collected via the <a href="#chget">CHGET</a> standard routine, and copied to the String Storage Area. Finally the result descriptor is created (<a href="#6654h">6654H</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6ceah"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6CEAH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the file I/O handlers to fill the buffer whose FCB address is contained in <a href="#ptrfil">PTRFIL</a> with two hundred and fifty-six zeroes.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6cfbh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6CFBH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the file I/O handlers to return, in register pair HL, the starting address of the buffer whose FCB address is contained in <a href="#ptrfil">PTRFIL</a>. This just involves adding nine to the FCB address.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6d03h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6D03H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>LOC</code>" function to the I/O buffer whose number is contained in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. The FCB is located (6A6AH) and the LOC function dispatched (<a href="#6f8fh">6F8FH</a>). An "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH) on a standard MSX machine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6d14h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6D14H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>LOF</code>" function to the I/O buffer whose number is contained in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. The FCB is located (6A6AH) and the LOF function dispatched (<a href="#6f8fh">6F8FH</a>). An "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH) on a standard MSX machine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6d25h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6D25H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>EOF</code>" function to the I/O buffer whose number is contained in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. The FCB is located (6A6AH) and the EOF function dispatched (<a href="#6f8fh">6F8FH</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6d39h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6D39H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>FPOS</code>" function to the I/O buffer whose number is contained in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. The FCB is located (6A6AH) and the <code>FPOS</code> function dispatched (<a href="#6f8fh">6F8FH</a>). An "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH) on a standard MSX machine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6d48h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6D48H
</code></pre>
<p>Control transfers to this routine when the Interpreter Mainloop encounters a direct statement, that is one with no line number. The <a href="#isflio">ISFLIO</a> standard routine is first used to determine whether a "<code>LOAD</code>" statement is active. If input is coming from the keyboard control transfers to the Runloop execution point (<a href="#4640h">4640H</a>) to execute the statement. If input is coming from the cassette buffer 0 is closed (<a href="#6b24h">6B24H</a>) and a "<code>Direct statement in file</code>" error generated (<a href="#6e71h">6E71H</a>). This could happen on a standard MSX machine either through a cassette error or by attempting to load a text file with no line numbers.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6d57h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6D57H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the "<code>INPUT</code>", "<code>LINE INPUT</code>" and "<code>PRINT</code>" statement handlers to check for the presence of a "#" character in the program text. If one is found the I/O buffer number is evaluated (<a href="#521bh">521BH</a>), the FCB located and its address placed in <a href="#ptrfil">PTRFIL</a> (6AAAH). The mode byte of the FCB is then compared with the mode number supplied by the statement handler in register C, if they do not match a "<code>Bad file number</code>" error is generated (<a href="#6e7dh">6E7DH</a>). With "<code>PRINT</code>" the allowable modes are output, random and append. With "<code>INPUT</code>" and "<code>LINE INPUT</code>" the allowable modes are input and random. Note that on a standard MSX machine not all these modes are supported at lower levels. Some sort of error will consequently be generated at a later stage for illegal modes.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6d83h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6D83H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the "<code>INPUT</code>" statement handler to input a string from an I/O buffer. A return is first set up to the "<code>READ/INPUT</code>" statement handler (4BF1H). The characters which delimit the input string, comma and space for a numeric Variable and comma only for a string Variable, are placed in registers D and E and control transfers to the "<code>LINE INPUT</code>" routine (6DA3H).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6d8fh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6D8FH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>LINE INPUT</code>" statement handler when input is from an I/O buffer. The buffer number is evaluated, the FCB located and the mode checked (6D55H). The Variable to assign to is then located (<a href="#5ea4h">5EA4H</a>) and its type checked to ensure it is a string type (<a href="#3058h">3058H</a>). A return is set up to the "<code>LET</code>" statement handler (487BH) to perform the assignment and the input string collected.</p>
<p>Characters are sequentially input (<a href="#6c71h">6C71H</a>) and placed in <a href="#buf">BUF</a> until the correct delimiter is found, EOF is reached or <a href="#buf">BUF</a> fills up (6E41H). When the terminating condition is reached and assignment is to a numeric Variable the string is converted to numeric form in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> (<a href="#3299h">3299H</a>). When assignment is to a string Variable the string is analyzed and the result descriptor created (6638H).</p>
<p>For "<code>LINE INPUT</code>" all characters are accepted until a CR code is reached. Note that if this CR code is preceded by a LF code then it will not function as a delimiter but will merely be accepted as part of the string. For "<code>INPUT</code>" to a numeric Variable leading spaces are stripped then characters accepted until a CR code, a space or a comma is reached. Note that as for "<code>LINE INPUT</code>" a CR code will not function as a delimiter when preceded by a LF code. In this case however the CR code will not be placed in <a href="#buf">BUF</a> but ignored. For "<code>INPUT</code>" to a string Variable leading spaces are stripped then characters accepted until a CR or comma is reached. Note that as for "<code>LINE INPUT</code>" a CR code will not function as a delimiter when preceded by a LF code. In this case however neither code will be placed in <a href="#buf">BUF</a> both are ignored. An alternative mode is entered when the first character read, after any spaces, is a double quote character. In this case all characters will be accepted, and stored in <a href="#buf">BUF</a>, until another double quote delimiter is read.</p>
<p>Once the input string has been accepted the terminating delimiter is examined to see if any special action is required with respect to trailing characters. If the input string was delimited by a double quote character or a space then any succeeding spaces will be read in and ignored until a non-space character is found. If this character is a comma or CR code then it is accepted and ignored. Otherwise a putback function is dispatched (<a href="#6f8fh">6F8FH</a>) to return the character to the I/O buffer. If the input string was delimited by a CR code then the next character is read in and checked. If this is a LF code it will be accepted but ignored. If it is not a LF code then a putback function is dispatched (<a href="#6f8fh">6F8FH</a>) to return the character to the I/O buffer.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6e6bh"></a>
<a name="user-content-6e6eh"></a>
<a name="user-content-6e71h"></a>
<a name="user-content-6e74h"></a>
<a name="user-content-6e77h"></a>
<a name="user-content-6e7ah"></a>
<a name="user-content-6e7dh"></a>
<a name="user-content-6e80h"></a>
<a name="user-content-6e83h"></a>
<a name="user-content-6e86h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6E6BH
</code></pre>
<p>This is a group of ten file I/O related error generators. Register E is loaded with the relevant error code and control transfers to the error handler (<a href="#406fh">406FH</a>):</p>
<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>ADDRESS</th>
<th>ERROR</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>6E6BH</td>
<td>Bad file name</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>6E6EH</td>
<td>File already open</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>6E71H</td>
<td>Direct statement in file</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>6E74H</td>
<td>File not found</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>6E77H</td>
<td>File not open</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>6E7AH</td>
<td>Field overflow</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>6E7DH</td>
<td>Bad file number</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>6E80H</td>
<td>Internal error</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>6E83H</td>
<td>Input past end</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>6E86H</td>
<td>Sequential I/O only</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<p><a name="user-content-6e92h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6E92H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>BSAVE</code>" statement handler. The filespec is analyzed (<a href="#6a0eh">6A0EH</a>) and the start address evaluated (<a href="#6f0bh">6F0BH</a>). The stop address is then evaluated (<a href="#6f0bh">6F0BH</a>) and placed in <a href="#savend">SAVEND</a> followed by the optional entry address (<a href="#6f0bh">6F0BH</a>) which is placed in <a href="#savent">SAVENT</a>. If no entry address exists the start address is taken instead. The device code is checked to ensure that it is CAS, if not a "<code>Bad file name</code>" error is generated (<a href="#6e6bh">6E6BH</a>), and the data written to cassette (<a href="#6fd7h">6FD7H</a>). Note that no buffering is involved, data is written directly to the cassette, and no error checking information accompanies the data.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6ec6h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6EC6H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>BLOAD</code>" statement handler. The filespec is analyzed (<a href="#6a0eh">6A0EH</a>) and <a href="#runbnf">RUNBNF</a> made non-zero if the auto-run "<code>R</code>" option is present in the program text. The optional load offset, with a default value of zero, is then evaluated (<a href="#6f0bh">6F0BH</a>) and the device code checked to ensure that it is CAS, if not a "<code>Bad file name</code>" error is generated (<a href="#6e6bh">6E6BH</a>). Data is then read directly from cassette (<a href="#7014h">7014H</a>), as with "<code>BSAVE</code>" no buffering or error checking is involved.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6ef4h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6EF4H
</code></pre>
<p>Control transfers to this routine when the "<code>BLOAD</code>" statement handler has completed loading data into memory. If <a href="#runbnf">RUNBNF</a> is zero buffer 0 is closed (<a href="#6b24h">6B24H</a>) and control returns to the Runloop. Otherwise buffer 0 is closed (<a href="#6b24h">6B24H</a>), a return address of 6CF3H is set up (this routine just pops the program text pointer back into register pair HL and returns to the Runloop) and control transfers to the address contained in <a href="#savent">SAVENT</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6f0bh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6F0BH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the "<code>BLOAD</code>" and "<code>BSAVE</code>" handlers to evaluate an address operand, the result is returned in register pair DE. The operand is evaluated (4C64H) then converted to an integer (<a href="#5439h">5439H</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6f15h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6F15H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the filespec analyzer to parse a device name such as "<code>CAS:</code>". On entry register pair HL points to the start of the filespec string and register E contains its length. If no device name is present the default device code (CAS=FFH) is returned in register A with FLAG Z. If a legal device name is present its code is returned in register A with FLAG NZ.</p>
<p>The filespec is examined until a ":" character is found then the name compared with each of the legal device names in the device table at 6F76H. If a match is found the device code is taken from the table and returned in register A. If no match is found control transfers to the external ROM search routine (<a href="#55f8h">55F8H</a>). Note that any lower case characters are turned to upper case for comparison purposes. Thus crt and CRT, for example, are the same device.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6f76h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6F76H
</code></pre>
<p>This table is used by the device name parser, it contains the four device names and codes available on a standard MSX machine:</p>
<pre><code>CAS ... FFH  LPT ... FEH  CRT ... FDH  GRP ... FCH
</code></pre>

<p><a name="user-content-6f87h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6F87H
</code></pre>
<p>This table is used by the function dispatcher (<a href="#6f8fh">6F8FH</a>), it contains the address of the function decoding table for each of the four standard MSX devices:</p>
<pre><code>CAS ... 71C7H  LPT ... 72A6H  CRT ... 71A2H  GRP ... 7182H
</code></pre>

<p><a name="user-content-6f8fh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6F8FH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the file I/O function dispatcher. In conjunction with the Interpreter's buffer structure it provides a consistent, device independent method of inputting or outputting data. The required function code is supplied in register A and the address of the buffer FCB in register pair HL.</p>
<p>The device code is taken from byte 4 of the FCB and examined to determine whether it is one of the four standard devices, if not control transfers to the external ROM function dispatcher (<a href="#564ah">564AH</a>). Otherwise the address of the device's function decoding table is taken from the table at 6F87H, the required function's address taken from it and control transferred to the relevant function handler.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6fb7h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6FB7H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>CSAVE</code>" statement handler. The filename is evaluated (7098H) followed by the optional baud rate operand (<a href="#7a2dh">7A2DH</a>). The identification block is then written to cassette (<a href="#7125h">7125H</a>) with a filetype byte of D3H. The contents of the Program Text Area are written directly to cassette as a single data block (<a href="#713eh">713EH</a>). Note that no error checking information accompanies the data.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-6fd7h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 6FD7H
</code></pre>
<p>Control transfers to this routine from the "<code>BSAVE</code>" statement handler to write a block of memory to cassette. The identification block is first written to cassette (<a href="#7125h">7125H</a>) with a filetype byte of D0H. The motor is then turned on and a short header written to cassette (<a href="#72f8h">72F8H</a>) The starting address is popped from the Z80 stack and written to cassette LSB first, MSB second (<a href="#7003h">7003H</a>). The stop address is taken from <a href="#savend">SAVEND</a> and written to cassette LSB first, MSB second (<a href="#7003h">7003H</a>). The entry address is taken from <a href="#savent">SAVENT</a> and written to cassette LSB first, MSB second (<a href="#7003h">7003H</a>). The required area of memory is then written to cassette one byte at a time (<a href="#72deh">72DEH</a>) and the cassette motor turned off via the <a href="#tapoof">TAPOOF</a> standard routine. Note that no error checking information accompanies the data.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7003h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7003H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine writes the contents of register pair HL to cassette with register L first (<a href="#72deh">72DEH</a>) and register H second (<a href="#72deh">72DEH</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-700bh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 700BH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine reads two bytes from cassette and places the first in register L (<a href="#72d4h">72D4H</a>), the second in register H (<a href="#72d4h">72D4H</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7014h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7014H
</code></pre>
<p>Control transfers to this routine from the "<code>BLOAD</code>" statement handler to load data from the cassette into memory. The cassette is read until an identification block with a file type of D0H and the correct filename is found (<a href="#70b8h">70B8H</a>). The data block header is then located on the cassette (<a href="#72e9h">72E9H</a>). The offset value is popped from the Z80 stack and added to the start address from the cassette (<a href="#700bh">700BH</a>). The stop address is read from cassette (<a href="#700bh">700BH</a>) and the offset added to this as well. The entry address is read from cassette (<a href="#700bh">700BH</a>) and placed in <a href="#savent">SAVENT</a> in case auto-run is required. Successive data bytes are then read from cassette (<a href="#72d4h">72D4H</a>) and placed in memory, at the start address initially, until the stop address is reached. Finally the motor is turned off via the <a href="#tapiof">TAPIOF</a> standard routine and control transfers to the "<code>BLOAD</code>" termination point (<a href="#6ef4h">6EF4H</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-703fh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 703FH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>CLOAD</code>" and "<code>CLOAD?</code>" statement handler. The program text is first checked for a trailing "<code>PRINT</code>" token (91H) which is how the "<code>?</code>" character is tokenized. The filename is then evaluated (<a href="#708ch">708CH</a>) and the cassette read until an identification block with a filetype of D3H and the correct filename is found (<a href="#70b8h">70B8H</a>). For "<code>CLOAD</code>" a "<code>NEW</code>" operation is then performed (6287H) to erase the current program text. For "<code>CLOAD?</code>" all pointers in the Program Text Area are converted to line numbers (54EAH) to match the cassette data.</p>
<p>The data block header is located on the cassette and successive data bytes read from cassette and placed in memory or compared with the current memory contents (<a href="#715dh">715DH</a>). When the data block has been completely read the message "<code>OK</code>" is displayed (<a href="#6678h">6678H</a>) and control transfers directly to the end of the Interpreter Mainloop (4237H) to reset the Variable storage pointers. For "<code>CLOAD?</code>" reading of the data block will terminate if the cassette byte is not the same as the program text byte in memory. If the address where this occurred is above the end of the Program Text Area then the handler terminates with an "<code>OK</code>" message as before. Otherwise a "<code>Verify error</code>" is generated.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-708ch"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 708CH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the "<code>CLOAD</code>" and "<code>CSAVE</code>" statement handlers to evaluate a filename in the program text. The two handlers use different entry points so that a null filename is allowed for "<code>CLOAD</code>" but not for "<code>CSAVE</code>". The filename string is evaluated (<a href="#4c64h">4C64H</a>), its storage freed (680FH) and the first six characters copied to <a href="#filnam">FILNAM</a>. If the filename is longer than six characters the excess is ignored. If the filename is shorter than six characters then <a href="#filnam">FILNAM</a> is padded with spaces.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-70b8h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 70B8H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the "<code>CLOAD</code>" and "<code>BLOAD</code>" statement handlers and for the dispatcher open function (when the device is CAS and the mode is input) to locate an identification block on the cassette. On entry the filename is in <a href="#filnam">FILNAM</a> and the file type in register C, D3H for a tokenized BASIC (<code>CLOAD</code>) file, D0H for a binary (<code>BLOAD</code>) file and EAH for an ASCII (<code>LOAD</code> or data) file.</p>
<p>The cassette motor is turned on and the cassette read until a header is found (<a href="#72e9h">72E9H</a>). Each identification block is prefixed by ten file type characters so successive characters are read from cassette (<a href="#72d4h">72D4H</a>) and compared to the required file type. If the file type characters do not match control transfers back to the start of the routine to find the next header. Otherwise the next six characters are read in (<a href="#72d4h">72D4H</a>) and placed in <a href="#filnam">FILNAM</a>. If <a href="#filnam">FILNAM</a> is full of spaces no filename match is attempted and the identification block has been found. Otherwise the contents of <a href="#filnam">FILNAM</a> and <a href="#filnm2">FILNM2</a> are compared to determine whether this is the required file. If the match is unsuccessful, and the Interpreter is in direct mode, the message "<code>Skip:</code>" is displayed (<a href="#710dh">710DH</a>) followed by the filename. Control then transfers back to the start of the routine to try the next header. If the match is successful, and the Interpreter is in direct mode, the message "<code>Found:</code>" is displayed (<a href="#710dh">710DH</a>) followed by the filename and the routine terminates.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-70ffh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 70FFH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the plain text message "<code>Found:</code>" terminated by a zero byte.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7106h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7106H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the plain text message "<code>Skip :</code>" terminated by a zero byte.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-710dh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 710DH
</code></pre>
<p>Unless <a href="#curlin">CURLIN</a> shows the Interpreter to be in program mode this routine first displays (<a href="#6678h">6678H</a>) the message whose address is supplied in register pair HL, followed by the six characters contained in <a href="#filnm2">FILNM2</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7125h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7125H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the "<code>CSAVE</code>" and "<code>BSAVE</code>" statement handlers and for the dispatcher open function (when the device is CAS and the mode is output) to write an identification block to cassette. On entry the filename is in <a href="#filnam">FILNAM</a> and the filetype in register A, D3H for a tokenized BASIC (<code>CSAVE</code>) file, D0H for a binary (<code>BSAVE</code>) file and EAH for an ASCII (<code>SAVE</code> or data) file. The cassette motor is turned on and a long header written to cassette (<a href="#72f8h">72F8H</a>) The filetype byte is then written to cassette (<a href="#72deh">72DEH</a>) ten times followed by the first six characters from <a href="#filnam">FILNAM</a> (<a href="#72deh">72DEH</a>). The cassette motor is turned off via the <a href="#tapoof">TAPOOF</a> standard routine and the routine terminates.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-713eh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 713EH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the "<code>CSAVE</code>" statement handler to write the Program Text Area to cassette as a single data block. All pointers in the program text are converted back to line numbers (54EAH) to make the text address independent. The cassette motor is turned on and a short header written to cassette (<a href="#72f8h">72F8H</a>) The entire Program Text Area is then written to cassette a byte at a time (<a href="#72deh">72DEH</a>) and followed with seven zero bytes (<a href="#72deh">72DEH</a>) as a terminator. The cassette motor is then turned off via the <a href="#tapoof">TAPOOF</a> standard routine and the routine terminates.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-715dh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 715DH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the "<code>CLOAD</code>" and "<code>CLOAD?</code>" statement handlers to read a single data block into the Program Text Area or to compare it with the current contents. On entry register A contains a flag to distinguish between the two statements, 00H for "<code>CLOAD</code>" and FFH for "<code>CLOAD?</code>". The cassette motor is turned on and the first header located (<a href="#72e9h">72E9H</a>). Successive characters are read from cassette (<a href="#72d4h">72D4H</a>) and placed in the Program Text Area or compared with the current contents. If the current statement is "<code>CLOAD?</code>" the routine will terminate with FLAG NZ if the cassette character is not the same as the memory character. Otherwise data will be read until ten successive zeroes are found. This sequence of zeroes is composed of the last program line end of line character, the end link and the seven terminator zeroes added by "<code>CSAVE</code>". Note that the routine will probably terminate during this sequence, when used by "<code>CLOAD?</code>", as memory comparison is still in progress. This accounts for the rather peculiar coding of the "<code>CLOAD?</code>" handler terminating conditions.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7182h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7182H
</code></pre>
<p>This table is used by the dispatcher when decoding function codes for the GRP device. It contains the address of the handler for each of the function codes, most are in fact error generators:</p>
<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>TO</th>
<th>FUNCTION</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>71B6H</td>
<td>0, open</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>71C2H</td>
<td>2, close</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>6E86H</td>
<td>4, random</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>7196H</td>
<td>6, sequential output</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>475AH</td>
<td>8, sequential input</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>475AH</td>
<td>10, loc</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>475AH</td>
<td>12, lof</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>475AH</td>
<td>14, eof</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>475AH</td>
<td>16, fpos</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>475AH</td>
<td>18, putback</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<p><a name="user-content-7196h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7196H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the dispatcher sequential output routine for the GRP device. <a href="#scrmod">SCRMOD</a> is first checked and an "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error generated (475AH) if the screen is in either text mode. The character to output is taken from register C and control transfers to the <a href="#grpprt">GRPPRT</a> standard routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-71a2h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 71A2H
</code></pre>
<p>This table is used by the device dispatcher when decoding function codes for the CRT device. It contains the address of the handler for each of the function codes, most are in fact error generators:</p>
<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>TO</th>
<th>FUNCTION</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>

<p><a name="user-content-71b6h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 71B6H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the dispatcher open routine for the CRT, LPT and GRP devices. The required mode, in register E, is checked and a "<code>Bad file name</code>" error generated (<a href="#6e6bh">6E6BH</a>) for input or append. The FCB address is then placed in <a href="#ptrfil">PTRFIL</a>, the mode in byte 0 of the FCB and the routine terminates. Note that the Z80 RET instruction at the end of this routine (71C2H) is the dispatcher close routine for the CRT, LPT and GRP devices.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-71c3h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 71C3H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the dispatcher sequential output routine for the CRT device. The character to output is taken from register C and control transfers to the <a href="#chput">CHPUT</a> standard routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-71c7h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 71C7H
</code></pre>
<p>This table is used by the dispatcher when decoding function codes for the CAS device. It contains the address of the handler for each of the function codes, several are error generators:</p>
<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>TO</th>
<th>FUNCTION</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>71DBH</td>
<td>0, open</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>7205H</td>
<td>2, close</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>6E86H</td>
<td>4, random</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>722AH</td>
<td>6, sequential output</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>723FH</td>
<td>8, sequential input</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>475AH</td>
<td>10, loc</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>475AH</td>
<td>12, lof</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>726DH</td>
<td>14, eof</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>475AH</td>
<td>16, fpos</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>727CH</td>
<td>18, putback</td>
</tr>

</table>

<p><a name="user-content-71dbh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 71DBH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the dispatcher open routine for the CAS device. The current I/O buffer position, held in byte 6 of the FCB, and <a href="#casprv">CASPRV</a>, which holds any putback character are both zeroed. The required mode, supplied in register E, is examined and a "<code>Bad file name</code>" error generated (<a href="#6e6bh">6E6BH</a>) for append or random modes. For output mode the identification block is then written to cassette (<a href="#7125h">7125H</a>) while for input mode the correct identification block is located on the cassette (<a href="#70b8h">70B8H</a>). The FCB address is then placed in <a href="#ptrfil">PTRFIL</a>, the mode in byte 0 of the FCB and the routine terminates.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7205h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7205H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the dispatcher close routine for the CAS device. Byte 0 of the FCB is examined and, if the mode is input, <a href="#casprv">CASPRV</a> is zeroed and the routine terminates. Otherwise the remainder of the I/O buffer is filled with end of file characters (1AH) and the I/O buffer contents written to cassette (722FH). <a href="#casprv">CASPRV</a> is then zeroed and the routine terminates.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-722ah"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 722AH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the dispatcher sequential output routine for the CAS device. The character to output is taken from register C and placed in the next free position in the I/O buffer (<a href="#728bh">728BH</a>). Byte 6 of the FCB, the I/O buffer position, is then incremented. If the I/O buffer position has wrapped round to zero this means that there are two hundred and fifty-six characters in the I/O buffer and it has to be written to cassette. The cassette motor is turned on, a short header is written to cassette (<a href="#72f8h">72F8H</a>) followed by the I/O buffer contents (<a href="#72deh">72DEH</a>), and the motor is turned off via the <a href="#tapoof">TAPOOF</a> standard routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-723fh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 723FH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the dispatcher sequential input routine for the CAS device. <a href="#casprv">CASPRV</a> is first checked (<a href="#72beh">72BEH</a>) to determine whether it contains a character which has been putback, in which case its contents will be non-zero. If so the routine terminates with the character in register A. Otherwise the I/O buffer position is checked (<a href="#729bh">729BH</a>) to determine whether it contains any characters. If the I/O buffer is empty the cassette motor is turned on and the header located (<a href="#72e9h">72E9H</a>). Two hundred and fifty-six characters are then read in (<a href="#72d4h">72D4H</a>), the cassette motor turned off via the <a href="#tapion">TAPION</a> standard routine and the I/O buffer position reset to zero. The character is then taken from the current I/O buffer position and the position incremented. Finally the character is checked to see if it is the end of file character (1AH). If it is not the routine terminates with the character in register A and FLAG NC. Otherwise the end of file character is placed in <a href="#casprv">CASPRV</a>, so that succeeding sequential input requests will always return the end of file condition, and the routine terminates with FLAG C.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-726dh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 726DH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the dispatcher eof routine for the CAS device. The next character is input (<a href="#723fh">723FH</a>) and placed in <a href="#casprv">CASPRV</a>. It is then tested for the end of file code (1AH) and the result placed in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> as an integer, zero for false, FFFFH for true.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-727ch"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 727CH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the dispatcher putback routine for the CAS device. The character is simply placed in <a href="#casprv">CASPRV</a> to be picked up at the next sequential input request.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7281h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7281H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the dispatcher close function to check if there are any characters in the I/O buffer and then zero the I/O buffer position byte in the FCB.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-728bh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 728BH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the dispatcher sequential output function to place the character in register A in the I/O buffer at the current I/O buffer position, which is then incremented.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-729bh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 729BH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the dispatcher sequential input function to collect the character at the current I/O buffer position, which is then incremented.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-72a6h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 72A6H
</code></pre>
<p>This table is used by the dispatcher when decoding function codes for the LPT device. It contains the address of the handler for each of the function codes, most are in fact error generators:</p>

<p><a name="user-content-72bah"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 72BAH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the dispatcher sequential output routine for the LPT device. The character to output is taken from register C and control transfers to the <a href="#outdlp">OUTDLP</a> standard routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-72beh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 72BEH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the dispatcher sequential input function to check if a putback character exists in <a href="#casprv">CASPRV</a>, and if not to return Flag Z. Otherwise <a href="#casprv">CASPRV</a> is zeroed and the character tested to see if it is the end of file character (1AH). If not it returns with the character in register A and FLAG NZ,NC. Otherwise the end of file character is placed back in <a href="#casprv">CASPRV</a> and the routine returns with FLAG Z,C.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-72cdh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 72CDH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by various dispatcher functions to check if the mode in register E is append, if so a "<code>Bad file name</code>" error is generated (<a href="#6e6bh">6E6BH</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-72d4h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 72D4H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by various dispatcher functions to read a character from the cassette. The character is read via the <a href="#tapin">TAPIN</a> standard routine and a "<code>Device I/O error</code>" generated (<a href="#73b2h">73B2H</a>) if FLAG C is returned.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-72deh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 72DEH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by various dispatcher functions to write a character to cassette. The character is written via the <a href="#tapout">TAPOUT</a> standard routine and a "<code>Device I/O error</code>" generated (<a href="#73b2h">73B2H</a>) if FLAG C is returned.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-72e9h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 72E9H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by various dispatcher functions to turn the cassette motor on for input. The motor is turned on via the <a href="#tapion">TAPION</a> standard routine and a "<code>Device I/O error</code>" generated (<a href="#73b2h">73B2H</a>) if FLAG C is returned.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-72f8h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 72F8H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by various dispatcher functions to turn the cassette motor on for output, control simply transfers to the <a href="#tapoon">TAPOON</a> standard routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7304h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7304H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Interpreter Mainloop "<code>OK</code>" point, the "<code>END</code>" statement handler and the run-clear routine to shut down the printer. <a href="#prtflg">PRTFLG</a> is first zeroed and then <a href="#lptpos">LPTPOS</a> tested to see if any characters have been output but left hanging in the printer's line buffer. If so a CR,LF sequence is issued to flush the printer and <a href="#lptpos">LPTPOS</a> zeroed.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7323h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7323H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine issues a CR,LF sequence to the current output device via the <a href="#outdo">OUTDO</a> standard routine. <a href="#lptpos">LPTPOS</a> or <a href="#ttypos">TTYPOS</a> is then zeroed depending upon whether the printer or the screen is active.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7347h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7347H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>INKEY$</code>" function. The state of the keyboard buffer is examined via the <a href="#chsns">CHSNS</a> standard routine. If the buffer is empty the address of a dummy null string descriptor is returned in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. Otherwise the next character is read from the keyboard buffer via the <a href="#chget">CHGET</a> standard routine. After checking that sufficient space is available (6625H) the character is copied to the String Storage Area and the result descriptor created (6821H).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7367h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7367H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the "<code>LIST</code>" statement handler to output a character to the current output device via the <a href="#outdo">OUTDO</a> standard routine. If the character is a LF code then a CR code is also issued.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7374h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7374H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Interpreter Mainloop to collect a line of text when input is from an I/O buffer rather than the keyboard, that is when a "<code>LOAD</code>" statement is active. Characters are sequentially input (<a href="#6c71h">6C71H</a>) and placed in <a href="#buf">BUF</a> until <a href="#buf">BUF</a> fills up, a CR is detected or the end of file is reached. All characters are accepted apart from LF codes which are filtered out. If <a href="#buf">BUF</a> fills up or a CR is detected the routine simply returns the line to the Mainloop. If the end of file is reached while some characters are in <a href="#buf">BUF</a> the line is returned to the Mainloop. When end of file is reached with no characters in <a href="#buf">BUF</a> then I/O buffer 0 is closed (6D7BH) and <a href="#filnam">FILNAM</a> checked to determine whether auto-run is required. If not control returns to the Interpreter "<code>OK</code>" point (411EH). Otherwise the system is cleared (<a href="#629ah">629AH</a>) and control transfers to the Runloop (<a href="#4601h">4601H</a>) to execute the program.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-73b2h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 73B2H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>Device I/O error</code>" generator.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-73b7h"></a><a name="user-content-motor"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 73B7H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>MOTOR</code>" statement handler. If no operand is present control transfers to the <a href="#stmotr">STMOTR</a> standard routine with FFH in register A. If the "<code>OFF</code>" token (EBH) follows control transfers with 00H in register A. If the "<code>ON</code>" token (95H) follows control transfers with 01H in register A.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-73cah"></a><a name="user-content-sound"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 73CAH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>SOUND</code>" statement handler. The register number operand, which must be less than fourteen, is evaluated (521CH) and placed in register A. The data operand is evaluated (521CH) and bit 7 set, bit 6 reset to avoid altering the PSG auxiliary I/O port modes' The data operand is placed in register E and control transfers to the <a href="#wrtpsg">WRTPSG</a> standard routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-73e4h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 73E4H
</code></pre>
<p>This is a single ASCII space used by the "<code>PLAY</code>" statement handler to replace a null string operand with a one character blank string.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-73e5h"></a><a name="user-content-play"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 73E5H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>PLAY</code>" statement handler. The address of the "<code>PLAY</code>" command table at 752EH is placed in <a href="#mcltab">MCLTAB</a> for the macro language parser and <a href="#prscnt">PRSCNT</a> zeroed. The first string operand, which is obligatory, is evaluated (<a href="#4c64h">4C64H</a>), its storage freed (<a href="#67d0h">67D0H</a>) and its length and address placed in <a href="#vcba">VCBA</a> at bytes 2, 3 and 4. The channel's stack pointer is initialized to <a href="#vcba">VCBA</a>+33 and placed in <a href="#vcba">VCBA</a> at bytes 5 and 6' If further text is present in the statement this process is repeated for voices B and C until a maximum of three operands have been evaluated, after this a "<code>Syntax error</code>" is generated (<a href="#4055h">4055H</a>). If there are less than three string operands present an end of queue mark (FFH) is placed in the queue (<a href="#7507h">7507H</a>) of each unused voice. Register A is then zeroed, to select voice A, and control drops into the play mainloop.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-744dh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 744DH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the play mainloop. The number of free bytes in the current queue is checked (<a href="#7521h">7521H</a>) and, if less than eight bytes remain, the next voice is selected (74D6H) to avoid waiting for the queue to empty. The remaining length of the operand string is then taken from the current voice buffer and, if zero bytes remain to be parsed, the loop again skips to the next voice (74D6H). Otherwise the current string length and address are taken from the voice buffer and placed in <a href="#mcllen">MCLLEN</a> and <a href="#mclptr">MCLPTR</a> for the macro language parser. The old stack contents are copied from the voice buffer to the Z80 stack (6253H), <a href="#mclflg">MCLFLG</a> is made non-zero and control transfers to the macro language parser (<a href="#56a2h">56A2H</a>).</p>
<p>The macro language parser will normally scan along the string, using the "<code>PLAY</code>" statement command handlers, until the string is exhausted. However, if a music queue fills up during note generation an abnormal termination is forced back to the play mainloop (748EH) so that the next voice can be processed without waiting for the queue to empty. When control returns normally an end of queue mark is placed in the current queue (<a href="#7507h">7507H</a>) and <a href="#prscnt">PRSCNT</a> is incremented to show the number of strings completed. If control returns abnormally then anything left on the Z80 stack is copied into the current voice buffer (6253H). Because of the recursive nature of the macro language parser where the "<code>X</code>" command is involved there may be a number of four byte string descriptors, marking the point where the original string was suspended, left on the Z80 stack at termination. Saving the stack contents in the voice buffer means they can be restored when the loop gets around to that voice again. Note that as there are only sixteen bytes available in each voice buffer an "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH) if too much data remains on the stack. This will occur when a queue fills up and multiple, nested "X" commands exist, for example:</p>
<pre><code>10 A$="XB$;"
20 B$="XC$;"
30 C$="XD$;"
40 D$=STRING$(150,"A")
50 PLAY A$
</code></pre>
<p>There seems to be a slight bug in this section as only fifteen bytes of stack data are allowed, instead of sixteen, before an error is generated.</p>
<p>When control returns from the macro language parser register A is incremented to select the next voice for processing. When all three voices have been processed <a href="#intflg">INTFLG</a> is checked and, if CTRL-STOP has been detected by the interrupt handler, control transfers to the <a href="#gicini">GICINI</a> standard routine to halt all music and terminate. Assuming bit 7 of <a href="#prscnt">PRSCNT</a> shows this to be the first pass through the mainloop, that is no voice has been temporarily suspended because of a full queue, <a href="#plycnt">PLYCNT</a> is incremented and interrupt dequeueing started via the <a href="#strtms">STRTMS</a> standard routine. <a href="#prscnt">PRSCNT</a> is then checked to determine the number of strings completed by the macro language parser. If all three operand strings have been completed the handler terminates, otherwise control transfers back to the start of the play mainloop to try each voice again.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7507h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7507H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the "<code>PLAY</code>" statement handler to place an end of queue mark (FFH) in the current queue via the <a href="#putq">PUTQ</a> standard routine. If the queue is full it waits until space becomes available.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7521h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7521H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the "<code>PLAY</code>" statement handler to check how much space remains in the current queue via the <a href="#lftq">LFTQ</a> standard routine. If less than eight bytes remain (the largest possible music data packet is seven bytes long) FLAG C is returned.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-752eh"></a></p>

</code></pre>
