<p><a name="user-content-755fh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 755FH
</code></pre>
<p>This table is used by the "<code>PLAY</code>" statement "<code>A</code>" to "<code>G</code>" command handler to translate a note number from zero to fourteen to an offset into the tone divider table at 756EH. The note itself, rather than the note number, is shown below with each offset value:</p>
<pre><code>16 ... A-
18 ... A
20 ... A+ or B-
22 ... B or C-
00 ... B+
00 ... C
02 ... C+ or D-
04 ... D
06 ... D+ or E-
08 ... E or F-
10 ... E+
10 ... F
12 ... F+ or G-
14 ... G
16 ... G+
</code></pre>

<p><a name="user-content-756eh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 756EH
</code></pre>
<p>This table contains the twelve PSG divider constants required to produce the tones of octave 1. For each constant the corresponding note and frequency are shown:</p>
<pre><code>3421 ... C  32.698 Hz
3228 ... C+ 34.653 Hz
3047 ... D  36.712 Hz
2876 ... D+ 38.895 HZ
2715 ... E  41.201 Hz
2562 ... F  43.662 Hz
2419 ... F+ 46.243 Hz
2283 ... G  48.997 Hz
2155 ... G+ 51.908 Hz
2034 ... A  54.995 Hz
1920 ... A+ 58.261 Hz
1812 ... B  61.773 Hz
</code></pre>

<p><a name="user-content-7586h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7586H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>PLAY</code>" statement "<code>V</code>" command handler. The parameter, with a default value of eight, is placed in byte 18 of the current voice buffer without altering bit 6 of the existing contents. No music data is generated.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-759eh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 759EH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>PLAY</code>" statement "<code>M</code>" command handler. The parameter, with a default value of two hundred and fifty-five, is compared with the existing modulation period contained in bytes 19 and 20 of the current voice buffer. If they are the same the routine terminates with no action. Otherwise the new modulation period is placed in the voice buffer and bit 6 set in byte 18 of the voice buffer to indicate that the new value must be incorporated into the next music data packet produced. No music data is generated.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-75beh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 75BEH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>PLAY</code>" statement "<code>S</code>" command handler. The parameter is placed in byte 18 of the current voice buffer and bit 4 of the same byte set to indicate that the new value must be incorporated into the next music data packet produced. No music data is generated. Because of the PSG characteristics the shape and volume parameters are mutually exclusive so the same byte of the voice buffers is used for both.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-75c8h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 75C8H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>PLAY</code>" statement "<code>L</code>" command handler. The parameter, with a default value of four, is placed in byte 16 of the current voice buffer where it is used in the computation of succeeding note durations. No music data is generated.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-75e2h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 75E2H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>PLAY</code>" statement "<code>T</code>" command handler. The parameter, with a default value of one hundred and twenty, is placed in byte 17 of the current voice buffer where it will be used in the computation of succeeding note durations. ho music data is generated.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-75efh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 75EFH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>PLAY</code>" statement "<code>O</code>" command handler. The parameter, with a default value of four, is placed in byte 15 of the current voice buffer where it is used in the computation of succeeding note frequencies. No music data is generated.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-75fch"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 75FCH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>PLAY</code>" statement "<code>R</code>" command handler. The length parameter, with a default value of four, is left in register pair DE and a zero tone divider value placed in register pair HL. The existing volume value is taken from byte 18 of the current voice buffer, temporarily replaced with a zero value and control transferred to the note generator (769CH).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7621h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7621H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>PLAY</code>" statement "<code>N</code>" command handler. The obligatory parameter is first examined, if it is zero a rest is generated (760BH). If it is greater than ninety-six an "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH). Otherwise twelve is repeatedly subtracted from the note number until underflow to obtain an octave number from one to nine in register E and a note number from zero to eleven in register C. Control then transfers to the note generator (7673H).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-763eh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 763EH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>PLAY</code>" statement "<code>A</code>" to "<code>G</code>" command handler. The note letter is first converted into a note number from zero to fourteen, this extended range being necessary because of the redundancy implicit in the notation. The table at 755FH is then used to obtain the offset into the tone divider table and the divider constant for the note placed in register pair DE. The octave value is taken from byte 15 of the current voice buffer and the divider constant halved until the correct octave is reached. The string operand is then examined directly (<a href="#56eeh">56EEH</a>) to determine whether a trailing note length parameter exists. If so it is converted (572FH) and placed in register C. If no parameter exists the default length is taken from byte 16 of the current voice buffer. The duration of the note is then computed from:</p>
<pre><code>Duration (Interrupt ticks) = 12,000/(LENGTH*TEMPO)
</code></pre>
<p>With the normal length value (4) and tempo value (120) this gives a note duration of twenty-five interrupt ticks of 20 ms each or 0.5 seconds. The string operand is then examined (<a href="#56eeh">56EEH</a>) for trailing "<code>.</code>" characters and, for each one, the duration multiplied by one and a half. Finally the resulting duration is checked and, if it is less than five interrupt ticks, it is replaced with a value of five. Thus the shortest note that can be generated on a UK machine is 0.10 seconds whatever the tempo or note length.</p>
<p>The music data packet, which will be three, five or seven bytes long, is then assembled in bytes 8 to 14 of the current voice buffer prior to placing it in the queue. The duration is placed in bytes 8 and 9 of the voice buffer. The volume and flag byte is taken from byte 18 and placed in byte 10 of the voice buffer with bit 7 set to indicate a volume change to the interrupt dequeuing routine. If bit 6 of the volume byte is set then the modulation period is taken from bytes 19 and 20 and added to the data packet at bytes 11 and 12. If the tone divider value is non-zero then it is added to the data packet at bytes 11 and 12 (without a modulation period) or bytes 13 and 14 (with a modulation period). Finally the byte count is mixed into the three highest bits of byte 8 of the voice buffer to complete the preparation of the music data packet.</p>
<p>If the tone divider value is zero, indicating a rest, the contents of <a href="#savvol">SAVVOL</a> are restored to byte 18 of the static buffer. The music data packet is then placed in the current queue via the <a href="#putq">PUTQ</a> standard routine and the number of free bytes remaining checked (<a href="#7521h">7521H</a>). If less than eight bytes remain control transfers directly to the "<code>PLAY</code>" statement handler (748EH), otherwise control returns normally to the macro language parser.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7754h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7754H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the single precision constant 12,000 used in the computation of note duration.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7758h"></a><a name="user-content-put"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7758H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>PUT</code>" statement handler. Register B is set to 80H and control drops into the "<code>GET</code>" statement handler.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-775bh"></a><a name="user-content-get"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 775BH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>GET</code>" statement handler. Register B is zeroed, to distinguish "<code>GET</code>" from "<code>PUT</code>" and the next program token examined. Control then transfers to the "<code>PUT SPRITE</code>" statement handler (<a href="#7aafh">7AAFH</a>) or the Disk BASIC "<code>GET/PUT</code>" statement handler (<a href="#6c35h">6C35H</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7766h"></a><a name="user-content-locate"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7766H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>LOCATE</code>" statement handler. If a column coordinate is present it is evaluated (521CH) and placed in register D, otherwise the current column is taken from <a href="#csrx">CSRX</a>. If a row coordinate is present it is evaluated (521CH) and placed in register E, otherwise the current row is taken from <a href="#csry">CSRY</a>. If a cursor switch operand exists it is evaluated (521CH) and register A loaded with 78H for a zero operand (OFF) and 79H for any non-zero operand (ON). The cursor is then switched by outputting ESC, 78H/79H, "<code>5</code>" via the <a href="#outdo">OUTDO</a> standard routine. The row and column coordinates are placed in register pair HL and the cursor position set via the <a href="#posit">POSIT</a> standard routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-77a5h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 77A5H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>STOP ON/OFF/STOP</code>" statement handler. The address of the device's <a href="#trptbl">TRPTBL</a> status byte is placed in register pair HL and control transfers to the "<code>ON/OFF/STOP</code>" routine (77CFH).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-77abh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 77ABH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>SPRITE ON/OFF/STOP</code>" statement handler. The address of the device's <a href="#trptbl">TRPTBL</a> status byte is placed in register pair HL and control transfers to the "<code>ON/OFF/STOP</code>" routine (77CFH).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-77b1h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 77B1H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>INTERVAL ON/OFF/STOP</code>" statement handler. As there is no specific "<code>INTERVAL</code>" token (control transfers here when an "<code>INT</code>" token is found) a check is first made on the program text for the characters "<code>E</code>" and "<code>R</code>" then the "<code>VAL</code>" token (94H). The address of the device's <a href="#trptbl">TRPTBL</a> status byte is placed in register pair HL and control transfers to the "<code>ON/OFF/STOP</code>" routine (77CFH).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-77bfh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 77BFH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>STRIG ON/OFF/STOP</code>" statement handler. The trigger number, from zero to four, is evaluated (<a href="#7c08h">7C08H</a>) and the address of the device's <a href="#trptbl">TRPTBL</a> status byte placed in register pair HL. The "<code>ON/OFF/STOP</code>" token is examined and the <a href="#trptbl">TRPTBL</a> status byte modified accordingly (77FEH). Control then transfers directly to the Runloop (4612H) to avoid testing for pending interrupts until the end of the next statement.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-77d4h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 77D4H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>KEY(n) ON/OFF/STOP</code>" statement handler. The key number, from one to ten, is evaluated (521CH) and the address of the devices' <a href="#trptbl">TRPTBL</a> status byte placed in register pair HL. The "<code>ON/OFF/STOP</code>" token is examined and the <a href="#trptbl">TRPTBL</a> status byte modified accordingly (77FEH). Bit 0 of the <a href="#trptbl">TRPTBL</a> status byte, the ON bit, is then copied into the corresponding entry in <a href="#fnkflg">FNKFLG</a> for use during the interrupt keyscan and control transfers directly to the Runloop (4612H).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-77feh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 77FEH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine checks for the presence of one of the interrupt switching tokens and transfers control to the appropriate routine: "<code>ON</code>" (<a href="#631bh">631BH</a>), "<code>OFF</code>" (632BH) or "<code>STOP</code>" (<a href="#6331h">6331H</a>). If no token is present a "<code>Syntax error</code>" is generated (4055H).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7810h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7810H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the "<code>ON DEVICE GOSUB</code>" statement handler (<a href="#490dh">490DH</a>) to check the program text for a device token. Unless none of the device tokens is present, in which case Flag C is returned, the device's <a href="#trptbl">TRPTBL</a> entry number is returned in register B and the maximum allowable line number operand count in register C:</p>
<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>DEVICE</th>
<th>TRPTBL#</th>
<th>LINE NUMBERS</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>KEY</td>
<td>00</td>
<td>10</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>STOP</td>
<td>10</td>
<td>01</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>SPRITE</td>
<td>11</td>
<td>01</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>STRIG</td>
<td>12</td>
<td>05</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>INTERVAL</td>
<td>17</td>
<td>01</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<p>Additionally, for "<code>INTERVAL</code>" only, the interval operand is evaluated (<a href="#542fh">542FH</a>) and placed in <a href="#intval">INTVAL</a> and <a href="#intcnt">INTCNT</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-785ch"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 785CH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the "<code>ON DEVICE GOSUB</code>" statement handler (<a href="#490dh">490DH</a>) to place the address of a program line in <a href="#trptbl">TRPTBL</a>. The <a href="#trptbl">TRPTBL</a> entry number, supplied in register B, is multiplied by three and added to the table base to point to the relevant entry. The address, supplied in register pair DE, is then placed there LSB first, MSB second.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-786ch"></a><a name="user-content-key"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 786CH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>KEY</code>" statement handler. If the following character is anything other than the "<code>LIST</code>" token (93H) control transfers to the "<code>KEY n</code>" statement handler (<a href="#78aeh">78AEH</a>). Each of the ten function key strings is then taken from <a href="#fnkstr">FNKSTR</a> and displayed via the <a href="#outdo">OUTDO</a> standard routine with a CR,LF (7328H) after each one. The DEL character (7FH) or any control character smaller than 20H is replaced with a space.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-78aeh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 78AEH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>KEY n</code>", "<code>KEY(n) ON/OFF/STOP</code>", "<code>KEY ON</code>" and "<code>KEY OFF</code>" statement handler. If the next program text character is "(" control transfers to the "<code>KEY(n) ON/OFF/STOP</code>" statement handler (<a href="#77d4h">77D4H</a>). If it is an "<code>ON</code>" token (95H) control transfers to the <a href="#dspfnk">DSPFNK</a> standard routine and if it is an "<code>OFF</code>" token (EBH) to the <a href="#erafnk">ERAFNK</a> standard routine. Otherwise the function key number is evaluated (521CH) and the key's <a href="#fnkstr">FNKSTR</a> address placed in register pair DE' The string operand is evaluated (<a href="#4c64h">4C64H</a>) and its storage freed (<a href="#67d0h">67D0H</a>)' Up to fifteen characters are copied from the string to <a href="#fnkstr">FNKSTR</a> and unused positions padded with zero bytes. If a zero byte is found in the operand string an "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH). Control then transfers to the <a href="#fnksb">FNKSB</a> standard routine to update the function key display if it is enabled.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7900h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7900H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>TIME</code>" function. The contents of <a href="#jiffy">JIFFY</a> are placed in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> as a single precision number (3236H).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-790ah"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 790AH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>CSRLIN</code>" function. The contents of <a href="#csry">CSRY</a> are decremented and placed in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> as an integer (2E9AH).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7911h"></a><a name="user-content-time"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7911H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>TIME</code>" statement handler. The operand is evaluated (542FH) and placed in <a href="#jiffy">JIFFY</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-791bh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 791BH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>PLAY</code>" function. The numeric channel selection operand is evaluated (<a href="#7c08h">7C08H</a>). If this is zero the contents of <a href="#musicf">MUSICF</a> are placed in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> as an integer of value zero or FFFFH. Otherwise the channel number is used to select the appropriate bit of <a href="#musicf">MUSICF</a> and this is then converted to an integer as before.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7940h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7940H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>STICK</code>" function to an operand contained in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. The stick number is checked (521FH) and passed to the <a href="#gtstck">GTSTCK</a> standard routine in register A. The result is placed in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> as an integer (4FCFH ) .</p>
<p><a name="user-content-794ch"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 794CH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>STRIG</code>" function to an operand contained in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. The trigger number is checked (521FH) and passed to the <a href="#gttrig">GTTRIG</a> standard routine in register A. The result is placed in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> as an integer of value zero or FFFFH.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-795ah"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 795AH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>PDL</code>" function to an operand contained in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. The paddle number is checked (521FH) and passed to the <a href="#gtpdl">GTPDL</a> standard routine in register A. The result is placed in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> as an integer (4FCFH).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7969h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7969H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>PAD</code>" function to an operand contained in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. The pad number is checked (521F) and passed to the <a href="#gtpad">GTPAD</a> standard routine in register A. The result is placed in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> as an integer for pads 1, 2, 5 or 6. For pads 0, 3, 4 or 7 the result is placed in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> as an integer of value zero or FFFFH.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7980h"></a><a name="user-content-color"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7980H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>COLOR</code>" statement handler. If a foreground colour operand exists it is evaluated (521CH) and placed in register E, otherwise the current foreground colour is taken from <a href="#forclr">FORCLR</a>. If a background colour operand exists it is evaluated (521CH) and placed in register D, otherwise the current background colour is taken from <a href="#bakclr">BAKCLR</a>. If a border colour operand exists it is evaluated (521CH) and placed in <a href="#bdrclr">BDRCLR</a>. The foreground colour is placed in <a href="#forclr">FORCLR</a> and <a href="#atrbyt">ATRBYT</a>, the background colour in <a href="#bakclr">BAKCLR</a> and control transfers to the <a href="#chgclr">CHGCLR</a> standard routine to modify the VDP.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-79cch"></a><a name="user-content-screen"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 79CCH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>SCREEN</code>" statement handler. If a mode operand exists it is evaluated (521CH) and passed to the <a href="#chgmod">CHGMOD</a> standard routine in register A. If a sprite size operand exists it is evaluated (521CH) and placed in bits 0 and 1 of <a href="#rg1sav">RG1SAV</a>, the Workspace Area copy of VDP <a href="#mode_register_1">Mode Register 1</a>. The VDP sprite parameters are then cleared via the <a href="#clrspr">CLRSPR</a> standard routine. If a key click operand exists it is evaluated (521CH) and placed in <a href="#cliksw">CLIKSW</a>, zero to disable the click and non-zero to enable it. If a baud rate operand exists it is evaluated and the baud rate set (<a href="#7a2dh">7A2DH</a>). If a printer mode operand exists it is evaluated (521CH) and placed in <a href="#ntmsxp">NTMSXP</a>, zero for an MSX printer and non- zero for a general purpose printer.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7a2dh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7A2DH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used to set the cassette baud rate. The operand is evaluated (521CH) and five bytes copied from <a href="#cs1200">CS1200</a> or <a href="#cs2400">CS2400</a> to <a href="#low">LOW</a> as appropriate.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7a48h"></a><a name="user-content-sprite"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7A48H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>SPRITE</code>" statement handler. If the next character is anything other than a "$" control transfers to the "<code>SPRITE ON/OFF/STOP</code>" statement handler (<a href="#77abh">77ABH</a>). <a href="#scrmod">SCRMOD</a> is then checked and an "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error generated (475AH) if the screen is in <a href="#40x24_text_mode">40x24 Text Mode</a>. The sprite pattern number is evaluated and its location in the VRAM Sprite Pattern Table obtained (7AA0H). The string operand is then evaluated (<a href="#4c5fh">4C5FH</a>) and its storage freed (<a href="#67d0h">67D0H</a>). The sprite size, obtained via the <a href="#gspsiz">GSPSIZ</a> standard routine, is compared with the string length and, if the string is shorter than the sprite, the Sprite Pattern Table entry is first filled with zeroes via the <a href="#filvrm">FILVRM</a> standard routine. Characters are then copied from the string body to the Sprite Pattern Table via the <a href="#ldirvm">LDIRVM</a> standard routine until the string is exhausted or the sprite is full. If the string is longer than the sprite size any excess characters are ignored.</p>
<pre><code>Address... 7A84H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>SPRITE$</code>" function. The sprite pattern number is evaluated and its location in the VRAM Sprite Pattern Table obtained (<a href="#7a9fh">7A9FH</a>). The sprite size, obtained via the <a href="#gspsiz">GSPSIZ</a> standard routine, is then placed in register pair BC to control the number of bytes copied. After checking that sufficient space is available in the String Storage Area (<a href="#6627h">6627H</a>) the sprite pattern is copied from VRAM via the <a href="#ldirmv">LDIRMV</a> standard routine and the result descriptor created (<a href="#6654h">6654H</a>). Note that as no check is made on the screen mode during this function some interesting side effects can be found, see below.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7a9fh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7A9FH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the "<code>SPRITE$</code>" statement and function to locate a sprite pattern in the VRAM Sprite Pattern Table. The pattern number operand is evaluated (<a href="#7c08h">7C08H</a>) and passed to the <a href="#calpat">CALPAT</a> standard routine in register A. The pattern address is placed in register pair DE and the routine terminates.</p>
<p>Note that no check is made on the pattern number magnitude for differing sprite sizes. Pattern numbers up to two hundred and fifty-five are accepted even in 16x16 sprite mode when the maximum pattern number should be sixty-three. As a result VRAM addresses greater than 3FFFH will be produced which will wrap around into low VRAM. With the "<code>SPRITE$</code>" statement this will corrupt the Character Generator Table, for example:</p>
<pre><code>10 SCREEN 3,2
20 SPRITE$(0)=STRING$(32,255)
30 PUT SPRITE 0,(0,0), ,0
40 SPRITE$(65)=STRING$(32,255)
50 GOTO 50
</code></pre>
<p>The above puts a real sprite in the top left of the screen and then uses an illegal statement in line 40 to corrupt the VRAM just to the right of it. The "<code>SPRITE$</code>" function can also be manipulated in this way and, as there is no screen mode check, up to thirty-two bytes of the Name Table can be read in <a href="#40x24_text_mode">40x24 Text Mode</a>, for example:</p>
<pre><code>10 SCREEN 0,2
20 PRINT"something"
30 A$=SPRITE$(64)
40 PRINT A$
</code></pre>

<p><a name="user-content-7aafh"></a><a name="user-content-put_sprite"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7AAFH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>GET/PUT SPRITE</code>" statement handler, control is transferred here from the general "<code>GET/PUT</code>" statement handler (<a href="#775bh">775BH</a>). Register B is first checked to make sure that the statement is "<code>PUT</code>" and an "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error generated (475AH) if otherwise. <a href="#scrmod">SCRMOD</a> is then checked and an "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error generated (475AH) if the screen is in <a href="#40x24_text_mode">40x24 Text Mode</a>. The sprite number operand, from zero to thirty-one, is evaluated (521CH) and passed to the <a href="#calatr">CALATR</a> standard routine to locate the four byte attribute block in the Sprite Attribute Table. If a coordinate operand exists it is evaluated and the X coordinate placed in register pair BC, the Y coordinate in register pair DE (<a href="#579ch">579CH</a>).</p>
<p>The Y coordinate LSB is written to byte 0 of the attribute block in VRAM via the <a href="#wrtvrm">WRTVRM</a> standard routine. Bit 7 of the X coordinate is then examined to determine whether it is negative, that is off the left hand side of the screen. If so thirty two is added to the X coordinate and register B is set to 80H to set the early clock bit in the attribute block. For example an X coordinate of -1 (FFFFH) would be changed to +31 with an early clock. The X coordinate LSB is then written to byte 1 of the attribute block via the <a href="#wrtvrm">WRTVRM</a> standard routine. Byte 3 of the attribute block is read in via the <a href="#rdvrm">RDVRM</a> standard routine, the new early clock bit is mixed in and it is then written back to VRAM via the <a href="#wrtvrm">WRTVRM</a> standard routine.</p>
<p>If a colour operand is present it is evaluated (521CH), byte 3 of the attribute block is read in via the <a href="#rdvrm">RDVRM</a> standard routine the new colour code is mixed into the lowest four bits and it is written back to VRAM via the <a href="#wrtvrm">WRTVRM</a> standard routine. If a pattern number operand exists it is evaluated (521CH) and checked for magnitude against the current sprite size provided by the <a href="#gspsiz">GSPSIZ</a> standard routine. The maximum allowable pattern number is two hundred and fifty-five for 8x8 sprites and sixty- three for 16x16 sprites. The pattern number is written to byte 2 of the attribute block via the <a href="#wrtvrm">WRTVRM</a> standard routine and the handler terminates.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7b37h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7B37H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>VDP</code>" statement handler. The register number operand, from zero to seven, is evaluated (<a href="#7c08h">7C08H</a>) followed by the data operand (521CH). The register number is placed in register C, the data value in register B and control transferred to the <a href="#wrtvdp">WRTVDP</a> standard routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7b47h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7B47H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>VDP</code>" function. The register number operand, from zero to eight, is evaluated (<a href="#7c08h">7C08H</a>) and added to <a href="#rg0sav">RG0SAV</a> to locate the corresponding register image in the Workspace Area. The VDP register image is then read and placed in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> as an integer (4FCFH).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7b5ah"></a><a name="user-content-base"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7B5AH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>BASE</code>" statement handler. The VDP table number operand, from zero to nineteen, is evaluated (<a href="#7c08h">7C08H</a>) followed by the base address operand (<a href="#4c64h">4C64H</a>). After checking that the base address is less than 4000H (<a href="#7bfeh">7BFEH</a>) the VDP table number is used to locate the associated entry in the masking table at 7BA3H. The base address is ANDed with the mask and an "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error generated (475AH) if any illegal bits are set. The VDP table number is then added to <a href="#txtnam">TXTNAM</a> to locate the current base address in the Workspace Area and the new base address placed there. The VDP table number is divided by five to determine which of the four screen modes the table belongs to. If this is the same as the current screen mode the new base address is also written to the VDP (<a href="#7b99h">7B99H</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7b99h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7B99H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the "<code>BASE</code>" statement handler to update the VDP base addresses. The current screen mode, in register A, is examined and control transfers to the <a href="#settxt">SETTXT</a>, <a href="#sett32">SETT32</a>, <a href="#setgrp">SETGRP</a> or <a href="#setmlt">SETMLT</a> standard routine as appropriate. Note that this is not a full VDP initialization and that the four current table addresses (<a href="#nambas">NAMBAS</a>, <a href="#cgpbas">CGPBAS</a>, <a href="#patbas">PATBAS</a> and <a href="#atrbas">ATRBAS</a>) which are the ones actually used by the screen routines, are not updated. This can be demonstrated with the following, where the Interpreter carries on outputting to the old VRAM Name Table:</p>
<pre><code>10 SCREEN 0
20 BASE(0)=&amp;H400
30 PRINT"something"
40 FOR N=1 TO 2000:NEXT
50 BASE(0)=0
</code></pre>
<p>Note also that this routine contains a bug. While <a href="#settxt">SETTXT</a> is correctly used for <a href="#40x24_text_mode">40x24 Text Mode</a>, <a href="#setgrp">SETGRP</a> is used for <a href="#32x24_text_mode">32x24 Text Mode</a> and <a href="#setmlt">SETMLT</a> for <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> and <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a>. Any "<code>BASE</code>" statement should therefore be immediately followed by a "<code>SCREEN</code>" statement to perform a full initialization.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7ba3h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7BA3H
</code></pre>
<p>This masking table is used by the "<code>BASE</code>" statement handler to ensure that only legal VDP base addresses are accepted. The table number and corresponding Workspace Area variable are shown with each mask:</p>

<p><a name="user-content-7bcbh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7BCBH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>BASE</code>" function. The VDP table number operand, from zero to nineteen, is evaluated (<a href="#7c08h">7C08H</a>) and added to <a href="#txtnam">TXTNAM</a> to locate the required Workspace Area base address. This is then placed in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> as a single precision number (3236H).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7be2h"></a><a name="user-content-vpoke"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7BE2H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>VPOKE</code>" statement handler. The VRAM address operand is evaluated (<a href="#4c64h">4C64H</a>) and checked to ensure that it is less than 4000H (<a href="#7bfeh">7BFEH</a>). The data operand is then evaluated (521CH) and passed to the <a href="#wrtvrm">WRTVRM</a> standard routine in register A to write to the required address.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7bf5h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7BF5H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>VPEEK</code>" function to an operand contained in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. The VRAM address operand is checked to ensure it is less than 4000H (<a href="#7bfeh">7BFEH</a>). VRAM is then read via the <a href="#rdvrm">RDVRM</a> standard routine and the result placed in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> as an integer (4FCFH).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7bfeh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7BFEH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine converts a numeric operand in <a href="#dac">DAC</a> to an integer (<a href="#2f8ah">2F8AH</a>) and places it in register pair HL. If the operand is equal to or greater than 4000H, and thus outside the allowable VRAM range, an "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7c08h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7C08H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine evaluates (521CH) a parenthesized numeric operand and returns it as an integer in register A. If the operand is greater than the maximum allowable value initially supplied in register A an "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7c16h"></a><a name="user-content-dsko$"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7C16H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>DSKO$</code>" statement handler. An "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH) on a standard MSX machine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7c1bh"></a><a name="user-content-set"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7C1BH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>SET</code>" statement handler. An "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH) on a standard MSX machine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7c20h"></a><a name="user-content-name"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7C20H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>NAME</code>" statement handler. An "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH) on a standard MSX machine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7c25h"></a><a name="user-content-kill"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7C25H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>KILL</code>" statement handler. An "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH) on a standard MSX machine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7c2ah"></a><a name="user-content-ipl"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7C2AH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>IPL</code>" statement handler. An "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH) on a standard MSX machine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7c2fh"></a><a name="user-content-copy"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7C2FH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>COPY</code>" statement handler. An "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH) on a standard MSX machine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7c34h"></a><a name="user-content-cmd"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7C34H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>CMD</code>" statement handler. An "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH) on a standard MSX machine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7c39h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7C39H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>DSKF</code>" function to an operand contained in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. An "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH) on a standard MSX machine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7c3eh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7C3EH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>DSKI$</code>" function. An "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH) on a standard MSX machine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7c43h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7C43H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>ATTR$</code>" function. An "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH) on a standard MSX machine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7c48h"></a><a name="user-content-lset"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7C48H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>LSET</code>" statement handler. An "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH) on a standard MSX machine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7c4dh"></a><a name="user-content-rset"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7C4DH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>RSET</code>" statement handler. An "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH) on a standard MSX machine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7c52h"></a><a name="user-content-field"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7C52H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>FIELD</code>" statement handler. An "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH) on a standard MSX machine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7c57h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7C57H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>MKI$</code>" function to an operand contained in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. An "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH) on a standard MSX machine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7c5ch"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7C5CH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>MKS$</code>" function to an operand contained in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. An "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH) on a standard MSX machine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7c61h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7C61H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>MKD$</code>" function to an operand contained in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. An "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH) on a standard MSX machine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7c66h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7C66H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>CVI</code>" function to an operand contained in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. An "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH) on a standard MSX machine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7c6bh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7C6BH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>CVS</code>" function to an operand contained in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. An "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH) on a standard MSX machine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7c70h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7C70H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the Factor Evaluator to apply the "<code>CVD</code>" function to an operand contained in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>. An "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error is generated (475AH) on a standard MSX machine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7c76h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7C76H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine completes the power-up initialization. At this point the entire Workspace Area is zeroed and only <a href="#exptbl">EXPTBL</a> and <a href="#slttbl">SLTTBL</a> have been initialized. A temporary stack is set at F376H and all one hundred and twelve hooks (560 bytes) filled with Z80 RET opcodes (C9H). <a href="#himem">HIMEM</a> is set to F380H and the lowest RAM location found (<a href="#7d5dh">7D5DH</a>) and placed in <a href="#bottom">BOTTOM</a>. The one hundred and forty-four bytes of data commencing at 7F27H are copied to the Workspace Area from F380H to F40FH The function key strings are initialized via the <a href="#inifnk">INIFNK</a> standard routine, <a href="#endbuf">ENDBUF</a> and <a href="#nlonly">NLONLY</a> are zeroed and a comma is placed in <a href="#bufmin">BUFMIN</a> and a colon in <a href="#kbfmin">KBFMIN</a>. The address of the MSX ROM character set is taken from locations 0004H and 0005H and placed in <a href="#cgpnt">CGPNT</a>+1 and <a href="#prmprv">PRMPRV</a> is set to point to <a href="#prmstk">PRMSTK</a>. Dummy values are placed in <a href="#stktop">STKTOP</a>, <a href="#memsiz">MEMSIZ</a> and <a href="#vartab">VARTAB</a> (their correct values are not known yet), one I/O buffer is allocated (<a href="#7e6bh">7E6BH</a>) and the Z80 SP set (62E5H). A zero byte is placed at the base of RAM, <a href="#txttab">TXTTAB</a> is set to the following location and a "<code>NEW</code>" executed (6287H).</p>
<p>The VDP is then initialized via the <a href="#initio">INITIO</a>, <a href="#init32">INIT32</a> and <a href="#clrspr">CLRSPR</a> standard routines, the cursor coordinates are set to row 11, column 10 and the sign on message "<code>MSX system etc.</code>" is displayed (<a href="#6678h">6678H</a>). After a three second delay a search is carried out for any extension ROMs (<a href="#7d75h">7D75H</a>) and a further "<code>NEW</code>" executed (6287H) in case a BASIC program has been run from ROM.</p>
<p>Finally the identification message "<code>MSX BASIC etc.</code>" is displayed (<a href="#7d29h">7D29H</a>) and control transfers to the Interpreter Mainloop "<code>OK</code>" point 411FH.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7d29h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7D29H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used during power-up to enable the function key display, place the screen in <a href="#40x24_text_mode">40x24 Text Mode</a> via the <a href="#initxt">INITXT</a> standard routine, and display (<a href="#6678h">6678H</a>) the identification message "<code>MSX BASIC etc.</code>". The amount of free memory is then computed by subtracting the contents of <a href="#vartab">VARTAB</a> from the contents of <a href="#stktop">STKTOP</a> and displayed (<a href="#3412h">3412H</a>) followed by the "<code>Bytes free</code>" message.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7d5dh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7D5DH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used during power-up to find the lowest RAM location. Starting at EF00H each byte is tested until one is found that cannot be written to or an address of 8000H is reached. The base address, rounded upwards to the nearest 256 byte boundary, is returned in register pair HL.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7d75h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7D75H
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used during power-up to perform an extension ROM search. Pages 1 and 2 (4000H to BFFFH) of each slot are examined and the results placed in <a href="#sltatr">SLTATR</a>. An extension ROM has the two identification characters "<code>AB</code>" in the first two bytes to distinguish it from RAM. Information about its properties is also present in the first sixteen bytes as follows:</p>
<p><a name="user-content-figure48"></a><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/52d041a450c2a43dcc99b2f2bf436d30ca280071/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830354634382e737667"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/52d041a450c2a43dcc99b2f2bf436d30ca280071/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830354634382e737667" alt="" data-canonical-src="https://rawgit.com/oraculo666/the-msx-red-book/master/images/CH05F48.svg" style="max-width:100%;"></a></p>
<p><strong>Figure 48:</strong> ROM Header</p>
<p>Each page in a given slot is examined by reading the first two bytes (<a href="#7e1ah">7E1AH</a>) and checking for the "<code>AB</code>" characters. If a ROM is present the initialization address is read (<a href="#7e1ah">7E1AH</a>) and control passed to it via the <a href="#calslt">CALSLT</a> standard routine. With a games ROM there may be no return to BASIC from this point. The "<code>CALL</code>" extended statement handler address is then read (<a href="#7e1ah">7E1AH</a>) and bit 5 of register B set if it is valid, that is non-zero. The extended device handler address is read (<a href="#7e1ah">7E1AH</a>) and bit 6 of register B set if it is valid. Finally the BASIC program text address is read (<a href="#7e1ah">7E1AH</a>) and bit 7 of register B set if it is valid. Register B is then copied to the relevant position in <a href="#sltatr">SLTATR</a> and the search continued until no more slots remain.</p>
<p><a href="#sltatr">SLTATR</a> is then examined for any extension ROM flagged as containing BASIC program text. If one is found its position in <a href="#sltatr">SLTATR</a> is converted to a Slot ID (<a href="#7e2ah">7E2AH</a>) and the ROM permanently switched in via the <a href="#enaslt">ENASLT</a> standard routine. <a href="#vartab">VARTAB</a> is set to C000H, as it is not known how large the Program Text Area is, <a href="#txttab">TXTTAB</a> is set to 8008H and <a href="#basrom">BASROM</a> made non-zero to disable the CTRL-STOP key. The system is cleared (<a href="#629ah">629AH</a>) and control transfers to the Runloop (<a href="#4601h">4601H</a>) to execute the BASIC program.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7e1ah"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7E1AH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used to read two bytes from successive locations in an extension ROM. The initial address is supplied in register pair HL and the Slot ID in register C. The bytes are read via the <a href="#rdslt">RDSLT</a> standard routine and returned in register pair DE. If both are zero FLAG Z is returned.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7e2ah"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7E2AH
</code></pre>
<p>This routine converts the <a href="#sltatr">SLTATR</a> position supplied in register B into the corresponding Slot ID in register C and ROM base address in register H. The position is first modified so that it runs from 0 to 63 rather than from 64 to 1, so that the required information is present in the form:</p>
<p><a name="user-content-figure49"></a><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/2ee99038a12ca6fc75159637fa8afb14e4c79e35/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830354634392e737667"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/2ee99038a12ca6fc75159637fa8afb14e4c79e35/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830354634392e737667" alt="" data-canonical-src="https://rawgit.com/oraculo666/the-msx-red-book/master/images/CH05F49.svg" style="max-width:100%;"></a></p>
<p><strong>Figure 49</strong></p>
<p>Bits 0 and 1 are shifted into the highest two bits of register H to form the address. Bits 4 and 5 are shifted to bits 0 and 1 of register C to form the Primary Slot number. Bits 2 and 3 are shifted to bits 2 and 3 of register C to form the Secondary Slot number and bit 7 of the corresponding <a href="#exptbl">EXPTBL</a> entry copied to bit 7 of register C.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7e4bh"></a><a name="user-content-maxfiles"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7E4BH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the "<code>MAXFILES</code>" statement handler. As control transfers here when a "<code>MAX</code>" token (CDH) is detected the program text is first checked for a trailing "<code>FILES</code>" token (B7H). The buffer count operand, from zero to fifteen, is then evaluated (521CH) and any existing buffers closed (<a href="#6c1ch">6C1CH</a>). The required number of I/O buffers are allocated (<a href="#7e6bh">7E6BH</a>), the system is cleared (62A7H) and control transfers directly to the Runloop (<a href="#4601h">4601H</a>).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7e6bh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7E6BH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the I/O buffer allocation routine. It is used during power-up and by the "<code>MAXFILES</code>" and "<code>CLEAR</code>" statement handlers to allocate storage for the number of I/O buffers supplied in register A. Two hundred and sixty-seven bytes are subtracted from the contents of <a href="#himem">HIMEM</a> for every buffer to produce a new <a href="#memsiz">MEMSIZ</a> value. The size of the existing String Storage Area (initially two hundred bytes) is computed by subtracting the old contents of <a href="#stktop">STKTOP</a> from the old contents of <a href="#memsiz">MEMSIZ</a>, this is then subtracted from the new <a href="#memsiz">MEMSIZ</a> value to produce the new <a href="#stktop">STKTOP</a> value. A further one hundred and forty bytes are subtracted for the Z80 stack and an "<code>Out of memory</code>" error generated (6275H) if this address is lower than the start of the Variable Storage Area. Otherwise the buffer count is placed in <a href="#maxfil">MAXFIL</a> and <a href="#memsiz">MEMSIZ</a> and <a href="#stktop">STKTOP</a> set to their new values. The caller's return address is popped, the Z80 SP set to the new position and the return address pushed back onto the stack. <a href="#filtab">FILTAB</a> is then set to the start of the I/O buffer pointer block and each pointer set to point to the associated FCB. Finally the address of I/O buffer 0, the Interpreter's "<code>LOAD</code>" and "<code>SAVE</code>" buffer, is placed in <a href="#nulbuf">NULBUF</a> and the routine terminates.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7ed8h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7ED8H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the plain text message "<code>MSX system</code>" terminated by a zero byte</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7ee4h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7EE4H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the plain text message "<code>version 1.0</code>" CR,LF terminated by a zero byte.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7ef2h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7EF2H
</code></pre>
<p>This is the plain text message "<code>MSX BASIC</code>" terminated by a zero byte.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7efdh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7EFDH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the plain text message "<code>Copyright 1983 by Microsoft</code>" CR,LF terminated by a zero byte.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7f1bh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7F1BH
</code></pre>
<p>This is the plain text message "<code>Bytes free</code>" terminated by a zero byte.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7f27h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7F27H
</code></pre>
<p>This block of one hundred and forty-four data bytes is used to initialize the Workspace Area from F380H to F40FH.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7fb7h"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7FB7H
</code></pre>
<p>This seven byte patch fixes a bug in the external device parsing routine (<a href="#55f8h">55F8H</a>). It checks for a zero length device name in register A and changes it to one if necessary.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-7fbeh"></a></p>
<pre><code>Address... 7FBEH
</code></pre>
<p>This section of the ROM is unused and filled with zero bytes.</p>
<p><br><br><br></p>
<p><a name="user-content-chapter_6"></a></p>
<h1><a id="user-content-6-memory-map" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#6-memory-map"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>6. Memory Map</h1>
<p>A maximum of 32 KB of RAM is available to the BASIC Interpreter to hold the program text, the BASIC Variables, the Z80 stack, the I/O buffers and the internal workspace. A memory map of these areas in the power-up state is shown below:</p>
<p><a name="user-content-figure50"></a><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/c8b8e57a73eed609b2c0eae3e952dad7484110f4/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830354635302e737667"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/c8b8e57a73eed609b2c0eae3e952dad7484110f4/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830354635302e737667" alt="" data-canonical-src="https://rawgit.com/oraculo666/the-msx-red-book/master/images/CH05F50.svg" style="max-width:100%;"></a></p>
<p><strong>Figure 50:</strong> Memory Map 8000H to FFFFH</p>
<p>The Program Text Area is composed of tokenized program lines stored in line number order and terminated by a zero end link, when in the "<code>NEW</code>" state only the end link is present. The zero byte at 8000H is a dummy end of line character needed to synchronize the Runloop at the start of a program.</p>
<p>The Variable and Array Storage Areas are composed of string or numeric Variables and Arrays stored in the order in which they are found in the program text. Execution speed improves marginally if Variables are declared before Arrays in a program as this reduces the amount of memory to be moved upwards.</p>
<p>The Z80 stack is positioned immediately below the String Storage Area, the structure of the stack top is shown below:</p>
<p><a name="user-content-figure51"></a><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/346d8a5378fa60374653db06a07b88dedd3cd94d/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830354635312e737667"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/346d8a5378fa60374653db06a07b88dedd3cd94d/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830354635312e737667" alt="" data-canonical-src="https://rawgit.com/oraculo666/the-msx-red-book/master/images/CH05F51.svg" style="max-width:100%;"></a></p>
<p><strong>Figure 51:</strong> Z80 Stack Top</p>
<p>Whenever the position of the stack is altered, as a result of a "<code>CLEAR</code>" or "<code>MAXFILES</code>" statement, two zero bytes are first pushed to function as a terminator during "<code>FOR</code>" or "<code>GOSUB</code>" parameter block searches. Assuming no parameter blocks are present the Z80 SP will therefore be at <a href="#stktop">STKTOP</a>-2 within the Interpreter Mainloop and at <a href="#stktop">STKTOP</a>-4 when control transfers from the Runloop to a statement handler.</p>
<p>The String Storage Area is composed of the string bodies assigned to Variables or Arrays. During expression evaluation a number of intermediate string results may also be temporarily present under the permanent string heap. The zero byte following the String Storage Area is a temporary delimiter for the "<code>VAL</code>" function.</p>
<p>The region between the String Storage Area and <a href="#himem">HIMEM</a> is used for I/O buffer storage. I/O buffer 0, the "<code>SAVE</code>" and "<code>LOAD</code>" buffer, is always present but the number of user buffers is determined by the "<code>MAXFILES</code>" statement. Each I/O buffer consists of a 9 byte FCB, whose address is contained in the table under FCB 0, followed by a 256 byte data buffer. The FCB contains the status of the I/O buffer as below:</p>
<p><a name="user-content-figure52"></a><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/c951b7dcd1a1a22edc8a8b2aa5a046c84bea1188/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830354635322e737667"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/c951b7dcd1a1a22edc8a8b2aa5a046c84bea1188/68747470733a2f2f7261776769742e636f6d2f6f726163756c6f3636362f7468652d6d73782d7265642d626f6f6b2f6d61737465722f696d616765732f434830354635322e737667" alt="" data-canonical-src="https://rawgit.com/oraculo666/the-msx-red-book/master/images/CH05F52.svg" style="max-width:100%;"></a></p>
<p><strong>Figure 52:</strong> File Control Block</p>
<p>The MOD byte holds the buffer mode, the DEV byte the device code, the POS byte the current position in the buffer (0 to 255) and the PPS byte the "<code>PRINT</code>" position. The remainder of the FCB is unused on a standard MSX machine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-workspace_area"></a></p>
<h2><a id="user-content-workspace-area" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#workspace-area"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Workspace Area</h2>
<p>The section of the Workspace Area from F380H to FD99H holds the BIOS/Interpreter variables. These are listed on the following pages in standard assembly language form:</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f380h"></a><a name="user-content-rdprim"></a>
<a name="user-content-f382h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f383h"></a></p>
<pre><code>F380H RDPRIM: OUT (0A8H),A ; Set new Primary Slot
F382H         LD E,(HL)    ; Read memory
F383H         JR WRPRM1    ; Restore old Primary Slot
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the <a href="#rdslt">RDSLT</a> standard routine to switch Primary Slots and read a byte from memory. The new Primary Slot Register setting is supplied in register A, the old setting in register D and the byte read returned in register E.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f385h"></a><a name="user-content-wrprim"></a>
<a name="user-content-f387h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f388h"></a><a name="user-content-wrprm1"></a>
<a name="user-content-f389h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f38bh"></a></p>
<pre><code>F385H WRPRIM: OUT (0A8H),A ; Set new Primary Slot
F387H         LD (HL),E    ; Write to memory
F388H WRPRM1: LD A,D       ; Get old setting
F389H         OUT (0A8H),A ; Restore old Primary Slot
F38BH         RET
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the <a href="#wrslt">WRSLT</a> standard routine to switch Primary Slots and write a byte to memory. The new Primary Slot Register setting is supplied in register A, the old setting in register D and the byte to write in register E.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f38ch"></a><a name="user-content-clprim"></a>
<a name="user-content-f38eh"></a>
<a name="user-content-f38fh"></a>
<a name="user-content-f392h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f393h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f394h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f396h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f397h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f398h"></a><a name="user-content-clprm1"></a></p>
<pre><code>F38CH CLPRIM: OUT (0A8H),A ; Set new Primary Slot
F38EH         EX AF,AF'    ; Swap to AF for call
F38FH         CALL CLPRM1  ; Do it
F392H         EX AF,AF'    ; Swap to AF
F393H         POP AF       ; Get old setting
F394H         OUT (0A8H),A ; Restore old Primary Slot
F396H         EX AF,AF'    ; Swap to AF
F397H         RET
F398H CLPRM1: JP (IX)
</code></pre>
<p>This routine is used by the <a href="#calslt">CALSLT</a> standard routine to switch Primary Slots and call an address. The new Primary Slot Register setting is supplied in register A, the old setting on the Z80 stack and the address to call in register pair IX.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f39ah"></a><a name="user-content-usrtab"></a>
<a name="user-content-f39ch"></a>
<a name="user-content-f39eh"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3a0h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3a2h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3a4h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3a6h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3a8h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3aah"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3ach"></a></p>
<pre><code>F39AH USRTAB: DEFW 475AH   ; USR 0
F39CH         DEFW 475AH   ; USR 1
F39EH         DEFW 475AH   ; USR 2
F3A0H         DEFW 475AH   ; USR 3
F3A2H         DEFW 475AH   ; USR 4
F3A4H         DEFW 475AH   ; USR 5
F3A6H         DEFW 475AH   ; USR 6
F3A8H         DEFW 475AH   ; USR 7
F3AAH         DEFW 475AH   ; USR 8
F3ACH         DEFW 475AH   ; USR 9
</code></pre>
<p>These ten variables contain the "<code>USR</code>" function addresses. Their values are set to the Interpreter "<code>Illegal function call</code>" error generator at power-up and thereafter only altered by the "<code>DEFUSR</code>" statement.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f3aeh"></a><a name="user-content-linl40"></a></p>
<pre><code>F3AEH LINL40: DEFB 37
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the <a href="#40x24_text_mode">40x24 Text Mode</a> screen width. Its value is set at power-up and thereafter only altered by the "<code>WIDTH</code>" statement.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f3afh"></a><a name="user-content-linl32"></a></p>
<pre><code>F3AFH LINL32: DEFB 29
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the <a href="#32x24_text_mode">32x24 Text Mode</a> screen width. Its value is set at power-up and thereafter only altered by the "<code>WIDTH</code>" statement.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f3b0h"></a><a name="user-content-linlen"></a></p>
<pre><code>F3B0H LINLEN: DEFB 37
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the current text mode screen width. Its value is set from <a href="#linl40">LINL40</a> or <a href="#linl32">LINL32</a> whenever the VDP is initialized to a text mode via the <a href="#initxt">INITXT</a> or <a href="#init32">INIT32</a> standard routines.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f3b1h"></a><a name="user-content-crtcnt"></a></p>
<pre><code>F3B1H CRTCNT: DEFB 24
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the number of rows on the screen. Its value is set at power-up and thereafter unaltered.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f3b2h"></a><a name="user-content-clmlst"></a></p>
<pre><code>F3B2H CLMLST: DEFB 14
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the minimum number of columns that must still be available on a line for a data item to be "<code>PRINT</code>"ed, if less space is available a CR,LF is issued first. Its value is set at power-up and thereafter only altered by the "<code>WIDTH</code>" and "<code>SCREEN</code>" statements.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f3b3h"></a><a name="user-content-txtnam"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3b5h"></a><a name="user-content-txtcol"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3b7h"></a><a name="user-content-txtcgp"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3b9h"></a><a name="user-content-txtatr"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3bbh"></a><a name="user-content-txtpat"></a></p>
<pre><code>F3B3H TXTNAM: DEFW 0000H   ; Name Table Base
F3B5H TXTCOL: DEFW 0000H   ; Colour Table Base
F3B7H TXTCGP: DEFW 0800H   ; Character Pattern Base
F3B9H TXTATR: DEFW 0000H   ; Sprite Attribute Base
F3BBH TXTPAT: DEFW 0000H   ; Sprite Pattern Base
</code></pre>
<p>These five variables contain the <a href="#40x24_text_mode">40x24 Text Mode</a> VDP base addresses. Their values are set at power-up and thereafter only altered by the "<code>BASE</code>" statement.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f3bdh"></a><a name="user-content-t32nam"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3bfh"></a><a name="user-content-t32col"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3c1h"></a><a name="user-content-t32cgp"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3c3h"></a><a name="user-content-t32atr"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3c5h"></a><a name="user-content-t32pat"></a></p>
<pre><code>F3BDH T32NAM: DEFW 1800H   ; Name Table Base
F3BFH T32COL: DEFW 2000H   ; Colour Table Base
F3C1H T32CGP: DEFW 0000H   ; Character Pattern Base
F3C3H T32ATR: DEFW 1B00H   ; Sprite Attribute Base
F3C5H T32PAT: DEFW 3800H   ; Sprite Pattern Base
</code></pre>
<p>These five variables contain the <a href="#32x24_text_mode">32x24 Text Mode</a> VDP base addresses. Their values are set at power-up and thereafter only altered by the "<code>BASE</code>" statement.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f3c7h"></a><a name="user-content-grpnam"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3c9h"></a><a name="user-content-grpcol"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3cbh"></a><a name="user-content-grpcgp"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3cdh"></a><a name="user-content-grpatr"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3cfh"></a><a name="user-content-grppat"></a></p>
<pre><code>F3C7H GRPNAM: DEFW 1800H   ; Name Table Base
F3C9H GRPCOL: DEFW 2000H   ; Colour Table Base
F3CBH GRPCGP: DEFW 0000H   ; Character Pattern Base
F3CDH GRPATR: DEFW 1B00H   ; Sprite Attribute Base
F3CFH GRPPAT: DEFW 3800H   ; Sprite Pattern Base
</code></pre>
<p>These five variables contain the <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> VDP base addresses. Their values are set at power-up and thereafter only altered by the "<code>BASE</code>" statement.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f3d1h"></a><a name="user-content-mltnam"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3d3h"></a><a name="user-content-mltcol"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3d5h"></a><a name="user-content-mltcgp"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3d7h"></a><a name="user-content-mltatr"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3d9h"></a><a name="user-content-mltpat"></a></p>
<pre><code>F3D1H MLTNAM: DEFW 0800H   ; Name Table Base
F3D3H MLTCOL: DEFW 0000H   ; Colour Table Base
F3D5H MLTCGP: DEFW 0000H   ; Character Pattern Base
F3D7H MLTATR: DEFW 1B00H   ; Sprite Attribute Base
F3D9H MLTPAT: DEFW 3800H   ; Sprite Pattern Base
</code></pre>
<p>These five variables contain the <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a> VDP base addresses. Their values are set at power-up and thereafter only altered by the "<code>BASE</code>" statement.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f3dbh"></a><a name="user-content-cliksw"></a></p>
<pre><code>F3DBH CLIKSW: DEFB 01H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable controls the interrupt handler key click: 00H=Off, NZ=On. Its value is set at power-up and thereafter only altered by the "<code>SCREEN</code>" statement.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f3dch"></a><a name="user-content-csry"></a></p>
<pre><code>F3DCH CSRY:   DEFB 01H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the row coordinate (from 1 to <a href="#ctrcnt">CTRCNT</a>) of the text mode cursor.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f3ddh"></a><a name="user-content-csrx"></a></p>
<pre><code>F3DDH CSRX:   DEFB 01H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the column coordinate (from 1 to <a href="#linlen">LINLEN</a>) of the text mode cursor. Note that the BIOS cursor coordinates for the home position are 1,1 whatever the screen width.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f3deh"></a><a name="user-content-cnsdfg"></a></p>
<pre><code>F3DEH CNSDFG: DEFB FFH
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the current state of the function key display: 00H=Off, NZ=On.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f3dfh"></a><a name="user-content-rg0sav"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3e0h"></a><a name="user-content-rg1sav"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3e1h"></a><a name="user-content-rg2sav"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3e2h"></a><a name="user-content-rg3sav"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3e3h"></a><a name="user-content-rg4sav"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3e4h"></a><a name="user-content-rg5sav"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3e5h"></a><a name="user-content-rg6sav"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3e6h"></a><a name="user-content-rg7sav"></a></p>
<pre><code>F3DFH RG0SAV: DEFB 00H
F3E0H RG1SAV: DEFB F0H
F3E1H RG2SAV: DEFB 00H
F3E2H RG3SAV: DEFB 00H
F3E3H RG4SAV: DEFB 01H
F3E4H RG5SAV: DEFB 00H
F3E5H RG6SAV: DEFB 00H
F3E6H RG7SAV: DEFB F4H
</code></pre>
<p>These eight variables mimic the state of the eight write-only <a href="#vdp_mode_registers">VDP Mode Registers</a>. The values shown are for <a href="#40x24_text_mode">40x24 Text Mode</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f3e7h"></a><a name="user-content-statfl"></a></p>
<pre><code>F3E7H STATFL: DEFB CAH
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is continuously updated by the interrupt handler with the contents of the <a href="#vdp_status_register">VDP Status Register</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f3e8h"></a><a name="user-content-trgflg"></a></p>
<pre><code>F3E8H TRGFLG: DEFB F1H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is continuously updated by the interrupt handler with the state of the four joystick trigger inputs and the space key.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f3e9h"></a><a name="user-content-forclr"></a></p>
<pre><code>F3E9H FORCLR: DEFB 0FH     ; White
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the current foreground colour. Its value is set at power-up and thereafter only altered by the "<code>COLOR</code>" statement. The foreground colour is used by the <a href="#clrspr">CLRSPR</a> standard routine to set the sprite colour and by the <a href="#chgclr">CHGCLR</a> standard routine to set the 1 pixel colour in the text modes. It also functions as the graphics ink colour as it is copied to <a href="#atrbyt">ATRBYT</a> by the <a href="#grpprt">GRPPRT</a> standard routine and used throughout the Interpreter as the default value for any optional colour operand.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f3eah"></a><a name="user-content-bakclr"></a></p>
<pre><code>F3EAH BAKCLR: DEFB 04H     ; Dark blue
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the current background colour. Its value is set at power-up and thereafter only altered by the "<code>COLOR</code>" statement. The background colour is used by the <a href="#cls">CLS</a> standard routine to clear the screen in the graphics modes and by the <a href="#chgclr">CHGCLR</a> standard routine to set the 0 pixel colour in the text modes.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f3ebh"></a><a name="user-content-bdrclr"></a></p>
<pre><code>F3EBH BDRCLR: DEFB 04H     ; Dark blue
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the current border colour. Its value is set at power-up and thereafter only altered by the "<code>COLOR</code>" statement. The border colour is used by the <a href="#chgclr">CHGCLR</a> standard routine in <a href="#32x24_text_mode">32x24 Text Mode</a>, <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> and <a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a> to set the border colour.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f3ech"></a><a name="user-content-maxupd"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3edh"></a></p>
<pre><code>F3ECH MAXUPD: DEFB C3H
F3EDH         DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>These two bytes are filled in by the "<code>LINE</code>" statement handler to form a Z80 JP to the <a href="#rightc">RIGHTC</a>, <a href="#leftc">LEFTC</a>, <a href="#upc">UPC</a> or <a href="#downc">DOWNC</a> standard routines.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f3efh"></a><a name="user-content-minupd"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3f0h"></a></p>
<pre><code>F3EFH MINUPD: DEFB C3H
F3F0H         DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>These two bytes are filled in by the "<code>LINE</code>" statement handler to form a Z80 JP to the <a href="#rightc">RIGHTC</a>, <a href="#leftc">LEFTC</a>, <a href="#upc">UPC</a> or <a href="#downc">DOWNC</a> standard routines.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f3f2h"></a><a name="user-content-atrbyt"></a></p>
<pre><code>F3F2H ATRBYT: DEFB 0FH
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the graphics ink colour used by the <a href="#setc">SETC</a> and <a href="#nsetcx">NSETCX</a> standard routines.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f3f3h"></a><a name="user-content-queues"></a></p>
<pre><code>F3F3H QUEUES: DEFW F959H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the address of the control blocks for the three music queues. Its value is set at power-up and thereafter unaltered.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f3f5h"></a><a name="user-content-frcnew"></a></p>
<pre><code>F3F5H FRCNEW: DEFB FFH
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains a flag to distinguish the two statements in the "<code>CLOAD/CLOAD?</code>" statement handler: 00H=CLOAD, FFH=CLOAD?.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f3f6h"></a><a name="user-content-scncnt"></a></p>
<pre><code>F3F6H SCNCNT: DEFB 01H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used as a counter by the interrupt handler to control the rate at which keyboard scans are performed.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f3f7h"></a><a name="user-content-repcnt"></a></p>
<pre><code>F3F7H REPCNT: DEFB 01H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used as a counter by the interrupt handler to control the key repeat rate.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f3f8h"></a><a name="user-content-putpnt"></a></p>
<pre><code>F3F8H PUTPNT: DEFW FBF0H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the address of the put position in <a href="#keybuf">KEYBUF</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f3fah"></a><a name="user-content-getpnt"></a></p>
<pre><code>F3FAH GETPNT: DEFW FBF0H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the address of the get position in <a href="#keybuf">KEYBUF</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f3fch"></a><a name="user-content-cs1200"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3fdh"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3feh"></a>
<a name="user-content-f3ffh"></a>
<a name="user-content-f400h"></a></p>
<pre><code>F3FCH CS1200: DEFB 53H     ; LO cycle 1st half
F3FDH         DEFB 5CH     ; LO cycle 2nd half
F3FEH         DEFB 26H     ; HI cycle 1st half
F3FFH         DEFB 2DH     ; HI cycle 2nd half
F400H         DEFB 0FH     ; Header cycle count
</code></pre>
<p>These five variables contain the 1200 baud cassette parameters. Their values are set at power-up and thereafter unaltered.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f401h"></a><a name="user-content-cs2400"></a>
<a name="user-content-f402h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f403h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f404h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f405h"></a></p>
<pre><code>F401H CS2400: DEFB 25H     ; LO cycle 1st half
F402H         DEFB 2DH     ; LO cycle 2nd half
F403H         DEFB 0EH     ; HI cycle 1st half
F404H         DEFB 16H     ; HI cycle 2nd half
F405H         DEFB 1FH     ; Header cycle count
</code></pre>
<p>These five variables contain the 2400 baud cassette parameters. Their values are set at power-up and thereafter unaltered.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f406h"></a><a name="user-content-low"></a>
<a name="user-content-f407h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f408h"></a><a name="user-content-high"></a>
<a name="user-content-f409h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f40ah"></a><a name="user-content-header"></a></p>
<pre><code>F406H LOW:    DEFB 53H     ; LO cycle 1st half
F407H         DEFB 5CH     ; LO cycle 2nd half
F408H HIGH:   DEFB 26H     ; HI cycle 1st half
F409H         DEFB 2DH     ; HI cycle 2nd half
F40AH HEADER: DEFB 0FH     ; Header cycle count
</code></pre>
<p>These five variables contain the current cassette parameters. Their values are set to 1200 baud at power-up and thereafter only altered by the "<code>CSAVE</code>" and "<code>SCREEN</code>" statements.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f40bh"></a><a name="user-content-aspct1"></a></p>
<pre><code>F40BH ASPCT1: DEFW 0100H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the reciprocal of the default "<code>CIRCLE</code>" aspect ratio multiplied by 256. Its value is set at power-up and thereafter unaltered.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f40dh"></a><a name="user-content-aspct2"></a></p>
<pre><code>F40DH ASPCT2: DEFW 01C0H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the default "<code>CIRCLE</code>" aspect ratio multiplied by 256. Its value is set at power-up and thereafter unaltered. The aspect ratio is present in two forms so that the "<code>CIRCLE</code>" statement handler can select the appropriate one immediately rather than needing to examine and possibly reciprocate it as is the case with an operand in the program text.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f40fh"></a><a name="user-content-endprg"></a>
<a name="user-content-f410h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f411h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f412h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f413h"></a></p>
<pre><code>F40FH ENDPRG: DEFB ":"
F410H         DEFB 00H
F411H         DEFB 00H
FE12H         DEFB 00H
F413H         DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>These five bytes form a dummy program line. Their values are set at power-up and thereafter unaltered. The line exists in case an error occurs in the Interpreter Mainloop before any tokenized text is available in <a href="#kbuf">KBUF</a>. If an "<code>ON ERROR GOTO</code>" is active at this time then it provides some text for the "<code>RESUME</code>" statement to terminate on.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f414h"></a><a name="user-content-errflg"></a></p>
<pre><code>F414H ERRFLG: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the Interpreter error handler to save the error number.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f415h"></a><a name="user-content-lptpos"></a></p>
<pre><code>F415H LPTPOS: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the "<code>LPRINT</code>" statement handler to hold the current position of the printer head.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f416h"></a><a name="user-content-prtflg"></a></p>
<pre><code>F416H PRTFLG: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable determines whether the <a href="#outdo">OUTDO</a> standard routine directs its output to the screen or to the printer: 00H=Screen, 01H=Printer.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f417h"></a><a name="user-content-ntmsxp"></a></p>
<pre><code>F417H NTMSXP: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable determines whether the <a href="#outdo">OUTDO</a> standard routine will replace headered graphics characters directed to the printer with spaces: 00H=Graphics, NZ=Spaces. Its value is set at power-up and thereafter only altered by the "<code>SCREEN</code>" statement.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f418h"></a><a name="user-content-rawprt"></a></p>
<pre><code>F418H RAWPRT: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable determines whether the <a href="#outdo">OUTDO</a> standard routine will modify control and headered graphics characters directed to the printer: 00H=Modify, NZ=Raw. Its value is set at power-up and thereafter unaltered.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f419h"></a><a name="user-content-vlzadr"></a>
<a name="user-content-f41bh"></a><a name="user-content-vlzdat"></a></p>
<pre><code>F419H VLZADR: DEFW 0000H
F41BH VLZDAT: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>These variables contain the address and value of any character temporarily removed by the "<code>VAL</code>" function.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f41ch"></a><a name="user-content-curlin"></a></p>
<pre><code>F41CH CURLIN: DEFW FFFFH
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the current Interpreter line number. A value of FFFFH denotes direct mode.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f41eh"></a><a name="user-content-kbfmin"></a></p>
<pre><code>F41EH KBFMIN: DEFB ":"
</code></pre>
<p>This byte provides a dummy prefix to the tokenized text contained in <a href="#kbuf">KBUF</a>. Its function is similar to that of <a href="#endprg">ENDPRG</a> but is used for the situation where an error occurs within a direct statement.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f41fh"></a><a name="user-content-kbuf"></a></p>
<pre><code>F41FH KBUF:   DEFS 318
</code></pre>
<p>This buffer contains the tokenized form of the input line collected by the Interpreter Mainloop. When a direct statement is executed the contents of this buffer form the program text.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f55dh"></a><a name="user-content-bufmin"></a></p>
<pre><code>F55DH BUFMIN: DEFB ","
</code></pre>
<p>This byte provides a dummy prefix to the text contained in <a href="#buf">BUF</a>. It is used to synchronize the "<code>INPUT</code>" statement handler as it starts to analyze the input text.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f55eh"></a><a name="user-content-buf"></a></p>
<pre><code>F55EH BUF:    DEFS 259
</code></pre>
<p>This buffer contains the text collected from the console by the <a href="#inlin">INLIN</a> standard routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f661h"></a><a name="user-content-ttypos"></a></p>
<pre><code>F661H TTYPOS: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the "<code>PRINT</code>" statement handler to hold the current screen position (Teletype!).</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f662h"></a><a name="user-content-dimflg"></a></p>
<pre><code>F662H DIMFLG: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is normally zero but is set by the "<code>DIM</code>" statement handler to control the operation of the variable search routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f663h"></a><a name="user-content-valtyp"></a></p>
<pre><code>F663H VALTYP: DEFB 02H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the type code of the operand currently contained in <a href="#dac">DAC</a>: integer, 3=String, 4=Single Precision, 8=Double Precision.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f664h"></a><a name="user-content-dores"></a></p>
<pre><code>F664H DORES:  DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
