<p>This variable is normally zero but is set to prevent the tokenization of unquoted keywords following a "<code>DATA</code>" token.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f665h"></a><a name="user-content-donum"></a></p>
<pre><code>F665H DONUM:  DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is normally zero but is set when a numeric constant follows one of the keywords <code>GOTO</code>, <code>GOSUB</code>, <code>THEN</code>, etc., and must be tokenized to the special line number operand form.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f666h"></a><a name="user-content-contxt"></a></p>
<pre><code>F666H CONTXT: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the <a href="#chrgtr">CHRGTR</a> standard routine to save the address of the character following a numeric constant in the program text.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f668h"></a><a name="user-content-consav"></a></p>
<pre><code>F668H CONSAV: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the <a href="#chrgtr">CHRGTR</a> standard routine to save the token of a numeric constant found in the program text.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f669h"></a><a name="user-content-contyp"></a></p>
<pre><code>F669H CONTYP: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the <a href="#chrgtr">CHRGTR</a> standard routine to save the type of a numeric constant found in the program text.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f66ah"></a><a name="user-content-conlo"></a></p>
<pre><code>F66AH CONLO:  DEFS 8
</code></pre>
<p>This buffer is used by the <a href="#chrgtr">CHRGTR</a> standard routine to save the value of a numeric constant found in the program text.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f672h"></a><a name="user-content-memsiz"></a></p>
<pre><code>F672H MEMSIZ: DEFW F168H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the address of the top of the String Storage Area. Its value is set at power-up and thereafter only altered by the "<code>CLEAR</code>" and "<code>MAXFILES</code>" statements.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f674h"></a><a name="user-content-stktop"></a></p>
<pre><code>F674H STKTOP: DEFW F0A0H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the address of the top of the Z80 stack. Its value is set at power-up to <a href="#memsiz">MEMSIZ</a>-200 and thereafter only altered by the "<code>CLEAR</code>" and "<code>MAXFILES</code>" statements.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f676h"></a><a name="user-content-txttab"></a></p>
<pre><code>F676H TXTTAB: DEFW 8001H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the address of the first byte of the Program Text Area. Its value is set at power-up and thereafter unaltered.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f678h"></a><a name="user-content-temppt"></a></p>
<pre><code>F678H TEMPPT: DEFW F67AH
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the address of the next free location in <a href="#tempst">TEMPST</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f67ah"></a><a name="user-content-tempst"></a></p>
<pre><code>F67AH TEMPST: DEFS 30
</code></pre>
<p>This buffer is used to store string descriptors. It functions as a stack with string producers pushing their results and string consumers popping them.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f698h"></a><a name="user-content-dsctmp"></a></p>
<pre><code>F698H DSCTMP: DEFS 3
</code></pre>
<p>This buffer is used by the string functions to hold a result descriptor while it is being constructed.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f69bh"></a><a name="user-content-fretop"></a></p>
<pre><code>F69BH FRETOP: DEFW F168H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the address of the next free location in the String Storage Area. When the area is empty <a href="#fretop">FRETOP</a> is equal to <a href="#memsiz">MEMSIZ</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f69dh"></a><a name="user-content-temp3"></a></p>
<pre><code>F69DH TEMP3: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used for temporary storage by various parts of the Interpreter.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f69fh"></a><a name="user-content-temp8"></a></p>
<pre><code>F69FH TEMP8:  DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used for temporary storage by various parts of the Interpreter.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f6a1h"></a><a name="user-content-endfor"></a></p>
<pre><code>F6A1H ENDFOR: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the "<code>FOR</code>" statement handler to hold the end of statement address during construction of a parameter block.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f6a3h"></a><a name="user-content-datlin"></a></p>
<pre><code>F6A3H DATLIN: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the line number of the current "<code>DATA</code>" item in the program text.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f6a5h"></a><a name="user-content-subflg"></a></p>
<pre><code>F6A5H SUBFLG: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is normally zero but is set by the "<code>ERASE</code>", "<code>FOR</code>", "<code>FN</code>" and "<code>DEF FN</code>" handlers to control the processing of subscripts by the variable search routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f6a6h"></a><a name="user-content-flginp"></a></p>
<pre><code>F6A6H FLGINP: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains a flag to distinguish the two statements in the "<code>READ/INPUT</code>" statement handler: 00H=INPUT, NZ=READ.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f6a7h"></a><a name="user-content-temp"></a></p>
<pre><code>F6A7H TEMP:   DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used for temporary storage by various parts of the Interpreter.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f6a9h"></a><a name="user-content-ptrflg"></a></p>
<pre><code>F6A9H PTRFLG: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is normally zero but is set if any line number operands in the Program Text Area have been converted to pointers.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f6aah"></a><a name="user-content-autflg"></a></p>
<pre><code>F6AAH AUTFLG: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is normally zero but is set when "<code>AUTO</code>" mode is turned on.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f6abh"></a><a name="user-content-autlin"></a></p>
<pre><code>F6ABH AUTLIN: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the current "<code>AUTO</code>" line number.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f6adh"></a><a name="user-content-autinc"></a></p>
<pre><code>F6ADH AUTINC: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the current "<code>AUTO</code>" line number increment.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f6afh"></a><a name="user-content-savtxt"></a></p>
<pre><code>F6AFH SAVTXT: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is updated by the Runloop at the start of every statement with the current location in the program text. It is used during error recovery to set <a href="#errtxt">ERRTXT</a> for the "<code>RESUME</code>" statement handler and <a href="#oldtxt">OLDTXT</a> for the "<code>CONT</code>" statement handler.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f6b1h"></a><a name="user-content-savstk"></a></p>
<pre><code>F6B1H SAVSTK: DEFW F09EH
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is updated by the Runloop at the start of every statement with the current Z80 SP for error recovery purposes.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f6b3h"></a><a name="user-content-errlin"></a></p>
<pre><code>F6B3H ERRLIN: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the error handler to hold the line number of the program line generating an error.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f6b5h"></a><a name="user-content-dot"></a></p>
<pre><code>F6B5H DOT:    DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is updated by the Mainloop and the error handler with the current line number for use with the "." parameter.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f6b7h"></a><a name="user-content-errtxt"></a></p>
<pre><code>F6B7H ERRTXT: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is updated from <a href="#savtxt">SAVTXT</a> by the error handler for use by the "<code>RESUME</code>" statement handler.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f6b9h"></a><a name="user-content-onelin"></a></p>
<pre><code>F6B9H ONELIN: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is set by the "<code>ON ERROR GOTO</code>" statement handler with the address of the program line to execute when an error occurs.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f6bbh"></a><a name="user-content-oneflg"></a></p>
<pre><code>F6BBH ONEFLG: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is normally zero but is set by the error handler when control transfers to an "<code>ON ERROR GOTO</code>" statement. This is to prevent a loop developing if an error occurs inside the error recovery statements.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f6bch"></a><a name="user-content-temp2"></a></p>
<pre><code>F6BCH TEMP2:  DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used for temporary storage by various parts of the Interpreter.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f6beh"></a><a name="user-content-oldlin"></a></p>
<pre><code>F6BEH OLDLIN: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the line number of the terminating program line. It is set by the "<code>END</code>" and "<code>STOP</code>" statement handlers for use with the "<code>CONT</code>" statement.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f6c0h"></a><a name="user-content-oldtxt"></a></p>
<pre><code>F6C0H OLDTXT: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the address of the terminating program statement.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f6c2h"></a><a name="user-content-vartab"></a></p>
<pre><code>F6C2H VARTAB: DEFW 8003H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the address of the first byte of the Variable Storage Area.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f6c4h"></a><a name="user-content-arytab"></a></p>
<pre><code>F6C4H ARYTAB: DEFW 8003H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the address of the first byte of the Array Storage Area.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f6c6h"></a><a name="user-content-strend"></a></p>
<pre><code>F6C6H STREND: DEFW 8003H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the address of the byte following the Array Storage Area.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f6c8h"></a><a name="user-content-datptr"></a></p>
<pre><code>F6C8H DATPTR: DEFW 8000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the address of the current "<code>DATA</code>" item in the program text.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f6cah"></a><a name="user-content-deftbl"></a>
<a name="user-content-f6cbh"></a>
<a name="user-content-f6cch"></a>
<a name="user-content-f6cdh"></a>
<a name="user-content-f6ceh"></a>
<a name="user-content-f6cfh"></a>
<a name="user-content-f6d0h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f6d1h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f6d2h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f6d3h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f6d4h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f6d5h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f6d6h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f6d7h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f6d8h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f6d9h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f6dah"></a>
<a name="user-content-f6dbh"></a>
<a name="user-content-f6dch"></a>
<a name="user-content-f6ddh"></a>
<a name="user-content-f6deh"></a>
<a name="user-content-f6dfh"></a>
<a name="user-content-f6e0h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f6e1h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f6e2h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f6e3h"></a></p>
<pre><code>F6CAH DEFTBL: DEFB 08H     ; A
F6CBH         DEFB 08H     ; B
F6CCH         DEFB 08H     ; C
F6CDH         DEFB 08H     ; D
F6CEH         DEFB 08H     ; E
F6CFH         DEFB 08H     ; F
F6D0H         DEFB 08H     ; G
F6D1H         DEFB 08H     ; H
F6D2H         DEFB 08H     ; I
F6D3H         DEFB 08H     ; J
F6D4H         DEFB 08H     ; K
F6D5H         DEFB 08H     ; L
F6D6H         DEFB 08H     ; M
F6D7H         DEFB 08H     ; N
F6D8H         DEFB 08H     ; O
F6D9H         DEFB 08H     ; P
F6DAH         DEFB 08H     ; Q
F6DBH         DEFB 08H     ; R
F6DCH         DEFB 08H     ; S
F6DDH         DEFB 08H     ; T
F6DEH         DEFB 08H     ; U
F6DFH         DEFB 08H     ; V
F6E0H         DEFB 08H     ; W
F6E1H         DEFB 08H     ; X
F6E2H         DEFB 08H     ; Y
F6E3H         DEFB 08H     ; Z
</code></pre>
<p>These twenty-six variables contain the default type for each group of BASIC Variables. Their values are set to double precision at power-up, "<code>NEW</code>" and "<code>CLEAR</code>" and thereafter altered only by the "<code>DEF</code>" group of statements.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f6e4h"></a><a name="user-content-prmstk"></a></p>
<pre><code>F6E4H PRMSTK: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the base address of the previous "<code>FN</code>" parameter block on the Z80 stack. It is used during string garbage collection to travel from block to block on the stack.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f6e6h"></a><a name="user-content-prmlen"></a></p>
<pre><code>F6E6H PRMLEN: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the length of the current "<code>FN</code>" parameter block in <a href="#parm1">PARM1</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f6e8h"></a><a name="user-content-parm1"></a></p>
<pre><code>F6E8H PARM1 : DEFS 100
</code></pre>
<p>This buffer contains the local Variables belonging to the "<code>FN</code>" function currently being evaluated.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f74ch"></a><a name="user-content-prmprv"></a></p>
<pre><code>F74CH PRMPRV: DEFW F6E4H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the address of the previous "<code>FN</code>" parameter block. It is actually a constant used to ensure that string garbage collection commences with the current parameter block before proceeding to those on the stack.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f74eh"></a><a name="user-content-prmln2"></a></p>
<pre><code>F74EH PRMLN2: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the length of the "<code>FN</code>" parameter block being constructed in <a href="#parm2">PARM2</a></p>
<p><a name="user-content-f750h"></a><a name="user-content-parm2"></a></p>
<pre><code>F750H PARM2:  DEFS 100
</code></pre>
<p>This buffer is used to construct the local Variables owned by the current "<code>FN</code>" function.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f7b4h"></a><a name="user-content-prmflg"></a></p>
<pre><code>F7B4H PRMFLG: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used during a Variable search to indicate whether local or global Variables are being examined.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f7b5h"></a><a name="user-content-aryta2"></a></p>
<pre><code>F7B5H ARYTA2: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used during a Variable search to hold the termination address of the storage area being examined.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f7b7h"></a><a name="user-content-nofuns"></a></p>
<pre><code>F7B7H NOFUNS: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is normally zero but is set by the "<code>FN</code>" function handler to indicate to the variable search routine that local Variables are present.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f7b8h"></a><a name="user-content-temp9"></a></p>
<pre><code>F7B8H TEMP9:  DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used for temporary storage by various parts of the Interpreter.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f7bah"></a><a name="user-content-funact"></a></p>
<pre><code>F7BAH FUNACT: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the number of currently active "<code>FN</code>" functions.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f7bch"></a><a name="user-content-swptmp"></a></p>
<pre><code>F7BCH SWPTMP: DEFS 8
</code></pre>
<p>This buffer is used to hold the first operand in a "<code>SWAP</code>" statement.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f7c4h"></a><a name="user-content-trcflg"></a></p>
<pre><code>F7C4H TRCFLG: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is normally zero but is set by the "<code>TRON</code>" statement handler to turn on the trace facility.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f7c5h"></a><a name="user-content-fbuffr"></a></p>
<pre><code>F7C5H FBUFFR: DEFS 43
</code></pre>
<p>This buffer is used to hold the text produced during numeric output conversion.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f7f0h"></a><a name="user-content-dectmp"></a></p>
<pre><code>F7F0H DECTMP: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used for temporary storage by the double precision division routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f7f2h"></a><a name="user-content-dectm2"></a></p>
<pre><code>F7F2H DECTM2: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used for temporary storage by the double precision division routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f7f4h"></a><a name="user-content-deccnt"></a></p>
<pre><code>F7F4H DECCNT: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the double precision division routine to hold the number of non-zero bytes in the mantissa of the second operand.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f7f6h"></a><a name="user-content-dac"></a></p>
<pre><code>F7F6H DAC:    DEFS 16
</code></pre>
<p>This buffer functions as the Interpreter's primary accumulator during expression evaluation.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f806h"></a><a name="user-content-hold8"></a></p>
<pre><code>F806H HOLD8:  DEFS 65
</code></pre>
<p>This buffer is used by the double precision multiplication routine to hold the multiples of the first operand.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f847h"></a><a name="user-content-arg"></a></p>
<pre><code>F847H ARG:    DEFS 16
</code></pre>
<p>This buffer functions as the Interpreter's secondary accumulator during expression evaluation.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f857h"></a><a name="user-content-rndx"></a></p>
<pre><code>F857H RNDX:   DEFS 8
</code></pre>
<p>This buffer contains the current double precision random number.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f85fh"></a><a name="user-content-maxfil"></a></p>
<pre><code>F85FH MAXFIL: DEFB 01H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the number of currently allocated user I/O buffers. Its value is set to 1 at power-up and thereafter only altered by the "<code>MAXFILES</code>" statement.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f860h"></a><a name="user-content-filtab"></a></p>
<pre><code>F860H FILTAB: DEFW F16AH
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the address of the pointer table for the I/O buffer FCBs.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f862h"></a><a name="user-content-nulbuf"></a></p>
<pre><code>F862H NULBUF: DEFW F177H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the address of the first byte of the data buffer belonging to I/O buffer 0.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f864h"></a><a name="user-content-ptrfil"></a></p>
<pre><code>F864H PTRFIL: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the address of the currently active I/O buffer FCB.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f866h"></a><a name="user-content-filnam"></a></p>
<pre><code>F866H FILNAM: DEFS 11
</code></pre>
<p>This buffer holds a user-specified filename. It is eleven characters long to allow for disc file specs such as "<code>FILENAME.BAS</code>".</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f871h"></a><a name="user-content-filnm2"></a></p>
<pre><code>F871H FILNM2: DEFS 11
</code></pre>
<p>This buffer holds a filename read from an I/O device for comparison with the contents of <a href="#filnam">FILNAM</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f87ch"></a><a name="user-content-nlonly"></a></p>
<pre><code>F87CH NLONLY: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is normally zero but is set during a program "<code>LOAD</code>". Bit 0 is used to prevent I/O buffer 0 being closed during loading and bit 7 to prevent the user I/O buffers being closed if auto-run is required.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f87dh"></a><a name="user-content-savend"></a></p>
<pre><code>F87DH SAVEND: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the "<code>BSAVE</code>" statement handler to hold the end address of the memory block to be saved.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f87fh"></a><a name="user-content-fnkstr"></a></p>
<pre><code>F87FH FNKSTR: DEFS 160
</code></pre>
<p>This buffer contains the ten sixteen-character function key strings. Their values are set at power-up and thereafter only altered by the "<code>KEY</code>" statement.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f91fh"></a><a name="user-content-cgpnt"></a>
<a name="user-content-f920h"></a></p>
<pre><code>F91FH CGPNT:  DEFB 00H     ; Slot ID
F920H         DEFW 1BBFH   ; Address
</code></pre>
<p>These variables contain the location of the character set copied to the VDP by the <a href="#initxt">INITXT</a> and <a href="#init32">INIT32</a> standard routines. Their values are set to the MSX ROM character set at power-up and thereafter unaltered.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f922h"></a><a name="user-content-nambas"></a></p>
<pre><code>F922H NAMBAS: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the current text mode VDP Name Table base address. Its value is set from <a href="#txtnam">TXTNAM</a> or <a href="#t32nam">T32NAM</a> whenever the VDP is initialized to a text mode via the <a href="#initxt">INITXT</a> or <a href="#init32">INIT32</a> standard routines.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f924h"></a><a name="user-content-cgpbas"></a></p>
<pre><code>F924H CGPBAS: DEFW 0800H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the current text mode VDP Character Pattern Table base address. Its value is set from <a href="#txtcgp">TXTCGP</a> or <a href="#t32cgp">T32CGP</a> whenever the VDP is initialized to a text mode via the <a href="#initxt">INITXT</a> or <a href="#init32">INIT32</a> standard routines.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f926h"></a><a name="user-content-patbas"></a></p>
<pre><code>F926H PATBAS: DEFW 3800H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the current VDP Sprite Pattern Table base address. Its value is set from <a href="#t32pat">T32PAT</a>, <a href="#grppat">GRPPAT</a> or <a href="#mltpat">MLTPAT</a> whenever the VDP is initialized via the <a href="#init32">INIT32</a>, <a href="#inigrp">INIGRP</a> or <a href="#inimlt">INIMLT</a> standard routines.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f928h"></a><a name="user-content-atrbas"></a></p>
<pre><code>F928H ATRBAS: DEFW 1B00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the current VDP Sprite Attribute Table base address. Its value is set from <a href="#t32atr">T32ATR</a>, <a href="#grpatr">GRPATR</a> or <a href="#mltatr">MLTATR</a> whenever the VDP is initialized via the <a href="#init32">INIT32</a>, <a href="#inigrp">INIGRP</a> or <a href="#inimlt">INIMLT</a> standard routines.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f92ah"></a><a name="user-content-cloc"></a>
<a name="user-content-f92ch"></a><a name="user-content-cmask"></a></p>
<pre><code>F92AH CLOC:   DEFW 0000H   ; Pixel location
F92CH CMASK:  DEFB 80H     ; Pixel Mask
</code></pre>
<p>These variables contain the current pixel physical address used by the <a href="#rightc">RIGHTC</a>, <a href="#leftc">LEFTC</a>, <a href="#upc">UPC</a>, <a href="#tupc">TUPC</a>, <a href="#downc">DOWNC</a>, <a href="#tdownc">TDOWNC</a>, <a href="#fetchc">FETCHC</a>, <a href="#storec">STOREC</a>, <a href="#readc">READC</a>, <a href="#setc">SETC</a>, <a href="#nsetcx">NSETCX</a>, <a href="#scanr">SCANR</a> and <a href="#scanl">SCANL</a> standard routines. <a href="#cloc">CLOC</a> holds the address of the byte containing the current pixel and <a href="#cmask">CMASK</a> defines the pixel within that byte.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f92dh"></a><a name="user-content-mindel"></a></p>
<pre><code>F92DH MINDEL: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the "<code>LINE</code>" statement handler to hold the minimum difference between the end points of the line.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f92fh"></a><a name="user-content-maxdel"></a></p>
<pre><code>F92FH MAXDEL: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the "<code>LINE</code>" statement handler to hold the maximum difference between the end points of the line.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f931h"></a><a name="user-content-aspect"></a></p>
<pre><code>F931H ASPECT: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the "<code>CIRCLE</code>" statement handler to hold the current aspect ratio. This is stored as a single byte binary fraction so an aspect ratio of 0.75 would become 00C0H. The MSB is only required if the aspect ratio is exactly 1.00, that is 0100H.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f933h"></a><a name="user-content-cencnt"></a></p>
<pre><code>F933H CENCNT: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the "<code>CIRCLE</code>" statement handler to hold the point count of the end angle.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f935h"></a><a name="user-content-clinef"></a></p>
<pre><code>F935H CLINEF: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the "<code>CIRCLE</code>" statement handler to hold the two line flags. Bit 0 is set if a line is required from the start angle to the centre and bit 7 set if one is required from the end angle.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f936h"></a><a name="user-content-cnpnts"></a></p>
<pre><code>F936H CNPNTS: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the "<code>CIRCLE</code>" statement handler to hold the number of points within a forty-five degree segment.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f938h"></a><a name="user-content-cplotf"></a></p>
<pre><code>F938H CPLOTF: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is normally zero but is set by the "<code>CIRCLE</code>" statement handler if the end angle is smaller than the start angle. It is used to determine whether the pixels should be set "inside" the angles or "outside" them.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f939h"></a><a name="user-content-cpcnt"></a></p>
<pre><code>F939H CPCNT:  DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the "<code>CIRCLE</code>" statement handler to hold the point count within the current forty-five degree segment, this is in fact the Y coordinate.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f93bh"></a><a name="user-content-cpcnt8"></a></p>
<pre><code>F93BH CPCNT8: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the "<code>CIRCLE</code>" statement handler to hold the total point count of the present position.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f93dh"></a><a name="user-content-crcsum"></a></p>
<pre><code>F93DH CRCSUM: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the "<code>CIRCLE</code>" statement handler as the point computation counter.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f93fh"></a><a name="user-content-cstcnt"></a></p>
<pre><code>F93FH CSTCNT: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the "<code>CIRCLE</code>" statement handler to hold the point count of the start angle.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f941h"></a><a name="user-content-csclxy"></a></p>
<pre><code>F941H CSCLXY: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the "<code>CIRCLE</code>" statement handler as a flag to determine in which direction the elliptic squash is to be applied: 00H=Y, 01H=X.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f942h"></a><a name="user-content-csavea"></a></p>
<pre><code>F942H CSAVEA: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used for temporary storage by the <a href="#scanr">SCANR</a> standard routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f944h"></a><a name="user-content-csavem"></a></p>
<pre><code>F944H CSAVEM: DEFB 00h
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used for temporary storage by the <a href="#scanr">SCANR</a> standard routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f945h"></a><a name="user-content-cxoff"></a></p>
<pre><code>F945H CXOFF:  DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used for temporary storage by the "<code>CIRCLE</code>" statement handler.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f947h"></a><a name="user-content-cyoff"></a></p>
<pre><code>F947H CYOFF:  DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used for temporary storage by the "<code>CIRCLE</code>" statement handler.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f949h"></a><a name="user-content-lohmsk"></a></p>
<pre><code>F949H LOHMSK: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the "<code>PAINT</code>" statement handler to hold the leftmost position of a LH excursion.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f94ah"></a><a name="user-content-lohdir"></a></p>
<pre><code>F94AH LOHDIR: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the "<code>PAINT</code>" statement handler to hold the new paint direction required by a LH excursion.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f94bh"></a><a name="user-content-lohadr"></a></p>
<pre><code>F94BH LOHADR: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the "<code>PAINT</code>" statement handler to hold the leftmost position of a LH excursion.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f94dh"></a><a name="user-content-lohcnt"></a></p>
<pre><code>F94DH LOHCNT: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the "<code>PAINT</code>" statement handler to hold the size of a LH excursion.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f94fh"></a><a name="user-content-skpcnt"></a></p>
<pre><code>F94FH SKPCNT: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the "<code>PAINT</code>" statement handler to hold the skip count returned by the <a href="#scanr">SCANR</a> standard routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f951h"></a><a name="user-content-movcnt"></a></p>
<pre><code>F951H MOVCNT: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the "<code>PAINT</code>" statement handler to hold the movement count returned by the <a href="#scanr">SCANR</a> standard routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f953h"></a><a name="user-content-pdirec"></a></p>
<pre><code>F953H PDIREC: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the "<code>PAINT</code>" statement handler to hold the current paint direction: 40H=Down, C0H=Up, 00H=Terminate.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f954h"></a><a name="user-content-lfprog"></a></p>
<pre><code>F954H LFPROG: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is normally zero but is set by the "<code>PAINT</code>" statement handler if there has been any leftwards progress.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f955h"></a><a name="user-content-rtprog"></a></p>
<pre><code>F955H RTPROG: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is normally zero but is set by the "<code>PAINT</code>" statement handler if there has been any rightwards progress.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f956h"></a><a name="user-content-mcltab"></a></p>
<pre><code>F956H MCLTAB: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the address of the command table to be used by the macro language parser. The "<code>DRAW</code>" table is at 5D83H and the "<code>PLAY</code>" table at 752EH.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f958h"></a><a name="user-content-mclflg"></a></p>
<pre><code>F958H MCLFLG: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is zero if the macro language parser is being used by the "<code>DRAW</code>", statement handler and non-zero if it is being used by "<code>PLAY</code>".</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f959h"></a><a name="user-content-quetab"></a>
<a name="user-content-f95ah"></a>
<a name="user-content-f95bh"></a>
<a name="user-content-f95ch"></a>
<a name="user-content-f95dh"></a>
<a name="user-content-f95fh"></a>
<a name="user-content-f960h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f961h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f962h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f963h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f965h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f966h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f967h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f968h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f969h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f96bh"></a>
<a name="user-content-f96ch"></a>
<a name="user-content-f96dh"></a>
<a name="user-content-f96eh"></a>
<a name="user-content-f96fh"></a></p>
<pre><code>F959H QUETAB: DEFB 00H     ; AQ Put position
F95AH         DEFB 00H     ; AQ Get position
F95BH         DEFB 00H     ; AQ Putback flag
F95CH         DEFB 7FH     ; AQ Size
F95DH         DEFW F975H   ; AQ Address

F95FH         DEFB 00H     ; BQ Put position
F960H         DEFB 00H     ; BQ Get position
F961H         DEFB 00H     ; BQ Putback flag
F962H         DEFB 7FH     ; BQ Size
F963H         DEFW F9F5H   ; BQ Address

F965H         DEFB 00H     ; CQ Put position
F966H         DEFB 00H     ; CQ Get position
F967H         DEFB 00H     ; CQ Putback flag
F968H         DEFB 7FH     ; CQ Size
F969H         DEFW FA75H   ; CQ Address

F96BH         DEFB 00H     ; RQ Put position
F96CH         DEFB 00H     ; RQ Get position
F96DH         DEFB 00H     ; RQ Putback flag
F96EH         DEFB 00H     ; RQ Size
F96FH         DEFW 0000H   ; RQ Address
</code></pre>
<p>These twenty-four variables form the control blocks for the three music queues (<a href="#voicaq">VOICAQ</a>, <a href="#voicbq">VOICBQ</a> and <a href="#voiccq">VOICCQ</a>) and the RS232 queue. The three music control blocks are initialized by the <a href="#gicini">GICINI</a> standard routine and thereafter maintained by the interrupt handler and the <a href="#putq">PUTQ</a> standard routine. The RS232 control block is unused in the current MSX ROM.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f971h"></a><a name="user-content-quebak"></a>
<a name="user-content-f972h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f973h"></a>
<a name="user-content-f974h"></a></p>
<pre><code>F971H QUEBAK: DEFB 00H     ; AQ Putback character
F972H         DEFB 00H     ; BQ Putback character
F973H         DEFB 00H     ; CQ Putback character
F974H         DEFB 00H     ; RQ Putback character
</code></pre>
<p>These four variables are used to hold any unwanted character returned to the associated queue. Although the putback facility is implemented in the MSX ROM it is currently unused.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-f975h"></a><a name="user-content-voicaq"></a>
<a name="user-content-f9f5h"></a><a name="user-content-voicbq"></a>
<a name="user-content-fa75h"></a><a name="user-content-voiccq"></a>
<a name="user-content-faf5h"></a><a name="user-content-rs2iq"></a></p>
<pre><code>F975H VOICAQ: DEFS 128     ; Voice A queue
F9F5H VOICBQ: DEFS 128     ; Voice B queue
FA75H VOICCQ: DEFS 128     ; Voice C queue
FAF5H RS2IQ:  DEFS 64      ; RS232 queue
</code></pre>
<p>These four buffers contain the three music queues and the RS232 queue, the latter is unused.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fb35h"></a><a name="user-content-prscnt"></a></p>
<pre><code>FB35H PRSCNT: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the "<code>PLAY</code>" statement handler to count the number of completed operand strings. Bit 7 is also set after each of the three operands has been parsed to prevent repeated activation of the <a href="#strtms">STRTMS</a> standard routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fb36h"></a><a name="user-content-savsp"></a></p>
<pre><code>FB36H SAVSP: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the "<code>PLAY</code>" statement handler to save the Z80 SP before control transfers to the macro language parser. Its value is compared with the SP on return to determine whether any data has been left on the stack because of a queue-full termination by the parser.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fb38h"></a><a name="user-content-voicen"></a></p>
<pre><code>FB38H VOICEN: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the current voice number being processed by the "<code>PLAY</code>" statement handler. The values 0, 1 and 2 correspond to PSG channels A, B and C.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fb39h"></a><a name="user-content-savvol"></a></p>
<pre><code>FB39H SAVVOL: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the "<code>PLAY</code>" statement "<code>R</code>" command handler to save the current volume setting while a zero-amplitude rest is generated.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fb3bh"></a><a name="user-content-mcllen"></a></p>
<pre><code>FB3BH MCLLEN: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the macro language parser to hold the length of the string operand being parsed.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fb3ch"></a><a name="user-content-mclptr"></a></p>
<pre><code>FB3CH MCLPTR: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the macro language parser to hold the address of the string operand being parsed.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fb3eh"></a><a name="user-content-queuen"></a></p>
<pre><code>FB3EH QUEUEN: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the interrupt handler to hold the number of the music queue currently being processed. The values 0, 1 and 2 correspond to PSG channels A, B and C.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fb3fh"></a><a name="user-content-musicf"></a></p>
<pre><code>FB3FH MUSICF: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains three bit flags set by the <a href="#strtms">STRTMS</a> standard routine to initiate processing of a music queue by the interrupt handler. Bits 0, 1 and 2 correspond to <a href="#voicaq">VOICAQ</a>, <a href="#voicbq">VOICBQ</a> and <a href="#voiccq">VOICCQ</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fb40h"></a><a name="user-content-plycnt"></a></p>
<pre><code>FB40H PLYCNT: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the <a href="#strtms">STRTMS</a> standard routine to hold the number of "<code>PLAY</code>" statement sequences currently held in the music queues. It is examined when all three end of queue marks have been found for one sequence to determine whether dequeueing should be restarted.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fb41h"></a><a name="user-content-vcba"></a>
<a name="user-content-fb43h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fb44h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fb46h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fb48h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fb49h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fb50h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fb51h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fb52h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fb53h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fb54h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fb56h"></a></p>
<pre><code>FB41H VCBA:   DEFW 0000H   ; Duration counter
FB43H         DEFB 00H     ; String length
FB44H         DEFW 0000H   ; String address
FB46H         DEFW 0000H   ; Stack data address
FB48H         DEFB 00H     ; Music packet length
FB49H         DEFS 7       ; Music packet
FB50H         DEFB 04H     ; Octave
FB51H         DEFB 04H     ; Length
FB52H         DEFB 78H     ; Tempo
FB53H         DEFB 88H     ; Volume
FB54H         DEFW 00FFH   ; Envelope period
FB56H         DEFS 16      ; Space for stack data
</code></pre>
<p>This thirty-seven byte buffer is used by the "<code>PLAY</code>" statement handler to hold the current parameters for voice A.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fb66h"></a><a name="user-content-vcbb"></a></p>
<pre><code>FB66H VCBB:   DEFS 37
</code></pre>
<p>This buffer is used by the "<code>PLAY</code>" statement handler to hold the current parameters for voice B, its structure is the same as <a href="#vcba">VCBA</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fb8bh"></a><a name="user-content-vcbc"></a></p>
<pre><code>FB8BH VCBC:   DEFS 37
</code></pre>
<p>This buffer is used by the "<code>PLAY</code>" statement handler to hold the current parameters for voice C, its structure is the same as <a href="#vcba">VCBA</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fbb0h"></a><a name="user-content-enstop"></a></p>
<pre><code>FBB0H ENSTOP: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable determines whether the interrupt handler will execute a warm start to the Interpreter upon detecting the keys CODE, GRAPH, CTRL and SHIFT depressed together: 00H=Disable, NZ=Enable.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fbb1h"></a><a name="user-content-basrom"></a></p>
<pre><code>FBB1H BASROM: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable determines whether the <a href="#iscntc">ISCNTC</a> and <a href="#inlin">INLIN</a> standard routines will respond to the CTRL-STOP key: 00H=Enable, NZ=Disable. It is used to prevent termination of a BASIC ROM located during the power-up ROM search.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fbb2h"></a><a name="user-content-linttb"></a></p>
<pre><code>FBB2H LINTTB: DEFS 24
</code></pre>
<p>Each of these twenty-four variables is normally non-zero but is zeroed if the contents of the corresponding screen row have overflowed onto the next row. They are maintained by the BIOS but only actually used by the <a href="#inlin">INLIN</a> standard routine (the screen editor) to discriminate between logical and physical lines.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fbcah"></a><a name="user-content-fstpos"></a></p>
<pre><code>FBCAH FSTPOS: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used to hold the cursor coordinates upon entry to the <a href="#inlin">INLIN</a> standard routine. Its function is to restrict the extent of backtracking performed when the text is collected from the screen at termination.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fbcch"></a><a name="user-content-cursav"></a></p>
<pre><code>FBCCH CURSAV: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used to hold the screen character replaced by the text cursor.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fbcdh"></a><a name="user-content-fnkswi"></a></p>
<pre><code>FBCDH FNKSWI: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the <a href="#chsns">CHSNS</a> standard routine to determine whether the shifted or unshifted function keys are currently displayed: 00H=Shifted, 01H=Unshifted.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fbceh"></a><a name="user-content-fnkflg"></a></p>
<pre><code>FBCEH FNKFLG: DEFS 10
</code></pre>
<p>Each of these ten variables is normally zero but is set to 01H if the associated function key has been turned on by a "<code>KEY(n) ON</code>" statement. They are used by the interrupt handler to determine whether, in program mode only, it should return a character string or update the associated entry in <a href="#trptbl">TRPTBL</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fbd8h"></a><a name="user-content-ongsbf"></a></p>
<pre><code>FBD8H ONGSBF: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is normally zero but is incremented by the interrupt handler whenever a device has achieved the conditions necessary to generate a program interrupt. It is used by the Runloop to determine whether any program interrupts are pending without having to search <a href="#trptbl">TRPTBL</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fbd9h"></a><a name="user-content-clikfl"></a></p>
<pre><code>FBD9H CLIKFL: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used internally by the interrupt handler to prevent spurious key clicks when returning multiple characters from a single key depression such as a function key.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fbdah"></a><a name="user-content-oldkey"></a></p>
<pre><code>FBDAH OLDKEY: DEFS 11
</code></pre>
<p>This buffer is used by the interrupt handler to hold the previous state of the keyboard matrix, each byte contains one row of keys starting with row 0.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fbe5h"></a><a name="user-content-newkey"></a></p>
<pre><code>FBE5H NEWKEY: DEFS 11
</code></pre>
<p>This buffer is used by the interrupt handler to hold the current state of the keyboard matrix. Key transitions are detected by comparison with the contents of <a href="#oldkey">OLDKEY</a> after which <a href="#oldkey">OLDKEY</a> is updated with the current state.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fbf0h"></a><a name="user-content-keybuf"></a></p>
<pre><code>FBF0H KEYBUF: DEFS 40
</code></pre>
<p>This buffer contains the decoded keyboard characters produced by the interrupt handler. Note that the buffer is organized as a circular queue driven by <a href="#getpnt">GETPNT</a> and <a href="#putpnt">PUTPNT</a> and consequently has no fixed starting point.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fc18h"></a><a name="user-content-linwrk"></a></p>
<pre><code>FC18H LINWRK: DEFS 40
</code></pre>
<p>This buffer is used by the BIOS to hold a complete line of screen characters.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fc40h"></a><a name="user-content-patwrk"></a></p>
<pre><code>FC40H PATWRK: DEFS 8
</code></pre>
<p>This buffer is used by the BIOS to hold an 8x8 pixel pattern.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fc48h"></a><a name="user-content-bottom"></a></p>
<pre><code>FC48H BOTTOM: DEFW 8000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the address of the lowest RAM location used by the Interpreter. Its value is set at power-up and thereafter unaltered.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fc4ah"></a><a name="user-content-himem"></a></p>
<pre><code>FC4AH HIMEM:  DEFW F380H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the address of the byte following the highest RAM location used by the Interpreter. Its value is set at power-up and thereafter only altered by the "<code>CLEAR</code>" statement.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fc4ch"></a><a name="user-content-trptbl"></a>
<a name="user-content-fc4fh"></a>
<a name="user-content-fc52h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fc55h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fc58h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fc5bh"></a>
<a name="user-content-fc5eh"></a>
<a name="user-content-fc61h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fc64h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fc67h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fc6ah"></a>
<a name="user-content-fc6dh"></a>
<a name="user-content-fc70h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fc73h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fc76h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fc79h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fc7ch"></a>
<a name="user-content-fc7fh"></a>
<a name="user-content-fc82h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fc85h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fc88h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fc8bh"></a>
<a name="user-content-fc8eh"></a>
<a name="user-content-fc91h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fc94h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fc97h"></a></p>
<pre><code>FC4CH TRPTBL: DEFS 3       ; KEY 1
FC4FH         DEFS 3       ; KEY 2
FC52H         DEFS 3       ; KEY 3
FC55H         DEFS 3       ; KEY 4
FC58H         DEFS 3       ; KEY 5
FC5BH         DEFS 3       ; KEY 6
FC5EH         DEFS 3       ; KEY 7
FC61H         DEFS 3       ; KEY 8
FC64H         DEFS 3       ; KEY 9
FC67H         DEFS 3       ; KEY 10
FC6AH         DEFS 3       ; STOP
FC6DH         DEFS 3       ; SPRITE
FC70H         DEFS 3       ; STRIG 0
FC73H         DEFS 3       ; STRIG 1
FC76H         DEFS 3       ; STRIG 2
FC79H         DEFS 3       ; STRIG 3
FC7CH         DEFS 3       ; STRIG 4
FC7FH         DEFS 3       ; INTERVAL
FC82H         DEFS 3       ; Unused
FC85H         DEFS 3       ; Unused
FC88H         DEFS 3       ; Unused
FC8BH         DEFS 3       ; Unused
FC8EH         DEFS 3       ; Unused
FC91H         DEFS 3       ; Unused
FC94H         DEFS 3       ; Unused
FC97H         DEFS 3       ; Unused
</code></pre>
<p>These twenty-six three byte variables hold the current state of the interrupt generating devices. The first byte of each entry contains the device status (bit 0=On, bit 1=Stop, bit 2=Event active) and is updated by the interrupt handler, the Runloop interrupt processor and the "<code>DEVICE 0=ON/OFF/STOP</code>" and "<code>RETURN</code>" statement handlers. The remaining two bytes of each entry are set by the "<code>ON DEVICE GOSUB</code>" statement handler and contain the address of the program line to execute upon a program interrupt.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fc9ah"></a><a name="user-content-rtycnt"></a></p>
<pre><code>FC9AH RTYCNT: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is unused by the current MSX ROM.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fc9bh"></a><a name="user-content-intflg"></a></p>
<pre><code>FC9BH INTFLG: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is normally zero but is set to 03H or 04H if the CTRL-STOP or STOP keys are detected by the interrupt handler.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fc9ch"></a><a name="user-content-pady"></a></p>
<pre><code>FC9CH PADY:   DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the Y coordinate of the last point detected by a touchpad.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fc9dh"></a><a name="user-content-padx"></a></p>
<pre><code>FC9DH PADX:   DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the X coordinate of the last point detected by a touchpad.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fc9eh"></a><a name="user-content-jiffy"></a></p>
<pre><code>FC9EH JIFFY:  DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is continually incremented by the interrupt handler. Its value may be set or read by the "<code>TIME</code>" statement or function.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fca0h"></a><a name="user-content-intval"></a></p>
<pre><code>FCA0H INTVAL: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable holds the interval duration set by the "<code>ON INTERVAL</code>" statement handler.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fca2h"></a><a name="user-content-intcnt"></a></p>
<pre><code>FCA2H INTCNT: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is continually decremented by the interrupt handler. When zero is reached its value is reset from <a href="#intval">INTVAL</a> and, if applicable, a program interrupt generated. Note that this variable always counts irrespective of whether an "<code>INTERVAL ON</code>" statement is active.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fca4h"></a><a name="user-content-lowlim"></a></p>
<pre><code>FCA4H LOWLIM: DEFB 31H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used to hold the minimum allowable start bit duration as determined by the <a href="#tapion">TAPION</a> standard routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fca5h"></a><a name="user-content-winwid"></a></p>
<pre><code>FCA5H WINWID: DEFB 22H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used to hold the LO/HI cycle discrimination duration as determined by the <a href="#tapion">TAPION</a> standard routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fca6h"></a><a name="user-content-grphed"></a></p>
<pre><code>FCA6H GRPHED: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is normally zero but is set to 01H by the <a href="#cnvchr">CNVCHR</a> standard routine upon detection of a graphic header code.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fca7h"></a><a name="user-content-esccnt"></a></p>
<pre><code>FCA7H ESCCNT: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the <a href="#chput">CHPUT</a> standard routine ESC sequence processor to count escape parameters.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fca8h"></a><a name="user-content-insflg"></a></p>
<pre><code>FCA8H INSFLG: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is normally zero but is set to FFH by the <a href="#inlin">INLIN</a> standard routine when insert mode is on.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fca9h"></a><a name="user-content-csrsw"></a></p>
<pre><code>FCA9H CSRSW:  DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>If this variable is zero the cursor is only displayed while the <a href="#chget">CHGET</a> standard routine is waiting for a keyboard character. If it is non-zero the cursor is permanently displayed via the <a href="#chput">CHPUT</a> standard routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fcaah"></a><a name="user-content-cstyle"></a></p>
<pre><code>FCAAH CSTYLE: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable determines the cursor style: 00H=Block, NZ=Underline.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fcabh"></a><a name="user-content-capst"></a></p>
<pre><code>FCABH CAPST:  DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the interrupt handler to hold the current caps lock status: 00H=Off, NZ=On.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fcach"></a><a name="user-content-kanast"></a></p>
<pre><code>FCACH KANAST: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used to hold the keyboard Kana lock status on Japanese machines and the DEAD key status on European machines.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fcadh"></a><a name="user-content-kanamd"></a></p>
<pre><code>FCADH KANAMD: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable holds a keyboard mode on Japanese machines only.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fcaeh"></a><a name="user-content-flbmem"></a></p>
<pre><code>FCAEH FLBMEM: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is set by the file I/O error generators but is otherwise unused.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fcafh"></a><a name="user-content-scrmod"></a></p>
<pre><code>FCAFH SCRMOD: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the current screen mode: 0=<a href="#40x24_text_mode">40x24 Text Mode</a>, 1=<a href="#32x24_text_mode">32x24 Text Mode</a>, 2=<a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a>, 3=<a href="#multicolour_mode">Multicolour Mode</a>.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fcb0h"></a><a name="user-content-oldscr"></a></p>
<pre><code>FCB0H OLDSCR: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable holds the screen mode of the last text mode set.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fcb1h"></a><a name="user-content-casprv"></a></p>
<pre><code>FCB1H CASPRV: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used to hold any character returned to an I/O buffer by the cassette putback function.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fcb2h"></a><a name="user-content-bdratr"></a></p>
<pre><code>FCB2H BDRATR: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the boundary colour for the "<code>PAINT</code>" statement handler. Its value is set by the <a href="#pntini">PNTINI</a> standard routine and used by the <a href="#scanr">SCANR</a> and <a href="#scanl">SCANL</a> standard routines.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fcb3h"></a><a name="user-content-gxpos"></a></p>
<pre><code>FCB3H GXPOS:  DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used for temporary storage of a graphics X coordinate.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fcb5h"></a><a name="user-content-gypos"></a></p>
<pre><code>FCB5H GYPOS:  DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used for temporary storage of a graphics Y coordinate.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fcb7h"></a><a name="user-content-grpacx"></a></p>
<pre><code>FCB7H GRPACX: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the current graphics X coordinate for the <a href="#grpprt">GRPPRT</a> standard routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fcb9h"></a><a name="user-content-grpacy"></a></p>
<pre><code>FCB9H GRPACY: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the current graphics Y coordinate for the <a href="#grpprt">GRPPRT</a> standard routine.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fcbbh"></a><a name="user-content-drwflg"></a></p>
<pre><code>FCBBH DRWFLG: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>Bits 6 and 7 of this variable are set by the "<code>DRAW</code>" statement "<code>N</code>" and "<code>B</code>" command handlers to turn the associated mode on.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fcbch"></a><a name="user-content-drwscl"></a></p>
<pre><code>FCBCH DRWSCL: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the "<code>DRAW</code>" statement "<code>S</code>" command handler to hold the current scale factor.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fcbdh"></a><a name="user-content-drwang"></a></p>
<pre><code>FCBDH DRWANG: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used by the "<code>DRAW</code>" statement "<code>A</code>" command handler to hold the current angle.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fcbeh"></a><a name="user-content-runbnf"></a></p>
<pre><code>FCBEH RUNBNF: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is normally zero but is set by the "<code>BLOAD</code>" statement handler when an auto-run "<code>R</code>" parameter is specified.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fcbfh"></a><a name="user-content-savent"></a></p>
<pre><code>FCBFH SAVENT: DEFW 0000H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable contains the "<code>BSAVE</code>" and "<code>BLOAD</code>" entry address.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fcc1h"></a><a name="user-content-exptbl"></a>
<a name="user-content-fcc2h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fcc3h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fcc4h"></a></p>
<pre><code>FCC1H EXPTBL: DEFB 00H     ; Primary Slot 0
FCC2H         DEFB 00H     ; Primary Slot 1
FCC3H         DEFB 00H     ; Primary Slot 2
FCC4H         DEFB 00H     ; Primary Slot 3
</code></pre>
<p>Each of these four variables is normally zero but is set to 80H during the power-up RAM search if the associated Primary Slot is found to be expanded.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fcc5h"></a><a name="user-content-slttbl"></a>
<a name="user-content-fcc6h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fcc7h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fcc8h"></a></p>
<pre><code>FCC5H SLTTBL: DEFB 00H     ; Primary Slot 0
FCC6H         DEFB 00H     ; Primary Slot 1
FCC7H         DEFB 00H     ; Primary Slot 2
FCC8H         DEFB 00H     ; Primary Slot 3
</code></pre>
<p>These four variables duplicate the contents of the four possible Secondary Slot Registers. The contents of each variable should only be regarded as valid if <a href="#exptbl">EXPTBL</a> shows the associated Primary Slot to be expanded.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fcc9h"></a><a name="user-content-sltatr"></a>
<a name="user-content-fccdh"></a>
<a name="user-content-fcd1h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fcd5h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fcd9h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fcddh"></a>
<a name="user-content-fce1h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fce5h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fce9h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fcedh"></a>
<a name="user-content-fcf1h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fcf5h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fcf9h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fcfdh"></a>
<a name="user-content-fd01h"></a>
<a name="user-content-fd05h"></a></p>
<pre><code>FCC9H SLTATR: DEFS 4       ; PS0, SS0
FCCDH         DEFS 4       ; PS0, SS1
FCD1H         DEFS 4       ; PS0, SS2
FCD5H         DEFS 4       ; PS0, SS3

FCD9H         DEFS 4       ; PS1, SS0
FCDDH         DEFS 4       ; PS1, SS1
FCE1H         DEFS 4       ; PS1, SS2
FCE5H         DEFS 4       ; PS1, SS3

FCE9H         DEFS 4       ; PS2, SS0
FCEDH         DEFS 4       ; PS2, SS1
FCF1H         DEFS 4       ; PS2, SS2
FCF5H         DEFS 4       ; PS2, SS3

FCF9H         DEFS 4       ; PS3, SS0
FCFDH         DEFS 4       ; PS3, SS1
FD01H         DEFS 4       ; PS3, SS2
FD05H         DEFS 4       ; PS3, SS3
</code></pre>
<p>These sixty-four variables contain the attributes of any extension ROMs found during the power-up ROM search. The characteristics of each 16 KB ROM are encoded into a single byte so four bytes are required for each possible slot. The encoding is:</p>
<pre><code>Bit 7 set=BASIC program
Bit 6 set=Device handler
Bit 5 set=Statement handler
</code></pre>
<p>Note that the entries for page 0 (0000H to 3FFFH) and page 3 (C000H to FFFFH) will always be zero as only page 1 (4000H to 7FFFH) and page 2 (8000H to BFFFH) are actually examined. The MSX convention is that machine code extension ROMs are placed in page 1 and BASIC program ROMs in page 2.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fd09h"></a><a name="user-content-sltwrk"></a></p>
<pre><code>FD09H SLTWRK: DEFS 128
</code></pre>
<p>This buffer provides two bytes of local workspace for each of the sixty-four possible extension ROMs.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fd89h"></a><a name="user-content-procnm"></a></p>
<pre><code>FD89H PROCNM: DEFS 16
</code></pre>
<p>This buffer is used to hold a device or statement name for examination by an extension ROM.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-fd99h"></a><a name="user-content-device"></a></p>
<pre><code>FD99H DEVICE: DEFB 00H
</code></pre>
<p>This variable is used to pass a device code, from 0 to 3, to an extension ROM.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-the_hooks"></a></p>
<h2><a id="user-content-the-hooks" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#the-hooks"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>The Hooks</h2>
<p>The section of the Workspace Area from FD9AH to FFC9H contains one hundred and twelve hooks, each of which is filled with five Z80 RET opcodes at power-up. These are called from strategic locations within the BIOS/Interpreter so that the ROM can be extended, particularly so that it can be upgraded to Disk BASIC. Each hook has sufficient room to hold a far call to any slot:</p>
<pre><code>RST 30H
DEFB Slot ID
DEFW Address
RET
</code></pre>
<p>The hooks are listed on the following pages together with the address they are called from and a brief note as to their function.</p>
<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>ADDRESS</th>
<th>NAME</th>
<th>SIZE</th>
<th>FROM</th>
<th>FUNCTION</th>
</tr>
</thead>

<p>The Workspace Area from FFCAH to FFFFH is unused. (on MSX 1)</p>

<p><a name="user-content-chapter_7"></a></p>
<h1><a id="user-content-7-machine-code-programs" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#7-machine-code-programs"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>7. Machine Code Programs</h1>
<p>This chapter contains a number of machine code programs to illustrate the use of MSX system resources. Although prepared with the ZEN Assembler they are designed t o run from BASIC and if necessary, may be entered in hex form using the loader shown below. The code should then be saved on cassette before any attempt is made to run it.</p>
<pre><code>10 CLEAR 200,&amp;HE000
20 ADDR=&amp;HE000
30 PRINT RIGHT$ ("000"+HEX$(ADDR),4);
40 INPUT D$
50 POKE ADDR,VAL("&amp;H"+D$)
60 ADDR=ADDR+l
70 GOTO 30
</code></pre>
<p>All the programs start at address E000H and are entered at the same point. Unless stated otherwise no parameter need be passed to a program, execution may therefore be initiated with a simple <code>DEFUSR=&amp;HE000:?USR(0)</code> statement.</p>
<p><a name="user-content-keyboard_matrix"></a></p>
<h2><a id="user-content-keyboard-matrix" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#keyboard-matrix"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Keyboard Matrix</h2>
<p>This program displays the keyboard matrix on the screen so that key depressions may be directly observed. The program may be terminated by pressing the CTRL and STOP keys. Note that spurious key depressions can be produced under certain circumstances if more than three or four keys are pressed at one time. This is a characteristic of all matrix type keyboards.</p>
<pre><code>                            ORG     0E000H
                            LOAD    0E000H

                    ; ******************************
                    ; *   BIOS STANDARD ROUTINES   *
                    ; ******************************

                    INITXT: EQU     006CH
                    CHPUT:  EQU     00A2H
                    SNSMAT: EQU     0141H
                    BREAKX: EQU     00B7H

                    ; ******************************
                    ; *     WORKSPACE VARIABLES    *
                    ; ******************************

                    INTFLG: EQU     0FC9BH

                    ; ******************************
                    ; *      CONTROL CHARACTERS    *
                    ; ******************************

                    LF:     EQU     10
                    HOME:   EQU     11
                    CR:     EQU     13

E000    CD6C00      MATRIX: CALL    INITXT              ; SCREEN 0
E003    3E0B        MX1:    LD      A,HOME              ;
E005    CDA200              CALL    CHPUT               ; Home Cursor
E008    AF                  XOR     A                   ; A=KBD row
E009    F5          MX2:    PUSH    AF                  ;
E00A    CD4101              CALL    SNSMAT              ; Read a row
E00D    0608                LD      B,6                 ; Eight cols
E00F    07          MX3:    RLCA                        ; Select col
E010    F5                  PUSH    AF                  ;
E011    E601                AND     1                   ;
E013    C630                ADD     A,"0"               ; Result
E015    CDA200              CALL    CHPUT               ; Display col
E018    F1                  POP     AF                  ;
E019    10F4                DJNZ    MX3                 ;
E01B    3E0D                LD      A,CR                ; Newline
E01D    CDA200              CALL    CHPUT               ;
E020    3E0A                LD      A,LF                ;
E022    CDA200              CALL    CHPUT               ;
E025    F1                  POP     AF                  ; A=KBD row
E026    3C                  INC     A                   ; Next row
E027    FE0B                CP      11                  ; Finished?
E029    20DE                JR      NZ,MX2              ;
E02B    CDB700              CALL    BREAKX              ; CTRL-STOP
E02E    30D3                JR      NC,MX1              ; Continue
E030    AF                  XOR     A                   ;
E031    329BFC              LD      (INTFLG),A          ; Clear possible STOP
E034    C9                  RET                         ; Back to BASIC

                            END
</code></pre>
<p><a name="user-content-40_column_graphics_text"></a></p>
<h2><a id="user-content-40-column-graphics-text" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#40-column-graphics-text"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>40 Column Graphics Text</h2>
<p>This program prints text on the <a href="#graphics_mode">Graphics Mode</a> screen at forty characters per line. The string to be displayed is passed as the <code>USR</code> call parameter, for example <code>A$=USR("something")</code>. There us no need to open a GRP file beforehand, the only requirement of the program is that the screen be in the correct mode. The heart of the program is functionally equivalent to the <a href="#grpprt">GRPPRT</a> standard routine but only the first six dot columns of a given character pattern are placed on the screen instead of eight. As the <a href="#grpprt">GRPPRT</a> the pattern is placed at the current graphics position and the only control character recognised is ASCII CR (13) which functions as a combined CR, LF. Unlike the <a href="#grpprt">GRPPRT</a> standard routine characters printed at negative coordinates, but which overlap the screen, will be correctly displayed. The program is currently set up to perform an auto linefeed after dot column 239, thus giving exactly forty characters per line. If required this may be changed, via the constant in the RMDCOL subroutine, so that the full width of the screen is usable.</p>
<pre><code>                            ORG     0E000H
                            LOAD    0E000H

                    ; ******************************
                    ; *   BIOS STANDARD ROUTINES   *
                    ; ******************************

                    RDSLT:  EQU     000CH
                    CNVCHR: EQU     00ABH
                    MAPXYC: EQU     0111H
                    SETC:   EQU     0120H

                    ; ******************************
                    ; *     WORKSPACE VARIABLES    *
                    ; ******************************

                    FORCLR: EQU     0F3E9H
                    ATRBYT: EQU     0F3F2H
                    CGPNT:  EQU     0F91FH
                    PATWRK: EQU     0FC40H
                    SCRMOD: EQU     0FCAFH
                    GRPACX: EQU     0FCB7H
                    GRPACY: EQU     0FCB9H

                    ; ******************************
                    ; *      CONTROL CHARACTERS    *
                    ; ******************************

                    CR:     EQU     13

E000    FE03        GFORTY: CP      3                   ; String type?
E002    C0                  RET     NZ                  ;
E003    3AAFFC              LD      A,(SCRMOD)          ; Mode
E006    FE02                CP      2                   ; Graphics?
E008    C0                  RET     NZ                  ;
E009    EB                  EX      DE,HL               ; HL-&gt;Descriptor
E00A    46                  LD      B,(HL)              ; B=String len
E00B    23                  INC     HL                  ;
E00C    5E                  LD      E,(HL)              ; Address LSB
E00D    23                  INC     HL                  ;
E00E    56                  LD      D,(HL)              ; DE-&gt;String
E00F    04                  INC     B                   ;
E010    05          GF2:    DEC     B                   ; Finished?
E011    C8                  RET     Z                   ;
E012    1A                  LD      A,(DE)              ; A=Chr from string
E013    CD19E0              CALL    GPRINT              ; Print it
E016    13                  INC     DE                  ;
E017    18F7                JR      GF2                 ; Next chr
E019    F5          GPRINT: PUSH    AF                  ;
E01A    C5                  PUSH    BC                  ;
E01B    D5                  PUSH    DE                  ;
E01C    E5                  PUSH    HL                  ;
E01D    FDE5                PUSH    IY                  ;
E01F    ED4BB7FC            LD      BC,(GRPACX)         ; BC=X coord
E023    ED5BB9FC            LD      DE,(GRPACY)         ; DE=Y coord
E027    CD39E0              CALL    GDC                 ; Decode chr
E02A    ED43B7FC            LD      (GRPACX),BC         ; New X coord
E02E    ED53B9FC            LD      (GRPACY),DE         ; New Y coord
E032    FDE1                POP     IY                  ;
E034    E1                  POP     HL                  ;
E035    D1                  POP     DE                  ;
E036    C1                  POP     BC                  ;
E037    F1                  POP     AF                  ;
E038    C9                  RET                         ;

E039    CDAB00      GDC:    CALL    CNVCHR              ; Check graphic
E03C    D0                  RET     NC                  ; NC=Header
E03D    2007                JR      NZ,GD2              ; NZ=Converted
E03F    FE0D                CP      CR                  ; Carriage Return?
E041    2873                JR      Z,GCRLF             ;
E043    FE20                CP      20H                 ; Other control?
E045    D8                  RET     C                   ; Ignore
E046    6F          GD2:    LD      L,A                 ;
E047    2600                LD      H,0                 ; HL=Chr code
E049    29                  ADD     HL,HL               ;
E04A    29                  ADD     HL,HL               ;
E04B    29                  ADD     HL,HL               ; HL=Chr*8
E04C    C5                  PUSH    BC                  ; X coord
E04D    D5                  PUSH    DE                  ; Y coord
E04E    ED5B20F9            LD      DE,(CGPNT+1)        ; Character set
E052    19                  ADD     HL,DE               ; HL-&gt;Pattern
E053    1140FC              LD      DE,PATWRK           ; DE-&gt;Buffer
E056    0608                LD      B,8                 ; Eight byte pattern
E058    C5          GD3:    PUSH    BC                  ;
E059    D5                  PUSH    DE                  ;
E05A    3A1FF9              LD      A,(CGPNT)           ; Slot ID
E05D    CD0C00              CALL    RDSLT               ; Get pattern
E060    FB                  EI                          ;
E061    D1                  POP     DE                  ;
E062    C1                  POP     BC                  ;
E063    12                  LD      (DE),A              ; Put in buffer
E064    13                  INC     DE                  ;
E065    23                  INC     HL                  ;
E066    10F0                DJNZ    GD3                 ; Next
E068    D1                  POP     DE                  ;
E069    C1                  POP     BC                  ;
E06A    3AE9F3              LD      A,(FORCLR)          ; Current colour
E06D    32F2F3              LS      (ATRBYT),A          ; Set ink
E070    FD2140FC            LD      IY,PATWRK           ; IY-&gt;Patterns
E074    D5                  PUSH    DE                  ;
E075    2608                LD      H,8                 ; Max dot rows
E077    CB7A        GD4:    BIT     7,D                 ; Pos Y coord?
E079    202A                JR      NZ,GD8              ;
E07B    CDBFE0              CALL    BMDROW              ; Bottom most row?
E07E    382B                JR      C,GD9               ; C=Y too large
E080    C5                  PUSH    BC                  ;
E081    2E06                LD      L,6                 ; Max dot cols
E083    FD7E00              LD      A,(IY+0)            ; A=Pattern row
E086    CB78        GD5:    BIT     7,B                 ; Pos X coord
E088    2015                JR      NZ,GD6              ;
E08A    CDC8E0              CALL    RMDCOL              ; Rightmost col?
E08D    3815                JR      C,GD7               ; C=X too large
E08F    CB7F                BIT     7,A                 ; Pattern bit
E091    280C                JR      Z,GD6               ; Z=0 Pixel
E093    F5                  PUSH    AF                  ;
E094    D5                  PUSH    DE                  ;
E095    E5                  PUSH    HL                  ;
E096    CD1101              CALL    MAPXYC              ; Map coords
E099    CD2001              CALL    SETC                ; Set pixel
E09C    E1                  POP     HL                  ;
E09D    D1                  POP     DE                  ;
E09E    F1                  POP     AF                  ;
E09F    07          GD6:    RLCA                        ; Shift pattern
E0A0    03                  INC     BC                  ; X=X+1
E0A1    2D                  DEC     L                   ; Finished dot cols?
E0A2    20E2                JR      NZ,GD5              ;
E0A4    C1          GD7:    POP     BC                  ; Initial X coord
E0A5    FD23        GD8:    INC     IY                  ; Next pattern byte
E0A7    13                  INC     DE                  ; Y=Y+1
E0A8    25                  DEC     H                   ; Finished dot rows?
E0A9    20CC                JR      NZ,GD4              ;
E0AB    D1          GD9:    POP     DE                  ; Initial Y coord
E0AC    210600              LD      HL,6                ; Step
E0AF    09                  ADD     HL,BC               ; X=X+6
E0B0    44                  LD      B,H                 ;
E0B1    4D                  LD      C,L                 ; BC=New X coord
E0B2    CDC8E0              CALL    RMDCOL              ; Rightmost col?
E0B5    D0                  RET     NC                  ;

E0B6    010000      GCRLF:  LD      BC,0                ; X=0
E0B9    210800              LD      HL,8                ;
E0BC    19                  ADD     HL,DE               ;
E0BD    EB                  EX      DE,HL               ; Y=Y+8
E0BE    C9                  RET                         ;

E0BF    E5          BMDROW: PUSH    HL                  ;
E0C0    21BF00              LD      HL,191              ; Bottom dot row
E0C3    B7                  OR      A                   ;
E0C4    ED52                SBC     HL,DE               ; Check Y coord
E0C6    E1                  POP     HL                  ;
E0C7    C9                  RET                         ; C=Below screen

E0C8    E5          RMDCOL: PUSH    HL                  ;
E0C9    21EF00              LD      HL,239              ; Rightmost dot col
E0CC    B7                  OR      A                   ;
E0CD    ED42                SBC     HL,BC               ; Check X coord
E0CF    E1                  POP     HL                  ;
E0D0    C9                  RET                         ; C=Beyond right

                            END
</code></pre>
<p><a name="user-content-string_bubble_sort"></a></p>
<h2><a id="user-content-string-bubble-sort" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#string-bubble-sort"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>String Bubble Sort</h2>
<p>This program will sort the contents os a string Array into ascending alphabetic order. The location of the Array is passed as the <code>USR</code> call parameter, for example <code>V=USR(VARPRT(A$(0)))</code>. There are no restrictions on the size of the Array or on its contents but it must only have one dimension. The program is based on the classic bubble sort algorithm where string pairs are compared and their positions swapped if the second is smaller than the first. a 250 element Array of randomly generated stringswill be sorted in approximately 2.5 seconds. The equivalent BASIC program takes over six minutes.</p>
<pre><code>                            ORG     0E000H
                            LOAD    0E000H

E000    FE02        SORT:   CP      2                   ; Integer type?
E002    C0                  RET     NZ                  ;
E003    23                  INC     HL                  ; HL-&gt;DAC+1
E004    23                  INC     HL                  ; HL-&gt;DAC+2
E005    5E                  LD      E,(HL)              ; Address LSB
E006    23                  INC     HL                  ; HL-&gt;DAC+3
E007    56                  LD      D,(HL)              ; Address MSB
E008    EB                  EX      DE,HL               ; HL-&gt;A$(0)
E009    E5                  PUSH    HL                  ;
E00A    DDE1                POP     IX                  ; IX-&gt;A$(0)
E00C    DD7EF8              LD      A,(IX-8)            ; Array type
E00F    FE03                CP      3                   ; String Array?
E011    C0                  RET     NZ                  ;
E012    DD7EFD              LD      A,(IX-3)            ; Dimension
E015    3D                  DEC     A                   ; Single dimension?
E016    C0                  RET     NZ                  ;
E017    DD4EFE              LD      C,(IX-2)            ;
E01A    DD46FF              LD      B,(IX-1)            ; BC=Element count
E01D    C5          SR2:    PUSH    BC                  ;
E01E    E5                  PUSH    HL                  ; HL-&gt;Dsc(N)
E01F    46          SR3:    LD      B,(HL)              ; B=Len(N)
E020    23                  INC     HL                  ;
E021    5E                  LD      E,(HL)              ;
E022    23                  INC     HL                  ;
E023    E5                  PUSH    HL                  ;
E024    56                  LD      D,(HL)              ; DE-&gt;String(N)
E025    23                  INC     HL                  ; HL-&gt;Dsc(N+1)
E026    4E                  LD      C,(HL)              ; C=Len(N+1)
E027    23                  INC     HL                  ;
E028    7E                  LD      A,(HL)              ;
E029    23                  INC     HL                  ;
E02A    E5                  PUSH    HL                  ;
E02B    66                  LD      H,(HL)              ;
E02C    6F                  LD      L,A                 ; HL-&gt;String(N+1)
E02D    EB                  EX      DE,HL               ; HL-&gt;(N),DE-&gt;(N+1)
E02E    04                  INC     B                   ;
E02F    0C                  INC     C                   ;
E030    05          SR4:    DEC     B                   ; Remaining len(N)
E031    2B25                JR      Z,NEXT              ; Z=(N)&lt;=(N+1)
E033    0D                  DEC     C                   ; Remaining len(N+1)
E034    2808                JR      Z,SWAP              ; Z=(N+1)&lt;(N)
E036    1A                  LD      A,(DE)              ; Chr from (N+1)
E037    BE                  CP      (HL)                ; Chr from (N)
E038    13                  INC     DE                  ;
E039    23                  INC     HL                  ;
E03A    28F4                JR      Z,SR4               ; Same, continue
E03C    301A                JR      NC,NEXT             ; NC=(N)&lt;(N+1)
E03E    E1          SWAP:   POP     HL                  ; HL-&gt;Dsc(N+1)
E03F    D1                  POP     DE                  ; DE-&gt;Dsc(N)
E040    0603                LD      B,3                 ; Descriptor size
E042    1A          SW2:    LD      A,(DE)              ; Swap descriptors
